# Changelog

All notable changes to this project will be documented in this file.

The format is based on [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/).

## [Unreleased]

### Fixed
- **`linear_pm_gate` no longer false-blocks a start when a higher-priority ticket is already in progress** (2026-07-07, audit P3). `higher_priority_available` counted `started` (In Progress) tickets as "startable" peers, so moving a lower-priority ticket to In Progress while already working a higher-priority one raised a spurious `BlockHigherPriorityAvailable` — telling the assignee to "start the most urgent work first" when that work is a ticket they are *already* on. `started` is now excluded from the startable set (only `backlog`/`unstarted`/`triage` count), matching the helper's own documented definition of startable. Regression test: a `started` higher-priority same-assignee peer must not block; a `backlog` one still must.

  *Deferred from the P3 batch (tracked, with rationale — not silent skips):* `team_name` deprecation migration (the field still works; CC has not dropped it — pre-emptive migration is speculative and the contract-diff guard will flag the actual removal); plaintext-secrets-at-rest in local snapshots (needs an architectural decision — `chmod 600` vs storing unresolved `$doppler:` refs vs encryption — and is local-only, not a new exfil surface); explicit gate error-behavior tests (the gates already behave fail-closed per the correctness-lane audit; adding tests for 6 gates is low-risk-reduction churn); `skill_telemetry` non-atomic rewrite (surfaced-not-confirmed — needs verification first).

### Changed
- **Audit P2 cleanup: single source of truth for the two hand-duplicated policies + dead CC-env branches removed** (2026-07-07). Follow-up to the 2026-07 sentinel audit, doing the consolidations properly rather than papering over them:
  - **`home_root()` deduplicated into a pure domain policy.** `sentinel-application::paths::home_root` and `sentinel-infrastructure::paths::try_home_root` were byte-identical copies of the same fail-closed `SENTINEL_HOME` resolution — a divergence would resolve state to different directories. The decision now lives once in `sentinel_domain::paths::resolve_home_root(sentinel_home, home_dir)` (pure — the caller does the env/`dirs::home_dir()` IO and passes results in, honouring domain purity); both crates are one-line wrappers. Divergence is now impossible by construction. 5 exhaustive policy tests (all 4 arms incl. empty-override fail-closed + non-Unicode) with the domain fn.
  - **Task status/priority emoji vocabulary deduplicated into a domain module.** `session_init` (render) and `task_persist` (parse) each carried their own glyph table — render/parse inverses kept in sync by hand (the code even commented "kept in sync with…"). A glyph added to one but not the other silently breaks round-tripping. Now `sentinel_domain::task_decoration` owns the canonical `DECOR_EMOJI` set + `status_glyph`/`decorated_status`/`status_from_glyph`/`priority_from_decoration`; both hooks delegate. **Latent bug fixed in passing:** the shared `DECOR_EMOJI` now includes `🚫` (blocked), which `session_init` renders but `task_persist`'s stripper was missing — so a blocked task's glyph is now correctly stripped. 4 tests incl. render/parse round-trip and a "DECOR_EMOJI covers every render glyph" drift guard.
  - **Dead CC-env branches corrected** (from the CC-contract audit): `hook_cmd.rs` read `CLAUDE_CODE_ENTRY_POINT` (CC exports `CLAUDE_CODE_ENTRYPOINT`, no underscore — the check could never succeed) and `CLAUDE_PROJECT` (CC never exports it — dead `[Project Context]` branch). Now read `CLAUDE_CODE_ENTRYPOINT` and derive the project name from `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR`'s basename (the path CC actually exports). Verified against the deobfuscated 2.1.201 bundle.
  - sentinel-application 1923/1923 green; domain + infrastructure paths tests green.

### Fixed
- **Sentinel audit fixes — 5 defects surfaced by verifying sentinel against Claude Code's deobfuscated 2.1.201 source** (2026-07-07). A read-only audit cross-checked every sentinel↔CC boundary contract against the deobfuscated bundle and found bugs invisible to greps and the 2,500-test suite because they were silent *drift* between two codebases:
  - **`tool_response` wire key (HIGH, security) — re-arms ~9 dark PostToolUse hooks.** CC sends PostToolUse tool output under the key `tool_response` (verified: payload + zod schema), but `HookInput`'s field was `tool_result` with no alias, so every PostToolUse hook inspecting output deserialized `None` and early-returned — silently disabling itself. Worst case: `prompt_injection_nudge` (the untrusted-tool-output scanner) never scanned. Also dark: `bug_task_gate`, `plan_organizer` (ExitPlanMode path), `pr_auto_monitor`, `good_citizen_observer`, `step_judge`, `account_cascade`, `ask_question_resync_nudge`. Fix: `#[serde(alias = "tool_response")]`. Regression test deserializes a real-CC-shaped payload and asserts the scanner fires.
  - **Heal-path `command` allowlist (CRITICAL, arbitrary-exec).** The MCP registration heal copied `command`/`args`/`env` verbatim from `marketplace.json` into `~/.claude.json`, which CC execs at session start — a conditional RCE if the marketplace clone is writable. Now `command` must be an approved launcher (`mcp-supervisor`/`mcp-router`) or a bare `<name>-mcp[.exe]` binary; shell interpreters, absolute/relative paths, and metacharacters are rejected with a warning while clean entries in the same declaration still heal. `HealOutcome` now carries the `(name, command)` pairs and the operator notice lists them, so a poisoned-but-allowlisted entry is visible not hidden behind a count.
  - **`subagent_start` typed-field read.** Read `agent_type` from the flattened `extra` map, but CC sends it as a top-level field serde routes to the typed `HookInput.agent_type` → always `"unknown"`. Mirror `subagent_stop::resolve_agent_identity` (typed-first).
  - **`good_citizen_observer` multibyte panic.** `&line[..120]` byte-sliced the excerpt and panicked when byte 120 landed mid-UTF-8 (non-ASCII tool output). Truncate to 120 chars on a char boundary.
  - **Dispatcher session-id env chain (closes the E2E-proven #9 gap).** The `hook_cmd` session fallback read only `CLAUDE_SESSION_ID`, but CC exports `CLAUDE_CODE_SESSION_ID` into hook/MCP children (verified in the bundle + proven live — the engine refused a payload carrying only that var). Now uses the same `VULCAN_SESSION_ID`→`CLAUDE_CODE_SESSION_ID`→`CLAUDE_SESSION_ID`→`SESSION_ID` precedence `channel_events` uses. Live-re-proven against the rebuilt engine.
  - Deferred (tracked): plaintext-secrets-at-rest in snapshots, `team_name` deprecation migration, gate error-behavior tests, `home_root()` dedup, emoji-vocabulary consolidation.

### Fixed
- **`[Todos]` loader: exact project matching + session/staleness split kills the 4,451-row aggregate; emoji vocabulary lands on every high-frequency hook surface** (2026-07-06). The `todo_loader` matched rows with `proj.contains(project_name)` — for a home-dir session (`project_name = "garys"`) that substring matches EVERY project path under `C:\Users\garys`, i.e. the whole 4,916-row store, producing `[Todos] Pending: 4451 | Top items: <stale rows from dead sessions>` on every session's first prompt. Now: **(1)** project matching is exact — normalized-path equality (`hooks::normalize_path`, same fold as `project_hash`) or exact-basename equality, never substring; **(2)** counts split into *this session* vs *other recent sessions* (14-day `updated_at` window, keyed on the row's `session_id`), and rows from dead sessions beyond the window are hidden (counted once as `💤 N stale hidden`); a project with only stale foreign rows injects nothing; **(3)** the line renders the shared emoji vocabulary (`📋 [Todos] project — this session: ⏳n 🔄n · recent (14d): ⏳n 🔄n · 🔴p0 🟠p1 | Top: 🔴 …`). Also swept emoji onto the other always-visible surfaces so the session banner reads as one system: 🛡️ SessionStart/MCP Guardian, 📦 Marketplace Sync, 🧩 Components, 📁 Project Init, ❌ Validation, 🚨 MCP REGISTRATION MISSING, 🕘 Last Session, 📌 Persistent Tasks (with 🔄/⏳ status icons instead of `~`/space), 🎯 Skill Router, 📊 Activity Tracker, 🧠 Memory, and zone-colored 🟢🟡🟠🔴 Context Monitor. `HookTier` gains the missing `High` (🟠) tier that `dry_run_then_commit`/`provenance_validate`/`requirements_traceability_gate` had been hand-rolling outside the envelope. And `[Last Session]` summaries now age out after 14 days — `task_rehydrate` replayed a stale `session-summary.json` verbatim forever ("ended 19d ago … 1 in progress" at every session start), because nothing rewrites the file until a later SessionEnd finds non-empty tasks for that project. 8 new/updated todo_loader tests + a summary age-out test.
- **Channel events respect sessions: producer/consumer session-id contract unified, idle spam debounced, unknown-agent completions muted, emoji vocabulary, stale-backlog file sweep** (2026-07-06). Five fixes making channel push notifications land in the right session and read at a glance: **(1)** `detect_session_id` (and `channel_event_from_webhook`) now resolve the session from the same 4-var chain the sentinel-mcp consumer uses — `VULCAN_SESSION_ID` → `CLAUDE_CODE_SESSION_ID` → `CLAUDE_SESSION_ID` → `SESSION_ID`, first *concrete* id wins — via the shared `SESSION_ID_ENV_VARS` const. The producer previously checked only `CLAUDE_SESSION_ID`/`SESSION_ID` while Claude Code actually exports `CLAUDE_CODE_SESSION_ID`, so env-resolved events were written to directories no live consumer watches (found three dirs holding 849/747/466 undelivered events, still receiving fresh writes). **(2)** `teammate_idle` channel emits are debounced per (session, teammate) with a 10-minute cooldown marker under `sentinel/state/idle-debounce/` — Claude Code fires TeammateIdle on every idle poll, pushing the same "going idle" notification several times a minute (observed 8× in 3 min); the quality-gate context injection itself is NOT debounced. **(3)** `subagent_stop` no longer emits a channel event for identity-less completions — anonymous inner helper agents (judge/classifier calls) pushed one `Agent "unknown" has finished` per call; named completions still emit. **(4)** Channel-event summaries carry a central emoji vocabulary stamped in `emit` (✅ completed, 💤 idle, 🔨 build, 🚀 deploy, 🚨 MCP failure/registration-missing, 🟡 context threshold, 📋 plan, 🔄 linear drift, 🔔 hookdeck webhooks), skipped when the producer already leads with a glyph. **(5)** New `cleanup_stale_events` sweeps event FILES older than 24h out of still-active directories at SessionStart: `cleanup_stale_sessions` removes whole dirs by mtime, so a dir with a live producer but dead/mismatched consumer (the split-brain in (1)) grew unbounded while staying mtime-fresh. The sweep never deletes directories — removing a live consumer's watched dir would sever its `notify` subscription. 9 new tests; sentinel-application suite green.
- **`project_hash` now normalizes path separators + drive-letter case before hashing — one dir, one key** (2026-07-06). Live-reproduced the exact mixed-separator divergence the storage audit's adversarial critic predicted: `C:\Users\…\sentinel` (backslash, from native/hook callers) and `C:/Users/…/sentinel` (forward-slash, from Bash/git callers) hashed to **different** project keys (`c08fea48` vs `fdf9d8fd`), scattering one project's tasks into two snapshots. `canonical_project_cwd` hashed the raw cwd string. New `normalize_path` (applied inside `canonical_project_cwd`, before the worktree-collapse and hash) folds `\`→`/` and lowercases a leading Windows drive letter (`C:`==`c:`), leaving sub-drive casing untouched (Windows is case-insensitive-but-preserving; folding the whole path could collide distinct paths on a case-sensitive mount). All spellings — backslash, forward-slash, lowercase-drive, mixed, and worktrees — now collapse to one key. Also corrected the stale `task_persist` module doc that described the key as `SHA-256(cwd)[..4]` (it omitted the canonicalization). 3 new tests (separator/drive folding, same-dir-different-spellings-same-hash, updated worktree-collapse expectation); sentinel-application green, zero new clippy.
- **Tasks are first-class in storage: session-id validators unified, cross-project task bleed killed at source, 8 ghost snapshots reclaimed** (2026-07-06). Making sentinel's task store coherent, driven by an adversarial audit of the whole scoping surface (the audit corrected the initial diagnosis — the "9 ghost snapshots" were **8 genuinely different projects** each holding a byte-identical session-global task list, not one key-scattered project). Three pieces: **(1) Session-id validator collapse.** ~12 divergent `concrete_session_id` / `session_path_component` copies across 11 hooks were replaced with delegation to the canonical `hooks::{session_path_component, concrete_input_session_id}` (which route through `sentinel_domain::SessionId::validate`). This is a **security hardening**: the three override/verification gates (`phase_gate`, `hygiene_override`, `pre_commit_verification`) previously ran the *loosest* validators — accepting `default`, path-traversal (`..`), oversized, and unsafe-char session ids that could key durable override authority — and each now rejects them and **fails safe** (no override granted / protection stays on / verification stays enforced). `task_persist`'s loose inline resolver is likewise corrected. New contract test pins the canonical validator's rejection of `unknown`/`default`/traversal/oversized/unsafe-char ids. **(2) Cross-project bleed killed at source.** The native `TaskList` is session-global, but `task_persist` tagged each snapshot with whatever project the cwd was in per-fire, so a session that `cd`s through N repos smeared its identical task list into N project snapshots (observed: one 2-task list copied into 8 distinct repos). Added a per-session projects-written ledger (`persistent-tasks/.session-projects/{session_id}.json`): after persisting the current project's snapshot, the session's stale copies in every *other* project it previously wrote are truncated (guarded by a `meta.session_id` ownership check so another session's data is never touched, and never touching the current live snapshot so there is no race). Net: a session's tasks live in exactly one project at a time and follow the session across repos. **(3) One-off reclamation.** The 8 pre-existing ghost snapshots (all owned by this session, verified) were archived to `persistent-tasks/.archive/` (recoverable, never hard-deleted) and truncated — the "Diagnose hookdeck" ghost dropped from 9 active snapshots to 1 (the current project's live copy). 6 new tests (ledger dedupe, bleed-clears-others-not-current, cross-session-safety, validator contract); sentinel-application 1890/1890 green, zero new clippy. This makes the storage layer first-class alongside the rendering/identity fixes shipped earlier the same day (truncate, normalize, status emoji, agent identity).
- **`agent_completed` channel events now carry the real agent identity instead of "unknown"** (2026-07-06). Every SubagentStop channel event rendered as `Background agent (unknown) has finished` with `agent_type`/`source_agent` = `unknown`, making a session's own agent-completion stream unreadable (you couldn't tell *which* agent finished). Root cause is the same wrong-field class as the earlier session-id / hookdeck-scoping bugs: `subagent_stop.rs` read `input.extra["agent_type"]`, but Claude Code sends `agent_type` and `agent_id` as **top-level** SubagentStop fields (confirmed against code.claude.com/docs), which serde deserializes into the *typed* `HookInput::agent_type` / `HookInput::agent_id` — and a value captured by a named struct field is never *also* placed in the `#[serde(flatten)]` `extra` map, so that read was always empty. Extracted `resolve_agent_identity()` which reads the typed fields first (empty-string treated as absent), falls back to `extra` only for resilience against a future harness that relocates them, and defaults `agent_type` to `"unknown"` with `agent_id` staying `None`. Events now render `Agent "Explore" (agent-42) has finished.` and carry both `agent_type` and `agent_id` in `meta`. The session **routing** was already correct — `channel_events::emit` keys the event dir on the payload's real `session_id` and `concrete_session_id()` rejects synthetic ids (`unknown`/`default`/empty) specifically to prevent cross-session event mixing — so this was purely lost *identity*, not misrouting (audited + already covered by tests). 5 new `resolve_agent_identity` unit tests (typed read, default-unknown, typed-beats-extra, extra-fallback, empty-as-absent); 7/7 subagent_stop tests green.
- **Task snapshot now clears when the live list empties, normalizes baked-in decoration on write, and renders a status emoji** (2026-07-06). Three defects in the task-persistence layer, all surfacing as "sentinel isn't handling tasks/emojis right": **(1, the functional core) `task_persist` had no empty→truncate path.** `process()` early-returned when the session task dir was absent *or* the live list was empty, leaving a `tasks.json` written while the list was non-empty **frozen on disk forever** once the list emptied. That stale snapshot then drove `task_coverage_check` to nag about tasks that no longer existed (the persistent phantom "#2"), rendered ghost rows in CLAUDE.md's Active Tasks table, and got re-injected by `task_rehydrate` on the next SessionStart. Added `truncate_persistent_tasks()`: on an empty/absent live list it writes `tasks.json = []`, resets `meta.json` to count 0, and clears the `tasks.md` marker block (bypassing the shrink guard, since going to zero here is intentional) — a no-op when there is no prior snapshot to clear. Only reached with a valid non-empty `session_id`, so a missing session id is still treated as a durability gap (never truncates). **(2) baked-in decoration is normalized on write.** Some tasks were stored with status/priority glyphs jammed into the subject STRING (e.g. `"🔄 🔴 1 [P0] — Fix memory-capture dual-judge gate"`) where the glyph *disagreed* with the `status` field (glyph = 🔄 in-progress, field = `pending`). `read_tasks` now runs each task through `normalize_task`: strips the leading decoration from the subject, and backfills `status`/`metadata.priority` from the glyph **only when the field is blank** — the explicit field is always authoritative. **(3) the Status column renders an emoji.** `render_tasks_section` printed the bare status word; it now renders `status_emoji(status)` (`🔄 in_progress`, `⏳ pending`, `✅ completed`, `🚫 blocked`, `❌ cancelled`), matching the codebase's existing status-glyph convention (`linear_inbound_sync::DesiredStatus::emoji`); an unknown status falls back to the bare word. 8 new tests (4 normalize + 2 truncate + 1 status_emoji + 1 strip); sentinel-application 1882/1882 green.
- **Active Tasks table now renders the SESSION's tasks, not another project's, and drops emoji baked into subjects** (2026-07-05). Two bugs in the CLAUDE.md task-table regeneration: (B, correctness) `regenerate_global_claude_md` keyed the per-project task snapshot off the hook PROCESS's `std::env::current_dir()`, which is not reliably the session's working directory — so a task mutation from one session could render a *different* project's tasks into the single global `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md` (cross-session task bleed; observed a "Install HoloDesktop CLI" task surfacing as #2 in an unrelated session). Added `regenerate_global_claude_md_for(cwd)` and made the `task_created` / `task_completed` hooks pass the SESSION's `input.cwd` so each session's table reflects its own tasks (mirrors the project_scope_tracker per-session-cwd approach; the no-arg form is retained for the CLI regeneration path). (A, cosmetic) task subjects sometimes carry status/priority decoration baked into the subject STRING by the caller (e.g. `"🔄 🔴 1 [P0] — Fix…"`), redundant with the Status/Priority columns; the renderer now strips a leading run of status/priority emoji (🔄 ⏳ ✅ ❌ 🔴 🟠 🟡 🟢), a `[P0]`..`[P3]` token, a bare numeric rank, and a `—`/`-`/`:` separator via `strip_status_priority_prefix` (idempotent; a clean subject and a mid-string emoji are untouched). Test covers both bugs.

### Added
- **`tab_title` hook — label each terminal tab with `claude <session-id>`** (2026-07-07). Windows Terminal (and any VT/OSC-capable terminal) shows nothing useful in the tab when running under the handler, because the handler sets `CLAUDE_CODE_DISABLE_TERMINAL_TITLE=1` to suppress Claude Code's own activity-summary title — leaving tabs indistinguishable ("PowerShell") across 6+ concurrent sessions. New side-effect-only hook writes the OSC-0 sequence `ESC ] 0 ; claude <session-id> BEL` **directly to `CONOUT$`** (Windows) / `/dev/tty` (unix), bypassing the hook stdout that Claude Code captures for context injection — so the bytes actually reach the terminal and move the tab title, while the hook returns a no-op `HookOutput` (nothing injected into the model). The session id is resolved from the hook payload's `session_id`, falling back to the `CLAUDE_CODE_SESSION_ID` env var Claude Code exports; placeholder ids (`unknown`/`none`/empty) are rejected, and control bytes in the id are stripped so a crafted id can't smuggle an early terminator. **Why a hook, not the handler:** the handler owns the spawn site but only knows the UUID for a `--resume` — a *fresh* session's UUID is generated by Claude Code after start, and `SessionStart` is the first lifecycle point where it's known for both cases. Wired on `SessionStart` (paints ASAP) **and** `UserPromptSubmit` (re-asserts every turn so the title snaps back after the PowerShell prompt or a launched program overwrites it). Opt out with `SENTINEL_NO_TAB_TITLE=1`. Registered in `HOOK_NAMES` + `hooks.toml` (both events); 9 unit tests (id resolution/precedence/fallback, placeholder + opt-out rejection, OSC framing, control-byte sanitization).
- **`project_scope_tracker` PostToolUse hook — publish the session's live working project for hookdeck channel scoping** (2026-07-05): sessions are launched from the home dir (`c` from `~`) and the working project is chosen — and changed — *during* the session, so the hookdeck MCP child (spawned once at session start with a fixed environment) cannot know which repo the session is working on. It fell back to the launch-cwd basename (`garys`), which matches no webhook, so GitHub events were dropped and sibling home sessions bled into each other. The new hook resolves, on every Bash/Edit/Write/Read, the git-repo-root of whatever the tool just touched and writes the repo name to `~/.vulcan/hookdeck/session-<key>.project` (keyed on the `CLAUDE_CONFIG_DIR` basename — the same session key vulcan-hookdeck's `resolve_session_key` uses, so producer and consumer agree with no handler involvement). Stickiness is *latest wins* — scope follows the most recent repo touched and re-scopes on a switch; a non-repo path (the home dir) clears the file so the session is unscoped and the router fails open (receives everything) until real work starts. The `vulcan-hookdeck` `resolve_cwd_project` (SDK, shipped alongside) reads this file first. Net: each session automatically receives the webhooks for the repo it's actually working in — no cross-session bleed, no silent drops. Observational (always allows; a write failure never blocks a turn). 6 tests; registered in `HOOK_NAMES` + the PostToolUse dispatch.
- **MCP registration guardian — detect / snapshot / heal for `~/.claude.json`** (2026-07-04): the `mcpServers` block has been lost before (Jun 17-18 corruption/rebuild) and the loss was invisible because every failure mode was coerced to a `0` count. Sentinel now owns the full control loop (marketplace stays declarative-only; the handler is zero-touch). (1) **Detect** — `scanner::mcp_registry_state()` classifies the live registry as `Missing` / `Unreadable` / `Tampered` (a `_mcpServers_disabled` stash marker or non-object block) / `Count(n)`; `count_mcp_servers()` is now a display-only wrapper over it. (2) **Tripwire** — `session_init` prints a loud `[MCP REGISTRATION MISSING]` startup-banner line and emits an `mcp_registration_missing` channel event when the state is compromised or `Count(0)` while `*-mcp-rust` repos exist on disk. (3) **Snapshot** — a healthy registry (>= 10 entries) gets a dated known-good copy under `~/.claude/sentinel/state/mcp-registry/registry-YYYYMMDD.json` (one/day, newest 14 kept). (4) **Heal** — on `Missing`/`Tampered`/empty-with-repos, the new `mcp_guardian` module rebuilds the block from the marketplace clone's `marketplace.json` `mcp[]` declaration (REGISTRY CONTRACT v1: `name`/`command`/`args`/`transport`/`env`, with `$doppler:<project>/<config>/<SECRET>` env refs resolved at heal time via `doppler-rs`→`doppler`, unresolved refs omitted-with-warning — degraded beats absent), skipping names tombstoned by the declaration's `retired` array plus the built-in `agents`/`skills` tombstones, falling back to the newest state snapshot when the declaration is absent/invalid; the merge preserves every other key (filesystem-atomic tmp+rename; an fs2 sidecar lock serializes sentinel-vs-sentinel heals only — Claude Code, the file's other writer, does not take that lock, so a read→write TOCTOU window vs the host remains and resolves last-writer-wins, accepted because heals fire only on `Missing`/`Tampered`/`Count(0)` states where the host isn't actively maintaining the block) and lands in both the global `~/.claude.json` and `$CLAUDE_CONFIG_DIR/.claude.json`; the standing `/reload-plugins` initialUserMessage autoheal then reconnects the restored servers in-session. `Unreadable` is deliberately alert-only (merging over unparseable JSON would clobber unknown state). See `docs/mcp-registration-guardian.md`. 15 new guardian tests + registry-state/banner tests; sentinel-application 1757/1757 green.

### Changed
- **CLAUDE.md template: fix stale sentinel dev-workflow path** (2026-06-15): the generated CLAUDE.md "Dev workflow" block in `generate_claude_md` (`session_init.rs`) pointed at `~/repos/claude-systems/sentinel`, a path that does not exist on any current machine — the sentinel source lives at `~/Documents/GitHub/sentinel`. The stale path shipped into every regenerated CLAUDE.md on both the Mac and Windows installs. Now corrected to `~/Documents/GitHub/sentinel` so the `cd … && cargo build --release -p sentinel && sentinel stage` instructions actually resolve. Surfaced while reconciling the Mac install after the marketplace/sentinel migration to the `legatus-ai` org.
- **Domain ports now use bespoke error enums — `anyhow` dropped from `sentinel-domain`** (2026-06-13): the DDD/hexagonal audit scored sentinel 94/A with the one ding being `anyhow::Result` on the domain port traits (an opaque "any error" contract leaking into the domain). All 22 `anyhow::Result` signatures across the 6 IO-bearing ports (`FileSystemPort`, `GitStatusPort`, `ProcessPort`, `LlmPort`, `VectorStorePort`, `MemoryMcpPort`) now return purpose-built domain errors defined in the new `port_errors` module (`FileSystemError`, `GitError`, …) — manual `Display` + `std::error::Error` + `From<io::Error>`, no `thiserror`, generated by a small `port_error!` macro mirroring the existing `AuditorError`. Infra adapters map their internal errors via `<Error>::backend(e)`; application callers using `?` are unaffected (`anyhow::Error: From<E: Error>` still absorbs them). **`anyhow` is no longer a dependency of `sentinel-domain`** — the domain crate carries zero error-framework coupling. 573 domain + 1568 application tests green, clippy clean (no new warnings). Takes the audit to ~100/A+.
- **`memory_inject` reranks the per-turn injected atoms** (2026-06-12). The hook now passes `rerank: true` to `memory_search`, so the memories surfaced into context on every `UserPromptSubmit` are ordered by the LLM reranker (better semantic ordering than raw embedding score) rather than noop. Safe in the hot path: the reranker degrades to base embedding order on any failure, and the call is already wrapped in the dedicated 10s budget that was sized with rerank in mind, so a slow/failed rerank never blocks the turn — it falls back to embedding order. One-line args insert; `StubMemoryMcp` ignores args so existing inject tests are unaffected (19/19 pass).
- **`memory_inject` now applies a relevance floor — no more low-score noise** (2026-06-12). The hook requested `top_k=8` from `memory_search` and injected all 8 verbatim with no quality bar, so a vague or conversational prompt dumped a tail of 0.03–0.06 atoms that "matched" only because something had to fill the k slots — clutter the model scrolls past, and noise in the feedback loop. Now hits below a relevance floor (default **0.10**, tunable at runtime via `MEMORY_INJECT_MIN_SCORE` — `0` restores inject-everything) are dropped before rendering; if nothing clears the floor, nothing is injected (a weak recall is the same signal as no recall). Sharp targeted queries (0.5–0.8 hits) are unaffected. Pure `apply_relevance_floor` helper + `min_inject_score` env resolver, 4 new unit tests.

### Added
- **`tool_usage_gate` is now operator-configurable — `sequential_thinking_check` knob (Check 1 only).** New shipped config `config/tool-usage-gate-defaults.toml` (compiled in via `include_str!`) with operator override at `~/.claude/sentinel/config/tool-usage-gate.toml`, following the exact `memory_provision` config pattern (wholesale replacement; parse failure fails closed to enforcement). Setting `sequential_thinking_check = false` skips ONLY the sequential-thinking transcript precondition; the task-list, plan-mode, and `in_progress`-task checks are unaffected. No env vars and no signature changes — config is read through the `FileSystemPort` inside `evaluate()`. Three new tests: override skips Check 1 when the other checks pass; override does NOT bypass the task checks; corrupt override fails closed.
- **`memory_provision` hook — register the memory MCP + broker the Qdrant credential via Doppler at SessionStart.** Fills the provisioning gap for the existing memory hooks (`memory_inject`/`memory_turn_capture`/…), which silently no-op without the `memory` MCP registered and a Qdrant credential present. The hook: (1) verifies the `memory`/`memory-mcp` binaries (warns with install guidance — never installs); (2) verifies `~/.qdrant/config.json` and, when missing/invalid/expired (JWT `exp` checked), fetches `QDRANT_URL`+`QDRANT_API_KEY` from Doppler (`legatus/dev` by default; configurable) and writes it atomically (+`.bak`) — no Doppler access surfaces a clear console error; (3) idempotently registers the `memory` MCP server in `~/.claude.json`. `require_remote` (default true): memory does not activate without a working remote credential (registration withheld). Distributes a revocable Doppler token instead of a raw shared Qdrant JWT; interim until per-user JWT minting. Config: `config/memory-provision-defaults.toml`.
- **Telemetry R2 lake pipeline + read-side report (LEG-258/259/260/261)** (2026-06-22). `sentinel telemetry collect|ship|report`: `collect` spools the per-harness hook-invocation ledgers (zstd NDJSON, `(dev,inode)+offset` checkpointed); `ship` drains them to the Cloudflare R2 lake (bearer ingest Worker, `R2_*` SigV4 fallback, idempotent content-hash keys); `report` reads the lake back and aggregates fleet activity, with **last updated** and **unique clients reporting in** as the headline metrics. Adds a backward-compatible `client_id` ledger field (additive `serde(default)` like `source_harness`; resolved `SENTINEL_CLIENT_ID` env -> `paths::try_claude_dir()/sentinel/client-id` -> hashed `/etc/machine-id`) so per-machine clients are countable; rows predating it use a labeled session estimate. New `telemetry::{ledger,spool,checkpoint,ship,sigv4,snapshot,lake,report}` — `lake` is the only IO (`ListObjectsV2` + `GET`), `report`'s aggregate/render are IO-free for a future read-side service. `--window 24h|7d|30d --harness --format html|json|table` (HTML default). Validated end-to-end against the live dev lake (two distinct client ids -> unique clients = 2 read back from R2).
- **Subscription-first provider ladder for BOTH high-stakes dual judges** (2026-06-13): the prod blast-radius **auditor** *and* the false-done **completion judge** now prefer **subscription-backed CLIs** over metered OpenRouter, per leg — Anthropic via `claude -p --append-system-prompt` (Claude Code subscription), OpenAI via `codex exec --output-last-message` (Codex subscription) — falling back to OpenRouter (`opus-4.8` / `gpt-5.5-pro`) only when the CLI isn't on `PATH`. New `resolve_cli` (cached PATH probe) + `build_claude_cli_prompt_fn` / `build_codex_cli_prompt_fn` (return `Some` only when the binary exists — **detect-and-use, never auto-installs**). The **auditor** routes per vendor via `RigAuditor::resolve_leg`; the **completion judge** routes via `resolve_judge_transport` in `rig_judge.rs`, but only for the `DualFrontier` frontier pair (`anthropic/claude-opus-*` → claude-cli, `openai/*` → codex-cli) — Sonnet/Kimi stay on OpenRouter (model identity matters; a bare `claude -p` isn't guaranteed to be Sonnet, Kimi has no CLI). Opt out with `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_NO_SUBSCRIPTION=1`. **Zero regression** — no subscription CLI present → exactly today's OpenRouter dual. Test isolation: `with_prompt_fn` pins `force_configured_prompt_fn=true` so stub tests never shell out to a real `claude`/`codex`. 43/43 auditor + 36/36 scorer-runtime + 7/7 rig_judge + 31/31 judge_service green, clippy clean, both legs live-verified returning clean JSON verdicts. **Cost:** $0 per-token when the subscription CLIs are present vs OpenRouter's $15/$75 + $30/$180. The `codex exec` leg feeds its prompt on **stdin** (codex ignores a positional prompt once `--output-schema` is set) and the completion-judge leg passes `--output-schema` with the `JudgeVerdict` shape, so the OpenAI judge returns **guaranteed-valid JSON** (no parse-failure path). Captured gotcha: OpenAI structured-output requires `required` to list *every* property (optional ⇒ nullable type + still required) — a guard test enforces it.
- **Native loop/cron/goal/Workflow guidance + orchestration nudges** (2026-06-12): aligned Sentinel with how Claude Code's four native async primitives actually compose (verified against code.claude.com/docs). (1) Removed the redundant custom `~/.claude/skills/loop` skill — native `/loop` is a superset (`/loop 5m <prompt>` fixed interval, `/loop <prompt>` self-paced, bare `/loop` → maintenance prompt or `loop.md`, `/loop 20m /cmd`) and the custom one only shadowed it. (2) Rewrote the `session_init` CLAUDE.md template: a four-primitive table (`/loop` poll · `CronCreate`/`/schedule` time-trigger · `/goal` work-till-condition · `Workflow` background fan-out) and **THE composition rule** mirroring Anthropic's own native fix (changelog v2.1.141/147) — don't `/loop` or short-cron a Workflow/background task that already notifies on completion; prefer the notification, Channels, or Monitor. (3) Extended the `orchestration_nudge` hook with two advisory signals: `workflow_orchestration_signal` (large fan-out → suggest `Workflow` over `/loop`-driven subagents) and `redundant_poll_signal` (about to poll a self-notifying task → suggest the notification/Channels/Monitor/`/goal`), both requiring strong evidence so legitimate external-service polling doesn't trip. 10/10 hook tests, clippy clean.
- **Cross-vendor dual-frontier judge (Opus 4.8 + GPT-5.5)** (2026-06-12): a new `JudgeTrustTier::DualFrontier` runs the two strongest closed frontier models, one per vendor, so an Anthropic blind spot is caught by OpenAI and vice versa. Wired into the two highest-stakes judgments: (1) the **prod blast-radius auditor** — `AuditorPort::score_dual` (default delegates to `score`, overridden by the OpenRouter `RigAuditor`) scores Irreversible/Catastrophic actions with both models and reconciles conservatively (block if either dissents; an inconclusive single-model pass is downgraded to block — a wrong "safe" = data loss); and (2) the **completion / false-done verdict** (opt-in via `dual: true` on `submit_phase_complete`) — `proof_engine` folds `evaluate_multi(DualFrontier)` into one verdict (`sufficient` = AND across judges, confidence = floor), leaving the proof-chain logic byte-for-byte unchanged. Both fail safe: two frontier models must agree to pass.
- **Firefly QA workflow redesign live in Linear** (2026-06-12): applied Pedro's proposal across FPCRM/FPFIELD/FPROUTE — new states Decomposition, QA Blocked, Backend Verify (No UI); renamed QA Testing → QA Testing (UI); added a Surface label group (UI / No-UI). Additive + reversible. Sentinel's PM gate/audit now treat any "…Blocked" state (incl. QA Blocked) as a do-not-start signal.
- **PM gate pickup rules: blocked, milestone, cherry-pick** (2026-06-12): the `linear_pm_gate` PreToolUse hook now refuses to start a ticket that is (a) **blocked** — by an open blocked-by relation, a Blocked state, or a blocked/blocker label; (b) **milestone-less** when its project uses milestones (untracked work; projects without milestones are exempt); or (c) a **cherry-pick** — a lower-priority ticket while a higher-priority, startable ticket waits in the same person's queue. Each fails open on anything it can't resolve. The `linear-audit` report + cron gained matching `blocked_open` and `no_milestone_open` flags.
- **Real-time PM gate** (2026-06-12): the gate now resolves the ticket being started via a live single-issue Linear fetch at pickup (new `LinearLookupPort` + a blocking-reqwest `LinearLookup` adapter, 2.5s timeout, `SENTINEL_LINEAR_TOKEN`), so its decision reflects this-instant state — falling back to the on-disk cache when the live port is absent or the call fails. Real-time when it can be, never bricked when it can't.
- **Auto-severity dual-judge** (2026-06-12): `sentinel severity scan [--apply]` judges each ticket's priority (1-4) from title+description using BOTH Opus 4.8 and GPT-5.5 via OpenRouter, reconciling (more-urgent wins). Shadow by default; `--apply` SETs priority on untriaged tickets and records suggestions (never auto-overrides a human). CLI + `sentinel__severity_scan` MCP tool (shadow-only).

### Changed
- **Judge/LLM stack bumped Opus 4.7 → 4.8** (2026-06-12): the live model routing across judge.rs, openrouter_llm.rs, dry_run_auditor (`DEFAULT_OPENROUTER_MODEL`), eval_scorer, and the capability routers now points at `anthropic/claude-opus-4.8` (verified OpenRouter slug). Historical token-log/pricing test fixtures left as-is.

### Fixed
- **`task_coverage_check` reminders debounced — no more identical warning on every Stop** (2026-07-02). The off-book warning (uncommitted changes, no `in_progress` task) re-fired verbatim on every single Stop while the condition persisted (observed: 8 consecutive turns), and the stale nudge fired on every stop once a task crossed the 3-stop threshold (`count >= 3`). Both are now fire-then-periodic: the off-book warning fires on the first off-book Stop, re-fires every 5th consecutive Stop while the condition persists (new `coverage-offbook-{session_id}` state marker, same fail-visible read/write contract as the existing coverage markers), and resets the moment the condition clears so a NEW episode warns immediately; the stale nudge fires at exact multiples of the threshold (stops 3, 6, 9, ...) instead of every stop past it. Reminder-only contract unchanged. 3 new/extended tests (debounce window, episode reset, periodic stale).
- **`memory_provision` hardening — credential re-validation, `require_remote` on re-runs, 0600 perms, Doppler timeout, atomic-write fixes** (2026-07-01). Seven review findings closed in the SessionStart provisioning hook: (1) a credential fetched from Doppler is now re-assessed (JWT `exp` etc.) before being written — an expired/invalid secret handed back by Doppler is refused with a distinct error instead of minting a `credential_ok` marker for a dead credential; (2) the `require_remote` withhold now also **removes** a previously registered `memory` MCP entry from `~/.claude.json` (same backup + atomic-write + no-clobber machinery), so the guarantee holds on re-runs, not just first registration; (3) credential material lands owner-only — `~/.qdrant/config.json`, its `.bak`, the transient temp sibling, and `~/.claude.json.bak` are written 0600 on unix via a new opt-in `FileSystemPort::write_private` (created with `OpenOptionsExt::mode(0o600)`, no world-readable window); (4) the `doppler secrets get` network call is bounded by a new `ProcessPort::run_with_timeout` (spawn + `try_wait` poll + kill, `ProcessError::Timeout`; default 10s, configurable via `doppler_timeout_secs` in `memory-provision-defaults.toml`) — timeout is treated as a fetch failure (withhold path), and the hook's `hooks.toml` entry is corrected to `has_api_call = true`; (5) the `~/.claude.json` atomic write uses a per-process-unique temp name (`.tmp.<pid>`) and a failed rename now cleans up the temp and propagates loudly instead of silently degrading to a non-atomic write (last-writer-wins across processes, documented); (6) registration additionally requires the engine binaries to be present (a PATH-resolved command that doesn't exist would give Claude Code a permanently failing MCP server), and `find_binary` now also probes `$PATH` directories; (7) `b64url_decode` accepts (strips) trailing `=` padding, so padded JWTs are expiry-assessable instead of Valid-forever. Orchestration test coverage added on the existing stub pattern: fetch success/failure/expired-token/timeout, end-to-end withhold-with-removal, register-skipped-when-binaries-absent, rename-failure propagation (memory_provision 16 → 29 tests). **Round 2 (adversarial review of PR #17, same day):** (a) the withhold path only removes an entry that is *recognizably sentinel-managed* (new pure `is_sentinel_managed_entry`: strict shape match against exactly what `merge_memory_server` writes — a user-owned custom `memory` entry is left untouched with a warn, `RemoveOutcome::ForeignEntry`); (b) non-private atomic rewrites of `~/.claude.json` preserve the destination's existing mode across the temp+rename (a user-tightened 0600 file is no longer silently loosened to umask 0644); (c) `write_private` tightens an EXISTING file to 0600 *before* truncating/writing the new secret into it (`mode()` only applies at creation — chmod-after-write left the fresh content world-readable during the write); (d) the binaries gate checks the EXACT launcher that will be registered (`memory-mcp-mirror` when a mirror is configured) and `find_binary` requires a regular file with an execute bit on unix (a plain data file no longer counts as installed); (e) on unix the timed-out child is started as its own process group (`CommandExt::process_group(0)`, safe — no `unsafe`/libc) and the deadline SIGKILLs the whole group, with drain threads detached instead of joined so an escaped descendant can't block past the deadline; the timeout message reports the exact configured `Duration` (no `as_secs` truncation of sub-second values) and the timing tests use CI-load-tolerant bounds (memory_provision 29 → 35 tests, process 3 → 4).
- **Test isolation: parallel-safe HOME/env mutation in MCP + decision-graph tests** (2026-06-22): the `mcp_handler` step-tools tests (20) and `decision_graph_store` config tests mutate process-global env (`HOME`/`USERPROFILE`, `SENTINEL_DECISION_GRAPH_*`) under a `Mutex` for isolation. Two parallel-execution defects: (a) on Windows `try_claude_dir()` fell through to `dirs::home_dir()`, which reads a CACHED `USERPROFILE` (SHGetKnownFolderPath) and does not honor a runtime-mutated value — so a temp-HOME test's graph write and its read could resolve to different dirs (`NotFound` flake); (b) when any such test panicked it POISONED the shared lock, cascading `PoisonError` to every other env-mutating test (1 real failure → 18+ reported). Fixed: `HomeGuard` now also pins `SENTINEL_CLAUDE_DIR` (read fresh+uncached by `try_claude_dir`, bypassing the `dirs` cache), and both env locks acquire poison-resiliently (`unwrap_or_else(|e| e.into_inner())`). sentinel-application now 1739/0 under default parallel `cargo test` (was 18 failing).
- **Gate hardening: never brick a session over unconfirmable state** (2026-06-19, builds on f27e7c0f): two PreToolUse gates could deadlock a session by demanding state it could not produce. (1) `task_decomposition_gate` now FAILS OPEN when the resolved session task dir is MISSING (`has_live_task_list` returns `None`, and `process()` blocks only on a present-but-empty `Some(false)`): the canonical `session_task_dir` resolver already tries both harness naming forms, so a still-missing dir is a store/gate desync we don't own — failing closed on it bricked every mutating tool with no fix path. The teeth (an agent skipping decomposition while the store is healthy) are preserved by the present-but-empty block. (2) `tool_usage_gate` only HARD-BLOCKS on missing sequential-thinking when a `sequential-thinking` MCP server is actually registered in `~/.claude.json` (new `sequential_thinking_mcp_registered()`, checks top-level + `projects.*` `mcpServers`); when it's absent the tool can't be called, so the gate warns and allows instead of demanding an uncallable tool. Decomp gate 27/27 + tool-usage gate tests green (incl. new fail-open + missing-dir cases).
- **`sentinel scan` MCP-server count is now sourced from the repo, not the live `~/.claude.json`** (2026-06-13): follow-on to the cwd-scoping fix below. `count_components` always read the MCP count from `~/.claude.json`'s `mcpServers`, so running `scan --sync-counts` inside a marketplace clone (which has no `~/.claude.json`) reported **0 MCP servers** and would have written `"0 MCP servers"` into the repo's own `marketplace.json`/README. Now `count_declared_mcp_servers()` reads the marketplace's *own* `marketplace.json` `mcp[]` array when present (the authoritative declaration of what the marketplace ships), falling back to the live `~/.claude.json` only when no marketplace declaration exists (e.g. scanning `~/.claude` directly). A clone now reports its declared count; `~/.claude` is unchanged. New `count_declared_mcp_servers()` + unit test covering the Some/None/no-mcp-key cases.
- **`sentinel scan` now operates on the repo it is invoked in, not always `~/.claude`** (2026-06-13): `scan --sync-counts` (and the other scan modes) resolved their root to `~/.claude/` whenever `--dir` was omitted, regardless of the working directory. Run from a marketplace *clone* it still counted `~/.claude/skills` (stale live state) and offered to rewrite ~49 files under `~/.claude` — plugin caches, the plugin-marketplace clone, and **other sessions'** `session-env/*/CLAUDE.md` — i.e. wrong blast radius and a stale count source (live 77 vs repo 79). The default now auto-detects the marketplace root by walking up from the cwd for a marker (`.claude-plugin/marketplace.json`, or a root `marketplace.json` beside a `skills/` dir), falling back to `~/.claude/` only when no marker is found. Running inside a repo clone now syncs *that* repo; bare invocation elsewhere is unchanged. The `session_init` hook is unaffected (it counts via `scanner::count_subdirs`, not `scan_cmd`). New `detect_marketplace_root()` helper in `scan_cmd.rs`.
- **Subscription codex leg was broken on Windows (os error 193)** (2026-06-13): `which_on_path` tried the extensionless name first, so on Windows it resolved npm's bare POSIX `#!/bin/sh` shim (installed next to the real `.cmd`) — which `CreateProcess` can't run (*"%1 is not a valid Win32 application"*). The codex subscription leg silently errored → fell back to OpenRouter, defeating the subscription-first win on this platform. Now tries only executable extensions (`.exe`/`.cmd`/`.bat`) on Windows and drops the bare candidate. Caught by a new opt-in live integration test (`tests/live_codex_schema.rs`, `#[ignore]`) that actually shells `codex exec --output-schema` and asserts a valid `JudgeVerdict` — the unit tests couldn't (they don't spawn the real CLI). Plus a Windows-only `which_on_path` regression unit test. 37/37 scorer-runtime green.
- **Dual auditor was secretly same-vendor — now a genuine cross-vendor pin** (2026-06-12): the prod blast-radius `score_dual` derived its primary leg from `self.model_id` (the capability router's single pick), but that router *excludes the acting vendor*, so it resolved to OpenAI — same vendor as the GPT-5.5-pro second leg. Live audits showed `dual:gpt-5.5 + openai/gpt-5.5-pro` (OpenAI judging itself), so the "cross-vendor" guarantee was hollow. Both legs are now pinned explicitly: `DUAL_PRIMARY_MODEL = anthropic/claude-opus-4.8`, `DUAL_SECOND_MODEL = openai/gpt-5.5-pro` (override via `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_MODEL` / `_MODEL_2`). Fable 5 was the intended Anthropic leg but is **suspended** — every OpenRouter provider 404s `anthropic/claude-fable-5` with *"Please use Opus 4.8"*, which would have made the auditor permanently inconclusive-block; verified callable by live chat-completion probe, not catalog presence. New `pinned_dual_pair_is_genuinely_cross_vendor` regression test; 40/40 `dry_run_auditor` tests pass.
- **OpenRouter scorer/auditor output tokens now bounded — fixes a latent gpt-5.5-pro 400** (2026-06-12): found while live-probing the freshly-pinned cross-vendor pair — `gpt-5.5-pro` 400s on `max_output_tokens < 16` ("integer below minimum value"). Two gaps closed: (1) the cross-vendor auditor's OpenRouter `prompt_fn` sent **no** `max_tokens`, so the reasoning-model leg ran unbounded (the stall the `openrouter_llm` path already warned about) — now capped at `OPENROUTER_SCORER_MAX_TOKENS = 2048` (verdict JSON + reasoning headroom); (2) `openrouter_llm` floored `max_tokens` at `1` — raised to `16` (OpenAI's documented minimum). Without these, a small/zero budget on the OpenAI leg would error every call and trip `block_for_inconclusive` — the same silent permanent-block the Fable-5 fix removed, via a different cause. Infra tests green (auditor 40, openrouter 10, scorer-runtime 32), clippy clean.
- **Task Decomposition Gate now ALWAYS fires** (2026-06-12): the gate failed *open* when task state was unreadable (no session id / home dir / read error), which let mutating work skip it intermittently. It now fails **closed** — the only allow path is a positively-confirmed live decomposed task list; both "readable, no decomposition" and "unreadable" block. The Read/Task*/Skill allowlist still passes so the fix path is never blocked.

### Added (earlier this session)
- **Linear PM-enforcement engine** (2026-06-12): codified the by-hand Linear PM analyses (proven against the Firefly Pro Beta initiative) into permanent, enforced infrastructure. `sentinel linear-audit scan [--velocity --weeks]` runs five checks — estimate hygiene (missing / non-Fibonacci), oversized-and-open (≥8pt decomposition candidates), QA-failed risk (points at risk), velocity burndown (on-track vs behind), and estimate-vs-actual cycle-time calibration (low-confidence flag when timestamps are batch-stamped). Surfaces as the CLI subcommand, a `sentinel__linear_pm_audit` MCP tool, a `linear_pm_gate` PreToolUse hook that **hard-blocks** starting a known undecomposed ≥8pt ticket (fails open on anything unresolved offline), and a `factory:linear-pm-audit` weekly cron. 9 unit tests; verified end-to-end against the live 40-issue initiative.
- **Linear dev-scorecard, code-audit, and health-score** (2026-06-12): three more report analyses turned into Sentinel features. `dev-scorecard` computes per-dev git-truth throughput + first-pass-QA rate + a composite 1-100 score, with an **attribution-divergence detector** that flags when git-authorship and Linear assignee-completions diverge (the merge-reassign regression that hid real developers). `linear-code-audit` is a false-done detector — Completed tickets with no code evidence (commits/files) get flagged. `linear-health` computes a composite 0-100 workspace-health score across hygiene / structure / data-quality / flow (scores the live Beta initiative 75/100, matching the by-hand 72/100). Each ships a CLI subcommand + MCP tool. 19 unit tests; clippy clean.
- **Per-model token cost with cached-vs-uncached split** (2026-06-12): `sentinel token-cost scan` prices the SEN-7 token aggregate at each model's published API rate (Opus 4.x / Sonnet 4.x / Haiku 4.x) and reports the cost WITH prompt caching vs WITHOUT (cache tokens re-priced as full input) plus the cache savings ($ and %). On the live tracked-ticket data: $4,061 cached vs $29,488 uncached = 86% saved. Unknown models fall to the Opus rate (never under-reports) and are counted separately. CLI + `sentinel__token_cost` MCP tool; 6 unit tests; clippy clean. (Complements `roi` — that's Claude-$-vs-human-$; this is metered-cost + cache efficiency.)
- **Four Linear PM tools exposed via the in-session MCP server** (2026-06-12): `sentinel-mcp-rust` now surfaces `linear_pm_audit`, `dev_scorecard`, `linear_code_audit`, and `linear_health` as MCP tools (calling the `sentinel-application` scan fns directly), so the analyses are callable from any Claude session, not just the CLI.

### Fixed
- **Linear enforcer no longer spams duplicate comments** (2026-06-11): `post_comment` (the single choke point for every enforcer comment — dev-ready, workflow-discipline, SLA, due-date) is now **idempotent** — it fetches the ticket's recent comments and skips posting when an identical body already exists. Previously the enforcer re-posted the same comment on every repeat `IssueChanged` event AND on every daemon restart (the in-memory per-issue debounce resets on restart, and re-seeds the poll cursor from a recent lower bound, so each restart re-swept the backlog). That piled up dozens of identical copies per ticket (1,366 duplicates across 56 firefly tickets in one session). Body-exact match, so genuinely-new content still posts. clippy clean; infra tests green.

### Fixed
- **Doppler `login`/`login_poll` no longer dead-lock the dry-run auditor** (2026-06-11): the browser-OAuth login flow's two tools weren't in `config/reversibility-defaults.toml`'s `[mcp.doppler]` block, so they fell to the conservative unknown-tool default (`Irreversible`) and got routed through the blast-radius auditor — which could hard-block with no reachable `hygiene_override`, dead-ending a benign operator-initiated auth step. Classified both as `TriviallyReversible` (they only return an auth URL / write a token to the local accounts.json — no remote secret read/write, no prod impact). Same deadlock class as the earlier MCP-default fixes. 11 reversibility tests green.

Separately, the legacy app was deleted as dead/superseded. 222 files removed; `cargo build --workspace` clean.

Dropped the `pub mod ccam`, the `/api` nest, and the `/api/ccam` auth-bypass clause in `daemon_cmd.rs`. The daemon still serves the JSON API (`/api/health`, proofs, workflows, hooks, memory, …). Builds clean; zero remaining references.

### Added
- **Linear enforcer — due-date gate, native SLA threshold, milestone check (Linear-API-docs audit)** (2026-06-10). A GraphQL-schema introspection of the Issue/Team types (vs. our coverage) surfaced enforceable fields we weren't using; built the high-value ones: (1) **due-date gate** — `is_overdue(dueDate, today)` flags an open (non-completed/canceled) ticket past its `dueDate` via comment (distinct from SLA); (2) **native SLA high-risk** — `evaluate_sla` now takes `slaHighRiskAt` and prefers Linear's own high-risk threshold over the 80%-elapsed heuristic, falling back to 80% only when Linear supplies none; (3) **project-milestone** — `extended_discipline()` flags a ticket in a project but with no `projectMilestone`. `TicketReadiness` + `fetch_readiness` gain `sla_high_risk_at`/`due_date`/`has_milestone`. 432 infra tests (+9); clippy clean. Confirmed NON-gaps from the audit: Linear has no `requireEstimate` team toggle (our L1/L2 estimate enforcement is value-add); `needs`/Asks-required-fields are a separate customer-request domain; audit-metadata fields aren't policy.

### Fixed
- **Memory-atom + `plans/*.md` writes no longer require Plan Mode** (2026-06-10). The four-check `tool_usage_gate` classified every `Write`/`Edit` as `ReversibleWithEffort`, forcing the full stack (sequential-thinking + task + **Plan Mode** + active task) even for a one-line memory note under `~/.claude/projects/*/memory/` — work that is local, recoverable, and explicitly not implementation. The gate's own docstring already claimed memory writes *should* be `TriviallyReversible`, but the `LayeredReversibilityClassifier` keyed only on tool *name* (and Bash *command*), never on the edited *path*, so the claim wasn't real. Fix: new **Layer 3.5 path-pattern** layer — `[[path.pattern]] match = "<regex>" class = "..."` in `reversibility-defaults.toml`, queried for `Write`/`Edit`/`NotebookEdit` before the Layer-1 builtin. The path is normalized to forward slashes so one pattern covers Windows + POSIX. Two shipped patterns classify the memory-atom store (`/.claude/projects/<key>/memory/`) and `plans/*.md` as `TriviallyReversible`; unmatched edits fall through to the unchanged RWE default (source-code edits still gated). 9 new tests (path layer + Windows-backslash normalization + NotebookEdit + shipped-defaults memory/plan/source cases); 74 reversibility tests pass, engine builds clean, clippy clean on the changed file.

### Added
- **Linear enforcer — blocked-relation integrity + portfolio coverage (closing the last discipline gaps)** (2026-06-10). (1) **Blocked-relation**: `has_live_blocker(issue)` scans `inverseRelations` for a `blocks` relation whose blocking issue isn't completed/canceled; `TicketReadiness.actively_blocked` feeds `extended_discipline()` so a *started but actively blocked* ticket is flagged (comment-only — work can't really proceed while blocked). (2) **Portfolio cron** extended to also flag: projects **not in any initiative** (roadmap-orphan), **orphan** started issues (no project), and **stale-in-Triage** (triage >3 days). 423 infra tests (+2 blocked-relation); session_init green; clippy clean. Pairs with the L3 PR-guard branch-name advisory (firefly-pro-crm) — together these close the "all of Linear" discipline surface at the right layer each (per-event / portfolio-cron / CI).

### Added
- **Linear enforcer — full ticket discipline ("all of Linear")** (2026-06-10). Extends the enforcer past the core Definition-of-Ready to the remaining per-ticket discipline. **Acceptance criteria** join the dev-ready set (heal-fillable): `has_acceptance_criteria(description)` (≥3 checklist `- [ ]` or numbered list items) → `missing()` → a started ticket lacking AC reverts/heals like a missing label. **Extended workflow discipline** (comment-only, never auto-filled/reverted — they need a human/planning call): `TicketReadiness::extended_discipline()` flags a *started* ticket with **no assignee**, **not in a cycle**, or **no project**, posting one consolidated "loose ends" comment. `fetch_readiness` now also pulls `description`/`assignee`/`cycle`/`project`. 421 infra tests (3 new: AC heuristic, extended-discipline started-only gating, AC-triggers-revert); clippy clean. (Deferred with reasons: blocked-relation graph integrity + initiative/roadmap/milestone alignment are project/relation-graph concerns better suited to the Tier-5 portfolio cron than the per-event enforcer; branch-name format is L3/CI's domain.)

- **Linear enforcer — SLA gates (Tier 3)** (2026-06-10). The enforcer now evaluates SLA health on every team-allowed issue event (comment-only, orthogonal to the dev-ready revert): **breached** (`slaBreachesAt` in the past) and **high-risk** (≥80% of the `slaStartedAt`→`slaBreachesAt` window elapsed) SLAs get an escalation comment, and **Urgent** tickets (priority 1) with no SLA clock running at all are flagged ("urgent ⇒ has-SLA"). Pure `evaluate_sla(priority, started, breaches, now)` → `SlaVerdict {Ok, HighRisk, Breached, UrgentNoSla}` (now injected, fully unit-tested); `TicketReadiness` + `fetch_readiness` extended with `priority`/`slaStartedAt`/`slaBreachesAt`. 418 infra tests; clippy clean.

### Added
- **Linear enforcer — actor-type differential (L2 agent-vs-human)** (2026-06-10). The enforcer now fetches each ticket's `botActor` + `integrationSourceType` and branches the Live path on authorship: **agent/integration-created** un-ready started tickets get the silent heal-first treatment (remediate → escalate gaps → revert last); **human-authored** tickets are *never silently rewritten* — the enforcer posts a "please complete before starting" comment listing the missing dev-ready fields and leaves the ticket for the operator. `TicketReadiness` gains `created_by_agent`; `parse_readiness` derives it (botActor present OR integrationSourceType set). 417 infra tests (incl. the actor-attribution test); clippy clean. (The Hookdeck-primary-feed half of this task is external webhook-gateway config — the poll+wss feeds already deliver the IssueChanged events the differential consumes.)

### Fixed
- **Stop/SubagentStop `additionalContext` was being silently stripped — found by the new E2E harness** (2026-06-10). The output-transform `match` in `hook_cmd.rs` keeps `hookSpecificOutput` only for an explicit native-support list of events; the `_ =>` arm sets it to `None`. `Stop` and `SubagentStop` were absent from that list, so every Stop-phase hook that injects context via `HookOutput::inject_context` — `claim_reality_check` (the false-done reality warning), `self_annealing`, the good-citizen + hygiene reminders — had its `additionalContext` **dropped at the output boundary** and never reached the agent. This was the true root of the F1 `{}` finding (compounded by two test-isolation red herrings: spawning the launcher instead of the engine binary, and camelCase input keys silently `#[serde(default)]`-dropping to None). Fixed by adding `HookEvent::Stop | HookEvent::SubagentStop` to the native-support arm; the F1 E2E test now asserts the reality-check context survives.

### Added
- **Black-box E2E hook harness (`crates/sentinel-cli/tests/e2e_hooks.rs`) + `SENTINEL_HOME` overridable root** (2026-06-10). A harness that spawns the real `sentinel-engine` and drives `sentinel hook --event <E>` exactly as Claude Code does (snake_case `HookInput` on stdin → `HookOutput` on stdout), covering the layer the ~90 inline unit suites don't: dispatch wiring, the stdin/stdout contract, caller-validation, session-id resolution, per-event serialization. 12 tests — every-event smoke (27 events), unknown-event rejection, missing-session-id no-op, offline fail-open, the blocking gates (`db_ops_gate`, `commit_message_validator`, `pr_merge_gate` ask), read-only/bare-allow, and the F1 reality-check scenario both ways. The harness immediately caught the Stop-strip bug above. Prerequisite: a single `SENTINEL_HOME` override (`sentinel_infrastructure::paths::home_root`) honored by `RealFileSystem::home_dir()` + `config_dir`/`state_dir`/`hmac_secret_dir`, so the engine's `~/.claude` access isolates to a tempdir on Windows too (`dirs::home_dir()` ignores HOME/USERPROFILE on Windows — it queries the OS profile API). Full workspace green; clippy clean on all new/changed files.

### Removed
- **Legatus AI / identity layer — full removal** (2026-06-10). The Legatus AI-Protocol "identity" integration (added later as a bolt-on: root commit `63f42c7`, the `sentinel-legatus` crate, + 39 follow-ups layered onto pre-existing hooks) is gone entirely — sentinel no longer talks to a Legatus AI/legatus-ai-daemon. Deleted: the `sentinel-legatus` crate (workspace member 8→7) + the 5 `Legatus AI-*` path-deps (legatus-ai-protocol/domain/storage/transport + legatus-ai-daemon); the application-layer identity clients (`legatus_client`, `praefectus_client`, `witness_verifier_adapter`); the identity hooks (`Legatus AI_inbox`, `upstream_block`, `catastrophic_escalation` — HOOK count 90→87); the `sentinel legatus` CLI subcommand (top-level subcommands 33→32) + all `--legatus-*` daemon flags + the daemon's legatus-hosting (`start_legatus_if_configured`, `legatus_routes`, the `/legatus/*` API routes, `LegatusOptions`/`WitnessVerifyMode`); the `legatus-ai-domain` `RoleBinding` `actor` field on `PhaseProof`/`StepProof` (so `sentinel-domain` no longer depends on `legatus-ai-domain`) + the `ProofEngine` Praefectus enrichment. **The pre-existing hooks were returned to their pre-Legatus AI form, not stubbed** — `git_hygiene`/`phase_gate`/`pre_commit_verification` deny/block locally via plain `HookOutput` (no upstream signal); `permission_denied`/`evidence_collector`/`execution_log`/`stop_failure` keep their real work, minus the legatus reporting. The daemon keeps the local API + the Linear enforcer. Full workspace builds clean (zero warnings); 1534 CLI + 585 domain + 414 app + drift/registration tests all green; CLAUDE.md counts reconciled.

### Fixed
- **Self-heal LLM path now completes end-to-end — three stacked fixes; FPCRM-596 healed live** (2026-06-10). The Tier B self-heal shipped but reverted every ticket because the `Codex` (`openai/gpt-5.5-pro`) proposal call never produced a usable plan. Root-caused to three independent bugs, each fixed: (1) **gzip decompression** — OpenRouter sends `Content-Encoding: gzip`; rig 0.38's own `reqwest 0.13` instance wasn't built with the `gzip` feature, so the body read failed with `error decoding response body` (manifested as a 45s "hang"). Fixed by declaring `reqwest 0.13` with `gzip`/`brotli`/`deflate` in `sentinel-infrastructure` so Cargo unifies the decompression feature onto rig's instance. (2) **`max_tokens` dropped** — rig 0.38's OpenRouter request struct has no `max_tokens` field, so the reasoning model ran unbounded; now injected via `additional_params` (which rig `#[serde(flatten)]`s into the body) + `temperature(0)`. (3) **parser dropped `type_label`** — `parse_plan`'s hand-rolled brace-counter terminated the JSON object early when an `acceptance_criteria` string contained `{`/`}` (e.g. a `${VAR}` snippet), silently losing fields; replaced with serde's streaming `Deserializer` (string-aware). rig bumped 0.35 → 0.38.2 (latest). **Live-proven**: FPCRM-596 moved to In Progress missing a Type label → enforcer inferred `Bug`, applied the label, ticket stayed In Progress (no revert). New `parse_plan_handles_braces_inside_string_values` regression test; 414 infra tests green; clippy clean.

### Removed
- **Glass-break emergency-override subsystem (full removal)** (2026-06-09). Removed sentinel's "bypass all enforcement" escape hatch in its entirety, per operator decision. Deleted: the `sentinel break` CLI (`break_cmd.rs`, 712 lines — the anti-AI TTY challenge + signed-token override), the `glass_break_gate` helper hook (`active_glass_break()`), the `SessionState.glass_break` field plus `GlassBreak`/`BreakToolUse` structs and `is_break_active()` / `clear_expired_break()` methods, the `check_glass_break_override()` file-token early-returns in `hook_cmd.rs` (both the supervisor and inline paths) and the dialog/token machinery, and `glass-break-spec.md`. Stripped the per-gate suppression short-circuits from `git_hygiene`, `pre_commit_verification`, `verification_gate`, `phase_gate`, `step_gate`, and the `glass_break_active` skip from `step_judge`. Hook registry 91→90 (deregistered from `mod.rs`/`HOOK_NAMES`; `hook_registration_completeness` + `claude_md_count_drift` updated). **Consequence:** there is no longer a built-in audited override if a gate wedges a session — enforcement is now unconditional. Operator-armed source-edit (`SENTINEL_ALLOW_INFRA_EDITS`) and the prod-override grant remain; those are unaffected.

### Docs
- **Work-assurance positioning + competitive reframe** (2026-06-09). New `docs/work-assurance-positioning.md` reframes sentinel's primary category from "federated agent gateway with cryptographic execution proofs" (CISO/attestation lineage) to **AI work-assurance / agent correctness verification** (engineering-leader / CI-eval lineage) — the proof chain is the audit substrate, not the value proposition. Backed by two adversarially-verified market sweeps: the fusion (judge-gated phase advancement + ground-truth false-done reopen + proof-of-work chain, vendor-neutral over coding agents) is white space as of 2026-06; of 12 strongest "direct" candidates, 1 verified-direct (Praetorian — unproductized whitepaper). Cross-reference note added at the top of `competitive-intelligence.md`; §7 documents the four Praetorian mechanics absorbed (all shipped below) and where sentinel stays ahead (proof chain + ground-truth false-done vs. Praetorian's gameable state-file trust). README counts corrected (27→~90 hooks, 5→7 crates).

### Added
- **Praetorian-inspired work-assurance hardening — 4 features** (2026-06-09). Absorbed the four execution mechanics from Praetorian's "Deterministic AI Orchestration" (the lone verified architectural twin), each built in an isolated worktree, test-green + clippy-clean: (1) **completion-promise + ground-truth verify** — `task_completed.rs` matches exact terminal strings (ALL_TESTS_PASSING / IMPLEMENTATION_COMPLETE / …) and treats a promise with no corroborating commit/PR as a hard mismatch reopened by `claim_reality_check`; (2) **output-similarity loop detector** — `step_anomaly.rs` 10th dimension `OutputSimilarity` (line-Jaccard ≥0.90 over the last 3 runs of a step = stuck loop), plus **layered redundant enforcement** running the false-done sweep on `SubagentStop` as well as `Stop`; (3) **role-dyad serialization** — `workflow.rs` `RoleDyad`/`DyadVerdicts`: a phase with `required_dyad` cannot complete until a *separate* reviewer PASS and/or tester tests_passed are recorded (the implementer cannot self-approve), applied to `review` + `qa-handoff`; (4) **self-annealing meta-agent** — new `self_annealing.rs` Stop hook reads the `failed_submissions` forensic record and, on the Nth gate failure, emits a `[Self-Annealing]` remediation (always) and, when operator-armed via `SENTINEL_ALLOW_SELF_ANNEAL=1`, appends a hard-constraint stanza to the diagnosed skill and opens a PR — gated by a default-deny predicate that never touches phase files / `~/.claude/sentinel` / `settings.json` / crates / the engine even when armed (composes with the Attack #201 guard), PR-only, never direct-to-main. Hook count 90→91. 24 new unit tests across the four; domain 589 / app 1617 / CLI 173 / graph 15 / infra 405 green.
- **`remediation` — Tier B self-heal: the enforcer as assistant, not bouncer** (2026-06-09). Flips the Live default from "revert an un-ready started ticket" to "**heal it in place**." When a started ticket is caught below the Definition-of-Ready, the enforcer auto-fills every gap it can confidently infer — Type/Area labels (mapped from a closed `LabelCatalog` so the model can't invent ids), estimate, priority, acceptance criteria — via an adversarial `Codex` proposal (`openai/gpt-5.5-pro` through the `OpenRouter` `LlmPort`), so the ticket reaches dev-ready and **stays in progress**. A checkpointed `langgraph-core` `StateGraph` (`classify → verify → clear | escalate | revert`) routes on the POST-heal state: fully healed → **Clear** (+ auto-remediated comment); partial (gaps need human judgment) → **Escalate** (comment listing exactly what a human must set, ticket stays in progress); nothing fillable → **Revert** (last resort). `parse_plan` is conservative — unparseable/out-of-range → escalate, never mis-fill. `run_enforcer`'s Live path is rewired remediate-first (fetch readiness → propose → apply → re-fetch → graph decides) with `fetch_label_catalog`/`fetch_ticket_text`/`post_comment` helpers; degrades to readiness-only revert when no LLM/graph. 8 `remediation` unit tests; 413 infra tests green; clippy clean. The "heal toward the 95-score, ask only the gaps, revert last" model.
- **`linear_enforcer` poll-source fallback — the reliable realtime feed (resolves the wss 4002)** (2026-06-09). Investigating legatus-desktop (the reference impl) revealed the wss `subscribe` 4002 ("need to authenticate") is *expected* Linear behavior for a personal API key — the same key authenticates REST + the `connection_init` ack, but the subscribe op is refused. legatus handles it by falling back to REST polling (`LinearPollActor`, "bump cadence when the WS auth is rejected"); our spine had copied only the wss client and omitted that fallback. This adds it: `run_poll_source` polls `issues(filter:{updatedAt:{gte:cursor}, state:{type:{in:[started]}}})` every 30s, advances a chronological cursor (RFC3339 strings sort correctly → string-max = timestamp-max), and feeds the SAME `IssueChanged` mpsc the wss uses — so the entire `run_enforcer` pipeline (debounce, team filter, shadow/live, escalation graph) is unchanged. Both feeds run into one channel: wss is the optimization, poll is the reliable backstop. Needs no wss/webhooks/OAuth — just the PAT (verified). `run_enforcer` spawns both; cursor seeds from `SENTINEL_LINEAR_POLL_SINCE` or a recent default. **Live shadow E2E verified**: temporarily nulling a started ticket's estimate produced `[SHADOW] WOULD revert FPFIELD-77 missing=estimate` on the next poll round (with correct cursor advancement: count=34 → count=1), zero mutations, ticket restored. Unblocks arm-live. 3 unit tests (filter shape, cursor picks-newest, cursor keeps-prev); 405 infra tests green; clippy clean.
- **`reconciliation_graph` — Tier D truth-audit (dead-code catcher)** (2026-06-09). Treats every *Completed* Linear ticket as a CLAIM ("shipped + live") and verifies it against fresh `origin/main` via a checkpointed `langgraph-core` `StateGraph` (`classify → judge → flag | clear`). Encodes the FPROUTE-14 lesson as a first-class verdict taxonomy — `Shipped` (code exists AND has a production caller), `DeadCode` (merged + compiles + tested, but no production caller), `Reverted` (gone from main), `Unverifiable` (infra/secret/external) — so a merged-but-dead feature can't masquerade as shipped. The `judge` is an adversarial `Codex` pass (`openai/gpt-5.5-pro` via the `OpenRouter` `LlmPort`) prompted to demand a real CALLER, not just a definition, and to answer `UNVERIFIABLE` (never guess `SHIPPED`) on inconclusive evidence; the parser maps anything unrecognized to `Unverifiable` so a wrongful flag never fires. `reconcile_ticket` orchestrates judge→graph; the caller posts the evidence comment + demotes out of Completed when the decision is `Flag`. Designed to run on a sentinel cron (audits shipped history; not a real-time gate) and reuses the Tier B graph/judge plumbing. 7 unit tests (verdict lie-classification, all parser forms incl. garbage→Unverifiable, the caller-distinction prompt, graph routing for DeadCode/Reverted→Flag and Shipped/Unverifiable→Clear). 402 infra tests green; clippy clean. Completes the factory's truth-audit tier.
- **`enforcement_graph` — Tier B LangGraph escalation layer (strict + adversarially-verified)** (2026-06-09). The decision brain on top of the Tier B spine: a checkpointed `langgraph-core` (LangGraph Rust) `StateGraph` — `classify → judge → revert | clear` — that decides whether an un-ready *started* ticket gets reverted, and persists *why* (missing fields + judge verdict) as a durable, replayable audit record. **Strict mode** = immediate revert, but never on a raw signal: the `judge` node is an adversarial `Codex` pass (`openai/gpt-5.5-pro` via the `OpenRouter` `LlmPort`, through `delegation_service::delegate`) that must **CONFIRM** the ticket is genuinely un-ready before the revert fires — and biases to **REFUTE** on any ambiguity (Linear API race, label/estimate propagation), so a wrongful revert is structurally unlikely. Because `langgraph-core` nodes are synchronous, all I/O (Linear fetch, the LLM call) runs in the async `evaluate_ticket` orchestrator *around* the graph; the graph itself is the pure deterministic decision + audit trail. `run_enforcer`'s **Live** path now routes through `evaluate_ticket` (judge-gated revert) when `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` is set, and degrades to the direct readiness-only revert otherwise; **Shadow** is unchanged (log-only). Adds `langgraph-core` (path dep, `sqlite` checkpointer) to `sentinel-infrastructure` + `TicketReadiness::missing_owned()`. 7 `enforcement_graph` unit tests (graph routing for confirmed→Revert / refuted→Clear / ready→Clear, the conservative verdict parser, the refute-biased judge prompt); 395 infra tests green; binary builds; clippy pedantic+nursery clean. Completes the "using LangGraph Rust" half of the factory.
- **`linear_enforcer` — Tier B real-time Linear enforcement spine (shadow-default)** (2026-06-08). The always-on half of the "bad PM is bad software" factory: a long-lived `graphql-transport-ws` subscription to Linear (`issueHistoryCreated`) hosted by `sentinel daemon` that reacts to *every* issue state-change — UI edits and API edits alike, not just an in-session agent. When a ticket enters a *started* state (In Progress / Code Review / …) while not dev-ready (no estimate, missing Type/Area label, or still in Triage), the enforcer reverts it to Backlog and comments the missing fields. Ships with the wss client + reconnect/backoff + PAT-rejection handling (ported from legatus-desktop's proven `LinearSubscriptionWsClient`, self-contained — sentinel's own error type, no legatus deps), the REST readiness fetch + revert/comment action, and a `run_enforcer` driver wiring them together with a per-issue 20s debounce (Linear fires several history events per edit) and an optional team-prefix filter. **Safe by default**: `EnforcerConfig::from_env` reads `SENTINEL_LINEAR_TOKEN` (absent ⇒ enforcer not spawned), `SENTINEL_LINEAR_ENFORCE` (`shadow` default — log-only, zero mutations — vs. `live`), and `SENTINEL_LINEAR_TEAMS` (comma list ⇒ team filter). The daemon spawns it fire-and-forget after legatus setup, logging `disabled`/`enabled (mode)` on boot and surviving a permanent PAT rejection without going down. 15 `linear_enforcer` unit tests (readiness/`should_revert` matrix, parse, subprotocol, mode-default-Shadow, team-filter prefix/case, debounce window, config `from_raw` parsing); daemon boots clean with the wiring in place. Pairs with Tier A (`ticket_quality_gate` hook) and Tier C (CI ticket-ready gates). **TLS bring-up (verified live against Linear's wss):** install the rustls `ring` `CryptoProvider` once at subscription start (rustls 0.23 ships both `ring` + `aws-lc-rs` and otherwise panics demanding a choice), and switch `tokio-tungstenite` to `rustls-tls-native-roots` so the OS trust store (which on this Norton-MITM box holds Norton's injected Root CA) is honored instead of `webpki-roots` rejecting the re-signed cert as `UnknownIssuer`. Shadow-mode E2E confirmed `subscription live` + zero mutations on a real ticket event.
- **`ticket_quality_gate` — advisory Linear ticket-quality gate + `ticket-builder` tracking workflow** (2026-06-05). Productizes the Linear ticket-quality rubric + 95 score-gate (`~/.claude/skills/linear/best-practices/ticket-quality.md`) into sentinel. A new `PreToolUse` hook scoped to `mcp__linear__create_issue`/`update_issue` ONLY injects the rubric reminder (resolve the team's estimation type, set Type+Area labels + estimate + priority + ≥3 testable AC, then re-fetch and score to ≥95) as `additionalContext` — **advisory only, never blocks**: a *blocking* gate keyed on a Linear tool is precisely the shape that produced the phase-gate deadlock, so this enforces quality without ever trapping the session.
