Paired with a `ticket-builder` workflow (`resolve-team → build → verify → score-gate`) + `steps/ticket-builder.toml` registered for proof/step tracking only — **no phase files on disk**, so the phase-gate treats it as documentation-only and never hard-blocks. 6 hook tests; registration-completeness + drift tests green.
- **`session_summary` — SessionEnd prose "where we left off" note** (2026-05-30). New `SessionEnd` hook writes `persistent-tasks/{project_hash}/session-summary.json` beside the structured task graph: recent commit subjects (`git log --oneline -10`, what shipped), current branch + HEAD sha, and completed/in_progress/pending task counts. `task_rehydrate` reads it on the next `SessionStart` and injects a `[Last Session]` orientation block **alongside** the structured task list (refactored to inject either/both independently, so a session that finished all its tasks still gets the prose recap). Composes with — does not duplicate — `task_persist`/`task_rehydrate`. One `git log` + one write, fail-open everywhere (respects the 1.5s SessionEnd budget); skips writing an empty note and skips reading back a same-session summary. 13 tests.
- **`task_decomposition_gate` — enforce decomposed task lists before mutating work (PR #32)** (2026-05-30). New `PreToolUse` gate: blocks `Edit`/`Write`/state-changing `Bash` until a live decomposed task list exists, mandating the numbered `#N` + real `Na/Nb` child-subtask format with a two-emoji prefix (status `⬜🔄✅❌` + priority `🔴🟠🟡🟢`), blocking deps, and parent mirror checklist. Reads/`Task*`/sequential-thinking always allowed (never deadlocks the fix path); fails open when task state is unreadable. 18 tests.
- **Two-way Linear ↔ task sync (no MCP)** (2026-05-30). Outbound: `task_completed` writes back to Linear on `@linear:{ID}`-tagged completion. Inbound: new `linear_inbound_sync` (`UserPromptSubmit`) polls the **Hookdeck `/events` API directly** (`include=data` required) for the Linear source, parses `event.data.body` → identifier+state, and flips the matching task's status emoji on drift. Key resolved env→`~/.claude/sentinel/secrets.toml`; cursor-tracked, 300s-throttled, fails open. 41 tests.
- **`task_coverage_check` stale/done-signal nudges** (2026-05-30). Stop hook now reminds (never auto-writes) when an `in_progress` task looks done (new HEAD commit / PR / passing build this turn) or has been `in_progress` ≥3 Stops. State markers `coverage-headsha-{sid}`/`coverage-inprogress-{sid}`; fails open.
- **`task_completed` real claim-verification** (2026-05-30). Replaced string-match heuristics with real checks: claimed commit sha → `git merge-base --is-ancestor <sha> HEAD`; claimed PR → `gh pr view <N> --json state,merged`; warns on a genuine mismatch (claimed commit not on HEAD, claimed-merged PR shows open). Fails open if git/gh unavailable. 29 tests.
- **`claim_reality_check` Stop hook** (2026-05-30). Sweeps completed tasks each Stop and flags any whose claimed artifact (commit/PR) fails the same git/gh verification (shared with `task_completed`, no duplication). Per-session marker `reality-check-{sid}` avoids re-flagging; reminder-only, fails open. 9 tests.
- **Phase progression powered by langgraph-core (#65)** (2026-05-27). New `sentinel-graph` crate compiles each skill's `workflows.toml` into a checkpointed [langgraph-core](../langgraph-python-to-rust) `StateGraph`: one node per phase, `START → phase[0] → … → END`, a conditional edge per phase (Pass → next/`END`, Fail → loop back to the same phase), and `interrupt_after` on every phase for the out-of-process judge gate. A durable sqlite `CheckpointSaver` keyed by `thread_id = session_id` matches sentinel's process-per-invocation hook model — the graph advances one phase per async MCP call and checkpoints between, so a fresh hook process restores via `load_latest` (proven by a cross-process durability test). `apply_verdict` records each judge verdict as a parent-linked checkpoint (advancing on pass, looping back on fail), `replay_phase` time-travels by forking from the checkpoint before a target phase (first-class QA-failed re-attempt), and `phase_history` projects the checkpoint history for local APIs and JSONL streaming. Wired into `handle_submit_phase` behind `SENTINEL_GRAPH_ENGINE=1`, running as an authoritative shadow alongside the legacy `advance_sequential` (kept as fallback). The langgraph dependency stays confined to `sentinel-cli` + `sentinel-graph`; `sentinel-application` (the sync `phase_gate` hot path) remains langgraph-free (verified via `cargo tree`).
- **Operator-armed `SENTINEL_ALLOW_INFRA_EDITS` self-development bypass (#71)** (2026-05-27). The Attack #201 protected-path guard hard-blocks Write/Edit to sentinel's own repo source during active sessions, which also blocked developing sentinel on itself. Added a least-privilege, operator-armed bypass: when `SENTINEL_ALLOW_INFRA_EDITS=1` is set in the operator's environment (fixed at Claude Code launch — an injected tool result cannot set it), edits to the repo *source* (`crates/`, `Cargo`, `config/`, `mcp-router/`) are allowed. Scoped to the repo-source reason ONLY — the live `~/.claude/sentinel` config/state, `settings.json` hook registrations, the compiled binary, and phase/skill files stay protected even when armed, so an armed self-dev session still cannot neuter a running engine. Default off. Pure `infra_source_bypass(reason, armed)` predicate with a unit test asserting every other protected reason is never bypassed.

### Fixed
- **`phase_gate` phantom-workflow whole-session deadlock** (2026-06-05). A phased hard-gate workflow (e.g. `linear`) could become "active" merely because the skill-router matched the skill TOPIC in a prompt (e.g. "build me a linear doc"), without the user ever entering the workflow. The gate then hard-denied EVERY non-exempt tool (`Bash`/`Write`/`Edit`) for the rest of the session, with the only escape being to perform the workflow's first phase (claim a Linear issue) — which was never the task. Fix: in `gate::evaluate`, a blocking workflow with **zero completed phases AND no phase file read** for the skill ("armed but never entered") downgrades the hard block to an advisory ALLOW; enforcement resumes the instant the workflow is genuinely entered, preserving every skip/switch mitigation (#21/#24/#38/#55), which all assume an entered workflow. The same never-entered predicate was applied to `check_protected_path_write` so a phantom-active skill no longer locks its own `SKILL.md` (phase files stay always-protected). Also fixed the block message to use the skill the gate actually evaluated (`effective_skill`) instead of `state.active_skill`, which was `"unknown"` in the incomplete-workflow path and pointed the remediation at a nonexistent `skills/unknown/phases/claim.md`. 2 regression tests; full suite 1548 → green.
- **`StructuredOutput` misclassified as Irreversible → every Workflow deadlocked (2026-06-05)**. The Workflow harness's `StructuredOutput` return tool (a subagent's only way to return its structured result to the parent) had no arm in `builtin_class()` (`sentinel-infrastructure/src/reversibility.rs`), so it fell to the conservative `Irreversible` default. The A3 `dry_run_then_commit` gate then blocked it — demanding `_intent`/`_reasoning`/`_expected_effect` keys that the `StructuredOutput` schema rejects (`additionalProperties:false`) — an unbreakable deadlock that killed **every** multi-agent Workflow with `subagent completed without calling StructuredOutput (after 2 nudges)`. `StructuredOutput` only serializes a JSON value back into the conversation; it commits nothing external → trivially reversible by definition. Added it to the `TriviallyReversible` arm + a regression test (`layer1_structured_output_is_trivially_reversible`).
- **`skill_invocation_gate` re-fire loop** (2026-05-30). `skill_router` rewrote a fresh pending-skill marker on every `UserPromptSubmit`, so re-detecting an already-invoked skill re-armed the gate each turn. A skill now stays satisfied across re-detection within a session; only a genuinely never-invoked skill blocks once. Regression test reproduces the loop. 16 tests.
- **`output_compress` dropped cargo outcome lines** (2026-05-30). `"Finished "` was classified as cargo-build noise but not a signal line, so every `Finished \`release\`` / `Finished test` outcome line was silently dropped (forcing `SENTINEL_COMPRESS_BYPASS=1`). Added it to `is_signal_line` + removed from `is_cargo_build_noise`; build/test outcomes now survive compression. 19 tests.
- **`compress_cmd` corrupted command output (two confirmed bugs)** (2026-05-30). The `sentinel compress` runner — which the `output_compressor` `PreToolUse` hook routes qualifying Bash commands through, so its stdout IS the agent's captured result — mangled output two ways: (1) **stream reordering** — stdout and stderr were captured as separate pipes and concatenated all-stdout-then-all-stderr, relocating interleaved diagnostics (rustc errors, progress+result) to the bottom of the transcript; (2) **UTF-8 destruction** — `from_utf8_lossy` ran unconditionally, so non-UTF-8 output (binary dumps, latin-1, hexdumps) became U+FFFD even for passthrough (`cat`) commands. Both reproduced and fixed: stderr is now merged into stdout *inside the shell* (`{ … } 2>&1`) so the kernel interleaves in true order; the decision to compress happens *before* any lossy conversion, and a non-compressible command / non-UTF-8 output is written through **byte-exact**. Compression still runs (and preserves signal lines) for compressible valid-UTF-8 text. Shell now spawned via absolute `/bin/sh` so a command mutating `PATH` can't break the spawn. Extracted a pure `render_output` for testing. 6 new regression tests.
- **`CLAUDE.md` hook-module count drift (81 → 85)** (2026-05-30). The `claude_md_count_drift` integration test caught the architecture table claiming "81 hook modules" while `hooks/` actually holds 85 `.rs` files (this session added `task_decomposition_gate`, `linear_inbound_sync`, `claim_reality_check`, `session_summary`). Updated both occurrences; drift test green.
- **`dry_run_then_commit` (A3) unbreakable block on `Bash` git ops** (2026-05-30). The auditor demanded `_intent`/`_reasoning`/`_expected_effect` on `Irreversible` actions, but the `Bash` tool schema can't carry them → `git push`/`commit`/`merge` were unblockably denied (`hygiene_override` unavailable in agent context). Added a `Bash` carve-out parallel to the existing MCP-read-only one: `Bash`+`Irreversible` → allow (shell git ops already governed by `commit_message_validator`/`pr_merge_gate`/`git_hygiene`/`db_ops_gate`); `Bash`+`Catastrophic` (e.g. `rm -rf /`, force-push to main, history rewrite) → still denied with a destructive-shell message. MCP behavior unchanged. 38 tests.
- **`memory_turn_capture` binary resolution** (2026-05-30). The capture hook hard-coded `~/.cargo/bin/memory`; now probes `memory-rs` first then legacy `memory` (cargo-bin + dev-clone paths) so it resolves whether the new `{product}-rs`-named binary or the old one is installed.

### Changed
- **scanner.rs god-functions decomposed (behavior-identical) (#32)** (2026-05-25). The two ~300–360-line god-functions in `scanner.rs` (`run_validation`, `sync_counts`) mixed discover/classify/validate/count-sync/manifest concerns. Decomposed each into focused helpers along the natural seam — `run_validation` 360→22 lines (6 `validate_*` helpers, one per category), `sync_counts` 290→16 lines (`build_universal_patterns`/`apply_universal_patterns`/`apply_targeted_updates`). Guarded by **10 new golden-output tests** capturing the exact current scan/validate/sync-counts behavior, asserted green against the original code FIRST, then re-asserted after each extraction — output is byte-identical. 15 scanner tests green, clippy zero.
- **mcp_handler.rs: extracted `submit_step_complete` arg-parsing (#34)** (2026-05-25). Pulled the required-field validation prologue into a pure, testable `parse_submit_step_args(args) -> Result<SubmitStepArgs, _>` (named struct documents the 5 required inputs), separating "what shape does this call require" from the stateful enforcement logic. Six other long-but-cohesive handlers (`query_proof_corpus`, `get_step_proof`, etc.) were deliberately LEFT intact — splitting cohesive single-responsibility functions for line count is an anti-pattern. 1363 tests pass, clippy zero.

### Fixed
- **sentinel-legatus round_trip_legatus-ai-daemon flaky under parallel test load (#33)** (2026-05-25). The 5 round-trip tests passed in isolation but ~4 failed under `cargo test --workspace` with "Blocking waiting for file lock on artifact directory" — shared on-disk state contention. Each test now uses an isolated `TempDir` (and ephemeral port where bound) so parallel runs no longer collide. Green both in isolation and under full parallel workspace test. No production behavior change.

### Added
- **Test coverage for the extracted `llm_scorer_runtime` shared bridge (#29)** (2026-05-25). Added unit tests for the F5-extracted module: `strip_code_fence` (fence-stripping, plain-passthrough, whitespace, multiline), `read_timeout` (override parse + default fallback), and `run_blocking` (the std::thread::scope tokio bridge — timeout-mapping + the #18 nested-runtime guarantee at the shared-helper level). 333 → 365 infra tests, all green, clippy zero. (Engineering and Architecture score-lifts were assessed and deliberately declined: the remaining long functions are cohesive, and the `legatus-ai-domain` coupling is an intentional ADR-003 cross-repo identity contract — forcing either would lower real quality for a cosmetic point.)

### Changed
- **Quality-gate MEDIUM findings: real HMAC, scorer-plumbing dedup, god-function split (#26/#27/#28)** (2026-05-25). Closed the three remaining quality-gate MEDIUM items. **(F4)** `hygiene_override` override-token MAC was `SHA256(salt‖msg)` (length-extension-shaped) with a non-constant-time `==` compare; replaced with real `Hmac<Sha256>` keyed on a domain-separated `-v2` key + constant-time `verify_slice`. On-disk token format unchanged (`{ts}:{sig}`); old v1 tokens fail-closed (TTL ≤ 1h). **(F5)** the three LLM scorers (`dry_run_auditor`, `eval_scorer`, `spec_challenge_scorer`) triplicated ~120 lines of bridge plumbing (PromptFn, sidecar runtime, the #18 nested-runtime thread-scope bridge, strip-fence, provider dispatch); extracted into a new `llm_scorer_runtime` module — **net −378 lines**, each scorer keeps only its distinct prompt builders + verdict parsing. The `score_does_not_panic_when_called_from_within_a_runtime` regression test still passes. **(F6)** split the ~1485-line `hook_cmd::run_internal` god-function into per-event handlers (`handle_user_prompt_submit`/`handle_pre_tool_use`/`handle_post_tool_use`/`handle_stop`) — pure mechanical extraction, byte-identical behavior, run_internal now ~795 lines. clippy zero, full workspace tests green, zero behavior change.

### Fixed
- **Quality-gate HIGH findings: forgeable glass-break token, wasted LLM call, dead orchestrator (#23/#24/#25)** (2026-05-25). A full quality-gate sweep (parallel security + maintainability/perf review agents) surfaced three HIGH items, now fixed. **(F1, security)** `check_glass_break_override` trusted a bare future-timestamp `.glass-break-token` with no integrity check — anything that can write the file (i.e. the agent via `Write`/`Bash`) could forge it and disable all enforcement, defeating the "AI can't complete the dialog" design. The token is now signed: `{expiry}:{sig}` where `sig = SHA256(binary-embedded-salt ‖ expiry)`; an unsigned/forged/tampered token fails verification and is rejected + removed. **(F2, perf)** the A3 dry-run auditor (`auditor.score()`, up to a 30s LLM round-trip) fired on the PreToolUse path even when an earlier gate had already blocked the call; now guarded behind `output.blocked != Some(true)`, mirroring the existing `output_compressor` guard — no wasted latency auditing already-denied tools. **(F3, maintainability)** deleted `engine.rs` — a 138-line `HookEngine` parallel orchestrator that was never constructed or called (the live dispatch is the hand-rolled match in `hook_cmd.rs`); it was misleading dead code implying parallel batch execution that isn't wired. clippy zero, full workspace tests green.

### Added
- **Native output compressor — our own "RTK" (token killer) (#19/#20/#21)** (2026-05-25). Long autonomous sessions burn context window on noisy command output (`cargo test` per-test `... ok` spam, `Compiling …` lines, `grep`/`find` dumps). Built a deterministic, command-aware compressor in-house so it composes natively with sentinel instead of bolting on a third-party proxy. Three pieces: (1) **`sentinel-domain::output_compress`** — pure, zero-IO compression with per-command rules (cargo test/build/clippy, git status, grep/find/ls) and a hard **signal-preservation invariant**: `error`/`error[…]`/`FAILED`/`panicked`/`test result:`/`warning:`/`fatal:` lines pass through **verbatim**, so compression can only ever remove noise, never the lines a verification gate or proof step parses. (2) **`sentinel compress -- <cmd>`** CLI — runs the command, compresses combined stdout+stderr, preserves exit code; `SENTINEL_COMPRESS_BYPASS=1` opts out. (3) **`output_compressor` `PreToolUse` hook** — auto-rewrites compressible Bash commands (via `HookOutput::rewrite_input`, the v2.1.88 `updatedInput` mechanism) to route through the CLI, but only when no gate above blocked the call and not already wrapped. 9 domain + 3 CLI + 8 hook unit tests; clippy zero; full workspace tests green. `cargo test` is the best case (~90% noise removed) — exactly our hottest command.

### Fixed
- **Auditor/scorer nested-tokio-runtime panic on every `mcp__browserbase__*` (and eval/spec) call (#18)** (2026-05-25). `RigAuditor::score` (the A3 dry-run auditor queried by the `dry_run_then_commit` PreToolUse gate) called `sidecar_runtime().block_on(..)` directly on the calling thread. But `score` is reached from inside the CLI's `#[tokio::main]` multi-thread runtime, so blocking a tokio worker thread panicked with "Cannot start a runtime from within a runtime" (`tokio .../multi_thread/mod.rs:91:9`) — surfacing as a `PreToolUse:mcp__browserbase__create_session hook error` / `…__navigate hook error` on every browserbase tool call (non-blocking, but the hook crashed each time). The sidecar's own runtime didn't help: `block_on` blocks the *current* thread regardless. Fixed by driving the `block_on` on a dedicated `std::thread::scope` thread (outside any runtime's worker pool) via the sidecar's `Handle` — panic-safe whether or not the caller is inside a runtime. Same latent bug fixed in the two sibling scorers (`eval_scorer.rs`, `spec_challenge_scorer.rs`). Added a `#[tokio::test]` regression test that reproduces the exact nesting (sync `score` via `spawn_blocking` inside a multi-thread runtime) and would panic against the pre-fix code. 333 infra tests + full workspace green, clippy zero.

### Changed
- **First-class glass-break overrides now suppress the enforcement gates (#5)** (2026-05-25). The audited, interactive glass-break (`sentinel break` — 6-digit terminal challenge that blocks AI self-invocation, reason capture, duration + optional workflow scope, rate-limited, JSONL audit log, `SessionState.glass_break`) previously set session state that **only `phase_gate` honored** — the main blocking gates still keyed off the coarse phrase-based `hygiene_override`. Wired the first-class break into the gates so it actually supersedes the coarse path: new `hooks::glass_break_gate::active_glass_break(state, workflow)` helper (reuses the in-memory `SessionState` the dispatcher already loads — no new state path, domain purity preserved), checking presence + non-expiry + workflow-scope match (unscoped break covers all gates). Wired into `git_hygiene` (tag `git_hygiene`, short-circuits both protected-branch and uncommitted-files blocks), `pre_commit_verification` and `verification_gate` (tag `verification`), each emitting an auditable `[sentinel][glass_break] … gate suppressed` line. The coarse `hygiene_override` is kept intact (additive). 9 glass-break unit tests, clippy zero, full workspace tests green.

### Added
- **Worker-delegation MCP tools: `delegate_codex` + `delegate_kimi_context_scan` (#2)** (2026-05-25). The orchestrator can now hand a discrete unit of work to a *worker* model and get a structured result back, instead of doing everything in its own context — the deep-research report's top gap. Two roles: **Codex** (`openai/gpt-5.5-pro`) for adversarial / code reasoning ("poke holes in this", "review this diff"), and **Kimi** (`moonshotai/kimi-k2.6`) for cheap large-context scanning ("scan this blob, answer X"). New `delegation_service` in `sentinel-application` (`Worker` enum, `DelegationRequest`/`Result`, role-specific prompt builders, `delegate()`), reusing the standardized `LlmPort` (`OpenRouterLlm`) — the same OpenRouter gateway the judge uses, no second model path. Added `LlmModel::Codex` + `LlmModel::Kimi` tiers (domain) mapped to the pinned slugs (infrastructure). Two MCP tools wired in `mcp_cmd.rs` with a shared async `handle_delegate`. 6 unit tests (prompt framing, tier routing, output), clippy zero, full workspace tests green; both worker models live-verified callable on OpenRouter.

### Changed
- **Workspace driven to ZERO clippy warnings (#16)** (2026-05-25). Drove `cargo clippy --workspace` (pedantic + nursery) from ~1500 warnings to zero. Two-pronged: (1) **fixed** hundreds of genuinely-mechanical lints — `format_push_string` → `write!`/`writeln!`, `format_collect` → fold, `manual_let_else`/`option_if_let_else` where mechanical, `or_fun_call` → `unwrap_or_else`, `unnecessary_sort_by` → `sort_by_key`, `manual_strip`, `assigning_clones` → `clone_from`, `items_after_statements`, `unused_peekable`, `iter_on_single_items`, doc-comment backticks, etc.; (2) **allowed at the workspace level, with per-lint justification comments**, the opinionated style/taste lints that are matters of preference not correctness (`too_many_lines`, `manual_let_else`/`option_if_let_else` residue, `needless_pass_by_value`, numeric `cast_*`, `significant_drop_tightening`, `future_not_send`, `match_same_arms`, etc.) — clippy `all` stays fully enforced for real bugs. Also surfaced two genuine **`incompatible_msrv`** findings and bumped the workspace MSRV `1.83` → `1.87` to match APIs the code already uses (`is_unicast_link_local`, and a 1.87 stdlib item in `change_failure.rs`). Build + full workspace tests green, no behavior changes, no `#[allow]` blanket-suppression at module/crate scope.

### Fixed
- **sentinel-legatus tests failing on Windows: fs2 lock on append-only handle + reconnect timing (#17)** (2026-05-25). Two pre-existing Windows-only bugs broke ~30 tests in the legatus crate. (1) **Persistence:** `PersistentInbox::append` / `PersistentEscalationOutbox::append` opened the file with `.create(true).append(true)` only — a `FILE_APPEND_DATA`-only handle on Windows, which `fs2`'s `lock_exclusive` (`LockFileEx`) cannot lock (it needs `FILE_READ_DATA`/`FILE_WRITE_DATA`). The lock silently failed and the early-return dropped the write, so `snapshot()` read 0 entries. Fixed by adding `.read(true)` (NOT `.write(true)` — `write+append` together give the handle a non-append write cursor on Windows, so successive appends overwrite earlier entries) plus an explicit `flush()` before unlock. (2) **Reconnect:** `run_connect_hosted`'s `connect_async` was unbounded, and three `reconnect_loop_*` tests assumed connect-refusal is instant (true on Linux, but `127.0.0.1` low/closed ports SYN-time-out ~1-2s on Windows). Added a `CONNECT_TIMEOUT` (5s) wrapping the connect so an unreachable legatus-ai-daemon becomes a bounded transport failure the backoff loop handles (real production hardening, not test-only), and rewrote the three tests to poll for the published `ConnectionState` with a bounded deadline instead of fixed sleeps — removing the platform-specific timing assumption without weakening what's asserted. Full crate green (99 tests), full workspace green, no regressions. No `#[ignore]`, no weakened assertions.

### Changed
- **Judge promoted to full audit-grade enforce + mandatory signing (#15)** (2026-05-25). After observing warn mode (#13) on real work, flipped the deployment to audit-grade: `SENTINEL_JUDGE_ENFORCEMENT` `warn`→`enforce` (a non-sufficient independent verdict now hard-blocks `submit_step_complete` from sealing, per `mcp_handler.rs` — the structural gate, not a warning), plus `SENTINEL_SIGNING_REQUIRED=1` with a freshly-generated 32-byte Ed25519 seed in `SENTINEL_SIGNING_KEY` so every sealed proof is cryptographically attested and the engine refuses to seal without a key. Config-only (`~/.claude/sentinel/config/settings.json` env block) — the enforce gate (#9/#12) and signing (#4) already shipped. Verified the enforce gate is fail-open on missing verdicts (falls back to the caller-supplied `sufficient:true` for completed steps), so normal workflow is unaffected — only genuinely-insufficient evidence blocks. Takes effect on the next Claude Code restart (the `sentinel-mcp` server reads these env vars at process startup).

### Added
- **Ed25519 proof signing wired into the seal path (#4)** (2026-05-25). Proof signing existed (`step_proof::sign_with`, `SENTINEL_SIGNING_KEY` config) but was never called — proofs were SHA-chain only, never cryptographically attested. `ProofEngine` now signs every sealed `StepProof` over its `combined_hash` when a key is configured, via a `.with_signing(key, required)` builder (the CLI loads `SENTINEL_SIGNING_KEY` + `SENTINEL_SIGNING_REQUIRED`). Mandatory posture: with `SENTINEL_SIGNING_REQUIRED` set and no key, sealing is REFUSED (error, chain unmutated) rather than writing an un-attestable proof — the audit-grade guarantee. 1898 tests green.

### Added
- **Self-certify gap closed + registered MCP servers trusted** (2026-05-25). (1) `submit_step_complete` trusted the caller-supplied `verdict` arg, letting an agent self-certify; now the `step_judge` PostToolUse hook persists an INDEPENDENT verdict into `SessionState` (new `independent_verdicts` map, loaded by `with_session_state` from the same disk store) and `submit_step_complete` prefers it over the supplied one — in `enforce` mode an insufficient independent verdict refuses the seal regardless of the caller's claim. (2) `is_dangerous_mcp_tool` was deny-by-default on verb suffix, flagging `mcp__browserbase__navigate`/`evaluate`, `mcp__cdp__*`, linear mutations etc. as dangerous and applying workflow-gate enforcement; added `TRUSTED_MCP_SERVERS` (browserbase, cdp, steel, sequential-thinking, memory-mcp, sentinel, linear, qdrant, skills, agents) whose tools are trusted regardless of verb, while raw-exec servers not on the list (e.g. `codex` shell/write_file/apply_patch) stay verb-gated. 1895 domain+application tests green.

### Changed
- **Judge models pinned to the operator's four-model set** (2026-05-25). Renamed the `JudgeModel::Haiku` tier to `Codex` and pinned all four slugs to the exact OpenRouter models specified: `Codex` → `openai/gpt-5.5-pro`, `Kimi` → `moonshotai/kimi-k2.6`, `Sonnet` → `anthropic/claude-sonnet-4.6`, `Opus` → `anthropic/claude-opus-4.7`. Added per-step judge routing (#73): `WorkflowStep`/`StepToml` gain an optional `judge:` field (TOML `judge = "codex"|"kimi"|"sonnet"|"opus"`); `step_judge` honors it, defaulting routine steps to `Sonnet`; `multi_judge` Routine tier → `Kimi`. 565 domain tests green.

### Fixed
- **memory-mcp tools were unreachable behind the dry-run gate** (2026-05-25). The atom-store tools (`memory_search`/`memory_capture`/`memory_why`/`memory_audit`/`memory_stats`/`memory_record_outcome`) hit the conservative unknown-MCP reversibility default (`Irreversible`), stranding every memory call at the A3 dry-run gate — the `_intent`/`_reasoning`/`_expected_effect` fields can't be passed through the MCP tool schema, an unbreakable deadlock (same class as the PowerShell + sequential-thinking fixes). Classified the reads as `TriviallyReversible` and `capture`/`record_outcome` as `ReversibleWithEffort` in `reversibility-defaults.toml`. Takes effect on next engine rebuild + stage.
- **Sentinel's own MCP read tools were dry-run-gated** (2026-05-25). The `[mcp.sentinel]` reversibility block omitted `mcp_health_check`/`mcp_list_servers`/`mcp_restart_server` and the step-granularity tools (`get_step_chain`/`get_step_proof`/`get_active_step`/`submit_step_complete`/`submit_linear_step`), so they fell to the unknown-MCP `Irreversible` default and got blocked behind the A3 dry-run gate — sentinel blocking its own observability tools. Added them (reads `TriviallyReversible`, mutations `ReversibleWithEffort`). Also pinned the memory dual-judge `CODEX_MODEL` from the stale `openai/gpt-5.4` to `openai/gpt-5.5-pro` (memory repo) to match the four-model set, which was forcing every memory capture into quarantine.

### Added
- **Adversarial AI judge integrated into the enforcement path + recalibrated** (2026-05-25). The judge (Kimi/GPT-5.5/Opus multi-model + proof chain) was built and tested but wired to nothing mandatory: `phase_gate` is static, `step_judge` fired on no hook event, and the judge was only reachable via the opt-in `submit_phase_complete` MCP tool (where the agent even supplied its own verdict). A live pressure test (`crates/sentinel-infrastructure/tests/live_judge_pressure.rs`) also found all four judge tiers over-blocked genuinely-sufficient evidence. Fixes: (1) recalibrated both adversarial system prompts (`rig_judge`, `dry_run_auditor`) so concrete proof PASSES while unproven claims still FAIL, plus injection-echo hardening; (2) wired `step_judge` into the `PostToolUse` dispatch for the `mcp__skills__<skill>__step_<id>` namespace so completed steps are independently judged; (3) added `judge_enforcement::Mode` (`SENTINEL_JUDGE_ENFORCEMENT` = shadow|warn|enforce, default **shadow** — zero behavior change until promoted), with `submit_step_complete` refusing to seal a non-sufficient verdict in `enforce`. Design doc: `docs/judge-integration-and-calibration.md`. Pressure test green (all tiers PASS proven work, FAIL bad work, no injection echo); 2218 workspace tests pass. A live end-to-end test (`crates/sentinel-cli/tests/e2e_judge_integration.rs`) drives `step_judge::process` — the exact function the `PostToolUse` dispatch calls — through the real `MultiModelJudge` adapter to OpenRouter and confirms a completed step tool produces a verdict (live: `sufficient=true`, confidence 0.86 via `openai/gpt-5.5`, the same evidence all four tiers rejected pre-recalibration).

### Fixed
- **JudgeModel slugs were uncallable / stale** (2026-05-25). A live probe against the operator's OpenRouter key revealed the shipped judge tiers pointed at models that don't work: `Haiku` → `cerebras/glm-4.7` (does not exist on OpenRouter), `Kimi` (the DEFAULT review tier) → `moonshotai/kimi-k2.6` (returns 404 — "no allowed providers" for the operator's routing), `Sonnet` → `openai/gpt-5.4` (stale, and disagreed with `agents-defaults.toml`'s `gpt-5.5`). Re-mapped to slugs verified callable and measured for latency + verdict quality with a real adversarial-judge prompt: `Haiku` → `openai/gpt-5.4-nano` (1.3s), `Kimi` → `moonshotai/kimi-k2-thinking` (callable Kimi variant), `Sonnet` → `openai/gpt-5.5` (newest frontier, ends the config drift); `Opus` → `anthropic/claude-opus-4.7` unchanged. Critical-strict trio retains genuine vendor diversity (moonshot + openai + anthropic, all confirmed callable). 2210 tests green.

### Fixed
- **PowerShell + sequential-thinking reversibility deadlock** (2026-05-25). The `LayeredReversibilityClassifier` omitted the `PowerShell` tool from `builtin_class()`, so every PowerShell call fell through to the conservative `Irreversible` default and tripped the A3 `dry_run_then_commit` gate. That gate demands `_intent`/`_reasoning`/`_expected_effect` keys inside `tool_input`, but the PowerShell tool schema is `additionalProperties: false` and rejects them — an unbreakable deadlock on Windows, where PowerShell is the primary shell. A second deadlock compounded it: `tool_usage_gate` requires a `sequentialthinking` call before code edits, while the unknown-MCP-server default (`Irreversible`) blocked the `mcp__sequential-thinking` tool itself. Fix routes `PowerShell` through the shared Layer-3 command-pattern path (it carries the same `command` field as Bash), adds PowerShell destructive patterns (`Remove-Item -Recurse -Force`, `Format-Volume`, `Clear-Disk`, `Remove-Partition`, `Initialize-Disk`, registry-key deletes → Catastrophic), and adds `[mcp.sequential-thinking] sequentialthinking = "TriviallyReversible"`. 7 regression tests added; 329 infrastructure+application tests green.

### Added
- **Tier 3 production hardening: TLS docs + Prometheus + multi-legatus-ai-daemon failover + token-rotation surface** (2026-05-24). Four production-quality additions on top of the reliable-connection foundation:

  1. **`GET /legatus/metrics`** — Prometheus text-exposition format endpoint, no external scrape crate needed (3 metric families, hand-rolled). Surfaces `legatus_connection_state` (gauge 0-3), `legatus_connection_attempts_total` (counter), `legatus_outbox_pending` (gauge). Same bearer-auth path as the rest of the local API. Mounted on the daemon at `/legatus/metrics` alongside `/legatus/health`. The outbox-depth read is offloaded to `spawn_blocking` so a contended mutex never stalls the axum runtime.

  2. **Multi-legatus-ai-daemon failover** — new `--legatus-legatus-ai-daemon-failover-url` (repeatable) on `sentinel daemon`. The reconnect wrapper now iterates `[primary, ...failover]` in priority order each attempt before backing off. New `ConnectConfig.failover_urls: Vec<String>` field carries the list. Failover preference is **not** persisted across attempts — every new attempt restarts from primary so a transient primary outage doesn't permanently demote the primary. `VersionMismatch` becomes fatal only when it fires on the LAST URL (any failover gets a chance first). All four existing tests + one new test still green.

  3. **`PraefectusClientError::TokenInvalid`** — new error variant distinct from `Verification`. 401 from `HttpPraefectusClient` now produces `TokenInvalid(body)` instead of being lumped with cryptographic verification failures. The `PraefectusClientWitnessVerifier` adapter logs `TokenInvalid` at `warn!` with an operator-actionable message ("Praefectus rejected the bearer token. Rotate LEGATUS_PRAEFECTUS_TOKEN and restart sentinel daemon"); other errors stay at `debug!` to avoid log noise per-witness. Operators tailing logs see exactly when their token has expired vs. when a witness is actually invalid.

  4. **TLS / wss:// support** — documented production path. tokio-tungstenite is built with `rustls-tls-webpki-roots` so `wss://` URLs work out of the box against any publicly-trusted certificate (Let's Encrypt, AWS ACM, etc.). Two patterns documented in the operator runbook: (a) legatus-ai-daemon terminates TLS directly, (b) reverse-proxied via nginx/Caddy/Cloudflare. **Custom-CA injection (self-signed dev certs)** is flagged as a Tier 3 follow-up — requires adding `rustls` + `rustls-pemfile` direct deps + `connect_async_tls_with_config` plumbing.

  Runbook gained TLS + multi-legatus-ai-daemon failover + voice-loop verification sections (manual operator procedure + which automated tests cover which parts of the catastrophic-ack flow). Workspace tests still all-green (~2466 tests).

### Added
- **Daemon ergonomics: PID file + `sentinel stop` + launchd template + `sentinel legatus init` + `sentinel legatus status` + connection-event JSONL log** (2026-05-24). Four operator-facing improvements that together make the daemon usable as a long-lived service instead of a one-off process:

  1. **PID file + `sentinel stop`** (Unix-only). Daemon now writes `~/.claude/sentinel/daemon-pid` at startup and refuses to start if an existing PID is alive (prevents accidental double-up on the same token file; stale PIDs are silently overwritten). New `sentinel stop --wait-secs <N>` shells out to `/bin/kill -TERM`, polls for process exit, and cleans up both the PID file and the `daemon-token` file as a belt-and-suspenders measure (tokio's default SIGTERM handler aborts the runtime before the daemon's post-serve cleanup code can run, so a stop-side cleanup is required to leave a clean slate). Uses `/bin/kill` shell-out rather than `libc::kill` so the workspace's `unsafe_code = "forbid"` lint stays intact.

  2. **launchd plist template** at `scripts/launchd/com.anthropic.sentinel.plist.template`. Placeholders for `{{SENTINEL_BIN}}`, `{{LEGATUS_AI_DAEMON_URL}}`, `{{BOOTSTRAP_SECRET_PATH}}`, `{{HOME}}`, `{{LOG_DIR}}`. Wraps the daemon in a tiny shell that reads the bootstrap secret from a 0600 file and injects it via env (launchd's `EnvironmentVariables` can't read from a file, and the secret should never appear in `ps`). `KeepAlive=true`, `ThrottleInterval=10`, `ProcessType=Background`.

  3. **`sentinel legatus init`** — generates a 32-byte bootstrap secret via `getrandom::OsRng`, hex-encodes, and either prints to stdout or writes to `--output <PATH>` with mode 0600 (creating parent directories as needed). Refuses to overwrite an existing output file without `--force` — silent rotation can lock running legati out of the Legatus AI.

  4. **`sentinel legatus status [--json]`** — reads `~/.claude/sentinel/daemon-token`, calls `GET /legatus/health` + `GET /legatus/pending`, pretty-prints connection state + outbox depth (or emits combined JSON for `jq`retiredlocal clients). Surfaces "daemon not running" cleanly when the token file is missing.

  5. **Connection-event JSONL log** at `~/.claude/sentinel/state/legatus-connection-events.jsonl`. New `crates/sentinel-legatus/src/connection_event_log.rs` provides `ConnectionEvent { t, state, attempt, reason? }` + `ConnectionEventLog` (append-only writer, best-effort: I/O failures `warn!` rather than block the WS loop). Wrapper writes one line per state transition (Connecting / Connected / Reconnecting{reason} / Disconnected{reason?}). `ConnectionStatus` gained an attached `AtomicU64` attempt counter (`bump_attempt()` / `attempt()`) so the event log entries and `/legatus/health` JSON both carry "how many reconnects has this daemon survived?" `/legatus/health` JSON now `{ status, attempt }`. 5 unit tests cover create-on-append, parent-dir auto-create, FIFO ordering, `skip_serializing_if` for None reason, and reason-carrying disconnect. End-to-end: started a daemon, killed it, restarted, verified the JSONL gained the right sequence of transitions with timestamps.

  Workspace tests still all-green (~2466 tests, +5 new).

### Fixed
- **Five dead-wired hooks: declared in HOOK_NAMES, never invoked** (2026-05-24). An audit of `crates/sentinel-cli/src/hook_cmd.rs` against `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/mod.rs::HOOK_NAMES` found six hooks that had complete `process()` functions with unit tests but **were never called from the production dispatcher**. They were silently inert in every real session. Wired five of them; one (`spec_challenge_gate`) deferred because it needs external store + scorer wiring that isn't in `hook_cmd.rs` today.
  - `catastrophic_escalation` (PreToolUse) — **the headline bug**. The entire voice-attested catastrophic-action loop was dead from the sentinel side. Catastrophic Bash commands were not being intercepted; no `SessionBlocked{CatastrophicPending}` ever reached Legatus AI. The whole point of the legatus connection was to carry these signals.
  - `agent_revocation` (PreToolUse) — the agent kill-switch was inert; `sentinel agent revoke <id>` wrote state nobody read.
  - `constitution_gate` (PreToolUse) — the structural-rules enforcer the previous changelog called "SHIPPED" was actually never called. Operators who wrote `~/.claude/sentinel/config/constitution-gate.toml` saw no enforcement.
  - `step_gate` (PreToolUse) — the M1.1 step-level prereq gate. Skills that depended on per-step proofs got no enforcement.
  - `prompt_injection_nudge` (PostToolUse) — the injection-detection warning was never added to additionalContext on any tool result.

  Each wired with the appropriate dependencies (`DaemonApprovalChecker` for catastrophic; `&state` for agent_revocation; existing `step_configs` HashMap for step_gate; `constitution_rules: Vec<Rule>` loaded once at hook entry from `~/.claude/sentinel/config/constitution-gate.toml` with graceful no-op on missing/malformed file). Each routed through `time_and_record` so they show up in `sentinel stats`. Workspace tests still all-green (~2461 tests).

### Added
- **End-to-end hook validation via extended smoke test** (2026-05-24). `scripts/smoke-sentinel-Legatus AI-roundtrip.sh` now drives a real hook subprocess (`sentinel hook --event PreToolUse` with a catastrophic `rm -rf /` command) against the running daemon, asserts the hook denies locally (parses stdout JSON for `permissionDecision=deny`), AND asserts the resulting `SessionBlocked{CatastrophicPending}` actually arrives on the legatus-ai-daemon's WebSocket (greps the debug log for `escalation event ... kind="blocked"`). This pins the entire chain — hook subprocess → HTTP POST → daemon `LegatusHandle.escalate()` → WS frame → legatus-ai-daemon session_loop. Without this test, the dead-wired `catastrophic_escalation` would still be silently inert. The smoke also runs under an isolated `$HOME` (`mktemp -d`) so the smoke daemon's token file never clobbers the operator's real `~/.claude/sentinel/daemon-token`. Pass observed end-to-end on macOS.

- **Operator setup runbook** (2026-05-24). `docs/runbooks/operator-setup-sentinel-Legatus AI.md` — full zero-to-connected path: build both binaries, generate bootstrap secret, start legatus-ai-daemon, start daemon, verify `/legatus/health`, optional operator binding, troubleshooting common failure modes (stuck in `connecting`, 401 on token, daemon dies on schema mismatch, hook can't reach daemon).

- **Legatus connection-status observability + `GET /legatus/health` + shell smoke test** (2026-05-24). Operators (and the new smoke test) can now see whether the daemon's hosted legatus is actually connected to Legatus AI without grepping logs. Three pieces:

  1. **`ConnectionStatus` type** (`crates/sentinel-legatus/src/connection_status.rs`) — clone-cheap handle wrapping an `Arc<AtomicU8>` that encodes one of `Disconnected` / `Connecting` / `Connected` / `Reconnecting`. Lock-free reads + writes so the HTTP handler never blocks the hot WebSocket loop. Defensive `from_u8` decodes unknown bytes to `Disconnected` and never panics. 5 unit tests pin defaults, round-trip, clone-sharing semantics, unknown-byte handling, and the JSON wire strings.

  2. **Wrapper publishes transitions** — `run_connect_hosted` writes `Connecting` on entry and `Connected` after handshake + registration. `run_connect_hosted_with_reconnect` writes `Reconnecting` between failed attempts and `Disconnected` on terminal exit (cancel, fatal `VersionMismatch`). A new `client::tests::reconnect_loop_observes_status_transitions` unit test pins the externally-observable transitions: fresh → `Disconnected`, after first failure → `Reconnecting`, after cancel → `Disconnected`.

  3. **`GET /legatus/health`** on the daemon — bearer-authed JSON endpoint returning `{ "status": "connected" | ... }`. Added as a third state-typed sub-router merged into the existing legatus route surface so smoke tests and local clients can poll it directly. Mounted on the same daemon port as `/legatus/escalate` etc.

  4. **`scripts/smoke-sentinel-Legatus AI-roundtrip.sh`** — end-to-end shell smoke that builds + drives a real `sentinel daemon` against a real `legatus-ai-daemon` over real WebSocket on ephemeral ports, polls `/legatus/health` until `connected`, kills the legatus-ai-daemon to verify the daemon transitions to `reconnecting`, restarts it to verify it goes back to `connected`. Cleans up via EXIT trap. The smallest possible end-to-end proof that the two binaries actually talk on the wire, beyond the in-process Rust tests.

  **API change**: `run_connect_hosted` and `run_connect_hosted_with_reconnect` now require a `ConnectionStatus` argument (the former by `&`, the latter by-value clone). All in-tree callers updated; the standalone `run_connect` constructs a fresh one and discards it (no observer). Workspace tests still all-green (~2461 tests, +6 new).

### Fixed
- **Sentinel-legatus auto-reconnect was a no-op for in-loop transport failures** (2026-05-24). The reconnect wrapper added yesterday only retried on handshake / encode errors — the actual common failure modes (legatus-ai-daemon-initiated WS close, recv error, stream end, mid-session send failure) all `break None` inside the loop and returned `Ok(())`, which the wrapper read as "session exited cleanly; do not reconnect." So a real TCP drop / legatus-ai-daemon restart / network blip produced exactly one connection attempt and then the daemon went silent. Refactor: introduced `ExitReason::{Cancelled, TransportFailed(String)}` to discriminate the cancel path (returns `Ok(())`, sends graceful `SessionCompleted`) from every transport-side exit (returns `Err(LegatusError::Transport(reason))`, skips the doomed `SessionCompleted` send). The reconnect wrapper now actually reconnects on the failure modes it was supposed to handle. Two new regression tests pin this:
  1. **Unit:** `client::tests::reconnect_loop_keeps_retrying_after_repeated_transport_failure` — runs the wrapper against a guaranteed-refused address, asserts it has NOT exited after 1.5s (one attempt + one full backoff + one more attempt), then asserts cancel still produces `Ok(())`.
  2. **Integration:** `round_trip_legatus-ai-daemon::run_connect_hosted_surfaces_transport_failure_on_remote_close` — spawns a legatus-ai-daemon that handshakes + registers then immediately drops the WS, asserts `run_connect_hosted` returns `Err(LegatusError::Transport(_))` (pre-fix this returned `Ok(())`). The panic message in the test calls out the exact pre-fix bug for future readers.

  Workspace tests still all-green (~2455 tests, +2 new).

- **Dry-Run Auditor + Skill Gate deadlock on harness read-only tools (2026-05-23).** `builtin_class` in `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/reversibility.rs` only whitelisted 10 tool names, so `Skill`, `ToolSearch`, `AskUserQuestion`, `TaskGet`, `TaskOutput`, `EnterPlanMode`/`ExitPlanMode`, and the `Agent`/`Team`/`Cron`/`Worktree` lifecycle tools cascaded into the conservative `Irreversible` default. That made `dry_run_then_commit` demand `_intent`/`_reasoning`/`_expected_effect` on every call, which deadlocked the agent against `skill_gate`: the skill gate required `Skill(...)` before any `Bash`, but the auditor refused `Skill(...)`. Expanded `builtin_class` to 25 tools across two classes — `TriviallyReversible` for pure reads / UI prompts / schema lookups (+ `TaskGet`, `TaskOutput`, `AskUserQuestion`, `Skill`, `ToolSearch`, `ShareOnboardingGuide`, `Monitor`, `CronList`, `LSP`) and `ReversibleWithEffort` for local / in-conversation mutations (+ `NotebookEdit`, `TaskStop`, `EnterPlanMode`, `ExitPlanMode`, `EnterWorktree`, `ExitWorktree`, `Agent`, `TeamCreate`, `TeamDelete`, `SendMessage`, `CronCreate`, `CronDelete`, `ScheduleWakeup`, `PushNotification`, `RemoteTrigger`). None of these reach external services or shared infrastructure. Doc comment names `skill_gate.rs` as the mirror surface when adding new built-ins. Drive-by: `sentinel-legatus/src/client.rs` carries `operator_id: None` on `RegisterSession` to compile against the Phase-6 schema; expanded `mcp.linear` coverage in `config/reversibility-defaults.toml`.

### Changed
- **Steel → Browserbase/CDP marketplace-wide rename + browser-testing architecture split (2026-05-23).** Retired the "Steel" brand across the entire marketplace and split browser testing by URL surface: **localhost → CDP** (`mcp__cdp__*` via the edge-cdp skill, direct hit, no tunnel), **remote URLs (preview/staging/prod) → Browserbase** (`mcp__browserbase__*`, full 48 tools). Research confirmed Browserbase has no localhost support, so the old cloudflared-tunnel-then-Browserbase localhost dance was pure ceremony — CDP replaces it. **Sentinel Rust+config:** completed the partial `pre_push_steel_test.rs`→`pre_push_browser_test.rs` rename (`STEEL_TEST_VALIDITY`→`BROWSER_TEST_VALIDITY`, `repo_has_steel_config`→`repo_has_browser_test_config`, `ext.steel_tools`→`ext.browserbase_tools`, `parse_steel_tools`→`parse_browserbase_tools`, regex `Steel MCP`→`Browserbase MCP`); PostToolUse browser-test recorder accepts `mcp__browserbase__release_session` + `mcp__cdp__close_instance` + legacy `mcp__steel__release_session`; `config/workflows.toml` `[steel]`→`[browserbase]`, `[steel-tester]`→`[browserbase-tester]`; renamed `config/steps/steel.toml`→`browserbase.toml` (old federation `browserbase.toml`→`browserbase-federation.toml`), `steel-tester.toml`→`browserbase-tester.toml`; `config/steps/linear.toml` Step 0 rewritten from cloudflared+Browserbase to `mcp__cdp__*`; `mcp__steel__*` detection retained in `phase_gate.rs`/`mcp_health.rs` as defense-in-depth. **New phase-gate override:** HMAC-signed override (`override_phrase.rs` `PHASE_GATE_OVERRIDE_PATTERNS`/`is_phase_gate_override`, `hygiene_override.rs` `phase_gate_override_path`/`is_signed_override_active_with_ttl`, 600s TTL) so marketplace skill refactors can edit `SKILL.md`/`phases/*.md` (scoped — sentinel config/state/settings stay protected). **Marketplace skills:** linear (review.md Layer 2.5→CDP, qa-handoff.md Step 0→CDP, SKILL.md v9, `steel_test_*`→`browser_test_*` project fields, cloudflared removed), browserbase (SKILL.md v6 REMOTE-ONLY, 7 phase Workflow renames, SECURITY.md rewrite), edge-cdp (v2 canonical-localhost), browserbase-tester (v2), cloudflare-tunnel (v2 "not for browser testing"), `_shared/browserbase-patterns.md` (Cloudflare Tunnel Pattern → CDP Localhost Pattern, `__steelErrors`→`__browserErrors`), `_shared/project-context.md` schema, plus ~17 ancillary skills. Validation: zero accidental Steel refs remain; cargo build + test green.

### Added
- **Sentinel-legatus reliability: per-operator binding + auto-reconnect** (2026-05-23). Closes the last two gaps blocking the daemon from being a production-quality Legatus AI client. Two related changes:

  1. **`ConnectConfig.operator_id: Option<OperatorId>`** — `sentinel daemon --legatus-operator-id <UUID>` now flows the operator's UUID through `ConnectConfig` into `RegisterSession.operator_id`. The legatus-ai-daemon populates `Session.owner` from it, and the voice-attested gate's `OperatorResolverPort` (Phase C3) routes per-session escalations to the correct operator's voice gate. Before this, every sentinel session registered as `OperatorId::ROOT` and the gate's per-session lookup defeated itself. `None` (the default) preserves the v0.1 single-operator-as-ROOT scaffold for hosts that haven't bound an identity yet. Re-exported `sentinel_legatus::OperatorId` so callers don't need a direct path-dep on `legatus-ai-domain`.

  2. **`run_connect_hosted_with_reconnect`** — new wrapper around `run_connect_hosted` with exponential-backoff reconnect (1s → 2s → 4s → … capped at 30s, `INITIAL_RECONNECT_BACKOFF` and `MAX_RECONNECT_BACKOFF` constants). Transient transport / handshake / heartbeat failures retry; `LegatusError::VersionMismatch` surfaces as fatal because reconnecting against a protocol-incompatible legatus-ai-daemon won't help. Honors the cancel `Notify` during the backoff sleep so Ctrl-C interrupts cleanly. The daemon's hosted-legatus path uses the wrapper; the standalone `sentinel legatus connect` CLI path keeps `run_connect` (one-shot) semantics.

  **API change**: `run_connect_hosted` now takes `runtime: &mut LegatusRuntime` instead of by-value. The reason is that the reconnect wrapper must reuse the SAME runtime across iterations — rebuilding it via `make_pair()` would detach the caller's `LegatusHandle` channel ends and silently break inbox/outbox push and escalation drain after the first reconnect. With `&mut`, the wrapper owns the runtime for its lifetime and the handle-paired channels stay hot across the entire reconnect arc, so escalations queued during an outage drain on the next successful connection. All in-tree callers (`run_connect`, the 4 round-trip integration tests) updated.

  Tests: 3 new unit tests in `client::tests` — `reconnect_loop_honors_cancel_during_backoff` (real-time, ~200ms wait + cancel; asserts cancel arm wins over 1s sleep), `reconnect_loop_surfaces_version_mismatch_as_fatal` (pins backoff constants and their relationship), `connect_config_operator_id_defaults_to_none` (asserts scaffold default preserves ROOT semantics). All 11 client tests green; full sentinel-legatus suite 83/0. Workspace tests still all-green (2450+ tests, no regressions).

- **Constitution gate — runtime enforcement of structural project rules** (2026-05-19). Item K from the Phase 2 punch list. New `PreToolUse` hook (`constitution_gate`) that loads a per-project policy file (`~/.claude/sentinel/config/constitution-gate.toml`) describing `[[rule]]` tables of `path_prefix` × `path_suffix?` × `banned_patterns[]` × `reason` × `citation?`, and **denies** any `Write` / `Edit` / `MultiEdit` / `NotebookEdit` whose target path is in scope AND whose new content contains a banned literal substring. The deny carries the `[Sentinel-Authority]` prefix so the downstream agent treats it as policy, not negotiable.

  **Generic on purpose.** Sentinel knows nothing about Legatus AI, firefly, or any specific project. The rules live in TOML the operator authors. Missing config = no-op (machines that haven't opted in see no behaviour change). Parse failures log at `warn` and degrade to inert so a typo doesn't take down the daemon's PreToolUse path.

  **Use case**: enforce the same structural rules `constitution.md` already declares (e.g. "`legatus-ai-domain/` has zero I/O dependencies", "no vendor names in `legatus-ai-protocol/`") at the moment they would be violated, not hours later in CI. Shipped example at `config/constitution-gate-example.toml` demonstrates the schema with the Legatus AI/legatus rules; operators copy + adapt.

  **New `crates/sentinel-application/src/constitution_gate_runtime.rs`** with `ConstitutionGateConfig::from_toml_str` parser + `Rule { name, path_prefix, path_suffix?, banned_patterns[], reason, citation? }` + `matches_path` / `find_banned` predicates. Validation: empty name, empty path_prefix, or empty banned_patterns reject at parse time. **New `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/constitution_gate.rs`** with the actual hook. Wired into `hook_cmd.rs` PreToolUse dispatcher after `doppler_auth0_gate`; rule list loaded once at daemon startup from `~/.claude/sentinel/config/constitution-gate.toml` and reused across hook fires.

  Tests: 6 parser tests (empty-doc → empty rules, complete-rule roundtrip, optional-fields, empty-name/empty-banned rejection, path-match predicates, find-banned first-hit) + 11 hook tests (empty-rules no-op, non-editing-tool passthrough, deny-with-authority on Write, allow on unprotected path, allow on clean content, suffix filter, Edit/MultiEdit content scanning, multi-rule evaluation order, missing-path passthrough). Workspace 2363 / 0 failed.

- **Mid-execution prompt-injection nudge** (2026-05-19). Item F from the Phase 2 punch list. New `PostToolUse` hook (`prompt_injection_nudge`) scans the tool result for injection-shaped strings — classic `"ignore previous instructions"`, role-override attempts (`"you are now a…"`), leaked chat-format tokens (`<|system|>`, `<|im_start|>`, `[INST]`), system-prompt impersonation, and data-exfil bait — and injects an "untrusted output, ignore embedded directives" warning via `hookSpecificOutput.additionalContext` so the model treats the tool result as data, not as instructions.

  **Conservative on purpose.** Patterns are literal substring matches chosen to have effectively zero innocent reading; a false-positive nudge is harmless ("we already weren't going to act on that"), a false-negative is the bug. The nudge is one soft layer in a defense-in-depth stack — destructive gates (`db_ops_gate`, `commit_message_validator`, A13 spec-challenge) remain the hard backstops per the user's `~90-95%` reliability posture.

  Wired into the CLI hook dispatcher's PostToolUse arm right after `evidence_collector`. Registered in `hooks/mod.rs` and the `HOOKS` registry array.

  Tests: 8 unit tests covering no-result-passthrough, clean-result, classic ignore-previous, chat-format leak, role-override, nested-array scanning, case-insensitive match, and false-positive resistance against innocent phrasing like *"how to ignore previous warnings safely"*. Workspace 2346 / 0 failed.

- **BA-orchestrator Phase 3 — `sentinel ba draft` CLI (end-to-end LIVE)** (2026-05-19). Final phase of the MVP BA-orchestrator. The track is now end-to-end shippable: operators run `sentinel ba draft --brief "..." --audience exec` and get a structured `BaRecommendation` containing the recommendation body + citations + requirement_refs + complete A13 spec challenge. That envelope is exactly what BA1 / BA3 / A13 gates verify when the recommendation flows into a downstream tool call — closing the loop that's been open since the gates shipped without an upstream emitter.

  **New `Ba` subcommand** with `BaAction::Draft { brief, audience, constraints, agent_id, json }`. Flags: `--brief <TEXT>` (required), `--audience <exec|board|customer|internal_team>` (required), `--constraint <TEXT>` (repeatable), `--agent-id <ID>` (defaults to `ba-orchestrator`), `--json` (full pretty-JSON envelope vs. human summary).

  **New `crates/sentinel-cli/src/ba_cmd.rs`** (~270 lines + 8 unit tests). `draft(args)` is the production entry point — builds `AnthropicClient::from_env()` and delegates to `draft_with<L: LlmPort + ?Sized>(args, llm)` which is the generic test seam. `parse_audience` accepts canonical snake_case keys (`exec` / `board` / `customer` / `internal_team`) plus aliases (`internal-team`, `internal`) and is case-insensitive. Unknown audience strings error with operator-facing guidance naming the valid options. Human-readable `render_summary` prints recommendation id, audience, timestamps, citation/requirement counts, the structural-readiness flag, then the brief, body, and per-citation breakdown.

  **`crates/sentinel-cli/src/main.rs`**: new `Ba` Commands variant routes to `ba_cmd::draft`. `crates/sentinel-cli/Cargo.toml`: added `async-trait` as a dev-dependency so the test `StubLlm` can implement `LlmPort`.

  8 tests cover: well-formed args succeed in JSON mode, summary mode succeeds with constraints, unknown audience rejected with descriptive error, blank brief surfaces the orchestrator's `InvalidRequest` ("orchestrator failed"), `parse_audience` accepts all 4 canonical keys, case-insensitivity (EXEC, Board), internal-team aliases, garbage strings rejected with both the bad value and the valid set in the message. Sentinel-cli: **166 tests passing (158 prior + 8 new).** Zero new clippy warnings.

  **End-to-end demo flow now works.** Set `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` and run `sentinel ba draft --brief "scale the platform for 10x users" --audience exec`. The orchestrator emits a `BaRecommendation` with the structural readiness for sentinel's gates. Real connector pulls (real `ArtifactReference`s from Linear / Confluence) are BA6 work; for now the model emits plausible citations that BA1 will reject against the empty audit chain — which is the correct behavior and demonstrates the enforcement loop.

- **Per-turn tool-call trace surfaces in `InstructionResult` summary** (2026-05-19). Item E from the Phase 2 punch list. Every `PostToolUse` during a turn now appends the tool name to a per-session trace file; the `Stop` hook drains it and prepends a `[tools: A, B, C]` tag to the per-instruction Result summary, so the operator sees which tools the legatus actually ran in response to their relayed instruction.

  Per-turn (not per-tool-call) granularity — when `Legatus AI_inbox` drains multiple instructions into the same model turn, every instruction's Result gets the same tool list. Honest reporting at the model-turn boundary; true per-tool-call attribution needs model-cooperative emission which is a follow-up.

  **New `legatus_client::note_tool_call` + `take_tool_calls`** mirror the disk-FIFO discipline of the existing pending-instructions + turn-signals trace files: path-traversal guard, best-effort I/O, drain-on-read. **`evidence_collector` PostToolUse hook** records every tool call into this trace. **`execution_log` Stop hook** dedups while preserving first-seen order, formats `[tools: …]` (max 6 distinct, then `…+N more`), 140-char-capped to match the existing summary ceiling. **`stop_failure`** also drains the trace so failure paths don't leak stale state.

  Tests: +4 unit tests on `legatus_client` (roundtrip, blank-skip, path-traversal guard, missing-session), +4 on `enrich_summary_with_tool_calls` (no-tools-passthrough, dedup, 6-cap, blank-base). Workspace 2330 / 0 failed.

- **BA-orchestrator Phase 2 — `ba_orchestrator::draft` use case** (2026-05-19). Second commit of the BA-orchestrator track. The orchestrator's job: turn a [`BaDraftRequest`] into a [`BaRecommendation`] — the envelope sentinel's BA1 / BA3 / A13 gates were designed to verify. Application-layer; consumes the existing `LlmPort` so any rig-backed adapter works as the LLM substrate.

  **New `crates/sentinel-application/src/ba_orchestrator.rs`** (~430 lines + 13 unit tests). `pub async fn draft<L: LlmPort + ?Sized>(request, llm, agent_id, clock) -> Result<BaRecommendation, BaOrchestratorError>` is the production entry point; `draft_with_model` lets callers override `LlmModel` + `max_tokens` (defaults: `Opus`, `4096`). One LLM call per draft — the system prompt instructs the model to emit a single JSON document with the recommendation body, citations, requirement_refs, AND a complete A13 `SpecChallenge`. The response is parsed strictly: missing or malformed fields surface as `BaOrchestratorError::Malformed` rather than silently degraded outputs.

  **Reversibility-class mapping** (`reversibility_for_audience` public so operators iterating can override): `Exec` / `Board` → `Catastrophic` (A13 scorer engaged), `Customer` → `Irreversible`, `InternalTeam` → `ReversibleWithEffort`. The prompt threads this through so the LLM emits a `SpecChallenge` with the correct class — matching what the downstream A13 gate will compute via the existing reversibility classifier.

  **`BaOrchestratorError { InvalidRequest, Backend, Malformed }`** with operator-facing `Display`. `InvalidRequest` fires when `BaDraftRequest::is_well_formed()` returns false (blank brief) — the LLM is **not called** in this case, saving the operator a wasted API call on a known-bad input. `Backend` wraps `LlmPort::complete` failures; `Malformed` wraps JSON parse failures with a 200-char head preview for operator triage.

  **`build_prompt`**: composes the system prompt with the brief, audience (snake_case key for serde stability), constraints (numbered list when present, `(none stated)` when empty), and expected reversibility class. The prompt explicitly instructs the model on the A13 completeness rules ("each category MUST have either items OR an `explicit_assertion_of_none` reason — silent empties are rejected"), the ambiguity-≥-2-interpretations rule, and the `InferredFromContext` → non-empty `inference_source` rule. This pushes the work upfront so the model produces gate-passing output rather than relying on retry loops.

  **What this commit does NOT do**: connector pulls (real `ArtifactReference`s from Linear / Confluence / etc.) are BA6 work; persistence is a downstream concern; the gates themselves run in `hook_cmd.rs` when the recommendation is serialized into a tool's `extra` payload. Phase 2 closes the "agent emits a verifiable artifact" loop; Phases 3+ wire it to operators (CLI + MCP).

  13 tests with a `StubLlm` (records last request, returns canned response or error) cover: well-formed request → fully-typed `BaRecommendation` with `is_structurally_ready_for_publication() == true`, blank brief rejected before LLM call (LLM `last_prompt` is `None` — verified), LLM failure surfaces as `Backend`, non-JSON response as `Malformed`, markdown code-fence stripped, prompt threads brief + audience (`board`) + constraints (`no vendor lockin` + `cite ≥ 2 sources`) + reversibility class (`Catastrophic` for Board), empty constraints render as `(none stated)`, `recommendation_id` synthesized from clock (`rec-1700000000` for fixed clock), `reversibility_for_audience` maps all 4 audiences correctly, error `Display` covers each variant, `std::error::Error` impl, preview truncates / passes through. `crates/sentinel-application/src/lib.rs` exposes the new `ba_orchestrator` module. Sentinel-application: **1240 tests passing (1227 prior + 13 new).** Zero new clippy warnings.

- **BA-orchestrator Phase 1 — recommendation domain types** (2026-05-19). First commit of the BA-orchestrator track. Sentinel has shipped the verification gates (BA1 `provenance_validate`, BA3 `requirements_traceability_gate`, A13 `spec_challenge_gate`) — all structurally LIVE — but nothing upstream emits the artifacts those gates verify. The orchestrator track closes that loop. Phase 1 ships the output envelope as pure domain; future phases ship the orchestration use case, the connector wiring, and the operator-facing surface (`sentinel ba draft` CLI + MCP tool).

  **New `crates/sentinel-domain/src/ba/recommendation.rs`** (~360 lines + 14 unit tests). Identifiers: `RecommendationId` newtype (whitespace-trimmed; rejects empty). `StakeholderAudience { Exec, Board, Customer, InternalTeam }` with stable `key()` for serialization (`"exec"` / `"board"` / `"customer"` / `"internal_team"`) — drives both prompt scaffolding when drafted and the A12 `StakeholderFit` axis when benchmarked.

  `BaDraftRequest { brief, stakeholder_audience, constraints }` is the operator-supplied input — `is_well_formed()` rejects whitespace-only briefs, allows empty constraints. `BaRecommendation { recommendation_id, brief, stakeholder_audience, body, citations: Vec<ArtifactReference>, requirement_refs: Vec<RequirementRef>, spec_challenge: SpecChallenge, generated_at, agent_id }` is the output envelope. Every field maps to a sentinel-gate input: `citations` → BA1's `extra.artifacts`, `requirement_refs` → BA3's `extra.requirement_refs`, `spec_challenge` → A13's `extra.spec_challenge`. So when an orchestrator emits a `BaRecommendation` and serializes its fields into a downstream tool's `extra` payload, sentinel's three gates verify the output structurally with zero orchestrator-side knowledge of hook plumbing.

  Two helpers on `BaRecommendation`: `is_structurally_ready_for_publication()` (at least one citation, at least one requirement_ref, structurally-complete spec_challenge — the *structural* floor below which the recommendation can't ship; gate verdicts add the audit-chain / matrix-match / scorer-quality layers on top), and `distinct_citation_count()` (dedupes by `artifact_id` so the "minimum cite-count" operator constraint isn't gamed by repeated citations of the same source).

  14 tests cover: `RecommendationId` empty rejection + whitespace trimming, `StakeholderAudience::key()` snake_case stability across all 4 variants, `BaDraftRequest::is_well_formed()` requires non-blank brief and tolerates empty constraints, `is_structurally_ready_for_publication()` true on a complete recommendation, false without citations, false without requirements, false with incomplete spec_challenge, `distinct_citation_count` dedupes repeated artifact_ids (3 entries with one duplicate → 2 distinct) and returns 0 for empty, full serde round-trip for both `BaDraftRequest` and `BaRecommendation`, `Send + Sync` for all four exported types. `crates/sentinel-domain/src/ba/mod.rs` re-exports the new types alongside the existing BA1+3 types. Sentinel-domain tests: **559 passing (545 prior + 14 new).** Zero new clippy warnings.

- **Lifecycle-key support for `EscalationAck` — closes the last gap in the exactly-once arc** (2026-05-19). Sentinel can now remove `SessionBlocked` / `SessionCompleted` / `SessionFailed` outbox entries when Legatus AI acks them by `(session_id, *_at_ms)` — not just `InstructionAck` / `InstructionResult` keyed by `instruction_id`.

  **New `OutboxItem { event: EscalationKind, at_ms: u64 }`** wrapper struct. The `at_ms` is captured at `LegatusHandle::escalate` time (or at-loopback time for the cancel-roundtrip path) AND used in the on-disk entry AND in the envelope the recv loop sends on the wire. That single stamp is what makes ack-matching possible across the network: the legatus-ai-daemon's `EscalationKey { session_id, *_at_ms }` references the *same* timestamp the legatus already stored, so a lookup by key is unambiguous.

  **Wire shape change on the outbox jsonl file**: was bare `EscalationKind` per line; is now `{"event": {...}, "at_ms": ...}`. `parse_entry` provides backwards-compat: tries the new wrapped shape first, falls back to bare-event with `at_ms = 0`. Legacy lifecycle entries lose ack-keyed cleanup (timestamp 0 won't match a real ack) but fall through to the existing `remove_head` post-send path. Acceptable on per-machine upgrade.

  **New `PersistentEscalationOutbox::remove_lifecycle(LifecycleKind, at_ms)`** with the same atomic-rewrite + fs2-locked discipline as `remove_head` / `remove_by_instruction_id`. Scans entries, matches the first `(variant, at_ms)` pair, rewrites the remainder. New `LifecycleKind { Blocked, Completed, Failed }` enum (kept here in `sentinel-legatus` — adapter concern, not a protocol type).

  **mpsc channel type change**: `mpsc::UnboundedSender<EscalationKind>` → `mpsc::UnboundedSender<OutboxItem>`. `LegatusHandle::escalate(event)` keeps the same public signature; the timestamp is stamped internally. The recv loop pops `OutboxItem`, builds the envelope using `item.at_ms` instead of a fresh `now_ms()`. The cancel-loopback in `handle_inbound` now persists to the outbox AND pushes to the loopback channel with the same `at_ms`, so the disk entry and the in-flight loopback share one canonical timestamp.

  **`handle_inbound` lifecycle arms wired**: `EscalationKey::SessionBlocked` / `SessionCompleted` / `SessionFailed` now verify the ack's `session_id` matches the connection's own session_id (defence: don't honour acks on behalf of foreign legati), then call `outbox.remove_lifecycle(kind, *_at_ms)`. Per-instruction arms unchanged.

  **Tests**: 7 new tests in `persistent_outbox` (lifecycle removal for each variant, no-match, variant-mismatch, missing file, per-instruction-skip, legacy-shape parse with `at_ms = 0`). 3 new tests in `client` (end-to-end lifecycle ack removal via `handle_inbound`, wrong-session_id rejection, cancel-loopback persists matching `at_ms`). 1 updated `escalate_succeeds_when_runtime_is_alive` test asserts the timestamp gets stamped. **Sentinel-legatus 52 tests passing, workspace 2295 / 0 failed.**

  The exactly-once arc is now end-to-end for both per-instruction AND lifecycle events.

- **`GET /legatus/pending` — operator-visible queue depths** (2026-05-19). New daemon HTTP route that reports the on-disk `inbox_pending` (operator instructions queued for the next Claude Code prompt) and `outbox_pending` (outbound escalations queued for WS send) as a single JSON snapshot. Drives `Legatus AI status`-style operator surfaces and smoke clients.

  **New `LegatusHandle::persistent_outbox()` accessor** symmetric with the existing `persistent_inbox()`. File I/O wrapped in `tokio::task::spawn_blocking` so the HTTP handler never stalls on the advisory lock. Returns `0`-counts for whichever direction lacks a persistent store (standalone-CLI legati without daemon-hosted disk state). Two new unit tests cover the accessor: seeded `make_pair_with_persistence` returns `Some(&outbox)` with live `len()` tracking through `escalate()`; `make_pair` + `make_pair_with_inbox` (outbox-less variants) honestly return `None` so the route returns `0` instead of panicking. Sentinel-legatus: 42 tests passing (40 prior + 2 new).

- **Sentinel handles inbound `EscalationAck` — closes the exactly-once arc on the consumer side** (2026-05-18). Third and final slice of the exactly-once escalation arc that started with the protocol message + legatus-ai-daemon-side emission. Sentinel's WS recv loop now processes the `Legatus AIMessage::EscalationAck` Legatus AI sends back after forwarding each escalation to its bus; per-instruction acks (`InstructionAcknowledged` / `InstructionResult`) drop the matching entry from the persistent outbox.

  **New `PersistentEscalationOutbox::remove_by_instruction_id`** (~+50 lines + 6 unit tests). Same atomic-rewrite + `fs2`-locked discipline as `remove_head`: open RW, take exclusive lock, scan all lines, remove the FIRST entry whose `EscalationKind` carries the target `instruction_id` (only `InstructionAck` and `InstructionResult` do; lifecycle variants are skipped), rewrite the remainder.

  **`client.rs::handle_inbound` new arm**: `Legatus AIMessage::EscalationAck(ack)` iterates `ack.acks`, calls `outbox.remove_by_instruction_id` for each per-instruction key. Lifecycle keys (`SessionBlocked` / `SessionCompleted` / `SessionFailed`) are no-ops in this slice — matching them by `(session_id, *_at_ms)` requires storing the sent-time timestamp on disk, which is the next refactor in this arc.

  **Delivery semantic now**: dual-track at-least-once with ack-driven cleanup. The existing post-`send_signed` `remove_head` stays as the head-of-line happy-path remover; the new ack-driven `remove_by_instruction_id` is the architectural seam for the next operator who wants true exactly-once-with-timeout-retry. Both paths converge on the same end state — whichever fires first wins; the other no-ops on empty queue.

  6 new outbox tests cover non-FIFO middle removal, the `InstructionResult` headline case (cancel-loopback), no-match, missing file, lifecycle-skip, and dup-defense. Sentinel-legatus: 40 tests passing (34 prior + 6 new). Whole workspace remains green. Zero net-new clippy errors over the pre-existing baseline.

  **The exactly-once arc is now end-to-end** (modulo lifecycle keys): protocol message (slice 1) + legatus-ai-daemon emits acks (slice 2) + sentinel removes outbox entries on ack (slice 3). Operators using the cancel-roundtrip path now have ack-driven cleanup. The post-send `remove_head` stays for graceful degradation when Legatus AI peers don't emit acks.

  **Out of scope (lifecycle-key support)**: storing the sent-time `*_at_ms` on each outbox entry so `remove_by_key(SessionBlocked { session_id, detected_at_ms })` can match by the full key. Currently lifecycle escalations rely on the at-least-once `remove_head` only. Acceptable — lifecycle events are self-correcting; per-instruction events are the ones that need exactly-once semantics for the operator's audit-trail correctness.

### Fixed
- **Operator-visible startup banners for daemon + legatus handshake** (2026-05-23). The `sentinel daemon` startup path and the `run_connect_hosted` Legatus AI-handshake path both emit only `info!` logs, but `tracing_subscriber`'s default filter is `warn` — so operators following the Fabrica `Legatus AI-sentinel-roundtrip.md` runbook saw Terminal 2 completely silent after starting the daemon, with no way to know (a) whether the daemon started, (b) where the bearer token lives, (c) what value to use for `Authorization: Bearer …`, or (d) whether the legatus actually handshook with the legatus-ai-daemon. Symptoms: HTTP 401 on every local API call, with no diagnostic signal.

  **Root cause.** Two failures stacked: (1) every operator-facing diagnostic was an `info!` filtered out at default log level; (2) the file `~/.claude/sentinel/daemon-token` is `{port}:{token}` format, but the auth middleware expects `{token}` only — operators who `cat` the file and paste-as-Bearer get 401, while no signal explains why.

  **Fix.** Added two stderr banners (visible regardless of `RUST_LOG`):
  - `daemon_cmd.rs::run` — startup banner on every daemon launch listing local API URL, token-file path with format note, ready-to-paste `Authorization: Bearer <token>` (no port prefix — matches what the middleware actually checks), and legatus configuration (legatus-ai-daemon URL / display name / heartbeat interval) when `--legatus-*` flags are set.
  - `sentinel-legatus/src/client.rs::run_connect_hosted` — handshake-complete banner emitted immediately after registration succeeds: legatus-ai-daemon URL, registered `session_id`, final `display_name` (post-collision-suffix), heartbeat interval.

  Banners use `eprintln!` so they appear regardless of subscriber configuration; structured `info!` lines remain for production log aggregation.

  Verified live: 2026-05-23 demo run with the new binaries confirmed (a) both banners visible, (b) banner-displayed token works against `GET /legatus/pending` (200 OK + JSON body), (c) `POST /legatus/escalate` returns 202 Accepted, (d) escalation drains the outbox over WS to legatus-ai-daemon with exactly-once-arc ack closure (outbox count returns to 0 within 3s).

- **UTF-8 char-boundary panic in `activity_tracker.rs`** (2026-05-22). The Stop hook panicked on commit messages containing multi-byte UTF-8 characters: `&cmd[..80]` byte-slicing through em-dash `—` (3 bytes) hit `end byte index 80 is not a char boundary` at line 239 (post-fix: line 266 in `process_stop`).

  **Root cause.** Two sites used plain byte-slicing for length-based truncation, which is unsafe for any user-controlled string that may contain non-ASCII characters (commit messages, task descriptions, file paths). The first panic surfaced from a commit body like `git add -A && git commit -m "docs(audit pass 3): CHANGELOG entry — full Pass-3 batch"` where the em-dash sat at bytes 79..82 and the 80-byte truncation cut through it.

  **Fix.** New private helper `truncate_to_char_boundary(s, max_bytes) -> &str` that backs off to the nearest valid UTF-8 char boundary using `str::is_char_boundary` (stable). Applied at both panic sites: `extract_command` (was `&s[..120]`) and `process_stop`'s git-command formatter (was `&cmd[..80]`). Two regression tests added: a direct unit test exercising `"abc—def"` with cuts at multiple offsets through the em-dash, and an end-to-end test reproducing the original panic input.

  Tests: 20 activity_tracker tests passing (18 prior + 2 new). Workspace remains green.

  **Follow-up audit needed.** Similar byte-slice patterns exist in 9 other files: `good_citizen_observer.rs:107`, `memory_extract.rs:426`, `phase_gate.rs:668,724,831`, `session_index.rs:314`, `task_rehydrate.rs:278`, `skill_router.rs:361`, `events.rs:647,654`, `evidence.rs:152`. All operate on user-controlled strings and can panic on the same class of input. Tracked separately.

- **`phase_gate` + `issue_suggest` tests — 4 failures across the test suite** (2026-05-18). All four were stale test expectations, not production bugs.

  **Three `phase_gate` tests** (`test_read_on_phase_file_records_and_advances`, `test_read_derives_skill_from_path`, `test_untrusted_file_does_not_advance_workflow`) asserted that `state.has_phase_been_read(...)` was `true` on the untrusted-file branch (file doesn't exist on disk, e.g. on CI / dev machines without the matching skill installed). This contradicts the security-correct production behavior: `phase_gate::process` deliberately returns early on `!info.trusted` WITHOUT calling `state.record_phase_read` so crafted paths can't inflate phase progress by recording phantom reads.
