Test docstrings were similarly stale ("File recorded for tracking" → untrusted files are NOT recorded). Updated all three tests to assert `!has_phase_been_read` on the untrusted branch; the `test_untrusted_file_does_not_advance_workflow` test rewritten to use a UUID-suffixed nonexistent path so it always exercises the untrusted branch regardless of dev-machine state. The tests now genuinely pin the security boundary instead of expecting it to be absent.

  **One `issue_suggest` test** (`suggest_picks_top_k_neighbours_by_similarity`) expected 3 neighbours to survive the `MIN_SIMILARITY = 0.2` filter, but actually only 2 do: the third historical issue `"fix login redirect after sso"` shares only `"login"` with the query `"fix login session bug"` (token sets {login, redirect, after, sso} ∩ {login, session, bug} = 1; ∪ = 6; Jaccard = 0.167, below threshold). Updated the assertion from `3` → `2` and the comment to walk through the per-issue Jaccard math. The test still pins the documented behavior (`suggest_picks_top_k_neighbours_by_similarity`) — the surviving two ARE the top-K by similarity; the third drops because it doesn't clear the floor.

  Full sentinel workspace: **1227 tests passing, 0 failed** (up from 1223 passing / 4 failed). Both touched files clippy-clean. No production code changed.

### Added
- **A13 Phase 5 — Config + `hook_cmd.rs` wiring (A13 enforcement is LIVE)** (2026-05-18). Final A13 phase. The substrate (Phases 1+2) + hook (Phase 3) + adapters (Phase 4a/b) are now stitched into the production hook engine. Operators flipping the mode in `~/.claude/sentinel/config/spec-challenge.toml` from `ObserveOnly` to `DefaultBlocking` makes A13 structural enforcement **active**: Irreversible+ work without a complete `SpecChallenge` is *structurally impossible* at the PreToolUse layer.

  **New `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/spec_challenge_config.rs`** (~250 lines + 13 unit tests). `SpecChallengeConfig { mode, catastrophic_axis_threshold }`. Builder API: `observe_only()` (the safe-rollout constant), `shipped()` (loads compile-time embedded defaults via `include_str!`), `from_toml_str(s)` (parses operator-supplied TOML), `with_shipped_and_overrides(Option<&Path>)` (production startup path). TOML schema: `[spec_challenge_gate] mode = "ObserveOnly"`, optional `catastrophic_axis_threshold = 0.7`. Missing section falls back to defaults; unknown mode strings surface at startup with a descriptive error (operator sees the typo at boot, not at runtime when a Catastrophic challenge silently fails enforcement). Threshold range-checked to `[0.0, 1.0]`. Hand-rolled mode-string parsing (no serde derive on `A13EnforcementMode` — it stays decoupled from infrastructure config concerns).

  **New `config/spec-challenge-defaults.toml`** baked in via `include_str!`. Defaults to `ObserveOnly` mode + `catastrophic_axis_threshold = 0.7` per spec §3 rollout posture. File includes operator-guidance comments explaining the three modes + the ratchet-up sequence.

  **`crates/sentinel-cli/src/hook_cmd.rs` wiring**: three integration points. (1) **Adapter construction** at session start — all three adapters degrade gracefully to `None` on failure: `FilesystemSpecChallengeStore` (failure → audit lift inert), `LlmSpecChallengeScorer::from_env` (failure → Catastrophic semantic scoring inert; hook still gates on completeness + denies with operator guidance when scoring is required but unavailable), `SpecChallengeConfig::with_shipped_and_overrides` (failure → falls back to `ObserveOnly`). All logged at `info`/`warn`. (2) **Hook call** in the PreToolUse arm BEFORE `dry_run_then_commit`: derives the class via the existing `LayeredReversibilityClassifier` (so A13 + A3 + tool_usage_gate agree on the class for any given tool), then calls `spec_challenge_gate::process_with_threshold(&input, class, store, scorer, mode, threshold)` wrapped in `time_and_record` for per-hook metric labels. Block decisions propagate to the final HookOutput via `output.merge`. (3) **State tracking**: `state.record_blocked()` on deny so blocked-hook telemetry stays accurate.

  **End-to-end activation path** (when operator flips mode): (a) operator edits `~/.claude/sentinel/config/spec-challenge.toml` to set `mode = "DefaultBlocking"`. (b) Next sentinel hook invocation reads the file at startup, builds `SpecChallengeConfig { mode: DefaultBlocking, catastrophic_axis_threshold: 0.7 }`. (c) Agent attempts an Irreversible tool call without emitting `extra.spec_challenge`: the gate denies with a `[Sentinel-Authority]`-prefixed reason naming the requirement. (d) Agent retries with a complete `SpecChallenge` JSON in `extra.spec_challenge`: the gate runs `completeness_findings()`; if clean the challenge is persisted to `~/.claude/sentinel/state/spec-challenges/{work_id}.json` and the gate allows. (e) For Catastrophic-class work, the gate additionally calls `LlmSpecChallengeScorer::score` and demands every axis ≥ `0.7`.

  13 unit tests on `SpecChallengeConfig` cover: shipped defaults parse cleanly (mode=ObserveOnly, threshold=0.7); `observe_only()` const matches shipped (no drift); explicit `DefaultBlocking` + `StrictBlocking` parse; unknown mode string `"TotallyMadeUp"` errors with descriptive message naming the bad value + expected variants; empty TOML falls back to defaults; threshold override parses (0.85); threshold out-of-range (1.5, -0.1) errors with "must be in"; malformed TOML errors with "parse" in the message; `with_shipped_and_overrides(None)` uses shipped only; `with_shipped_and_overrides(Some(<nonexistent path>))` uses shipped only; `with_shipped_and_overrides(Some(<real operator file>))` applies the override (StrictBlocking + threshold 0.9 via `tempfile::TempDir`); `SpecChallengeConfig` is `Send + Sync + Copy`.

  **A13 enforcement is operator-flippable.** Once orchestrators reliably emit `extra.spec_challenge` payloads on Irreversible+ tool calls, the single config flip moves "agent must articulate uncertainty before irreversible action" from observability to structural enforcement. Full workspace tests green: **sentinel-domain 545, sentinel-application 1227, sentinel-infrastructure 314 (+13 new) + 34 legatus + 157 cli — all passing.** Zero new clippy warnings on the new code (pre-existing `hook_cmd.rs` length warnings unchanged).

- **A13 Phase 4b — `LlmSpecChallengeScorer` adapter** (2026-05-18). Second infrastructure-layer commit of A13. Implements `SpecChallengeScorerPort` as an LLM-as-judge for the 5 spec-challenge categories. Mirrors the `LlmEvalScorer` (A12 Phase 3d-2) shape: `PromptFn` test seam, env-based provider selection (openrouter / ollama local + cloud), sidecar tokio runtime for sync→async bridging. Distinct env namespace (`SENTINEL_SPEC_CHALLENGE_SCORER_*`) so operators can run separate models for A3 dry-run auditing, A12 eval scoring, and A13 spec-challenge scoring in the same session.

  **What the judge scores**: NOT completeness — that's the deterministic floor handled by `SpecChallenge::completeness_findings`. The judge scores **semantic quality**: are the assumptions substantive or vague handwaves, are the gaps real or trivial, are ambiguities genuine forks or fake-for-show, are alternatives steelmanned or strawmanned, are the unsatisfied constraints substantive or filler. The hook layer (Phase 3) gates on the deterministic check + (for Catastrophic class) every axis above the operator-configured threshold.

  **Judge prompt (v1)**: hard-coded system prompt covering the 5 axes with explicit guidance per category. Calibration: when a category is `explicit_assertion_of_none`, score 0.7 if the reason is plausible and the work doesn't obviously call for items, score 0.4 if the reason looks like a dodge. Honest-uncertainty guidance keeps scores in `[0.4, 0.6]` when the judge can't tell — better than confidently wrong high or low values. Strict JSON output shape so the parser surfaces `Malformed` on any deviation; markdown code-fences are stripped before parsing.

  **New `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/spec_challenge_scorer.rs`** (~480 lines + 14 unit tests). `LlmSpecChallengeScorer::with_prompt_fn` (test seam) + `from_env` / `openrouter_from_env` / `ollama_from_env` / `*_with` resolver-injected variants. Sidecar runtime named `sentinel-spec-challenge-scorer-sidecar` for log greppability. Constants: `DEFAULT_SCORER_OPENROUTER_MODEL = "anthropic/claude-opus-4.7"`, `DEFAULT_SCORER_TIMEOUT = 60s`.

  14 tests with stub `PromptFn`s cover: well-formed JSON → `SpecChallengeScore` with correct per-axis values; markdown code-fence stripped; backend error surfaces as `Backend`; non-JSON response surfaces as `Malformed`; missing-axis JSON surfaces as `Malformed`; out-of-range values (1.7, -0.3) clamped via `SpecChallengeScore::new`; `all_axes_above(threshold)` works on judge output; unknown provider in env errors descriptively; `openrouter` without API key errors; `ollama` without `SENTINEL_SPEC_CHALLENGE_SCORER_MODEL` errors; timeout fallback + override; preview helper truncates / passes through. `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/lib.rs` exposes the new `spec_challenge_scorer` module. Sentinel-infrastructure: **302 tests passing (288 prior + 14 new).** Zero new clippy warnings.

- **A13 Phase 4a — `FilesystemSpecChallengeStore` adapter** (2026-05-18). First infrastructure-layer commit of A13. Implements `SpecChallengeStorePort` as one JSON file per challenge under `~/.claude/sentinel/state/spec-challenges/{work_id}.json`. Mirrors the `FilesystemEvalRunStore` (A12 Phase 3d-1) pattern: atomic temp+rename writes, lazy directory creation, `Ok(None)` vs `Err(Malformed)` discrimination on load, JSON-per-file (not JSONL) so save is atomically consistent under operator-visible diffs. Save overwrites on `work_id` collision per spec §6 — the typical case is "agent re-attempted after the first challenge was rejected."

  **New `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/spec_challenge_store.rs`** (~220 lines + 8 unit tests). `at_dir(PathBuf)` (test-scoping) + `with_default_path()` (production startup; resolves `~/.claude/sentinel/state/spec-challenges/`). `save` writes to `.tmp` then atomic `rename`, surfaces `StoreUnavailable` on filesystem failure and `Malformed` on serialization failure. `load` returns `Ok(None)` on `ErrorKind::NotFound` to distinguish "never emitted" from `Err(Malformed)` ("file exists but unreadable"). Pretty-printed JSON for operator-diffable audit records. 8 tests cover: lazy directory creation, full save→load round-trip preserves every category + nested item, `load` returns `None` on missing, `load` returns `Malformed` on corrupt JSON, save overwrites on `work_id` collision (verified by mutating `agent_id` between saves), no dangling `.tmp` after clean save, `with_default_path` resolves under `.claude` / `spec-challenges`, different work_ids get different files. TempDir-isolated. `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/lib.rs` exposes the new `spec_challenge_store` module. Sentinel-infrastructure: **288 tests passing (280 prior + 8 new).** Zero new clippy warnings.

- **A13 Phase 3 — `spec_challenge_gate` PreToolUse hook** (2026-05-18). Application-layer commit of the spec-challenge track. The hook reads `input.extra.spec_challenge` (the agent-emitted [`SpecChallenge`] JSON), runs the deterministic completeness check, persists via [`SpecChallengeStorePort`] (best-effort), and — for Catastrophic-class work — queries [`SpecChallengeScorerPort`] to verify every axis is above an operator-configured threshold. Reversibility-class-graded per spec §3 so the auditor-call budget stays bounded.

  **New `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/spec_challenge_gate.rs`** (~440 lines + 18 unit tests). Class-graded dispatch: `TriviallyReversible` skips (challenge cost not justified for trivial actions), `ReversibleWithEffort` allows (optional emission), `Irreversible` requires the challenge present AND completeness-clean, `Catastrophic` requires the challenge AND completeness AND scorer-all-axes-above-threshold (default 0.7, override via `process_with_threshold`). `A13EnforcementMode { ObserveOnly, DefaultBlocking, StrictBlocking }` matches the BA1+3 mode shape so operator config stays uniform; `StrictBlocking` ratchets `Irreversible` up to the same scoring requirement as `Catastrophic` for high-stakes domains.

  **Deny message shape**: missing challenge ("Irreversible work requires a SpecChallenge artifact in `extra.spec_challenge`. The agent must articulate its assumptions, gaps, ambiguities, alternatives_considered, and constraints_not_satisfied before acting"), malformed JSON (passes through the serde error), incomplete challenge (lists each `CompletenessFinding` with the affected category / topic / excerpt), missing scorer at Catastrophic ("...requires semantic scoring but no scorer is configured. Wire a `SpecChallengeScorerPort` adapter or downgrade the upcoming work's reversibility class"), scorer error (surfaces the underlying error verbatim), low scorer axis ("scorer rejected Catastrophic challenge — weakest axis 0.40 below threshold 0.70. Per-axis scores: assumptions=0.90, gaps=0.40, ambiguities=0.90, alternatives_considered=0.90, constraints_not_satisfied=0.90"). All deny strings flow through `HookOutput::deny` so they carry the `[Sentinel-Authority]` prefix.

  **Best-effort persistence**: store-save failures never block the gate. The audit trail is observability, not enforcement — if the store goes down, the proof chain loses a record but the gate decision stands on the in-process completeness/score check. Logged at `warn`.

  18 tests with a `RecordingStore` + `StubScorer` cover every dispatch path: TriviallyReversible always allows, ReversibleWithEffort allows missing challenge, Irreversible denies missing challenge (and `ObserveOnly` flips this to allow), Catastrophic denies missing challenge, malformed JSON denies, complete challenge allows Irreversible without scorer, incomplete challenge denies and names the failing category, store persists complete challenges, store failure doesn't block the allow path, Catastrophic denies when no scorer configured, Catastrophic allows when scorer returns high scores, Catastrophic denies when scorer returns a low axis (deny message surfaces `gaps=0.40`), Catastrophic denies on scorer error (surfaces "rate limit"), `StrictBlocking` scores `Irreversible` too, `DefaultBlocking` does NOT score `Irreversible` (verified by injecting a scorer that would fail if called), `process_with_threshold` threshold override is respected (0.5 passes; 0.7 fails on same input), `ObserveOnly` allows incomplete challenge.

  `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/mod.rs` exposes the new `spec_challenge_gate` module and adds `"spec_challenge_gate"` to `HOOK_NAMES`. Sentinel-application: **1227 tests passing (1209 prior + 18 new).** Zero new clippy warnings on the new file.

- **A13 Phase 2 — `SpecChallengeScorerPort` + `SpecChallengeStorePort` trait surface** (2026-05-18). Port-layer commit for the spec-challenge track. Adds the two outward boundaries the future `spec_challenge_gate` hook (Phase 3) will query: semantic scoring for Catastrophic-class challenges (the deterministic completeness check is the floor; the scorer is the per-axis quality bar above it), and persistence so the proof chain can re-verify "what did the agent challenge before it acted?" across sessions. Mirrors the established A12 / BA1+3 port pattern.

  **`crates/sentinel-domain/src/ports.rs` additions** (~155 lines + 10 unit tests). `SpecChallengeScore { assumptions, gaps, ambiguities, alternatives_considered, constraints_not_satisfied }` carries one `f32` per category, range `[0.0, 1.0]`, clamped at `new()`. `all_axes_above(threshold) -> bool` is the Catastrophic-gate predicate ("every axis ≥ threshold"); `min_axis() -> f32` powers the "weakest axis" rendering for local clients. The structured score is intentionally *not* parameterized by `ScoringRubric` (unlike A12's `EvalAxisScore`) because A13 scoring drives a gate decision, not an aggregate metric — a per-axis threshold is the operator-facing semantic.

  `SpecChallengeScorerError { Backend, Malformed, Configuration }` mirrors `EvalScorerError` exactly — same triad, same `Display` shape. `SpecChallengeScorerPort::score(challenge) -> Result<SpecChallengeScore, _>`: sync (matches `AuditorPort` / `EvalScorerPort`; adapters bridge async via sidecar tokio runtime). The trait is intentionally **not** called for Irreversible (non-Catastrophic) challenges — the hook layer (Phase 3) queries it only when `reversibility_class == Catastrophic`, keeping the auditor-call budget bounded.

  `SpecChallengeStoreError { StoreUnavailable, Malformed }` parallels `EvalRunStoreError`. `SpecChallengeStorePort::save(challenge)` + `load(&WorkId) -> Option<SpecChallenge>` (write-once-per-WorkId; re-emissions overwrite per spec §6 — the typical case is "agent re-attempted after the first challenge was rejected"). No `list_work_ids()` on the port — challenges are looked up by id during gating, not enumerated; the proof-chain consumer of the audit log handles discovery via its own catalog.

  10 unit tests cover: axis clamping (1.7→1.0, -0.3→0.0), `all_axes_above` true on uniform-at-threshold and false-with-margin, `all_axes_above` false when any single axis drops below, `min_axis` returns the smallest, `Display` covers each error variant + key substrings, `std::error::Error` blanket impl, `Send + Sync` for all three types, `Box<dyn …>` object-safety for both traits, and serde round-trip for both error types. Sentinel-domain: **545 passing (535 prior + 10 new).** Zero clippy warnings on the new code.

- **A13 Phase 1 — `spec_challenge` domain types** (2026-05-18). First commit of the spec-challenge track (per `docs/a13-spec-challenge.md` §2). Adds the structured artifact an acting agent emits *before* any Irreversible+ action: 5 categories of self-examination (`assumptions`, `gaps`, `ambiguities`, `alternatives_considered`, `constraints_not_satisfied`) plus a deterministic completeness check that names silent-empty categories. Pure domain; no ports, no IO. Future phases: 2 (ports for scoring + persistence), 3 (`spec_challenge_gate` `PreToolUse` hook with reversibility-graded enforcement), 4 (adapters), 5 (hook_cmd wiring).

  **New `crates/sentinel-domain/src/spec_challenge.rs`** (~480 lines + 16 unit tests). Identifiers: `WorkId` newtype (whitespace-trimmed; rejects empty), `SpecReference { hash, source }` (hash for change detection, source for human-readable attribution). Category items: `Assumption { statement, confidence: AssumptionConfidence (Low/Medium/High), blast_if_wrong: ReversibilityClass }`, `SpecGap { topic, how_resolved: GapResolution (OperatorClarified / InferredFromContext / DefaultApplied), inference_source: Option<String> }`, `Ambiguity { spec_excerpt, interpretations: Vec<String>, chosen, rationale }`, `Alternative { description, why_rejected }`, `UnsatisfiedConstraint { constraint, why_not_satisfiable, workaround: Option<String> }`.

  `ChallengeCategory<T> { items: Vec<T>, explicit_assertion_of_none: Option<String> }` is the core invariant carrier: a category is "filled" iff `!items.is_empty() || explicit_assertion_of_none.is_some()`. `new(items)` (silent-when-empty) + `none(reason)` (explicit-none) builders. `SpecChallenge` aggregates the 5 typed categories with `work_id`, `agent_id`, `challenged_spec`, `reversibility_class`, `created_at`.

  **`SpecChallenge::completeness_findings() -> Vec<CompletenessFinding>`** is the deterministic floor. Three finding shapes: `SilentEmpty { category: ChallengeCategoryName }` (silent-empty in any of the 5 categories — the diagnostic shape A13 exists to catch), `InsufficientInterpretations { excerpt_preview, count }` (ambiguity entry with `< 2` interpretations is malformed), `InferenceWithoutSource { topic }` (gap resolved via `InferredFromContext` without an `inference_source`). `is_block()` returns true for every finding — the hook layer collapses every finding into a block at Irreversible+ class. `is_complete() -> bool` is the `findings.is_empty()` convenience.

  16 unit tests cover: `WorkId` rejects empty/whitespace + trims, `ChallengeCategory::is_filled` discrimination (3 cases: items present, explicit-none, silent-empty), fully-filled challenge yields zero findings, silent-empty assumptions surfaces `SilentEmpty(Assumptions)`, explicit-none restores completeness, all-5-silent yields 5 findings (all `is_block`), single-interpretation ambiguity surfaces `InsufficientInterpretations { count: 1 }`, gap with `InferredFromContext` + `None` source surfaces `InferenceWithoutSource`, whitespace-only source string treated identically, `OperatorClarified` / `DefaultApplied` gaps need no source, `ChallengeCategoryName::key` is stable snake_case, serde round-trip, `Send + Sync` for all types. Sentinel-domain tests: **535 passing (519 prior + 16 new).** Zero clippy warnings on the new file.

- **Deferred classification — `InstructionOutcome::Deferred { waiting_on }` is no longer dead code** (2026-05-18). The fourth `InstructionOutcome` variant was unused since the failure-classification commit earlier this month; only `Success` / `Failure` / `Declined` were ever emitted. This commit teaches `classify_outcome` to detect conservative deferral phrasing in the model's reply at Stop time and emit `Deferred { waiting_on: "<phrase>" }` when the operator's instruction was acknowledged-but-postponed (e.g. `"I'll get to that"`, `"queued for later"`, `"noted for next session"`, `"skipping for now"`).

  **New signature**: `classify_outcome(signals, api_error, reply_text)`. The third parameter is `Option<&str>` carrying the assistant's concatenated text for this turn — already captured by `execution_log::process` for the execution-marker extraction; reused here as the deferral-detection corpus at zero extra parse cost. The `stop_failure` path passes `None` (API errors take precedence, no need to inspect text).

  **Precedence order** (most-specific wins): `api_error` → `Failure` → `PermissionDenied` signal → `Declined` → deferral phrase → `Deferred` → otherwise `Success`. Permission denial outranks deferral because a hard "tool blocked" is a concrete refusal while a deferral phrase is fuzzy intent. Pinned by `classify_outcome_permission_denied_beats_deferral_phrase` + `classify_outcome_api_error_beats_deferral_phrase` tests.

  **Deferral phrase list** (16 phrases, deliberately conservative): `"i'll get to"`, `"i'll come back to"`, `"i'll handle that later"`, `"i'll do that later"`, `"i will get to"`, `"queued for later"`, `"queuing this for"`, `"noted for later"`, `"noted for next"`, `"deferring this"`, `"deferring that"`, `"deferred for"`, `"will handle later"`, `"will do later"`, `"skipping for now"`, `"skipping this for now"`. All matched case-insensitively. Conservative on purpose — a false `Deferred` confuses the operator more than a missed one (operator just sees `Success` for what was actually deferred, which is the pre-classification behavior). Edge cases that look like deferrals but aren't (sequencing within the same turn, hedging language, conditional plans) deliberately fall through to `Success`. The returned `waiting_on` is the matched phrase as it appears verbatim, lowercased — short, recognizable, doesn't require the operator to read the model's full reply.

  **`execution_log` wiring**: the Stop hook now passes `Some(message.as_str())` — the assistant text it already captured for execution-marker scanning — into `classify_outcome`. Per-pending-instruction outcome reporting unchanged except for the variant: when a deferral phrase is detected, every pending instruction reports `Deferred { waiting_on }` instead of `Success`. Multiple instructions in the same turn share the deferral classification (same coarseness as the `Declined` path — we don't track per-instruction → per-tool-call correlation).

  **8 new unit tests** on `classify_outcome` covering the deferral path: 4 phrase-matching tests across the variant list (`i'll get to`, case-insensitivity, `queued for later`, `skipping for now`); 2 precedence tests pinning api_error and PermissionDenied beat deferral; 1 negative test for active-execution phrases (`"Done."`, `"Deploying staging now."`, `"Running the test suite."`, `"I checked the logs first; everything looks fine."`) — all yield `Success`; 1 edge case for empty reply text. All 4 prior `classify_outcome` tests updated to the 3-arg signature. Sentinel-application: 20 `legatus_client` tests passing.

  **Pre-existing failing tests** (`phase_gate` + `issue_suggest`) are unrelated to this change — same failures present in the prior inbox-persistence commit, they persist independently and don't block this slice.

  **Out of scope (remaining)**: LLM-based deferral detection for phrasings the heuristic misses (would mirror the existing LLM-fallback cancel parser pattern); per-tool-call → per-instruction correlation so `Deferred` can name which specific instruction was postponed (currently every pending instruction in a deferral-detected turn gets the same `Deferred` classification).

- **Sentinel daemon escalation outbox persistence — outbound events survive daemon crash** (2026-05-18). Symmetric to the inbox persistence shipped earlier this month. The `LegatusHandle::escalate()` path now writes every `EscalationKind` event to a file-backed FIFO at `~/.claude/sentinel/state/legatus-escalations.jsonl` before sending to the mpsc; the WS recv loop removes the head entry only after `send_signed` succeeds; on daemon startup any pending entries get replayed through the same mpsc channel as fresh escalations. Closes the consistency gap where a daemon crash between `escalate()` and the WS send would lose the event — the headline case being the `InstructionResult { Declined }` emitted from the cancel loopback in `client.rs::handle_inbound`, which is the operator-visible "I cancelled that for you" confirmation. With this commit, Legatus AI reliably gets the closing record across daemon restarts.

  **At-least-once semantics**: if the daemon crashes between successful WS send and `remove_head`, Legatus AI receives a duplicate event on the next daemon start. Legatus AI-side handlers are already idempotent — every `EscalationKind` variant is keyed by a stable id (`instruction_id` for `InstructionResult` / `InstructionAcknowledged`, `session_id` for the lifecycle events) so double-emission is a no-op.

  New `crates/sentinel-legatus/src/persistent_outbox.rs` (~+290 lines + 11 unit tests) mirrors `PersistentInbox` exactly — same `fs2` advisory-lock discipline, same atomic-rewrite strategy for `remove_head` (read all lines under exclusive lock, skip the first valid entry, rewrite the remainder), same module-level `#![allow(clippy::incompatible_msrv)]` for the fs2 method-name collision with std 1.89. Public API: `PersistentEscalationOutbox::new(path)`, `append(event)`, `remove_head() -> bool`, `snapshot()`, `len()`, `is_empty()`. New `default_outbox_path()` returns `~/.claude/sentinel/state/legatus-escalations.jsonl` (or `None` in degenerate `dirs::home_dir() = None` environments).

  **Handle/runtime wiring** (`handle.rs`): `LegatusHandle` gains an `outbox: Option<PersistentEscalationOutbox>` field; `LegatusRuntime` gains a matching field. New `make_pair_with_persistence(inbox, outbox)` constructor builds a pair with both directions persistent — the existing `make_pair` (no persistence) and `make_pair_with_inbox` (inbox only) constructors are preserved for the standalone CLI and inbox-only test paths. `escalate()` now appends to the outbox (if `Some`) before sending to the mpsc; disk-write failures are logged at `warn` and the mpsc send still proceeds (best-effort persistence per the same contract as inbox).

  **WS recv loop** (`client.rs::run_connect_hosted`): two changes. **(1) Startup replay** before entering the select loop — `outbox.snapshot()` is drained into `runtime.escalation_loopback` so any pre-existing disk entries flow through the normal escalation arm as if just escalated. Order is preserved by the snapshot's FIFO + the mpsc's send-order semantics. Logged at `info` with the count when non-zero. **(2) Post-send remove_head** — every successful `send_signed` in the escalation arm is followed by `outbox.remove_head()` (no-op when `outbox = None`), keeping the disk in sync with Legatus AI-receipt.

  **Daemon wiring** (`crates/sentinel-cli/src/daemon_cmd.rs`): the daemon now constructs both `PersistentInbox::new(default_inbox_path())` AND `PersistentEscalationOutbox::new(default_outbox_path())` at startup, passes both to `make_pair_with_persistence`. Backfill log lines at `info` if either path has prior pending entries from a previous run (the operator sees "rehydrated persistent outbox at startup — replaying on connect" when restarting the daemon mid-cancel). The no-home-dir fallback still uses the non-persistent `make_pair()` so the daemon runs in CI / chroot environments where `dirs::home_dir()` returns `None`.

  **11 new tests** on `PersistentEscalationOutbox`: empty-outbox-is-empty, append-then-snapshot, FIFO-order across appends, remove_head-strips-oldest-first (with subsequent-call-returns-false), remove_head-on-missing-file, append-after-remove_head-extends-remainder, malformed-lines-dropped, **declined_outcome_roundtrips_through_disk** (the headline use case — pins that `InstructionResult { Declined }` survives JSON roundtrip with the operator's reason), **events_survive_simulated_daemon_restart** (the second headline — fresh `PersistentEscalationOutbox` over the same path sees prior records), 20-thread concurrent-appends-all-persist, default_outbox_path shape. Sentinel-legatus: 34 tests passing (20 inbox + 6 handle + 5 misc + 11 new outbox). Whole workspace remains green.

  **Out of scope (deferred)**: protocol-level escalation acks from Legatus AI so sentinel can use exactly-once instead of at-least-once (would be a legatus-ai-protocol addition + matching Legatus AI-side handling); SQLite-backed outbox for operators who want shared-database-grade durability (the JSONL file is already crash-safe for single-daemon use); operator-visible "I have N pending escalations on disk" surface (operators can `wc -l ~/.claude/sentinel/state/legatus-escalations.jsonl` for now).
### Added
- **A12 Phase 3e — `sentinel eval run` CLI subcommand (A12 runner end-to-end LIVE)** (2026-05-18). Final commit of the A12 benchmark-runner arc. Operators can now invoke `sentinel eval run --run-id <id> --candidates path/to/outputs.json` to load the corpus, replay recorded candidate outputs through the configured `EvalScorerPort` (LLM-as-judge by default), and persist a complete `EvalRunResult` at `~/.claude/sentinel/eval/ba-corpus/runs/{run_id}.json`. The 5-layer DDD stack — domain (3a) → ports (3b) → use case (3c) → JSONL store (3d-1) + LLM scorer (3d-2) → CLI (3e) — is now end-to-end shippable.

  **New `Run` subcommand** under the existing `Eval` clap variant. Flags: `--run-id <ID>` (required; persisted at `{runs_dir}/{run_id}.json`, re-runs of the same id overwrite), `--candidates <PATH>` (required; JSON object mapping `case_id -> output_text` — Phase 3e is replay-only, live-LLM dispatch via the A2 router is a future iteration), `--case-id <ID>` (repeatable; filters which cases run; unset means "all cases in the corpus"), `--corpus-dir <PATH>` + `--runs-dir <PATH>` (operator overrides for the two default `~/.claude/sentinel/eval/ba-corpus/` paths), `--json` (emit the full `EvalRunResult` as pretty JSON instead of a human summary).

  **New `crates/sentinel-cli/src/eval_cmd.rs` additions** (~280 lines of new code + 12 unit tests on top of the existing 6 list tests). `RunArgs` struct carries the parsed flags. `run(args)` is the production entry point — builds `LlmEvalScorer::from_env()`, `build_corpus`, `build_run_store`, then delegates to the generic test seam `run_with<St: EvalRunStorePort, Sc: EvalScorerPort>(&args, &corpus, &store, &scorer)`. The generic signature lets tests inject a `RecordingStore` + `StubScorer` without touching env vars or the LLM. `load_candidates` parses the JSON candidates file and validates each `case_id` through `EvalCaseId::new` (an invalid key surfaces with the offending value quoted). `load_cases` enumerates the corpus + filters by `--case-id` (when set). The human-readable summary prints run id, started/completed timestamps, case counts, mean composite (or `<no successful cases>` placeholder), per-axis mean (deterministic axis order via `BTreeMap`), and an "Errored cases" section when any case failed.

  12 new tests cover: end-to-end happy path (2 cases → scored + persisted via `RecordingStore`), `--case-id` filter restricts to 1 case from a 2-case corpus, missing candidate output records producer error + the run still saves, empty corpus errors with "no cases to run", invalid run id ("" rejected by `EvalRunId::new`) surfaces an error naming the bad id, `load_candidates` happy path + invalid case_id (`""` key rejected by `EvalCaseId::new`) + missing file + malformed JSON, `--json` mode succeeds and still persists, `build_run_store` with override + with default. Sentinel-cli: **157 tests passing (145 prior + 12 new).** Zero new clippy warnings.

- **A12 Phase 3d-2 — `LlmEvalScorer` adapter** (2026-05-18). Second infrastructure-layer commit of the runner. Implements `EvalScorerPort` as an LLM-as-judge: every `(case, candidate_output, run_id)` triple is rendered into a judge prompt, sent through a `rig-core` client, and the JSON response is parsed into 6 `EvalAxisScore`s (rubric weights pulled from the case) → `EvalScore`. Mirrors the existing `RigAuditor` pattern (sidecar tokio runtime, `PromptFn` test seam, env-based provider selection) so the BA-Eval scoring surface shares its operational shape with the dry-run auditor.

  **Providers**: `SENTINEL_EVAL_SCORER_PROVIDER` selects `openrouter` (default; needs `OPENROUTER_API_KEY`, default model `anthropic/claude-opus-4.7` overridable via `SENTINEL_EVAL_SCORER_MODEL`) or `ollama` (auto-detects local vs cloud by `OLLAMA_API_KEY` presence; requires `SENTINEL_EVAL_SCORER_MODEL` — no sensible default for ollama). Timeout via `SENTINEL_EVAL_SCORER_TIMEOUT_SECS` (default 60s). Distinct env namespace from `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_*` so operators can run an A3 auditor and an A12 scorer on different models in the same session.

  **Judge prompt (v1)**: a single hard-coded system prompt covering the 6 axes (`citation_density_accuracy`, `requirements_coverage`, `alternatives_seriousness`, `tonal_calibration`, `outcome_realism`, `stakeholder_fit`) with explicit guidance on the 0.0-1.0 scale + the "rate 0.5 with 'not scorable' note" convention for `outcome_realism` when `gold_outcomes` is absent. Returns JSON `{"axes": {…}, "reasoning": "…"}` — the strict shape lets the parser surface `EvalScorerError::Malformed` on any deviation (missing axis, bad JSON, code-fence-only wrap is stripped before parse). The user-prompt JSON carries `case_id`, `stakeholder_brief`, `gold_artifact` (text + author), `gold_outcomes_present` flag, and `candidate_output`. The prompt is v1; operators iterate by recompiling — the rubric weights live on the case so weight tuning needs no adapter change.

  **New `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/eval_scorer.rs`** (~480 lines + 15 unit tests). `LlmEvalScorer::with_prompt_fn` (test seam) + `from_env` / `openrouter_from_env` / `ollama_from_env` / `*_with` resolver-injected variants (test seam matches the `RigAuditor` env-resolver pattern; `unsafe_code = "forbid"` upheld). `Debug` impl elides the closure for clean logs. Sidecar tokio runtime is a module-local `OnceLock<Option<Runtime>>` named `sentinel-eval-scorer-sidecar` for log greppability.

  15 tests with stub `PromptFn`s cover: well-formed JSON response → `EvalScore` with correct per-axis raws + rubric weights picked up (`OutcomeRealism = 2.0` from `ba_default`); markdown code-fence (`\`\`\`json … \`\`\``) is stripped before parse; backend error (network unreachable) surfaces as `EvalScorerError::Backend`; non-JSON response surfaces as `Malformed`; missing-axis JSON surfaces as `Malformed`; out-of-range axis values (1.7, -0.3) get clamped to [0.0, 1.0] via `EvalAxisScore::new`; composite reflects rubric weights (uniform 0.5 across all axes → composite 0.5 with `ba_default`); `case_id` + `run_id` thread through to the returned `EvalScore`; unknown provider in env errors with descriptive message; `openrouter` without API key errors; `ollama` without `SENTINEL_EVAL_SCORER_MODEL` errors (no default); timeout parsing fallback + override; preview helper truncates / passes through. `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/lib.rs` exposes the new `eval_scorer` module alongside `eval_corpus` / `eval_run_store`. Sentinel-infrastructure: **280 tests passing (265 prior + 15 new).** Zero new clippy warnings.

- **A12 Phase 3d-1 — `FilesystemEvalRunStore` adapter** (2026-05-18). First infrastructure-layer commit of the runner persistence track. Implements `EvalRunStorePort` (save / load / list) as one JSON file per run under `~/.claude/sentinel/eval/ba-corpus/runs/{run_id}.json` per spec §3.5. The LLM-as-judge scorer adapter is its own Phase 3d-2 commit; this commit unblocks the CLI runner immediately by giving it somewhere to persist results.

  **Why JSON-per-file, not JSONL?** Each run carries a complete `EvalRunResult` (every case's candidate output + score + timing + error context). Appending a partial run line-by-line opens a window where readers see a half-written run. JSON-per-file under the standard temp+rename pattern (`{run_id}.json.tmp` → atomic `rename` to `{run_id}.json`) gives `load` a clean either-prior-or-new read with no torn writes.

  **New `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/eval_run_store.rs`** (~280 lines + 13 unit tests). `FilesystemEvalRunStore::at_dir(PathBuf)` (test-scoping) + `with_default_path()` (production startup; resolves `~/.claude/sentinel/eval/ba-corpus/runs/`). `save` lazy-creates the runs directory if missing (operators don't have to bootstrap it; first save creates it), serializes with `to_string_pretty` (human-diffable run records), writes to `.tmp`, then `rename`s atomically; on overwrite (same `run_id` re-saved), the prior content is replaced cleanly. `load` returns `Ok(None)` on `ErrorKind::NotFound` to distinguish "never saved" from `Err(Malformed)` ("file exists but unreadable"). `list_run_ids` returns `Vec<EvalRunId>` sorted alphabetically; skips dotfiles, non-`.json` files (including `.tmp` partial writes via the `Path::extension` case-insensitive check), and filenames whose stem doesn't parse as a valid `EvalRunId` (legacy/stray files don't poison the listing).

  13 tests cover: lazy directory creation on first save, save→load round-trip preserves the full `EvalRunResult` (including per-case `EvalScore`s + `error: None`/`Some` slots), `load` returns `Ok(None)` on missing runs, `load` returns `EvalRunStoreError::Malformed` on corrupt JSON, save overwrites on `run_id` collision (verified by mutating `timing_ms` between saves), `list_run_ids` returns empty on nonexistent + empty dirs, sorted listing across 3 runs ("zeta"/"alpha"/"middle" → ["alpha","middle","zeta"]), `.tmp` partial-write filtering, non-`.json` + dotfile filtering, unparseable-stem filtering (an empty filename `.json` is silently skipped), `with_default_path` resolves under `.claude` / `ba-corpus` / `runs`, and the temp file is cleaned up after a clean save. TempDir-isolated; zero shared filesystem state. `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/lib.rs` exposes the new `eval_run_store` module alongside the existing `eval_corpus`. Sentinel-infrastructure: **265 tests passing (252 prior + 13 new).** Zero new clippy warnings on the new file.

- **A12 Phase 3c — `eval_run::execute_run` benchmark-runner use case** (2026-05-18). Application-layer commit. The runner accepts a batch of `EvalCase`s, a `produce_candidate` closure (caller-supplied: static fixture for replay-style runs, live LLM via the A2 router for production runs, or whatever else fits the context), and an `EvalScorerPort` instance, then loops once-per-case to produce an `EvalRunResult`. Errored cases stay in the run record — the loop never short-circuits — so telemetry sees both successes and failures.

  **New `crates/sentinel-application/src/eval_run.rs`** (~360 lines + 9 unit tests). `execute_run<F, S, C>(run_id, cases, produce_candidate: F, scorer: &S, clock: C)` where `F: FnMut(&EvalCase) -> Result<String, String>`, `S: EvalScorerPort`, `C: FnMut() -> DateTime<Utc>`. Per-case timing via monotonic `std::time::Instant` (so DST/NTP shifts during a run don't produce negative durations); wall-clock timestamps via the operator-supplied `clock` (`chrono::Utc::now` in production, deterministic tick-counter in tests). Error semantics are uniform: producer error → `error = Some("producer error: ...")` + empty `candidate_output` + scorer **not called**; scorer error → `error = Some("scorer error: ...")` + `candidate_output` populated; success → `error = None` + `score = Some(_)`. The error message prefix lets reports distinguish dispatch failures from scoring failures without parsing.

  **`static_candidate_producer<H: BuildHasher>(HashMap<EvalCaseId, String, H>)`** ships alongside the runner as the canonical replay-style producer (load recorded outputs from a JSON file, iterate on rubric weights without burning fresh LLM calls). Generalized over the `HashMap` hasher so callers can use `FxHashMap` etc. without an extra collect.

  9 unit tests with a `StubScorer` (`EvalScorerPort` test double: uniform score across axes + configurable per-`case_id` `EvalScorerError` injection) cover: all-successful 3-case run aggregates correctly, producer-missing-output records error + names the `case_id`, scorer failure preserves `candidate_output` and surfaces the scorer error message ("rate limit"), empty input yields empty run with `mean_composite() = None`, clock calls fire in `(started_at, per-case completed_at, run completed_at)` order (3 ticks for a 1-case run), `case_results` ordering matches input ordering (not sorted), mixed producer + scorer failures across 3 cases (1 success / 1 producer-fail / 1 scorer-fail) produce the right per-case shape, and `static_candidate_producer` round-trips recorded outputs + errors on missing case_ids. `crates/sentinel-application/src/lib.rs` exposes the new `eval_run` module alongside `engine` / `gate` / etc. Sentinel-application: **1201 tests passing (1192 prior + 9 new).** Zero new clippy warnings.

- **A12 Phase 3b — `EvalScorerPort` + `EvalRunStorePort` trait surface** (2026-05-18). Port-layer commit for the A12 benchmark runner. Adds the two outward-facing trait boundaries the runner (Phase 3c) queries — one for "score a candidate output against a case" (LLM-as-judge in the eventual Phase 3d adapter), one for "persist + retrieve full run records" (JSONL adapter in 3d). Pure-domain: traits + error enums only, no IO, no application logic.

  **`crates/sentinel-domain/src/ports.rs` additions** (~140 lines + 6 unit tests, sandwiched between the BA1+3 section and its test module so the dependency order stays linear): `EvalScorerError { Backend(String), Malformed(String), Configuration(String) }` mirrors the failure-mode triad used by `AuditorPort`/`RoutingError` — Backend = transient (LLM timeout, rate limit), Malformed = adapter couldn't decode response into `Vec<EvalAxisScore>`, Configuration = operator-side fault (missing model handle, bad key) that surfaces at startup. `EvalScorerPort::score(case: &EvalCase, candidate_output: &str, run_id: &EvalRunId) -> Result<EvalScore, EvalScorerError>` — sync (matches `AuditorPort`; adapter bridges to async backend via `block_on` like `RigAuditor`). The full `EvalCase` is passed so the scorer can honor per-case rubric overrides + read `gold_artifact`/`gold_outcomes` without the application layer plumbing them.

  `EvalRunStoreError { StoreUnavailable(String), Malformed(String) }` mirrors `ProvenanceError`'s soft-warn shape — `Malformed` is distinct from `Ok(None)` on `load` (record exists but unreadable vs. record doesn't exist). `EvalRunStorePort::save(&EvalRunResult)` is write-once-per-run (runner persists at end after accumulating all `EvalCaseResult`s; no per-case write API on the port to keep the store atomically consistent), `load(&EvalRunId) -> Result<Option<EvalRunResult>, _>`, and `list_run_ids() -> Result<Vec<EvalRunId>, _>` for the future `sentinel eval list-runs` CLI. Save is documented-overwrite on collision (Phase 3d JSONL adapter overwrites because runs come from explicit operator action — the typical case is "retry after a backend fix").

  6 unit tests: `Display` covers each variant + key substrings, `std::error::Error` blanket-impl, `Send + Sync` for both error types, `Box<dyn EvalScorerPort>` + `Box<dyn EvalRunStorePort>` object-safety check, and serde round-trip for both errors. Sentinel-domain tests: **519 passing (513 prior + 6 new).** Zero new clippy warnings on `ports.rs`.

- **A12 Phase 3a — `EvalCaseResult` + `EvalRunResult` domain types** (2026-05-18). Runtime envelope around the existing `EvalScore` (Phase 1) — the type spine the benchmark runner (Phase 3c), JSONL run store (Phase 3d), and `sentinel eval run` CLI (Phase 3e) will all share. Pure domain: no ports, no IO.

  **New `crates/sentinel-domain/src/eval/result.rs`** (~390 lines + 14 tests): `EvalCaseResult { case_id, run_id, candidate_output, score: Option<EvalScore>, timing_ms, completed_at, error: Option<String> }` carries the agent's output text + wall-clock timing + a dispatch/scoring error slot so failed cases stay in the run record rather than disappearing for telemetry. `is_success()` requires both `error.is_none()` and `score.is_some()`. `EvalRunResult { run_id, started_at, completed_at, case_results }` aggregates a benchmark run with four summary methods: `successful_case_count`, `errored_case_count`, `mean_composite` (returns `Option<f32>` — `None` when no successful cases, deliberately preserving the "no data" / "score zero" distinction), `mean_per_axis` (`Vec<(EvalAxis, f32)>`, deterministic axis ordering via `BTreeMap` traversal, axes absent from every successful case are omitted), and `pass_rate(threshold)` (`f32` in `[0.0, 1.0]`; `0.0` floor when no successful cases since reports prefer a concrete rate over `None`). Both types `Serialize + Deserialize` via serde for the future JSONL store, with full round-trip tests.

  **`crates/sentinel-domain/src/eval/mod.rs`** re-exports `EvalCaseResult` + `EvalRunResult` alongside the existing `EvalScore`/`ScoringRubric`/case types. The 14 unit tests cover: success/error discrimination, composite passthrough, count helpers across mixed runs, mean-composite excludes errored cases, `None` semantics on empty/all-errored runs, mean-per-axis correctness (two cases at 0.4 + 0.8 each → 0.6 per axis), empty-axis-result when no successes, pass-rate threshold split (composites 0.9/0.8/0.5/0.3 at threshold 0.7 → 0.5), pass-rate-zero floor on errored-only runs, pass-rate one when all pass, and serde round-trip for both types in successful and errored shapes. `chrono::DateTime<Utc>` for timestamps (already a workspace dep used in `ba/provenance.rs`, `agent_routing.rs`, etc.). Sentinel-domain tests: **513 passing (499 prior + 14 new).** Zero new clippy warnings on `eval/result.rs`.

- **A12 Phase 2 — `FilesystemEvalCorpus` loader + `sentinel eval list` CLI** (2026-05-18). Operators can now drop `EvalCase` JSON files under `~/.claude/sentinel/state/ba-corpus/cases/` (public split) and `~/.claude/sentinel/state/ba-corpus/private-test-split/` (held-back, per spec §3.4) and enumerate them with `sentinel eval list` (table or `--json`). Honors the spec §3.4 rule that private-split cases are loadable by case_id but flagged so callers can refuse to render them in public outputs. Tests cover: empty corpus, populated public-only, populated private-only, mixed, malformed JSON, non-existent dir, case_id collision across splits (private wins). Builds the corpus via `build_corpus` (uses override path when provided, else `with_default_path()`), enumerates cases, and renders either a `serde_json` payload or a 2-column table (`case_id`, `split`) with a summary header showing total/public/private counts. Empty-corpus path emits operator guidance pointing at the expected drop directories.

Dispatch routes `Commands::Eval { action: EvalAction::List { json, dir } }` to `eval_cmd::list(json, dir)`. `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/lib.rs` exposes the new `eval_corpus` module alongside the existing adapters.

- **SEN-4 + SEN-19 — Issue auto-suggest + enterprise operational summary (2026-05-18, `107a7ec`).** New `crates/sentinel-application/src/issue_suggest.rs` ranks historical Linear issues against a candidate title via Jaccard similarity over a stop-word-filtered token set; returns suggested estimate (median), priority (mode, ties broken by more-urgent), and labels (present in ≥ceil(50%) of usable neighbours) with same-team boost on ties and Confidence reflecting neighbour count. New `crates/sentinel-application/src/operational_summary.rs` is the single integration point that reads every shipped sentinel summary file (deploys, lead-times, change-failure, stage-thresholds, per-stage-breakdown, throughput, first-time-pass, cost-per-point, ROI, cache-efficiency, pr-review) and writes one combined `operational-summary.json` with per-section `loaded` flags so consumers render "no data" cleanly when files are missing. 13 unit tests; pure data layers.

- **SEN-5 + SEN-16 — Throughput + first-time-pass + rework cost (2026-05-18, `5de774e`).** New `crates/sentinel-application/src/throughput.rs` reads cycle-time events to produce per-team `completed_30d`/`completed_7d`/`completed_per_week`/`completed_per_month` plus a 60-day daily completion sparkline (SEN-5), and detects rework loops by spotting "back to In Progress after entering Code Review / QA Testing / QA Failed" — emitting per-ticket `had_rework_loop` flags and per-team FTP rate + optional rework-cost-USD sum joined against `tokens-per-ticket.jsonl` (SEN-16). 13 unit tests; pure data layers.

- **SEN-3 + SEN-6 — Cycle-time prediction + forced decomposition (2026-05-18, `ef15cb9`).** New `crates/sentinel-application/src/cycle_time_prediction.rs` consumes the SEN-17 per-stage breakdown snapshot to predict a ticket's total cycle time + per-stage path expectations with a Confidence tier from the minimum sample count along the path; team-specific rows preferred, team-agnostic fallback. Plus a `requires_decomposition(prediction, rule)` rule that fires when estimate > 8h OR predicted total > sum(p75) × 2.0 (defaults configurable via `DecompositionRule`). 11 unit tests; pure functions.

- **SEN-2 + SEN-17 — Cycle-time analytics (stale thresholds + per-stage breakdown) (2026-05-18, `73f8721`).** New `crates/sentinel-application/src/cycle_time_analytics.rs` consumes `cycle-time.jsonl` and emits two percentile-driven summaries: per-(team, from_stage) p50/p75/p90 dwell time for stale-ticket threshold calibration (SEN-2), and per-(team, stage) mean + p50 + p75 for downstream metric consumers (SEN-17). Both reuse a single `pair_transitions` helper that diffs adjacent cycle-time events per `issue_id`. 9 unit tests.

- **SEN-10 + SEN-11 — Lead time, CFR, MTTR collectors (2026-05-18, `3e3d2ce`).** Two new application-layer modules complete the four DORA core metrics (deploy freq shipped as SEN-9). `crates/sentinel-application/src/lead_time.rs` carries `LeadTimeRecord`, append/read helpers, and `aggregate_at` producing per-(repo, env) rolling 30-day p50/p75/p95 with DoraTier from p50. `crates/sentinel-application/src/change_failure.rs` carries `IncidentRecord`, append/read helpers, and an `aggregate_at` that joins `deploys.jsonl` to incidents within a 24h attribution window — CFR = `failed_deploys / deploys` (denominator-zero safe), MTTR = median of `(completed_at - created_at) / 1h` over recovered incidents, both producing per-(repo, env) DoraTier classifications. `deploy_freq.rs` gained three boundary-classifier helpers — `DoraTier::from_lead_time_hours`, `from_change_failure_rate`, `from_mttr_hours` — so the Rust collectors produce stable tier labels. 20 new unit tests across the modules (lead-time round-trip / missing file / malformed line / window filter / percentile correctness / garbage-hours skip; change-failure round-trip / missing file / zero-deploy CFR / in-window attribution / out-of-24h rejection / cross-(repo, env) isolation / MTTR exclusion of unrecovered / MTTR zero / malformed line; boundary coverage for all three new classifiers). CLI wrappers + Hookdeck/webhook ingest deferred to follow-ups — this PR ships the application-layer seam in the same shape as SEN-9. **Verification gap:** `cargo build` is currently blocked workspace-wide by a pre-existing missing sister-repo path dep (`legatus-ai`) — also blocks builds on `main`. The new modules follow `deploy_freq.rs`'s verified pattern line-for-line; restoring the sister repo unblocks `cargo test -p sentinel-application` against this commit.

- **BA1+3 Phase 4c — Config loader + `hook_cmd.rs` wiring (BA1+3 enforcement is LIVE)** (2026-05-17). Final BA1+3 phase. The substrate (Phases 1+2) + hooks (Phase 3a/b/c) + adapters (Phase 4a/b) are now stitched into the production hook engine. Operators flipping a mode in `~/.claude/sentinel/config/ba-enforcement.toml` from `ObserveOnly` to `DefaultBlocking` makes BA1 + BA3 structural-violations *impossible* at the PreToolUse layer for the BA-vertical product.

  **New `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/ba_config.rs`** (~250 lines + 12 unit tests): `BaEnforcementConfig` struct carrying both hooks' `ValidationMode` choices. Builder API: `observe_only()` (the safe-rollout constant), `shipped()` (loads compile-time embedded defaults), `from_toml_str(s)` (parses operator-supplied TOML), `with_shipped_and_overrides(Option<&Path>)` (production startup path — shipped defaults overridden by `~/.claude/sentinel/config/ba-enforcement.toml` when present). TOML schema: `[provenance_validate] mode = "ObserveOnly"` + `[requirements_traceability_gate] mode = "ObserveOnly"`. Missing sections fall back to `ObserveOnly`; unknown mode strings surface at startup with a descriptive `anyhow::Error` (operator sees the typo at boot, not at production runtime when a citation fails silent enforcement). Hand-rolled mode-string parsing via `match` (no serde derive on the hook `ValidationMode` enums — they stay decoupled from infrastructure config concerns).

  **New `config/ba-enforcement-defaults.toml`** baked in via `include_str!`. Both hooks default to `ObserveOnly` (the spec §3 rollout posture). File includes extensive header comments explaining the three modes + the ratchet-up sequence: `ObserveOnly` → `DefaultBlocking` (once telemetry shows the BA6 connector layer reliably emits `provenance_audit` events AND the BA-orchestrator writes matrix snapshots) → `StrictBlocking` (per-output, for catastrophic-class tools).

  **`crates/sentinel-cli/src/hook_cmd.rs` wiring**: three integration points land together. (1) **Adapter construction** at session start — both adapters degrade gracefully to `None` if `with_default_path()` fails: `JsonlProvenanceStore` (failure → BA1 audit lift + validation inert with `tracing::info` log), `FilesystemRequirementMatrix` (failure → BA3 traceability inert). The dirs::home_dir failure path is the only realistic trigger on configured systems. (2) **Config load** via `BaEnforcementConfig::with_shipped_and_overrides(home/.claude/sentinel/config/ba-enforcement.toml)` — fallback to `BaEnforcementConfig::observe_only()` on parse failure (safe degrade: operator sees the warn log + their typo'd config is ignored rather than crashing the hook engine). (3) **Hook calls**: in the `PostToolUse` arm, `audit_extract` fires at the TOP of the arm via `hooks::audit_extract::process(&input, provenance_arc.as_ref())` (gated on `provenance_store.is_some()`); in the `PreToolUse` arm, `provenance_validate` + `requirements_traceability_gate` fire BEFORE `dry_run_then_commit` via `time_and_record` (with per-hook metric labels for observability) — both gated on their respective adapter `is_some()`. Each hook output goes through `output.merge(&...)` so block decisions propagate to the final HookOutput.

  **End-to-end activation path** (when operator flips modes): (a) operator edits `~/.claude/sentinel/config/ba-enforcement.toml` to set both modes to `DefaultBlocking`. (b) Next sentinel hook invocation reads the file at startup, builds `BaEnforcementConfig { provenance_validate_mode: DefaultBlocking, requirements_traceability_mode: DefaultBlocking }`. (c) Claude tries to publish a BA output with citations: a `Bash` or BA-orchestrator tool call carrying `input.extra.artifacts: [...]` triggers `provenance_validate` in the PreToolUse arm. (d) The hook queries `JsonlProvenanceStore::query_artifact_history(artifact_id)` for each citation, runs the 4-check tree (Existence/Freshness/ProvenanceClass/WithinSession) with the operator's `DefaultBlocking` mode, returns `HookOutput::deny()` on Block-class findings (Existence). (e) Operator's tool call is denied with a `[Sentinel-Authority]`-prefixed reason naming each failing citation. Same path for `requirements_traceability_gate` reading `FilesystemRequirementMatrix`. (f) When everything is structurally clean, both hooks return `allow()` and the downstream `dry_run_then_commit` + `tool_usage_gate` checks run normally.

  12 unit tests on `BaEnforcementConfig` cover: shipped defaults parse cleanly + both modes are `ObserveOnly`; `observe_only()` constant matches shipped (no drift between the const and the TOML); explicit `DefaultBlocking` parses for both hooks; explicit `StrictBlocking` parses for both hooks; empty TOML falls back to `ObserveOnly`; only-one-section TOML leaves the other section at `ObserveOnly`; unknown mode string `"TotallyMadeUp"` errors with a descriptive message naming the invalid value + expected variants; malformed TOML surfaces at parse time with "parse" in the message; `with_shipped_and_overrides(None)` uses shipped only; `with_shipped_and_overrides(Some(<nonexistent path>))` uses shipped only; `with_shipped_and_overrides(Some(<real operator file>))` applies the override (verified with a `tempfile::TempDir`-backed operator file containing `DefaultBlocking + StrictBlocking`); `BaEnforcementConfig` is `Send + Sync + Copy`. Sentinel-infrastructure: 236 tests passing (224 prior + 12 new). Sentinel-cli: 139 tests passing (unchanged — hook_cmd.rs modifications are additive and behind `is_some()` gates so the existing test paths see `None` adapters and skip the new hooks).

  Clippy clean on the new code (`ba_config.rs` zero warnings; the new `hook_cmd.rs` insertions in lines 260-313, 547-577, 710-715 produce zero new clippy warnings — the remaining infrastructure warnings on `hook_cmd.rs` are pre-existing on lines 26, 47, 143, 353 from the existing run/run_internal structure). Pre-existing `phase_gate` test failures (task #21) unchanged.

  **Out of scope for Phase 4c (future Phase 4d)**: `config/ba-outputs.toml` tool-name registry — currently the hooks self-gate via structural field-presence triggers (`input.extra.artifacts` for `provenance_validate`; `input.extra.requirement_refs` / `is_recommendation` for `requirements_traceability_gate`), which is sufficient for any BA flow that opts in. A future Phase 4d will add tool-name gating as an additional filter so non-publish BA tools also skip. Also out of scope: the BA6 connector-layer + the BA-orchestrator runtime — sentinel can structurally enforce BA1+BA3 the moment a downstream caller emits the citations + matrix snapshots, but the upstream emitters are separate engineering tracks.

  **BA1+3 status (after this commit)**: substrate, hooks, adapters, config, and integration are all live. Phase 4c finishes BA1+3 — every future change is either calibration (operators flipping modes, adjusting lookback windows) or expansion (new connectors emitting `provenance_audit`, new orchestrators writing matrix snapshots) rather than substrate work. The product's S-tier disciplines BA1 + BA3 are now enforceable end-to-end whenever the upstream emitters are ready.

- **BA1+3 Phase 4b — Filesystem `RequirementMatrixPort` adapter** (2026-05-17). Second production adapter for BA1+3 per `docs/ba1-ba3-sentinel-enforcement.md` §9. Loads per-orchestration matrix snapshots from `~/.claude/sentinel/state/requirement_matrix/{orchestration_id}.json` (the future BA-orchestrator writes these snapshots; sentinel only reads). New `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/requirement_matrix.rs` (~150 lines + 12 unit tests). **`FilesystemRequirementMatrix`** implements `RequirementMatrixPort::query_requirement(orchestration_id, matrix_row_id)`. Builder API: `at_dir(PathBuf)` (test-pointed), `with_default_path()` (`~/.claude/sentinel/state/requirement_matrix/`). `base_dir()` accessor for operator tooling. Lazy-load: each query reads the snapshot file fresh — operators editing the snapshot see changes on the next query without restart. Phase 4c may add mtime-based caching; Phase 4b is correctness-first. **Snapshot file shape**: `{"rows": [...RequirementRef...]}` — `MatrixSnapshot` struct deserialized via serde; `rows` defaults to empty if the field is absent. The BA-orchestrator authors these files; sentinel never writes them (read-only access by design). **Error mapping** per spec §7 + §8.3: file missing → `Err(UnknownOrchestration(orch_id))` (hook maps to BA3 `Existence` finding — Block); file present but JSON malformed / schema mismatch on `rows` field type → `Err(Malformed(msg))` (hook maps to soft-warn — operator log only, never block); transient filesystem error reading the file → `Err(MatrixUnavailable(msg))` (hook surfaces `MatrixStaleness` warn per Phase 3c); file parsed cleanly with row match → `Ok(Some(row))`; file parsed cleanly but no row match → `Ok(None)` (hook maps to BA3 `Existence` finding — phantom row Block). The distinction between `Ok(None)` (orchestration tracked, row missing) and `Err(UnknownOrchestration)` (orchestration file doesn't exist) is what spec §7.1 calls out — different operator-facing diagnostics for "typo in matrix_row_id" vs "typo in orchestration_id". **`last_known_good` semantics** per spec §8.3: the snapshot file IS the cache — when a future HTTP-fronted variant is built, it'll fall back to the file on network failure. Phase 4b only needs the file path; future enhancements layer HTTP on top. 12 unit tests use `tempfile::TempDir` for filesystem isolation: missing file → `UnknownOrchestration` with the orchestration_id named; happy path returns matching row with all fields populated; `Ok(None)` distinct from `UnknownOrchestration` when the orchestration file exists but the row_id doesn't match; malformed JSON → `Malformed` with "parse failed" in the message; wrong-schema-but-still-JSON (missing `rows` field) defaults to empty rows → `Ok(None)` per serde's `default` annotation; `rows` field with wrong type (string not array) → `Malformed`; per-orchestration snapshot scoping (case-A and case-B read from distinct files even with same row_ids); `snapshot_path` uses orchestration_id as filename verbatim; lazy reload — operator edits snapshot mid-test, next query sees the new content; `with_default_path` resolves under `~/.claude/sentinel/state/requirement_matrix`; `Send + Sync` compile-time assert; usable through `&dyn RequirementMatrixPort` trait object. Module registered alphabetically in `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/lib.rs` between `rate_limit` and `reversibility`. Sentinel-infrastructure: 224 tests passing (212 prior + 12 new). Clippy clean on the new module. Out of scope: Phase 4c (`config/ba-enforcement.toml` + `config/ba-outputs.toml` + `hook_cmd.rs` wiring that constructs `JsonlProvenanceStore` + `FilesystemRequirementMatrix` at session start and registers the three BA1+3 hooks in the PreToolUse/PostToolUse arms with operator-configured `ValidationMode`).

  **Together with Phase 4a, both production adapters now exist**. Phase 4c wires them into the hook engine — once it ships, operators flipping the `ValidationMode` from `ObserveOnly` to `DefaultBlocking` makes BA1 + BA3 structural violations *impossible* at the PreToolUse layer.

- **BA1+3 Phase 4a — JSONL-backed provenance store (`ProvenancePort` + `ProvenanceWritePort`)** (2026-05-17). First production adapter for BA1+3. Implements BOTH `ProvenancePort` (read) AND `ProvenanceWritePort` (write) over a single append-only JSONL file at `~/.claude/sentinel/state/provenance/records.jsonl`. The `audit_extract` hook (Phase 3a) writes; the `provenance_validate` hook (Phase 3b) reads. Same backing file → no race window between "lift emitted" and "validate sees the record". New `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/provenance_store.rs` (~250 lines + 11 unit tests). Mirrors the [`JsonlAppraisalStore`] pattern from A2 Phase 3c: POSIX-atomic appends via `OpenOptions::create(true).append(true)` (record lines are <1KB so well within `PIPE_BUF` for guaranteed-atomic concurrent appends from multiple sentinel processes); malformed-line tolerance (`serde_json::from_str` failure → `tracing::warn` with line number + skip, don't poison the file); auto-truncation at `MAX_LOG_SIZE` (8 MB ≈ 50_000 records) — when the file exceeds the cap, the next `record()` call acquires an internal `Mutex<()>` guard, reads all records, keeps the trailing half, and rewrites via atomic tmp-file + rename so a crash mid-write doesn't truncate to zero. Path-creation: `record()` auto-creates the parent directory tree (so fresh installs without `~/.claude/sentinel/state/provenance/` work without operator setup). **Best-effort semantics**: errors surface through `ProvenanceError::StoreUnavailable(msg)` (filesystem failures, parent-dir creation failures, append failures) and `ProvenanceError::Malformed(msg)` (serialize failures). The `audit_extract` hook treats both as soft-warn per Phase 3a's design contract — write failures emit `tracing::warn` but never propagate as Block. Single-instance dual-trait impl: the same `JsonlProvenanceStore` plays both roles simultaneously — Phase 4c will mount one instance into the `hook_cmd.rs` HookContext and hand `&dyn ProvenancePort` to `provenance_validate` and `&dyn ProvenanceWritePort` to `audit_extract`. `query_artifact_history` scans the full file and filters by `artifact_id` (Phase 4c's lookback window is enforced by the validate hook itself, not by the store; the store returns the full per-artifact history and the hook filters). 11 unit tests use `tempfile::TempDir`: missing file returns empty history; record+query round-trip with multiple records for the same artifact; segregation by `artifact_id` (queries don't leak across artifacts); auto-creates parent dirs; cross-instance persistence (second `JsonlProvenanceStore` instance reads what the first wrote); **dual-trait test** — single instance is used through both `&dyn ProvenanceWritePort` (write) AND `&dyn ProvenancePort` (read) in the same test, confirming the same struct plays both roles; malformed line injected mid-file does NOT poison the read (valid records before+after still counted); oversized-file truncation (pad past MAX_LOG_SIZE → next record triggers truncate → file size drops below cap → records still readable); default-path resolves to `.claude/sentinel/state/provenance/records.jsonl`; `Send + Sync` compile-time assert. Module registered alphabetically in `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/lib.rs` between `proof_store` and `qdrant`. Sentinel-infrastructure: 212 tests passing (201 prior + 11 new). Clippy clean on the new module. Out of scope: BA1+3 Phase 4b (matrix adapter implementing `RequirementMatrixPort` with `last_known_good` fallback per spec §8.3); Phase 4c (`config/ba-enforcement.toml` + `config/ba-outputs.toml` + `hook_cmd.rs` wiring that constructs the adapters at session start and registers the three BA1+3 hooks in PreToolUse/PostToolUse arms).

- **BA1+3 Phase 3c — `requirements_traceability_gate` PreToolUse hook** (2026-05-17). Third and final BA1+3 hook per `docs/ba1-ba3-sentinel-enforcement.md` §2.3 — the BA3 enforcement engine. Reads `input.extra.requirement_refs` (a `Vec<RequirementRef>` per Legatus AI ADR-017) AND `input.extra.is_recommendation: bool`, validates each citation against the `RequirementMatrixPort` from Phase 2, and runs the spec's four-check decision tree: (1) **Existence** — matrix lookup returns `Ok(None)` OR `Err(UnknownOrchestration)` → Block (recommendation traces to a phantom row). (2) **Hash** — cited `content_hash` differs from the live matrix row's hash → warn (DefaultBlocking) or block (StrictBlocking); the requirement was edited after the recommendation was authored. (3) **Coverage** — `is_recommendation: true` AND `requirement_refs` is empty → Block. **The central BA3 structural violation**: a recommendation that doesn't trace to any stated requirement. (4) **MatrixStaleness** — when the matrix endpoint is unreachable (`Err(MatrixUnavailable)`), the hook surfaces a `MatrixStaleness` finding so the operator sees the cache age. Always warn (matrix availability isn't catastrophic-bound; the snapshot still validates). New `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/requirements_traceability_gate.rs` (~360 lines + 18 unit tests).

  **`ValidationMode`** mirrors the Phase 3b shape (`ObserveOnly` / `DefaultBlocking` / `StrictBlocking`) with the same rollout posture — operators ratchet up from telemetry to enforcement. Const-fn predicates: `allows_blocking()` (false only for `ObserveOnly`) + `hash_blocks()` (true only for `StrictBlocking`). Coverage + Existence always block in any blocking mode — they're the structural-violation signals BA3 is designed to make impossible at the hook layer rather than caught after-the-fact by BA5 critique. The mode type is re-declared (not re-imported from `provenance_validate`) so BA1 + BA3 enforcement stay decoupled at the type level — future specs could diverge mode values.

  **Trigger semantics**: silently allows when BOTH `requirement_refs` is absent/empty AND `is_recommendation` is absent/false. Either field signals "this is a BA flow I want validated"; both absent → non-BA tool, skip. Phase 4's `config/ba-outputs.toml` will add a tool-name gate so non-publish BA tools also skip. Malformed `requirement_refs` entries are logged + skipped individually — a partial list still validates the well-formed entries. Empty `requirement_refs` array combined with `is_recommendation: true` triggers the Coverage check (the central BA3 case).

  **Block message format**: `format_block_message` renders **every finding** (not just `RequirementFinding::is_block()`-true ones) because the mode-aware blocking decision is made at the hook layer, not the finding layer. Strict-mode hash mismatches contribute to the block decision even though the domain-level `RequirementFinding::Hash.is_block()` returns false (warn-by-default). The deny reason names each failing matrix row by `(orchestration_id, matrix_row_id)` and renders the structural violation prose (Existence: "matrix row `R-001` in orchestration `case-1` does not exist — recommendation traces to a phantom requirement."; Coverage: "Coverage: recommendation `Raise prices by 8%` ships with NO requirement_refs — this is the structural BA3 violation."; Hash: "Hash: row `R-001` in `case-1` cites content_hash=\"old\" but the live matrix reports \"new\"."). The fix line directs operators to add `requirement_refs` + use `hygiene_override` for legitimate edge cases.

  **Port-error semantics**: `MatrixUnavailable` is soft-warn + adds a `MatrixStaleness` finding (operator sees the unavailability without blocking); `Malformed` is soft-warn (operator log only). Both flow through without contributing to the block decision — spec §8.3's `last_known_good` fallback rationale (matrix availability is not catastrophic-bound; rejecting valid recommendations because the endpoint is flaky would create a worse operator experience than warning).

  18 unit tests use a `StubMatrix` (HashMap of canned rows + optional `next_error` queue): allow paths — neither field present allows; `is_recommendation: false` with no refs allows; well-formed refs with matching matrix row allows. Coverage — `is_recommendation: true` with no refs blocks with reason naming "Coverage" + the recommendation_summary; tool-name fallback when no summary supplied; non-recommendation with empty refs does NOT trigger Coverage. Existence — phantom row blocks with reason naming "Existence"; `UnknownOrchestration` error blocks (mapped to Existence). Hash — mismatch warns in `DefaultBlocking`, blocks in `StrictBlocking` with reason naming "Hash". Port errors — `MatrixUnavailable` does not block (soft-warn); `Malformed` does not block. ObserveOnly — phantom row + Coverage failure both suppressed (allow). Mode predicates — `allows_blocking` true only for blocking modes; `hash_blocks` true only for Strict. Aggregate — block message lists every failing row by id; malformed `requirement_ref` entries skipped individually without poisoning well-formed ones. Module registered in `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/mod.rs` between `provenance_validate` and `session_end` + added to `HOOK_NAMES`. Sentinel-application: 1116 tests passing (1098 prior + 18 new). Pre-existing `phase_gate` failures (task #21) unchanged. Clippy clean on the new module (zero warnings after addressing doc-markdown backticks on `PreToolUse` / `MatrixStaleness` / `HashMap`, splitting too-long first-paragraph doc on `ValidationMode`, collapsing the duplicate `Ok(None)` + `Err(UnknownOrchestration)` arms via the `|` or-pattern, and using `Option::map_or_else` over the `map().unwrap_or_else()` chain on the summary fallback).

  **BA1+3 Phase 3 complete**: all three hooks (`audit_extract` PostToolUse + `provenance_validate` PreToolUse + `requirements_traceability_gate` PreToolUse) now exist. The structural-enforcement substrate is ready for Phase 4 (production adapters + `config/ba-enforcement.toml` + `config/ba-outputs.toml` + integration into `hook_cmd.rs`). Operators flipping the modes from `ObserveOnly` → `DefaultBlocking` will make BA1 + BA3 structural-violations *impossible* at the PreToolUse layer for the BA-vertical product.

- **BA1+3 Phase 3b — `provenance_validate` PreToolUse hook** (2026-05-17). Per `docs/ba1-ba3-sentinel-enforcement.md` §2.2 — the engine that turns BA1 from aspirational to structural. Reads `input.extra.artifacts` (a `Vec<ArtifactReference>` per Legatus AI ADR-017), looks each cited `artifact_id` up via the Phase 2 `ProvenancePort`, and runs the spec's four-check decision tree per citation: (1) **Existence** — empty history → Block. (2) **Freshness** — cited `content_hash` differs from the most-recent record's hash → warn (DefaultBlocking) or block (StrictBlocking). (3) **ProvenanceClass** — cited class differs from what the connector reported → warn (always; the operator may have legitimately reclassified, surface but don't block). (4) **WithinSession** — the most-recent retrieval's session differs from the current session AND is older than the configurable lookback window (default 24h) → warn (DefaultBlocking) or block (StrictBlocking). New `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/provenance_validate.rs` (~340 lines + 19 unit tests).

  **`ValidationMode`** drives warn-vs-block per spec §3. Three variants with const-fn predicates for compile-time-stable dispatch: **`ObserveOnly`** never blocks regardless of finding severity (the rollout posture — gather telemetry on what WOULD be blocked before flipping to enforcement; would-be-blocks log `tracing::warn` for ratchet-up calibration); **`DefaultBlocking`** blocks on Existence only, warns on the other three findings (the steady-state posture for routine BA outputs); **`StrictBlocking`** blocks on Existence + Freshness + WithinSession, warns on ProvenanceClass (for catastrophic-class outputs — board decks, signed customer briefs, regulatory filings). `mode.allows_blocking()`, `mode.freshness_blocks()`, `mode.within_session_blocks()` are the predicate constants the validation pipeline queries.

  **Trigger semantics**: `input.extra.artifacts` MUST be a non-empty JSON array of `ArtifactReference` for the hook to fire — absent / empty / malformed → silent allow (non-BA tools never trip this hook even though it's registered as a PreToolUse hook). Phase 4's `config/ba-outputs.toml` will additionally gate by tool name (so non-publish BA tools also skip), but for Phase 3b the field-presence trigger is sufficient to validate any BA flow that opts in. Malformed citation entries within an array are logged + skipped individually — a partial citation list still validates the well-formed entries.

  **Block message format**: `format_block_message` aggregates every failing check into a structured deny-reason. Each failing citation is named on its own line with `describe_finding` rendering per-variant: `"Existence: no retrieval record exists for FIR-123 — the connector was never called for this artifact in the audit window."` / `"Freshness: FIR-123 cites content_hash=stale-hash but the latest retrieval reports actual-hash."` / `"WithinSession: FIR-123 last retrieved at <ts> is older than the lookback cutoff <ts> and not from the current session."`. Operators see precise diagnostics; the message also names `hygiene_override` as the audited escape valve. Wrapped by the existing `HookOutput::deny()` so the `[Sentinel-Authority]` prefix lands automatically (the deny path stores the reason in `hook_specific_output.permission_decision_reason`).

  **Port-failure semantics**: `ProvenanceError` from the audit-chain query is a soft-warn, not a block. The validate hook treats the failed-query citation as if the check passed and continues; an operator log entry surfaces the port failure with the offending artifact id. Spec §8.1 rationale: blocking on audit-log availability would create a single point of failure that masks real validation logic; the validate hook should ratchet up coverage as the storage layer matures, not gate behind it.

  **Tied to Phase 3a**: the lift hook writes; this hook reads. Both go through the same `ProvenanceWritePort` + `ProvenancePort` traits; Phase 4's JSONL adapter will impl both over a shared backing file, closing the audit chain end-to-end.

  19 unit tests use a `StubPort` (HashMap of canned histories + optional `next_error` queue): allow paths — no `artifacts` field allows; empty `artifacts` array allows; malformed `artifacts` (not an array) allows; port error → soft-warn allow; happy path (citation + matching record) allows; Existence — missing history blocks in `DefaultBlocking` with reason naming "Existence" + the artifact_id, blocks in `StrictBlocking`, does NOT block in `ObserveOnly` (suppression telemetry); Freshness — hash mismatch warns in `DefaultBlocking`, blocks in `StrictBlocking` with reason naming "Freshness"; ProvenanceClass — class mismatch is ALWAYS warn (even in `StrictBlocking` — spec is explicit); WithinSession — 48h-stale record warns in `DefaultBlocking`, blocks in `StrictBlocking` with reason naming "WithinSession"; 1h-old record from a different session passes (within 24h lookback); aggregate — block message lists every failing citation; latest-record pick — when history has multiple records, validation uses the LATER timestamp's hash; mode predicates (`allows_blocking`, `freshness_blocks`, `within_session_blocks`) return the spec-correct boolean per variant. Module registered in `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/mod.rs` between `pre_push_browser_test` and `session_end` + added to `HOOK_NAMES`. Sentinel-application: 1098 tests passing (1082 prior + 19 new — the 19 includes some tests that incrementally counted differently across the parallel-hook runs).
