Pre-existing `phase_gate` failures (task #21) unchanged. Clippy clean on the new module (zero warnings after addressing unused `ProvenanceClass` import in main code via `#[cfg(test)]` re-import, doc-markdown backticks on `PreToolUse` / `ProvenanceClass` / `WithinSession` / `ProvenancePort` / `HashMap`, switching `push_str(&format!(...))` to `writeln!(buf, ...)` per `format_in_format_args` lint, and hoisting the mutex-guard `next_error.take()` out of the `if let` scrutinee to avoid temporary-lifetime warning). Out of scope: Phase 3c (`requirements_traceability_gate` PreToolUse hook for BA3), Phase 4 (JSONL adapter + `config/ba-enforcement.toml` + `config/ba-outputs.toml`).

- **BA1+3 Phase 3a — `audit_extract` hook + `ProvenanceWritePort`** (2026-05-17). Per `docs/ba1-ba3-sentinel-enforcement.md` §2.1. Adds the FIRST of the three BA1+3 hooks: a `PostToolUse` lift hook that detects successful documentation-connector calls (`mcp__*` tools that emit a structured `provenance_audit` field per BA6 §3.4) and persists a `RetrievalRecord` via the new `ProvenanceWritePort`. The future `provenance_validate` hook (Phase 3b) reads the same chain via `ProvenancePort` to validate BA-orchestrator citations — the read + write sides share storage, so Phase 4's JSONL adapter will impl both traits over the same backing file. New `crates/sentinel-domain/src/ports.rs` addition: **`ProvenanceWritePort`** — `fn record(&self, RetrievalRecord) -> Result<(), ProvenanceError>`. Returns `Result` so adapter IO failures can surface to consumer hooks (which log + drop, never propagate as Block — observational). Idempotency contract documented: implementations MAY skip duplicate `(artifact_id, content_hash, retrieved_at)` writes but MUST still return `Ok(())`; consumers de-dupe at read time. New `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/audit_extract.rs` (~200 lines + 13 unit tests): `pub fn process(input: &HookInput, provenance_writer: &dyn ProvenanceWritePort) -> HookOutput`. Decision pipeline: (1) Tool name missing → allow + skip. (2) Tool name doesn't start with `mcp__` → allow + skip (only MCP servers emit connector audit). (3) `extra.provenance_audit` field absent → allow + skip silently (the MCP tool isn't a documented connector per BA6 — older connectors / non-doc connectors don't emit). (4) `provenance_audit` field present but malformed (not an object, missing `artifact_id`/`content_hash`/`provenance_class`, unknown class string) → log `tracing::warn` + allow + skip. (5) `session_id` missing or empty → log warn + allow + skip (can't persist without session scoping). (6) Happy path: construct `RetrievalRecord { artifact_id, connector_name: tool_name, content_hash, provenance_class, session_id, retrieved_at: now() }` and call `provenance_writer.record(...)`. (7) Write failure → log warn + allow (NEVER propagate as Block — the tool call already completed; PostToolUse hooks are observational). The `connector_name` field is filled from the FULL tool name (`mcp__linear__get_issue` not just `linear`) so the audit chain knows exactly which MCP server + which tool emitted the retrieval — useful for downstream filtering when multiple connectors front the same upstream system.

  **Hex/DDD layering** preserved: port lives in `sentinel-domain`; hook lives in `sentinel-application` and consumes the port via `&dyn`; no IO in the hook itself; Phase 4 ships the production adapter in `sentinel-infrastructure`. **Always-observational contract**: every test asserts `output.blocked == None` regardless of input shape — there is no code path in this hook that returns a Block. The hook is named `audit_extract` rather than `audit_validate` deliberately: extracting + lifting is its job; validation is `provenance_validate`'s.

  13 unit tests cover (a) the allow-only contract — missing tool name allows; non-`mcp__` tool allows + skips; (b) the skip paths — non-MCP tools never produce records; MCP tools without `provenance_audit` field don't produce records (silently); malformed audit value (not an object) skips; missing `artifact_id` skips; unknown `provenance_class` string skips; missing/empty `session_id` skips; (c) the happy path — valid audit event with `SystemOfRecord` class persists a record with all 6 fields populated correctly (`artifact_id`, `connector_name` from tool name, `content_hash`, class, `session_id`, `retrieved_at`); `connector_name` is the FULL tool name (`mcp__confluence__get_page` not `confluence`); all four `ProvenanceClass` variants parse correctly when the connector sends each variant string; (d) best-effort persistence — when the stub writer returns `ProvenanceError::StoreUnavailable`, the hook still returns `allow()` and doesn't propagate. Tests use a `StubWriter` recording-stub that captures every `record()` call in a `Mutex<Vec>` + optional `next_error` queue. Module registered in `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/mod.rs` alphabetically between `agent_revocation` and `block_context` + added to `HOOK_NAMES` between `agent_revocation` and `bug_task_gate`. Sentinel-application: 1082 tests passing (1069 prior + 13 new). Sentinel-domain: 499 tests unchanged. Clippy clean on both new sections (zero warnings after doc-markdown backticks on `audit_extract` / `provenance_validate` / `PostToolUse` references in the new `ProvenanceWritePort` doc). The 3 pre-existing `phase_gate` test failures (task #21) unchanged. Out of scope: Phase 3b (`provenance_validate` PreToolUse hook), Phase 3c (`requirements_traceability_gate` PreToolUse hook), Phase 4 (`config/ba-enforcement.toml` + `config/ba-outputs.toml` + JSONL adapter implementing both `ProvenancePort` + `ProvenanceWritePort` + matrix adapter).

- **BA1+3 Phase 2 — `ProvenancePort` + `RequirementMatrixPort` traits in sentinel-domain** (2026-05-17). Second slice of BA1+3 (`docs/ba1-ba3-sentinel-enforcement.md` §9). Adds the two domain traits the future `provenance_validate` and `requirements_traceability_gate` hooks query — pure traits, no logic; Phase 3 (the application-layer hooks) and Phase 4 (the infrastructure adapters) follow. Appended to `crates/sentinel-domain/src/ports.rs` (matching the existing flat-ports convention rather than introducing a `ports/` subdirectory — same pattern as `AuditorPort` + `CapabilityRouterPort` + `AppraisalStorePort`). **`ProvenancePort`** — `query_artifact_history(artifact_id: &str) -> Result<Vec<RetrievalRecord>, ProvenanceError>`. Returns the FULL retrieval history for the artifact (not just the latest) so callers can pick the most-recent record, scan within a freshness window, or detect repeated retrievals (some workflows pull an artifact multiple times within a session — each should appear in the audit chain). Empty `Vec` means the artifact was never retrieved through any registered connector in the configured window → BA1's `Existence` finding fires. **`ProvenanceError`** — `StoreUnavailable(String)` for backing-store IO failures (hooks treat as soft-warn — the validator can't run without history but the call shouldn't be blocked on the audit log being temporarily down) + `Malformed(String)` for corrupt JSONL lines / schema mismatches. Hand-rolled `Display` + `std::error::Error` (no thiserror dep in sentinel-domain). **`RequirementMatrixPort`** — `query_requirement(orchestration_id: &str, matrix_row_id: &str) -> Result<Option<RequirementRef>, RequirementMatrixError>`. Returns the LIVE row content so the caller can compare against the citation's `content_hash` (BA3's `Hash` finding). The `Result<Option<…>>` shape distinguishes three states: `Ok(Some(row))` (row exists; validate fields), `Ok(None)` (orchestration is tracked but row doesn't exist → BA3 `Existence` finding), `Err(UnknownOrchestration)` (the orchestration_id itself is unknown — likely a typo, not a coverage failure). **`RequirementMatrixError`** — three variants: `MatrixUnavailable` (no `last_known_good` snapshot available — fresh install or never-fetched orchestration), `UnknownOrchestration` (orchestration_id has no matrix entry at all), `Malformed` (schema mismatch / corrupt response). Per spec §8.3 the production adapter (future Phase 4) will have a `last_known_good` fallback for ordinary unavailability — the `MatrixUnavailable` error is reserved for the no-snapshot-at-all case so callers can distinguish "transient flake" (use fallback) from "fundamentally cold cache" (must surface to operator). 6 unit tests pin behavior: `ProvenanceError::Display` names each variant + carries the payload string; `RequirementMatrixError::Display` same for all 3 variants (including the named-orchestration `UnknownOrchestration`); both errors `impl std::error::Error`; both are `Send + Sync`; both round-trip through JSON (so they can flow through proof-chain serialization); both traits are object-safe (compile-time check via `Box<dyn ProvenancePort>` / `Box<dyn RequirementMatrixPort>` in a test helper). Sentinel-domain: 499 tests passing (493 prior + 6 new). Clippy clean on the new section. **Drive-by cleanup**: deleted `plans/a3-3b.md` — a 61-byte stub from the A3 Phase 3b kickoff that's been flagged by `[Doc Cleanup]` hook every session since merge. The plan it described is captured in the A3 Phase 3b CHANGELOG entry; the stub adds no value and removing it clears the recurring doc-cleanup nudge. Out of scope: BA1+3 Phase 3 (the `audit_extract` / `provenance_validate` / `requirements_traceability_gate` hooks in sentinel-application); Phase 4 (the production adapters + `config/ba-enforcement.toml` + `config/ba-outputs.toml`); A12 Phase 2 (the `sentinel eval` CLI scaffold — A12 has no new domain port per spec §6, so its Phase 2 is application-layer not ports).

- **BA1+3 + A12 Phase 1 — BA-vertical and external-benchmark domain types in sentinel-domain** (2026-05-17). Kicks off two new tracks per `docs/ba1-ba3-sentinel-enforcement.md` §9 and `docs/a12-external-benchmarks.md` §3. Pure-domain value objects only — hooks, ports, adapters, and the `sentinel eval` CLI subcommand all land in future phases. **BA1+3** (`crates/sentinel-domain/src/ba/`): new `provenance.rs` defines `ProvenanceClass` (`SystemOfRecord | ExpertSynthesis | Inference | Unverified` — the four-tier classification from Legatus AI ADR-017), `ArtifactReference` (the citation wire format: `artifact_id` + `content_hash` + claimed `provenance_class` + `retrieved_at`), `RetrievalRecord` (one entry in sentinel's connector-audit chain; emitted by the future `audit_extract` hook), `ProvenanceCheck` (validation result with builder API + `has_block()` predicate), `ProvenanceFinding` (4 variants matching the spec's decision tree: `Existence` always-blocks, `Freshness` blocks-per-flag for catastrophic-class outputs, `ProvenanceClass` warn-only, `WithinSession` blocks-per-flag). New `requirements.rs` defines `RequirementRef` (four-tuple `orchestration_id + matrix_row_id + content_hash + statement` per ADR-017), `RequirementCheck` + `RequirementFinding` (4 variants: `Existence` blocks, `Coverage` blocks — the structural BA3 violation, `Hash` warn, `MatrixStaleness` warn). Module `ba/mod.rs` re-exports the public surface. The Block-class findings (`Existence` for provenance, `Existence` + `Coverage` for requirements) are exactly the structural failures BA1/BA3 exist to prevent — and once the future hooks ship, will be impossible to commit at the PreToolUse layer rather than caught after-the-fact by BA5 critique. **A12** (`crates/sentinel-domain/src/eval/`): new `case.rs` defines `EvalCaseId` + `EvalRunId` (newtype `String` IDs with empty-rejection like `AgentId`), `SourceCorpus` (3 variants per spec §3.2: `Public` with url + license, `PartnerContributed` with `RedactionLevel`, `SyntheticGenerated` with `generation_method`), `RedactionLevel` (None / Light / Heavy / Synthetic), `GoldArtifact` (the human-authored reference output), `GoldOutcomes` (real-world outcome data with `attribution_confidence` 0.0-1.0 + `observation_window_days`), `CaseProvenance` (`contributor` + `license` + `is_private_test` flag for the held-back split per spec §3.4), and `EvalCase` itself wrapping everything. `EvalCase::outcome_scoring_valid()` enforces the spec's rule that synthetic cases — even when they carry `gold_outcomes` — must NOT score on the `OutcomeRealism` axis because the outcome is fabricated. New `rubric.rs` defines `EvalAxis` (the 6 spec axes: `CitationDensityAccuracy`, `RequirementsCoverage`, `AlternativesSeriousness`, `TonalCalibration`, `OutcomeRealism`, `StakeholderFit`) with stable `snake_case` keys for serialization + `requires_outcomes()` predicate; `EvalAxisScore` (raw + weight, clamped at construction); `ScoringRubric` with per-axis weights (`ba_default()` weights `OutcomeRealism` at 2.0 and all others at 1.0 — total 7.0); `EvalScore` with weighted-mean composite computed at construction. Module `eval/mod.rs` re-exports the public surface and documents the R5 quarantine boundary: eval scores are dispatch input + reporting only, never training feedback. 34 unit tests across both tracks (15 for BA1+3, 19 for A12). Sentinel-domain: 493 tests passing (459 prior + 34 new). Clippy clean on the new modules. **Hex/DDD layering**: both modules live entirely in `sentinel-domain`; no IO, no business logic, no hooks. Future phases land ports + adapters in the application + infrastructure layers.

- **`CancelInstruction` hit emits explicit `InstructionResult { Declined }` via escalation loopback** (2026-05-17). Follow-up to the cancel handler that landed earlier today. When a cancel removes a queued instruction (`PersistentInbox::remove_by_id` returns true), the WS recv loop now feeds a synthetic `InstructionResult { Declined { reason } }` into the runtime's new `escalation_loopback` channel — same `mpsc::UnboundedSender<EscalationKind>` the daemon-side `LegatusHandle::escalate` uses, cloned onto the runtime side at `make_pair`/`make_pair_with_inbox` construction. The main `run_connect_hosted` select arm drains `escalation_rx` and signs+sends the result over the WS via the standard escalation path — exactly one "event → WS send" code path, no duplicated sink handling. The declined reason is `"cancelled by operator: <cancel.reason>"` when the operator supplied one, or `"cancelled by operator"` otherwise.

  Closes the accounting gap flagged in the prior commit's "Out of scope" note: Legatus AI no longer has to infer cancellation from a missing Result; the Declined record arrives explicitly with the operator's reason echoed back. Cancel-misses (instruction already drained or never queued) still don't emit anything — there's nothing for Legatus AI to confirm in that case, and the cancel arrival itself is the operator-side record.

  Implementation surface: **(a)** `handle.rs` adds `escalation_loopback: mpsc::UnboundedSender<EscalationKind>` to `LegatusRuntime`; both `make_pair` and `make_pair_with_inbox` clone the original sender (one copy goes to the handle, one to the runtime). **(b)** `client.rs::handle_inbound`'s `CancelInstruction` arm now constructs the `Declined` event when `removed=true` and sends it via the loopback; silent skip when the loopback receiver is gone (loop already exited / shutting down). **(c)** No changes to the public API surface — `LegatusHandle::escalate` semantics unchanged, daemon callers see the same channel.

  3 new tokio-async tests on `handle_inbound`: `cancel_instruction_hit_pushes_declined_via_loopback` (full path: append queued instruction → cancel → assert escalation_rx receives Declined with reason naming the operator's reason); `cancel_instruction_miss_does_not_push_anything` (cancel for never-queued id → escalation_rx is empty); `cancel_without_reason_uses_default_declined_reason` (reason field is `None` → declined reason is the default string). Sentinel-legatus: 23 tests passing (20 prior + 3 new). Zero net-new clippy errors over the pre-existing baseline.

- **Sentinel-side `CancelInstruction` handling — operator-driven undo for queued instructions** (2026-05-17). Completes the cancel path opened by the protocol-side `CancelInstruction` variant landed in `legatus-ai` earlier today. New `PersistentInbox::remove_by_id(instruction_id) -> bool` in `crates/sentinel-legatus/src/persistent_inbox.rs` (~+40 lines + 4 unit tests) plus a new `remove_by_id_under_lock(file, id)` private helper that mirrors `pop_first_under_lock`'s atomic-rewrite discipline: open RW, take exclusive `fs2` advisory lock, read all lines, filter out the first line whose parsed `RelayInstruction.instruction_id` matches, rewrite the remainder via `seek(0) + set_len(0) + writeln` per surviving line. Returns `true` on a hit, `false` on file-missing / no-match / lock-failure. Concurrent appends serialize on the same lock — no race window between the read and the rewrite.

  `client.rs::handle_inbound` now matches `Legatus AIMessage::CancelInstruction` and routes to `runtime.inbox.remove_by_id(cancel.instruction_id)`. Two log paths — `removed=true` emits an info log with the instruction id + operator reason ("CancelInstruction removed queued instruction"); `removed=false` (already drained into the model's context window, or never queued, or no persistent inbox in the standalone CLI path) emits "CancelInstruction arrived too late". No `InstructionResult` is currently fired for the cancelled id: when the instruction is gone from the inbox before draining, no `Legatus AI_inbox` hook will ever drain it and therefore no execution-log Stop will ever fire a Result — the cancel arrival itself is Legatus AI's confirmation. A future improvement could explicitly emit `InstructionResult { Declined { reason: cancel.reason } }` for the cancelled id; flagged in the code as deferred until the sentinel ↔ daemon Result-emission path is wired here.

  `lib.rs` re-exports `CancelInstruction` from `legatus_ai_protocol::messages` alongside the existing `RelayInstruction` / `InstructionOutcome` / `BlockReason` / `RuntimeKind` re-exports so downstream crates can match on the new variant without a direct path-dep on legatus-ai-protocol.

  4 new unit tests on `PersistentInbox`: `remove_by_id_on_missing_file_returns_false` (no panic, no file creation); `remove_by_id_removes_matching_queued_instruction` (FIFO order of survivors preserved); `remove_by_id_returns_false_when_id_not_queued` (queue untouched, returns false); `remove_by_id_only_removes_first_match` (defensive — if a duplicate ever lands on disk, drop one occurrence not all, matching operator "cancel this one queued copy" intent). Sentinel-legatus: 20 tests passing (16 prior + 4 new). Zero net-new clippy errors over the pre-existing baseline (two warnings I introduced — `Option::map_or` opportunity and missing backticks in a doc — fixed before commit).

  Reliability stance preserved: ~90-95% target. The cancel is **definitive** in the `removed=true` path (the instruction is gone from disk before any Claude Code turn can see it) and **advisory** in the `removed=false` path (instruction is already in the model's context window — sentinel logs the late cancel and lets the operator's follow-up instruction do the rest of the work). **Out of scope (deferred)**: explicit `InstructionResult { Declined }` emission for cancelled ids (needs the sentinel ↔ daemon Result wiring to land here, separate slice); mid-execution nudge for already-drained instructions (would need a prompt-injection path into the running model, big surgery and outside the cancel slice's footprint).

- **Mid-run failure classification for `InstructionResult` — `Success` is no longer the only outcome** (2026-05-17). Closes the second gap in the operator → Claude Code feedback loop: per-instruction Result reports now reflect what actually happened during the turn instead of unconditionally claiming `Success`. New `TurnSignal` enum in `crates/sentinel-application/src/legatus_client.rs` (~+100 lines + 6 unit tests) — currently one variant, `PermissionDenied { tool }`, recorded mid-turn by hooks and consumed at Stop. Per-session signals file at `~/.claude/sentinel/state/<session_id>.legatus-turn-signals.jsonl` follows the same append-on-event + read-and-clear-on-Stop pattern as the existing pending-instructions file; same sanitization (`turn_signals_path` rejects `/`, `\`, `\0`, `..`, empty), same best-effort I/O (debug-log on failure, never propagated). New `classify_outcome(signals, api_error) -> InstructionOutcome` is the single source of truth for the mapping: `Some(api_error)` → `Failure { error }`; any `PermissionDenied` signals → `Declined { reason: "permission denied for tool(s): X, Y" }`; otherwise `Success`. The `api_error` wins over signals because StopFailure is the more informative event (the turn aborted before the model could decide whether to declined-vs-failed retry).

  Three hook wirings: **(a)** `permission_denied.rs` now calls `note_turn_signal(session_id, PermissionDenied { tool })` alongside the existing `SessionBlocked` escalation — escalation is the operator-visible chat ping ("blocked on Bash"), the turn signal is the late-stage classification input. Skips silently when `session_id` is absent. **(b)** `execution_log.rs` (Stop hook) now reads turn signals via `take_turn_signals(session_id)` and feeds them through `classify_outcome(&signals, None)` to derive the per-instruction outcome — replaces the hard-coded `InstructionOutcome::Success`. The take-and-clear ensures stale signals don't leak into the next turn's classification. **(c)** `stop_failure.rs` (StopFailure hook — API-error path) now drains pending instructions early in the handler and fires `InstructionResult { Failure { error: "<error>: <error_details>" } }` for each, with no summary. Also clears any turn signals so a subsequent normal Stop on the same session doesn't double-classify on stale state. Pending-only branch — when there are no pending instructions the StopFailure path is unchanged (still rotates accounts, still emits the `[Rate Limit]` / `[Auth Error]` system messages).

  Reliability stance preserved from the inbox-persistence commit: ~90-95% target, not 100% deterministic. The Declined classification is coarse — every pending instruction in a turn with a permission denial is reported Declined, even though we can't prove the denial relates to a specific instruction. That's the right trade for the operator: "one of your instructions ran into a permission gate" is strictly better signal than "all succeeded silently." Operators can drill into the chat surface for the specific tool name from the existing `SessionBlocked` escalation.

  10 new unit tests across the touched files: `legatus_client::tests::turn_signals_path_rejects_traversal` + `note_then_take_roundtrips_turn_signals` + `take_turn_signals_for_missing_session_returns_empty` (basic file plumbing); `classify_outcome_api_error_wins_over_signals` + `classify_outcome_permission_denied_yields_declined` + `classify_outcome_multiple_denied_tools_joined_in_reason` + `classify_outcome_no_signals_yields_success` (mapping rules pinned); `hooks::permission_denied::tests::test_permission_denied_records_turn_signal` + `test_permission_denied_without_session_id_skips_signal_record` (hook integration with the recorder); `hooks::stop_failure::tests::test_stop_failure_clears_pending_instructions` + `test_stop_failure_clears_turn_signals` (the API-error drain path). Sentinel-application: 12 + 3 + 16 = 31 tests across the touched modules, all passing. Zero net-new clippy errors over the pre-existing baseline.

  **Out of scope (deferred)**: `Deferred { waiting_on }` classification (requires text-classifying the model's reply for "I'll do that later" intent, separate problem); fine-grained "which instruction did this denial relate to" (would need per-tool-call → per-instruction correlation in the relay flow, big surgery); cancel/redirect support for in-flight instructions (the next slice — new `CancelInstruction` protocol message).

- **Sentinel daemon legatus inbox persistence — operator instructions survive daemon restart** (2026-05-17). Closes the reliability gap where a daemon crash between "received `RelayInstruction` over WS" and "drained by the `Legatus AI_inbox` hook" silently lost the instruction. The inbox was an in-memory `tokio::sync::mpsc` channel; nothing on disk meant nothing survived. New `crates/sentinel-legatus/src/persistent_inbox.rs` (~290 lines + 9 unit tests) introduces `PersistentInbox`, a file-backed FIFO at `~/.claude/sentinel/state/legatus-inbox.jsonl` (overridable via `PersistentInbox::new(path)` for tests). Storage is one JSON-encoded `RelayInstruction` per line in arrival order; every operation (`append`, `try_pop`, `snapshot`, `len`) takes an `fs2` advisory exclusive (or shared, for read-only paths) lock on the file so concurrent producers + the consumer + cross-process touches are serialized. `try_pop` reads all lines under lock, skips the first parseable line as the popped item, and atomically rewrites the remainder via `seek(0) + set_len(0) + writeln` for each remaining line — concurrent appends block on the lock until the rewrite completes. Malformed lines (e.g. from a `legatus-ai-protocol` schema change) are dropped silently with a `tracing::warn` so they don't re-trigger the same parse failure forever. I/O errors are best-effort (logged at warn, never propagated) so the WS recv loop is never blocked on a transient filesystem issue — the design contract is ~90-95% reliability with Legatus AI re-sending if the operator re-instructs, not 100% deterministic delivery.

  `LegatusHandle` + `LegatusRuntime` refactored to drop the pre-persistence `mpsc::UnboundedSender/Receiver<RelayInstruction>` pair in favor of `Option<PersistentInbox>` on both halves. New constructor `make_pair_with_inbox(inbox: PersistentInbox)` builds a paired `(handle, runtime)` where both sides share the same path — `PersistentInbox` is `Clone` (path-only), so cloning into spawned tasks is free. The original `make_pair()` is preserved for the standalone `sentinel legatus connect` CLI path where instructions are still log-only (no daemon to drain them). `LegatusHandle::try_pop_inbox` wraps the synchronous file I/O in `tokio::task::spawn_blocking` so the executor never stalls on the advisory lock. `client.rs::handle_inbound` writes the inbound `RelayInstruction` via `runtime.inbox.append(instr)` if a persistent inbox is wired (daemon path), falls back to debug-log if not (standalone path). The escalation channel stays in-memory because escalations come from hooks that have already returned to the operator's chat surface — losing one to a crash is a non-fatal "next Stop hook fires instead" event, not a missed instruction.

  Daemon wiring in `crates/sentinel-cli/src/daemon_cmd.rs::start_legatus_if_configured`: builds the persistent inbox via `default_inbox_path()` → `PersistentInbox::new(path)`, then calls `make_pair_with_inbox(inbox)` instead of `make_pair()`. On daemon startup the inbox is rehydrated naturally — `inbox.len()` is reported at info level if non-zero so operators can see backlogged instructions surviving a previous crash. If `dirs::home_dir()` can't resolve (degenerate chroot/CI), falls back to in-memory `make_pair()` with a `tracing::warn` so the daemon still runs; that path matches pre-persistence behavior.

  9 unit tests on `PersistentInbox` use `tempfile::tempdir()` for isolation: empty inbox pops `None`; append-then-pop returns the same instruction; FIFO order preserved across three appends and three pops; append-after-pop extends the remainder (the WS-recv → hook-drain → WS-recv pattern); `snapshot()` is non-consuming; malformed lines are dropped on pop (good-line-after-bad-line still pops the good one); **instructions survive simulated daemon restart** (the headline test — drop the first `PersistentInbox`, construct a fresh one at the same path, pop returns the queued instruction); 20 concurrent appends from threads all persist (lock discipline holds under contention); `default_inbox_path()` returns a path containing `.claude` + `sentinel` ending in `legatus-inbox.jsonl`. 4 additional tests on the refactored `LegatusHandle`: `escalate_succeeds_when_runtime_is_alive`, `escalate_errors_after_runtime_drop`, `try_pop_inbox_returns_none_for_standalone_pair` (`make_pair()` with no inbox), `try_pop_inbox_drains_persistent_inbox` (`make_pair_with_inbox()` round-trip), `handle_and_runtime_share_persistent_inbox` (appends via runtime are visible to handle). Sentinel-legatus: 16 tests passing (6 prior + 10 new). Zero net-new clippy errors over the pre-existing baseline; fmt clean.

  `fs2::FileExt::{lock_exclusive,lock_shared,unlock}` share method names with `std::fs::File` inherent methods stabilized in Rust 1.89, so clippy flags them as `incompatible_msrv` against the workspace's 1.83 MSRV even though fs2's trait impl is what the compiler actually picks; suppressed at module level with a documented `#![allow(clippy::incompatible_msrv)]` referencing the rationale. **Out of scope for this commit**: mid-run failure detection (the next slice — `InstructionResult` outcome classification beyond `Success`); cancel/redirect support (after that — new `CancelInstruction` protocol message). Escalation persistence is a future improvement (separate file, same lock discipline) — flagged in the module docstring.

### Fixed
- **`tasks.md` shrink guard — prevent auto-block wipe from small sessions** (2026-05-16). The `task_persist` hook used to unconditionally overwrite `<repo>/tasks.md`'s `<!-- SENTINEL:TASKS:START -->` marker block with whatever the current session's `TaskList` rendered. When a brand-new session opened with only a handful of fresh tasks, the persist hook replaced an 80–100-task accumulated block with the new 3–5-task render — the user's visible task history vanished from the auto-block on the first `TaskCreate` of the new session. Root cause: `write_project_tasks_md` had no notion of "this would shrink the visible content"; it deduplicated only on byte-equality of the merged output. Fix: `write_project_tasks_md` now counts task entries in the existing block (incomplete `### [_] N. …` headers + completed `- [x] **N. …` lines) and refuses to overwrite when the new render has fewer than `SHRINK_GUARD_RATIO` (= 0.5) of the existing block's count AND the existing block has at least `SHRINK_GUARD_MIN_EXISTING` (= 10) tasks. Below the 10-task floor, small projects shrink freely (no false alarms on first-few-tasks sessions). The shrink-refuse path returns `Ok(false)` (write skipped, not a hard error) and emits a single `tracing::warn` naming both counts plus the override env var. `SENTINEL_FORCE_TASKS_MD_WRITE=1` bypasses the guard for the bulk-cleanup / project-pivot cases where shrinking is intentional. Two new helpers (`count_block_tasks`, `extract_existing_block`) and 10 new unit tests pin the behavior: counter handles open + completed + empty bodies, marker extraction returns inner body or `None`, guard refuses 80→5 wipe, guard allows 75% routine churn, guard stays off for 8-task baselines, force env overrides, initial write (no prior block) always succeeds, growth always writes through. Env-touching tests serialize on a module-local `Mutex` to avoid races in Rust's parallel test runner. Sentinel-application: 998 tests passing (988 prior + 10 new). Clippy --all-targets clean on the new code.

### Added
- **A2 Phase 5 — `route_capability` MCP tool exposes the router to Legatus AI peers** (2026-05-17). Final A2 slice (`docs/a2-capability-aware-routing.md` §5.5). The capability router substrate is now reachable from outside sentinel — Legatus AI peers, external orchestrators, and any tool that speaks MCP can query the same routing logic sentinel's internal hooks use, keeping the substrate single-source-of-truth across the AI-factory. New MCP tool `sentinel__route_capability` registered in `crates/sentinel-cli/src/mcp_cmd.rs` (~+100 lines + 5 unit tests). Takes a `CapabilityRequirement` JSON arg; returns the full `RoutingExplanation` (chosen `AgentId` or null, candidate set, eliminated agents with reasons, fired tie-breakers, requirement signature) so callers can inspect *why* the router picked what it picked — not just the outcome. Loads agent profiles at call time via `TomlCapabilityRouter::with_shipped_and_overrides(~/.claude/sentinel/config/agents.toml)`, the same constructor `hook_cmd.rs` uses for internal dispatch, so external and internal consumers see exactly the same catalog. Implementation in `handle_route_capability(request, args)`: (1) parses `args.requirement` as `CapabilityRequirement` (clear error message naming the field + linking to the spec section if parse fails); (2) constructs the router (clear error if `agents.toml` loading fails); (3) calls `router.explain(&req)` (NOT `route()` — `explain` returns even when no agent satisfies, so callers can see the decision tree on misses; the same trait surface is available via `route()` for callers wanting an error-on-miss path); (4) returns the serde-serialized `RoutingExplanation`. Synchronous handler (no async I/O on the hot path); embedded in the existing async `handle_request` dispatcher. Tool definition in `tool_definitions()` documents the input schema with examples of every Capability variant (Reasoning / DifferentVendorFrom / StructuredOutput / CostBudget / etc.) so Legatus AI peers don't need to read the Rust source to author requirements. Description references `docs/a2-capability-aware-routing.md` for the full vocabulary. **End-to-end example**: a Legatus AI peer authoring a BA orchestrator wants to pick "the cheapest non-Anthropic standard-reasoning auditor for a `git push` review" — sends `{"requirement": {"required": [{"Reasoning": "standard"}, {"DifferentVendorFrom": "Anthropic"}, {"StructuredOutput": "AuditorVerdict"}], "preferred": [], "forbidden": []}}` via `mcp__sentinel__route_capability`, receives `{"chosen": "kimi-k2-6-ollama-cloud", "candidates": ["kimi-k2-6-ollama-cloud", "openai-gpt-5-5"], "eliminated": [{"agent_id": "claude-opus-4-7", "reason": ...}, {"agent_id": "claude-sonnet-4-6", "reason": ...}], "tie_breakers_applied": [{"Cost": {"winner": "kimi-k2-6-ollama-cloud", "cost_per_input_token": 0.000001}}], "requirement_signature": "..."}`. Same decision sentinel's internal A3 auditor selection would make; same catalog; same algorithm. 5 unit tests pin behavior: missing `requirement` field returns `isError=true` with a descriptive error; malformed `requirement` (e.g. `"required": "not-an-array"`) returns `isError=true` with a parse-error message; valid requirement against shipped defaults returns a populated `RoutingExplanation` with a non-empty `candidates` list; contrived no-satisfy requirement returns `isError=false` (explain() always succeeds even on no-match — that's the contract) with `chosen=null`; tool definition listing includes `sentinel__route_capability`. Sentinel-cli: 139 tests passing (134 prior + 5 new). Clippy clean on the new function + tests.

  **A2 status (after this commit)**: feature-complete. The full pipeline — capability domain types (Phase 1) → ports (Phase 2) → static router + in-memory store (Phase 3a) → TOML router + shipped agent profiles (Phase 3b) → JSONL appraisal store (Phase 3c) → A3 auditor selection wiring (Phase 4) → MCP tool surface (Phase 5) — is live, tested, and operator-configurable via `~/.claude/sentinel/config/agents.toml`. Operators register profiles; sentinel routes auditor / future-critic / future-coder picks via the router; Legatus AI peers query the same router through the MCP tool; appraisal records feed back into the router's tie-breakers. A future phase will add appraisal-record emission from `dry_run_then_commit` after each auditor verdict (closing the tie-breaker-step-3 feedback loop), plus the planned A2-driven refactors of BA5 critic selection and budget-coder routing — but all of that is on top of this completed substrate.

- **A2 Phase 4 — A3 auditor selection consumes the capability router** (2026-05-17). Connects the A2 substrate to A3's production auditor selection so operators registering profiles in `agents.toml` actually drive which model audits Irreversible/Catastrophic actions, replacing the static `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_PROVIDER + SENTINEL_AUDITOR_MODEL` env-var pick with capability-aware routing. Two new constructors on `RigAuditor` in `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/dry_run_auditor.rs` (~+200 lines + 7 new unit tests): **(a)** `RigAuditor::for_profile(profile: &AgentCapabilityProfile) -> Result<Self>` — builds an auditor from a router-picked profile. Maps `profile.vendor.true_vendor()` to the appropriate rig-core provider via an exhaustive match (no wildcard — new `VendorClass` variants force a compile-time routing decision): `VendorClass::Ollama` → Ollama provider (auto-detects local vs cloud via `OLLAMA_API_KEY` presence per Phase 5); all other variants (`Anthropic | Openai | Google | Xai | Meta | Mistral | Openrouter | Other(..) | Unknown`) → OpenRouter provider (single auth surface `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` fronts the multi-vendor catalog). `profile.model_id` is used directly — the SENTINEL_AUDITOR_MODEL env var is IGNORED when a profile is supplied (the router has decided which model to use; env var overrides would defeat the point). `for_profile_with(profile, env_resolver)` is the test seam — the public `for_profile` wraps it with `real_env`. **(b)** `RigAuditor::via_router(router, profiles, acting_vendor) -> Result<Self>` — queries the router with the A3 auditor `CapabilityRequirement` (`Reasoning(Standard)` + `DifferentVendorFrom(acting_vendor)` + `StructuredOutput(AuditorVerdict)`, preferred `Reasoning(Deep)`), looks up the chosen `AgentId` in the supplied catalog, and constructs via `for_profile`. Errors when the router has no candidates (router returns `NoAgentSatisfies`) or when the chosen `AgentId` isn't in the catalog (programming error — caller passed mismatched router + profiles list); both surface as `anyhow::Error` with descriptive messages. `via_router_with(router, profiles, acting_vendor, env)` is the test seam. **(c)** Both constructors honor existing semantics: `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_TIMEOUT_SECS` read via the same `read_timeout` helper; `provider_prefix` (`"openrouter"` / `"ollama-local"` / `"ollama-cloud"`) propagates to the `auditor_model` attribution string so the proof chain can tell which provider produced each verdict.

  Production wiring in `crates/sentinel-cli/src/hook_cmd.rs` constructs a `TomlCapabilityRouter` at hook entry via `with_shipped_and_overrides(Some("~/.claude/sentinel/config/agents.toml"))` (degrades to empty profile list on load failure with a `tracing::warn`). The auditor construction then runs a two-step priority chain: (1) **Router-based** — if the router has registered profiles, try `RigAuditor::via_router(&router, router.profiles(), VendorClass::Anthropic)` (acting vendor hardcoded to Anthropic since Claude Code is Anthropic; future enhancement can make this dynamic). Success → use this auditor + log "A3 auditor selected via A2 capability router" at info level. (2) **Env-only fallback** — if the router has no profiles OR `via_router` fails (no matching profile, missing API key for the chosen profile's vendor, etc.), fall back to `RigAuditor::from_env()` (the Phase 4 legacy path driven by `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_PROVIDER + SENTINEL_AUDITOR_MODEL`). This preserves the behavior for operators who haven't customized `agents.toml`: shipped defaults + `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` or `OLLAMA_API_KEY` keeps working without ceremony. Both paths failing keeps A3 inert (`a3_enabled = false`); `tool_usage_gate`'s four-check stack handles Irreversible/Catastrophic as the pre-A3 fallback per the existing Phase 4 contract.

  **End-to-end flow with both layers wired**: operator (a) keeps `OLLAMA_API_KEY` set, (b) shipped `agents-defaults.toml` already includes `kimi-k2-6-ollama-cloud` profile, (c) Claude Code runs a `git push origin main` (classified Catastrophic). `dry_run_then_commit` fires; router Legatus AItation: requirement is `Reasoning(Standard) + DifferentVendorFrom(Anthropic) + AuditorVerdict + preferred(Deep)`. Anthropic profiles (`claude-opus-4-7`, `claude-sonnet-4-6`) eliminated by `DifferentVendorFrom`. Remaining candidates: `kimi-k2-6-ollama-cloud` (Standard) + `openai-gpt-5-5` (Deep). Preferred-score tie-breaker: GPT wins on `Reasoning(Deep)` if `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` is configured; otherwise GPT's `for_profile` errors at the API-key check + falls through to Kimi. Verdict ships from whichever model the operator's configured keys + the router's catalog converges on. Operator can override by adding their own `agents.toml` entries; the merge replaces same-`agent_id` profiles. **Operator UX**: `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_PROVIDER + SENTINEL_AUDITOR_MODEL` still work (legacy path); operators wanting capability-based routing add an `agents.toml` with their preferred profiles. A `tracing::info` log at session start names which path succeeded so operators can confirm router vs env in their telemetry.

  7 new unit tests in `dry_run_auditor.rs` (all using the `*_with` env-resolver seam + a `StubRouter` test helper that asserts the requirement carries `DifferentVendorFrom` + `StructuredOutput(AuditorVerdict)`): `for_profile_ollama_local_when_no_api_key` (Ollama profile, no OLLAMA_API_KEY → `provider_prefix=ollama-local`); `for_profile_ollama_cloud_when_api_key_present` (Ollama profile + OLLAMA_API_KEY → `ollama-cloud`); `for_profile_openrouter_path_for_anthropic_vendor` (Anthropic profile + OPENROUTER_API_KEY → `openrouter`); `for_profile_openrouter_errors_when_key_missing` (no key → clear error naming `OPENROUTER_API_KEY`); `for_profile_ignores_sentinel_auditor_model_env` (profile.model_id wins over env — the router-has-decided contract); `via_router_picks_chosen_agent_and_constructs_for_it` (full path: stub router picks `kimi-k2-6-ollama-cloud`, env has `OLLAMA_API_KEY`, result is `ollama-cloud:kimi-k2.6`); `via_router_errors_when_chosen_agent_id_not_in_catalog` (ghost agent_id → descriptive error); `via_router_errors_when_router_returns_no_agent_satisfies` (empty router → "router could not pick" error). Sentinel-infrastructure: 201 tests passing (194 prior + 7 new). Sentinel-cli: 134 tests passing (unchanged — hook_cmd's modifications don't break existing tests). Clippy clean on the modified files (zero new warnings — addressed unused-imports, doc-markdown backticks on `OpenRouter`, `match_wildcard` via exhaustive vendor match, format-args inlining, and items-after-statements by hoisting the `EmptyRouter` test struct out of its `#[test]` function). Out of scope: A2's `route_capability` MCP tool surface (Phase 5 — exposes the router to Legatus AI peers so they can query the same substrate); appraisal-record emission from `dry_run_then_commit` after auditor verdicts (a future phase will record outcomes to feed back into tie-breaker step 3).

- **A2 Phase 3c — JSONL-backed `AppraisalStorePort` adapter in sentinel-infrastructure** (2026-05-17). Production appraisal-store complement to Phase 3a's in-memory variant. Persists [`AppraisalRecord`]s to a single append-only JSONL file at `~/.claude/sentinel/state/appraisal/records.jsonl` (overridable for tests). Closes the Phase 3a → Phase 3b → Phase 3c trio: Phase 3a was the algorithm + in-memory store, Phase 3b was the TOML router, and Phase 3c is the persistent appraisal-data layer that completes the substrate. New `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/appraisal_store.rs` (~310 lines + 12 unit tests) defines: **(a)** `JsonlAppraisalStore` — implements `AppraisalStorePort` with append-only writes + scan-and-filter reads. Builder API: `at_path(PathBuf)` (test-pointed), `with_default_path()` (`~/.claude/sentinel/state/appraisal/records.jsonl`). `path()` accessor for operator tooling. **(b)** Atomic appends via `OpenOptions::new().create(true).append(true)`. POSIX guarantees atomic writes ≤ `PIPE_BUF` (4096 bytes) under `O_APPEND` so concurrent appends from multiple sentinel processes interleave at line boundaries without explicit file locking — auditor-verdict-sized records are typically 300-800 bytes, well within the atomic regime. Lines that exceed `PIPE_BUF` (currently impossible at our record shape) would not be guaranteed atomic; the reader's `serde_json::from_str` would fail on the malformed line and the record would be skipped with a `tracing::warn`. **(c)** Best-effort persistence: `record()` returns `()` per the port trait, never propagates I/O errors to the calling hook — writes that fail emit `tracing::warn` and drop the record. The dispatching hook is never blocked or aborted by appraisal failures (the design contract is that appraisal is observability data, not critical-path correctness data). **(d)** Auto-truncation at `MAX_LOG_SIZE` (8 MB ≈ 50_000 records — well past the router's 200-record window). When the file grows past the cap, the next `record()` call: (1) acquires the internal `Mutex<()>` truncate guard, (2) double-checks size under the lock, (3) reads all records, (4) keeps the trailing half, (5) rewrites via atomic `tmp + rename` so a crash mid-write doesn't truncate to zero. Concurrent appends during the rewrite are POSIX-atomic and land after the rename; the brief window between snapshot-read and rename-into-place could lose 1-2 records from concurrent appends — acceptable for observability data. **(e)** Malformed-line tolerance: `read_all_records` parses line-by-line, skipping unparseable lines with a warn-level log + line number for diagnostic. Partial writes (rare; impossible under PIPE_BUF) don't poison the whole file. **(f)** Window semantics match Phase 3a's `InMemoryAppraisalStore`: `All` (every record), `LastN(n)` (trailing n via slice), `LastHours(h)` (timestamp ≥ now() - h hours). Both stores share the [`sentinel_domain::agent_routing::AggregateStats::from_records`] computation so router behavior is identical regardless of which store is mounted.

  12 unit tests use `tempfile::TempDir` for isolation: missing file returns empty aggregate cleanly; record-then-aggregate returns correct strict-success rate (`2 Success + 1 Failure → 2/3`); `record()` auto-creates the parent directory tree (so `with_default_path()` works on fresh installs that don't have `~/.claude/sentinel/state/appraisal/`); records segregate by `(agent_id, requirement_signature)` (4-way cross of two agents × two sigs → 4 distinct buckets); `LastN(2)` against `[F, F, F, F, F, S, S]` returns 2 trailing Successes (rate=1.0); `LastHours(24)` excludes a record timestamped 48 hours back; second `JsonlAppraisalStore` instance pointed at the same file reads what the first instance wrote (cross-instance persistence); malformed line injected mid-file does NOT propagate — valid records before+after are still counted; `truncate_keeps_trailing_half_when_oversized` pads the file with `MAX_LOG_SIZE + 1024` bytes of garbage, fires `record()`, asserts file size dropped below `MAX_LOG_SIZE` and the aggregate still has records; `with_default_path` resolves to a path containing `.claude` + `sentinel` + ends with `records.jsonl`; compile-time `Send + Sync` assert on `JsonlAppraisalStore`. Module registered alphabetically in `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/lib.rs` between `anthropic` and `capability_router`. Sentinel-infrastructure: 194 tests passing (181 prior + 12 new + 1 incremental for Phase 3b mid-test landing). Clippy clean on the new module (zero warnings after addressing too-long-first-paragraph on `MAX_LOG_SIZE`, `finish_non_exhaustive` on the manual `Debug` impl that hides `truncate_guard`, `const fn at_path`, and `usize::try_from` conversions for the `MAX_LOG_SIZE` size hints). **R5 quarantine boundary**: documented at module-level and on the trait — appraisal records flow ONE WAY from dispatching hook → store → router as a tie-breaker input. Agents must never see appraisal data as feedback. The contract is on the port; both adapters (in-memory + JSONL) honor it by exposing only `record` + `aggregate`. **Operator UX**: the JSONL file is human-readable; operators can `cat ~/.claude/sentinel/state/appraisal/records.jsonl | jq` to inspect routing history. The file location matches sentinel's existing state-store convention (`~/.claude/sentinel/state/` namespace). Out of scope: A3 wiring (Phase 4 — refactor `dry_run_auditor.rs` to query the router instead of the static `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_MODEL` env var); `route_capability` MCP tool surface (Phase 5).

- **A2 Phase 3b — TOML-backed `CapabilityRouterPort` adapter in sentinel-infrastructure** (2026-05-17). Production adapter that loads [`AgentCapabilityProfile`]s from TOML and delegates routing to the Phase 3a shared `pick()` algorithm — so the TOML adapter and the `StaticCapabilityRouter` test helper produce identical decisions on identical inputs. New `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/capability_router.rs` (~380 lines + 15 unit tests) defines: **(a)** `TomlCapabilityRouter` — production [`CapabilityRouterPort`] implementation; profile list immutable after construction (operator-driven hot reload via sentinel restart). Builder API: `from_profiles(v)` (tests / hand-crafted), `with_shipped_defaults()` (loads the embedded baseline), `from_toml_str(s)` (parse + validate), `from_toml_path(p)` (file-load wrapper), `with_shipped_and_overrides(Option<&Path>)` (production startup path: shipped defaults + optional operator overrides from `~/.claude/sentinel/config/agents.toml`), `with_appraisal_store(Arc<dyn AppraisalStorePort>)` (tie-breaker step 3 enable), `with_window(w)` (appraisal window override). All three trait methods implemented by delegating to `sentinel_application::capability_router::pick`. `profiles()` accessor returns the registered catalog for operator-facing tooling. **(b)** `SHIPPED_AGENTS_DEFAULTS` — `pub const &str` containing `config/agents-defaults.toml` baked in via `include_str!` at compile time. Sentinel ships with 4 baseline profiles registered: `claude-opus-4-7` (deep-reasoning strong coder, $0.000015/in-token), `claude-sonnet-4-6` (standard-reasoning daily driver, $0.000003/in-token), `kimi-k2-6-ollama-cloud` (Kimi K2.6 via Ollama Cloud, $0.000001/in-token — vendor `Ollama` so A3's `DifferentVendorFrom(Anthropic)` qualifies), `openai-gpt-5-5` (deep alt-vendor, $0.000005/in-token). Operators register additional profiles or override these by `agent_id` in `~/.claude/sentinel/config/agents.toml`; the loader merges same-id REPLACES + new-id APPENDS. **(c)** `AgentsConfigToml` schema — single `[[agent]]` array-of-tables; per-entry fields match `AgentCapabilityProfile` exactly. Capability variants encoded externally-tagged per the Phase 1 serde shape (`{ Reasoning = "deep" }`, `{ ToolUse = ["Read", "Edit"] }`, `{ StructuredOutput = "AuditorVerdict" }`, etc.). `ReasoningLevel` is `rename_all = "snake_case"` so TOML uses `"shallow" | "standard" | "deep"` (lowercase) — the shipped defaults + test fixtures + the operator doc-comment all use this casing. **(d)** Validation rules enforced at load (`validate_profiles`): unique `agent_id` within a file (duplicate → load error naming the duplicate); non-negative `cost_per_input_token` + `cost_per_output_token`; `typical_latency_ms` strictly in `(0, 300_000]` (rejects 0 and >5min as misconfiguration signals); `max_context_tokens > 0`; non-empty `display_name` (trim-aware). Each validation failure surfaces as `anyhow::Error` with the offending `agent_id` named in the message — sentinel refuses to start with invalid profiles rather than route to ghost agents (per spec §7.2). **(e)** Merge semantics in `merge_overrides(shipped, overrides)`: same-`agent_id` overrides REPLACE shipped entries at the same Vec position (preserves declaration order in the merged catalog); new-`agent_id` overrides APPEND. `with_shipped_and_overrides` returns the shipped-only router cleanly when the overrides path is `None` or doesn't exist on disk (operator hasn't customized yet — common first-run state, logged at debug).

  New `config/agents-defaults.toml` (~110 lines including extensive schema-documenting comments). The comments enumerate every capability variant the operator can declare so a new operator doesn't need to read the source to author overrides. Operators register OpenRouter-fronted models with `vendor = { Other = { underlying_vendor = "<vendor>" } }` so A3's `DifferentVendorFrom` check sees the true upstream vendor (per Phase 1's `VendorClass::Other::true_vendor` semantics). The shipped Kimi K2.6 profile uses `vendor = "Ollama"` to match the verified Phase 5 live smoke (Ollama Cloud at `https://ollama.com/v1`); operators using Kimi via OpenRouter instead would register a separate profile with `vendor = { Other = { underlying_vendor = "Unknown" } }`.

  15 unit tests: shipped defaults parse + load cleanly (catches any embedded-TOML regression at CI time); minimal one-agent profile parses; multi-agent TOML parses to a 2-profile catalog; malformed TOML produces an `anyhow::Error` whose message contains "parse"; unknown vendor surfaces at parse time (`"TotallyMadeUp"` triggers serde's "unknown variant" error path); validation: duplicate `agent_id` is rejected with a "duplicate agent_id" message naming the duplicate; negative `cost_per_input_token` rejected; `typical_latency_ms = 0` rejected; `typical_latency_ms > 300_000` rejected with the 300_000 cap in the message; empty/whitespace `display_name` rejected; `merge_overrides` REPLACES on same-id; `merge_overrides` APPENDS on new-id; end-to-end route through the TOML adapter on the realistic A3 fixture picks `kimi` (Standard reasoning + non-Anthropic) over `opus` (Anthropic — eliminated by `DifferentVendorFrom`); `NoAgentSatisfies` carries the nearest-miss diagnostics so operators can fix profiles or requirements; compile-time `Send + Sync` on `TomlCapabilityRouter`. Module registered alphabetically in `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/lib.rs` between `anthropic` and `config`. Sentinel-infrastructure: 181 tests passing (166 prior + 15 new). Clippy clean on the new module (zero warnings — addressed `match_wildcard_for_single_variants` with explicit `RoutingError::Configuration` exhaustive pattern). **Algorithm equivalence**: the TOML adapter and `StaticCapabilityRouter` both delegate to `sentinel_application::capability_router::pick`; identical inputs produce identical decisions. Operators picking the TOML adapter for production get exactly the same routing semantics tests pin. Out of scope: JSONL-backed `AppraisalStorePort` adapter (Phase 3c — split from 3b to keep diffs reviewable); A3 wiring (Phase 4); `route_capability` MCP tool (Phase 5). **Operator UX note**: the shipped defaults file at `config/agents-defaults.toml` is the primary reference for what fields and capability variants look like in TOML — operators copy-paste from there into their overrides file rather than parsing the Rust source.

- **Per-instruction roundtrip (sentinel side) — `Legatus AI_inbox` emits Ack, `execution_log` emits Result** (2026-05-17). Closes per-instruction accounting on the sentinel side (the Legatus AI-side wiring shipped in `legatus-ai` as `a3f6702`). Now the operator sees per-instruction confirmation in chat: `"firefly is on it (id abcd1234)."` when sentinel's `Legatus AI_inbox` hook drains the daemon's inbox, then `"firefly finished (id abcd1234): <summary>."` when the next `Stop` hook fires. The `EscalationKind` enum in `sentinel-legatus` gained two variants — `InstructionAck { instruction_id }` and `InstructionResult { instruction_id, outcome, summary }` — both serializable so the daemon's existing `POST /legatus/escalate` route accepts them with zero new HTTP surface. The connect loop in `client.rs` matches the new variants and produces the matching `InstructionAcknowledged` / `InstructionResult` Legatus AI Protocol envelopes signed with the outbound MAC key. New `legatus_client::ack_fire_and_forget(instruction_id)` and `report_result_fire_and_forget(instruction_id, outcome, summary)` helpers wrap `escalate_fire_and_forget` for hook-call ergonomics. Per-session pending-id tracking lives at `~/.claude/sentinel/state/<session_id>.legatus-pending.txt` (one instruction id per line) — `Legatus AI_inbox` appends on drain via `note_pending_instruction`, `execution_log` reads + clears via `take_pending_instructions` on Stop and fires one `InstructionResult` per pending id with `outcome: Success` and the run's existing summary (last `[RUN]`/`[STEP]`/`[PHASE]` marker truncated to 140 chars). Pending-file path validates against directory traversal (`../`, `/`, `\`, empty session id rejected). Race tolerance per the operator's ~90-95% reliability target: an `append` racing with a `read+delete` may lose one id; operator just misses one Result ping. MVP outcome classification is always `Success` — sentinel doesn't yet detect mid-run failures and translate them to `Failure { error }` / `Declined { reason }`. 3 new unit tests in `legatus_client`: path traversal rejection, note → take roundtrip (file is consumed), take on missing session returns empty. Existing `Legatus AI_inbox` and `execution_log` tests still pass (fire-and-forget threads are invisible to sync test harnesses).

  **End-to-end runtime path now per-instruction visible**:
  ```
  Operator: (Telegram) "firefly please deploy staging"
    → Legatus AI: "✓ relayed to firefly: deploy staging [id abcd1234]"
    → daemon-hosted legatus inbox: <buffered>
    → next UserPromptSubmit hook drains: Legatus AI_inbox calls ack_fire_and_forget
      → operator: "firefly is on it (id abcd1234)."
      → Legatus AI_inbox appends abcd1234 to legatus-pending.txt
      → Legatus AI_inbox injects PRIMARY-ASK additionalContext for Claude Code
    → Claude Code acts on the instruction, finishes turn
    → Stop hook fires: execution_log emits SessionCompleted (existing) AND
      for each id in legatus-pending.txt: report_result_fire_and_forget(Success, summary)
      → operator: "firefly finished (id abcd1234): <summary>."
  ```

- **A2 Phase 3a — Static router + in-memory appraisal store in sentinel-application** (2026-05-17). Third slice of A2 (`docs/a2-capability-aware-routing.md` §3 algorithm). Ships the **pure routing algorithm** + an **application-layer test helper** for both ports. The TOML-backed production adapters (Phase 3b in sentinel-infrastructure) wrap the same algorithm, so the behavior here IS the contract — adapters only differ in where they load profiles from. New `crates/sentinel-application/src/capability_router.rs` (~330 lines + 11 unit tests) defines: **(a)** `pub fn pick(profiles, requirement, appraisal_store, window) -> RoutingExplanation` — the pure algorithm implementing the spec's 6-step tie-breaker chain. Step 1: required + forbidden filtering (eliminated agents carry per-step `EliminationReason::UnsatisfiedRequirement` or `ForbiddenCapabilityMatched`). Step 2: preferred score (most preferred-capabilities satisfied wins). Step 3: appraisal success rate when an `AppraisalStorePort` is configured AND the cohort meets `MIN_COHORT_FOR_APPRAISAL_TIE_BREAK` (=20) — strict `Success` rate via `agg.success_rate`; below-threshold cohorts fall through so a "100% on 3 calls" agent doesn't dominate a "92% on 200 calls" agent. Step 4: cost (`cost_per_input_token` lowest). Step 5: latency (`typical_latency_ms` lowest). Step 6: stable `AgentId` lexical order (final deterministic fallback). Every step records a `TieBreaker` entry in the explanation iff it actually fired (eliminated a candidate). Same input always produces the same output. **(b)** `pub const DEFAULT_APPRAISAL_WINDOW: AppraisalWindow = LastN(200)` — spec's calibration target. **(c)** `pub const MIN_COHORT_FOR_APPRAISAL_TIE_BREAK: u32 = 20` — small-cohort guard. **(d)** `StaticCapabilityRouter` — the test helper. Wraps a static `Vec<AgentCapabilityProfile>` + optional `Arc<dyn AppraisalStorePort>` + configurable window. Builder API: `empty()` / `from_profiles(v)` / `with_agent(p)` (chainable) / `with_appraisal_store(arc)` / `with_window(w)`. Implements all three trait methods: `route` returns the chosen `AgentId` or `RoutingError::NoAgentSatisfies(unsatisfied)`; `candidates` returns the post-required/forbidden set BEFORE tie-breakers (useful for debate-style fan-out + the future `sentinel routing explain` CLI); `explain` returns the full decision tree. **(e)** `static_router(profiles)` convenience builder for test prose readability. 11 router tests: empty-router error path; required-filter picks only qualifying agent; forbidden eliminates correctly; realistic A3 requirement scenario (acting=Anthropic, required `DifferentVendorFrom(Anthropic) + StructuredOutput(AuditorVerdict)`, preferred `Reasoning(Deep)` → GPT wins over Kimi via preferred-score step 2); each of steps 2/4/5/6 wins isolated correctly (preferred score, cost after preferred tie, latency after cost tie via identical-cost twins, stable-ID lexical order after latency tie); `candidates()` returns the pre-tie-break qualifying set; `explain()` records eliminated agents with the correct `EliminationReason`; `explain()` records `TieBreaker::PreferredScore` when it fires.

  New `crates/sentinel-application/src/appraisal_store.rs` (~150 lines + 8 unit tests) defines: **`InMemoryAppraisalStore`** — `HashMap<(AgentId, RequirementSignature), Vec<AppraisalRecord>>` behind a `RwLock` so it's `Send + Sync` and `Arc`-wrappable for sharing across hooks within a session. Implements `AppraisalStorePort`: `record(r)` (best-effort persistence — poisoned-lock failures log via `tracing::warn` instead of panicking, so a dispatching hook never blocks on lock-recovery semantics); `aggregate(agent, signature, window)` (HashMap lookup → window filter → `AggregateStats::from_records`). Window semantics: `All` returns every record; `LastN(n)` returns the trailing `n` (or all if fewer exist); `LastHours(h)` filters by `timestamp >= now() - h hours`. `record_count()` snapshot helper for tests + observability. 8 appraisal tests: empty-store aggregates to `empty()` with `has_data() == false`; record + aggregate returns correct strict-success rate (`2 success + 1 failure → 2/3`); records segregate correctly by agent_id (kimi=1.0 success, opus=0.0 from the same bucket); records segregate correctly by signature; `LastN(2)` of `[F, F, F, F, F, S, S]` returns only the last 2 (both `Success` → rate=1.0); `LastHours(24)` excludes a record timestamped 48 hours ago; `record_count()` reflects persisted count; compile-time `Send + Sync`.

  Modules registered alphabetically in `crates/sentinel-application/src/lib.rs` — `pub mod appraisal_store` before `auditor`, `pub mod capability_router` between `cache_efficiency` and `channel_events`. Sentinel-application: 1052 tests passing (1027 prior + 25 new — 11 capability_router + 8 appraisal_store + 6 shadow that incrementally landed). The 3 pre-existing `phase_gate` failures (task #21) remain unchanged. Clippy clean on the new modules (zero warnings after addressing `let...else` over match-on-RwLock, splitting too-long-first-paragraph on `DEFAULT_APPRAISAL_WINDOW` + `MIN_COHORT_FOR_APPRAISAL_TIE_BREAK` docs, and a single `#[allow(clippy::too_many_lines)]` on `pick` — the 6-step chain reads cleaner inline than fragmented across helpers, and the function is heavily commented step-by-step). **Algorithm-equivalent contract**: the Phase 3b TOML adapter MUST delegate to this `pick` function or replicate its exact tie-breaker order; both routers MUST produce identical decisions on identical inputs. Out of scope: TOML profile loading + JSONL appraisal persistence (Phase 3b — `sentinel-infrastructure`); A3 wiring (Phase 4); `route_capability` MCP tool (Phase 5).

- **A2 Phase 2 — `CapabilityRouterPort` + `AppraisalStorePort` traits in sentinel-domain** (2026-05-17). Second slice of A2 (`docs/a2-capability-aware-routing.md` §§3-4). Adds the substrate dispatch trait + appraisal-history trait + supporting data types — still no logic; Phase 3a/3b add the static and TOML-backed implementations. New `crates/sentinel-domain/src/agent_routing.rs` (~360 lines + 11 unit tests) defines all the routing-decision data types A2's ports return: (a) `RequirementSignature` — newtype-`String` carrying the first 16 hex chars of SHA-256 over a canonicalized JSON encoding of a `CapabilityRequirement`. Each of `required` / `preferred` / `forbidden` is sorted by lexical JSON-string order before hashing so order-of-construction doesn't shift the bucket key — two semantically-equal requirements always hash to the same signature. Used as the per-agent / per-requirement bucket key in the appraisal store. (b) `EliminationReason` — `UnsatisfiedRequirement(Vec<UnsatisfiedRequirement>)` and `ForbiddenCapabilityMatched(String)`; `UnsatisfiedRequirement` carries a JSON-rendered capability + human-readable explanation. (c) `TieBreaker` — fully enumerates the spec's 6-step tie-breaker order so `routing explain` traces every step that actually fired: `PreferredScore`, `AppraisalSuccessRate`, `Cost`, `Latency`, `StableId`. (d) `RoutingExplanation` — `chosen` (the picked `AgentId` or `None`), `candidates`, `eliminated`, `tie_breakers_applied`, `requirement_signature`. Returned by `CapabilityRouterPort::explain` and serialized for the future `sentinel routing explain` CLI subcommand. (e) `AppraisalOutcome` — `Success / PartialSuccess / Failure / Abandoned` per-record outcome label. (f) `AppraisalRecord` — single past dispatch outcome: agent + signature + outcome + optional `AuditorVerdict` + actual cost + actual latency + tokens-in/out + timestamp. Doc comment carries the **R5 quarantine boundary** load-bearing note: appraisal records are dispatch input only, never training feedback. (g) `AggregateStats` — `cohort_size`, `success_rate` (strict — only `Success`), `permissive_success_rate` (`Success + PartialSuccess`), `mean_cost_usd`, `mean_latency_ms`. Const `empty()` constructor for the no-data fallthrough path; `has_data()` predicate; `from_records(&[AppraisalRecord]) -> Self` aggregation helper computed once at the call site so neither the router nor adapter need to redo the math. (h) `AppraisalWindow` — `LastN(u32) / LastHours(u32) / All` time/count windowing argument for aggregation queries.

  Two new traits appended to existing `crates/sentinel-domain/src/ports.rs` (rather than a `ports/` subdirectory, matching the codebase convention): **`CapabilityRouterPort`** — `route(&CapabilityRequirement) -> Result<AgentId, RoutingError>` (the substrate dispatch primitive every consumer hook queries); `candidates(&CapabilityRequirement) -> Vec<AgentId>` (returns every requirement-clearing agent before tie-breakers, used for debate-style fan-out + `explain` subcommand); `explain(&CapabilityRequirement) -> RoutingExplanation` (full decision tree). **`AppraisalStorePort`** — `record(AppraisalRecord)` (best-effort persistence — failures log but never block dispatching); `aggregate(&AgentId, &RequirementSignature, AppraisalWindow) -> AggregateStats` (returns `AggregateStats::empty()` for missing buckets so the router falls through to the next tie-breaker rather than erroring). Both `Send + Sync` per existing port convention. New `RoutingError` enum in `ports.rs` — `NoAgentSatisfies(Vec<UnsatisfiedRequirement>)` carries nearest-miss diagnostics so operators can fix profiles or relax requirements, `Configuration(String)` for startup-time misconfiguration. Hand-rolled `Display` + `std::error::Error` (no thiserror in sentinel-domain — deps are deliberately minimal).

  11 unit tests pin: `RequirementSignature::of` is stable across construction order (sorting `required` deterministically before hashing); changes when required levels differ; changes when preferred capabilities differ; is exactly 16 hex chars; `AggregateStats::from_records` returns empty for `&[]` with `has_data() == false`; strict-vs-permissive success rate accounting (2/4 strict vs 3/4 permissive when set is `[Success, Success, PartialSuccess, Failure]`); `Abandoned` outcome counts as non-success in both modes; mean cost + mean latency arithmetic; `AppraisalRecord` serde round-trip with `AuditorVerdict` payload; `RoutingExplanation` serde round-trip with all variant types populated; compile-time `Send + Sync` asserts on `RequirementSignature` / `AppraisalRecord` / `AggregateStats` / `RoutingExplanation` / `AppraisalWindow`. Module registered alphabetically in `crates/sentinel-domain/src/lib.rs` between `pub mod` (top) and `pub mod capability`. Sentinel-domain: 459 tests passing (448 prior + 11 new). Clippy clean on the new module + port-trait section (zero warnings on agent_routing.rs / new ports.rs section after addressing `derive_partial_eq_without_eq` on `EliminationReason` + `UnsatisfiedRequirement` + `RoutingError`, and one `AgentId` backtick on doc). **Note on R5 boundary**: the doc comment on `AppraisalRecord` + `AppraisalStorePort` explicitly forbids using appraisal data as training feedback for agents. The trait surface enforces this naturally — the port only exposes `record` / `aggregate`, not "stream back to agent for fine-tuning" — but the explicit doc comment is the contract for downstream readers. Out of scope: static `StaticCapabilityRouter` test helper (Phase 3a), TOML-backed router + JSONL appraisal store (Phase 3b), A3 wiring (Phase 4), MCP tool surface (Phase 5).

- **A2 Phase 1 — Capability domain types in sentinel-domain** (2026-05-17). First implementation slice of A2 (`docs/a2-capability-aware-routing.md`), the substrate dispatch primitive that replaces R1's retired role-persona pipelines and ports every "which agent / which model for this work" decision onto a shared capability-graph axis. Pure-domain value objects — no business logic; subsequent phases add the ports, static router, TOML adapter, and consumer-hook refactors. New `crates/sentinel-domain/src/capability.rs` (~600 lines + 28 unit tests) defines: (a) `AgentId` — newtype-`String` stable identifier with `new()` rejecting empty / whitespace-only inputs (returns `AgentIdError::Empty`), `as_str()` accessor, `Display` impl, hand-rolled `std::error::Error` for `AgentIdError`. (b) `VendorClass` — externally-tagged enum with explicit named variants for Anthropic / Openai / Google / Xai / Meta / Mistral / Ollama / Openrouter plus `Other { underlying_vendor: Box<Self> }` for gateway-fronted agents (OpenRouter fronting Claude → `Other { underlying_vendor: Anthropic }`) plus `Unknown` for unidentified third parties. `true_vendor()` recursively unwraps `Other` so A3's `DifferentVendorFrom` comparisons see the actual upstream vendor, not the gateway. `is_different_from()` treats `Unknown` as distinct from every other vendor (including another `Unknown` — separate gateway calls aren't presumed to share an upstream). (c) `ReasoningLevel` — `Shallow < Standard < Deep` with manual `Ord` + `PartialOrd` (rank-based) so `agent.has_at_least(required)` is expressible directly; const `at_least()` for compile-time comparisons. (d) `ToolKind` — enumerates `Read / Glob / Grep / Edit / Write / Bash / Task / TaskUpdate / WebFetch / WebSearch` plus `Other(String)` for MCP tools and unknown future tools; not `Copy` because of the `Other(String)` variant. (e) `SchemaRef` — externally-tagged with `AuditorVerdict` (A3 auditor seats), `BaCritique` (BA5 critic seats), `AnyJson` (looser — any JSON shape works), and `Named(String)` for future schemas. `AnyJson` is satisfied by any specific-schema declaration; specific schemas require exact match. (f) `DataZone` — `UsEast / UsWest / Eu / OnPremise / Named(String)` — **reserved for A2 v2 enforcement**; the field is wired now so requirements can declare zones, but the v1 router doesn't enforce actual API geography. (g) `Capability` — externally-tagged enum with 10 variants: `Reasoning(ReasoningLevel)`, `ToolUse(Vec<ToolKind>)`, `StructuredOutput(SchemaRef)`, `Vendor(VendorClass)`, `DifferentVendorFrom(VendorClass)`, `OpenWeights`, `LatencyBudget(u32)`, `CostBudget(f32)`, `ReversibilityClass(ReversibilityClass)` (re-exports A6's class for catastrophic-class routing per A2 spec §5.4), `DataLocality(DataZone)`. `is_satisfied_by(profile)` implements the per-variant resolution rules — `Reasoning` uses `at_least()`, `ToolUse` requires superset, `CostBudget` / `LatencyBudget` use `<=` semantics (agent's actual ≤ requirement's budget = satisfied), `DifferentVendorFrom` uses `true_vendor()` comparison, `StructuredOutput::AnyJson` is satisfied by any specific schema. (h) `AgentCapabilityProfile` — operator-managed declaration with `agent_id`, `display_name`, `vendor`, `model_id`, `declared: Vec<Capability>`, `cost_per_input_token`, `cost_per_output_token`, `typical_latency_ms`, `max_context_tokens`, `data_zones`. Will live in `config/agents.toml` (Phase 3b). (i) `CapabilityRequirement` — `required` / `preferred` / `forbidden` constraint sets with builder-style `with_preferred(c)` / `with_forbidden(c)` and `is_satisfied_by(profile)` (all `required` pass AND no `forbidden` passes) plus `preferred_score(profile)` (count of preferred-satisfied for router tie-breaker step 2). 28 unit tests pin: AgentId construction (empty rejected, whitespace trimmed, Display works); VendorClass `Other` true-vendor resolution + `DifferentVendorFrom` correctly compares through gateways + `Unknown` always distinct; ReasoningLevel ordering (`Deep > Standard > Shallow`, `at_least` semantics); Capability satisfaction — Reasoning satisfies by `at_least`, ToolUse requires superset, CostBudget/LatencyBudget use `<=`, Vendor matches via `true_vendor`, DifferentVendorFrom passes when distinct, StructuredOutput exact + AnyJson special case, OpenWeights / ReversibilityClass per-variant; CapabilityRequirement composition — required-all-pass / forbidden-any-fail / preferred-score; realistic A3 auditor scenario (acting=Anthropic, requirement={Standard reasoning, DifferentVendorFrom(Anthropic), StructuredOutput(AuditorVerdict)} → Anthropic profiles disqualified, non-Anthropic with the schema qualify); catastrophic-class routing scenario (Deep + DifferentVendorFrom + CostBudget forbidden as no-shortcuts gate per spec §5.4); serde round-trip for Capability / CapabilityRequirement / AgentCapabilityProfile; compile-time `Send + Sync` asserts. **Serde shape note**: the spec drafted `#[serde(tag = "kind")]` (internally-tagged), but that collides with `Capability::ToolUse(Vec<ToolKind>)` (newtype-containing-sequence is unsupported with internal tags) and `VendorClass::Other { underlying_vendor: Box<VendorClass> }` (nested same-enum produces "duplicate field `kind`"). Switched to externally-tagged (the serde default) for `VendorClass`, `Capability`, `SchemaRef`, `DataZone` — the on-wire shape becomes `"Anthropic"` (unit), `{"Reasoning":"Deep"}` (newtype), `{"ToolUse":["Edit"]}` (sequence-newtype), which is more idiomatic Rust serde anyway. Module registered alphabetically in `crates/sentinel-domain/src/lib.rs` between `pub mod commit` and pre-existing `pub mod config`. Sentinel-domain: 448 tests passing (420 prior + 28 new). Clippy clean on the new module (zero warnings on capability.rs after addressing doc backticks, `Box<Self>` over `Box<VendorClass>`, `const fn` for rank/at_least/new, and split-first-paragraph for SchemaRef + DataZone). Note: existing `crates/sentinel-domain/src/routing.rs` is the skill-routing regex matcher — unrelated to A2's agent routing. To avoid the name collision, A2 Phase 2's ports will land in `ports/capability_router.rs` (new) rather than reusing `routing.rs`. Out of scope: ports (Phase 2), static router (Phase 3a), TOML config + JSONL appraisal store (Phase 3b), A3 wiring (Phase 4), MCP tool surface (Phase 5).

- **A3 Phase 5 follow-up — Live Ollama Cloud smoke test (`#[ignore]`-gated)** (2026-05-17). Adds `live_ollama_smoke` to `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/dry_run_auditor.rs`'s test module, gated by `#[ignore]` so it stays out of the default suite. Operators verify connectivity + attribution against real Ollama (Cloud or Local) by setting `OLLAMA_API_KEY` + `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_PROVIDER=ollama` + `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_MODEL` and running `cargo test -p sentinel-infrastructure --lib dry_run_auditor::tests::live_ollama -- --ignored --nocapture`. The test constructs `RigAuditor::ollama_from_env()`, scores a fixture `DryRunRequest`, and asserts the `auditor_model` attribution begins with `ollama-`. Verdict shape (decision / confidence / axes / reasoning) is printed via `eprintln!` but not asserted — model judgment varies, this is a connectivity check not a behaviour pin. **Verified against real Ollama Cloud with `kimi-k2.6`** before commit: handshake → bearer auth → `https://ollama.com/v1/chat/completions` → JSON verdict parses cleanly → `auditor_model=ollama-cloud:kimi-k2.6` recorded → Kimi-K2.6 returned a Pass verdict with `confidence=0.90`, axes `correctness=0.95 / intent_alignment=0.95 / safety=0.9 / unstated_assumptions=0.8`, and operator-quality reasoning prose. **Endpoint shape confirmed**: `https://ollama.com/v1` is the OpenAI-compat base URL (matches Phase 5's `DEFAULT_OLLAMA_CLOUD_BASE_URL`). Ollama Cloud catalog at smoke-time included `kimi-k2.6`, `kimi-k2-thinking`, `deepseek-v3.2`, `qwen3-coder-next`, `glm-5.1`, `nemotron-3-super` and many others — operators have broad model choice. No code change beyond the one `#[test] #[ignore]` function (~30 lines) — pure additive op-tooling commit.

- **A3 Phase 5 — Ollama provider (local + cloud) alongside OpenRouter** (2026-05-17). `RigAuditor` now supports either `openrouter` or `ollama` as the LLM backend, selected via `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_PROVIDER` (default `openrouter`). The Ollama path auto-detects local vs cloud by `OLLAMA_API_KEY` presence — both modes route through rig-core's `openai` provider (Ollama's OpenAI-compatible endpoint is the single seam) so the prompt, JSON-parsing, sidecar-runtime, and verdict-decision logic stays identical for every provider. **API changes**: `RigAuditor::from_env()` is now a dispatcher; new `RigAuditor::openrouter_from_env()` and `RigAuditor::ollama_from_env()` expose the per-provider constructors directly. New builder `RigAuditor::with_provider_prefix(prefix)` lets tests assert on the attribution string. New `provider_prefix: String` field on `RigAuditor` records which provider built it (`"openrouter"`, `"ollama-cloud"`, `"ollama-local"`); the `AuditorVerdict::auditor_model` attribution is now `"{provider_prefix}:{model_id}"` (e.g. `"ollama-cloud:moonshotai/kimi-k2"`). `parse_verdict`'s signature changed from `(text, model_id)` to `(text, auditor_model)` — it now records the full attribution string verbatim instead of synthesising the prefix. **Env vars**: `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_PROVIDER` (default `openrouter`, case-insensitive); for `ollama`: `OLLAMA_API_KEY` (presence triggers Cloud mode), `OLLAMA_BASE_URL` (Cloud only, default `https://ollama.com/v1`), `OLLAMA_HOST` (Local only, default `http://localhost:11434` — the adapter appends `/v1`), `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_MODEL` (required — no sensible default for Ollama since operators choose what they've pulled). New public constants: `DEFAULT_AUDITOR_PROVIDER`, `DEFAULT_OPENROUTER_MODEL`, `DEFAULT_OLLAMA_LOCAL_BASE_URL`, `DEFAULT_OLLAMA_CLOUD_BASE_URL`. Existing `DEFAULT_AUDITOR_MODEL` const is `#[deprecated]` (alias for `DEFAULT_OPENROUTER_MODEL`) so Phase 3b callers keep building. **Local Ollama detail**: a dummy bearer token (`"ollama-local"`) is passed because Ollama's OpenAI-compat endpoint ignores it; this keeps the rig-core `openai::Client` (which requires bearer auth) happy. **Testability**: introduced private `*_from_env_with(env_resolver)` variants that take a `Fn(&str) -> Option<String>` closure. Public `*_from_env` constructors wrap them with `real_env` (`std::env::var(k).ok()`). 11 new unit tests use HashMap-backed closures via the `_with` seam — no `unsafe { std::env::set_var(...) }` (workspace forbids unsafe and Rust 2024 marks `set_var` unsafe).
