Tests cover: `score_uses_provider_prefix_in_auditor_model_attribution`, `with_provider_prefix_overrides_default`, `from_env_unknown_provider_errors` (names the invalid value + lists valid ones), `from_env_defaults_to_openrouter_when_provider_unset`, `ollama_from_env_local_mode_when_api_key_absent` (provider_prefix == "ollama-local"), `ollama_from_env_cloud_mode_when_api_key_present` (provider_prefix == "ollama-cloud"), `ollama_from_env_requires_model_id` (clear error naming the env var), `from_env_dispatches_to_ollama_when_provider_ollama`, `from_env_provider_is_case_insensitive` (`"OLLAMA"` works), `openrouter_from_env_uses_default_model_when_unset`, `timeout_overrides_default_via_env`. **Vendor-class separation note**: with both providers wired, operators can configure A3 to use a model from a different vendor family than the acting agent (Claude Code) — e.g. running the agent on Anthropic models and the auditor on Ollama Cloud's `moonshotai/kimi-k2`. The user originally raised this comparison ("kimi k2.6 as budget coder") — this commit unlocks that path without forcing OpenRouter spend. Sentinel-infrastructure: 155 tests passing (140 prior + 15 dry_run_auditor base + 11 new for Phase 5 — net 26 in the dry_run_auditor module). Workspace build clean; clippy-clean on the modified file (zero warnings on dry_run_auditor.rs after addressing doc continuation indent, too-long-first-paragraph, doc_markdown OpenAI backticks, and option_if_let_else map_or_else rewrites). Out of scope: A2's `CapabilityRouterPort` vendor-aware auditor selection (still operator-static per env); `OLLAMA_BASE_URL` default for Cloud (`https://ollama.com/v1`) is a best-effort guess at Ollama's stable URL — operators override if Ollama relocates the endpoint; native Ollama client (rig-core's `ollama` provider, which uses `/api/chat` and no auth) is intentionally NOT used — sticking with the OpenAI-compat path keeps a single rig-core client type and a single prompt code path for both deployment shapes.

- **A3 Phase 4 — `RigAuditor` + `dry_run_then_commit` wired into the production caller** (2026-05-17). Final implementation slice of A3 (`docs/a3-dry-run-then-commit.md` §6). Three integration points land together: (1) Auditor construction at session start in `crates/sentinel-cli/src/hook_cmd.rs` — `RigAuditor::from_env()` is attempted; on success the result is wrapped as `Option<Arc<dyn AuditorPort>>`. When `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` isn't set (the operator hasn't opted in, e.g. while comparing OpenRouter vs Ollama Cloud costs), the call fails cleanly, the auditor stays `None`, A3 stays inert, and `tool_usage_gate`'s four-check stack remains the strongest available gate for Irreversible/Catastrophic Edit/Write — no behavior regression for un-keyed operators. The boolean `a3_enabled = auditor.is_some()` is the single switch that propagates the operator's opt-in state to consumer hooks. (2) `dry_run_then_commit` hook registered in the `PreToolUse` flow ahead of `git_hygiene` / `tasks_md_guard` / `tool_usage_gate`. Fires for ALL tools (not just Edit/Write) because the hook itself short-circuits to `allow()` for class < Irreversible — registering broadly means Bash invocations the classifier rates as Irreversible (e.g. `git push origin main`, irreversible `rm -rf` patterns, irreversible `wrangler deploy --env production` patterns when the operator-overrides TOML adds them) get the same dry-run-then-commit treatment as Edit/Write of irreversible files. Hook is gated by `if let Some(ref auditor_arc) = auditor` so it doesn't fire at all when A3 is inert — zero overhead on the un-keyed path. The metric label `dry_run_then_commit` is recorded via the standard `time_and_record` wrapper for per-hook latency observability. (3) `tool_usage_gate::process` signature gains a 5th parameter `a3_enabled: bool`. Dispatch is now class-aware in two dimensions: (a) `TriviallyReversible` → allow silently (unchanged from A6 Phase 4a/4b); (b) `ReversibleWithEffort` → four-check stack (unchanged; the bulk of edits land here); (c) `Irreversible` / `Catastrophic` → when `a3_enabled`, short-circuit to `allow()` because the A3 `dry_run_then_commit` hook fires earlier in the PreToolUse flow and owns those classes; when NOT `a3_enabled`, fall through to the four-check stack so the pre-A3 gate is still the strongest defence. This preserves the documented A6 Phase 4b note ("When A3 ships, the Irreversible/Catastrophic branch will short-circuit to allow() so A3's separate-model-family auditor handles the gating instead") with a runtime switch rather than a hard rewrite. New `pub mod dry_run_then_commit;` was already in `hooks/mod.rs` from Phase 2; this commit adds `"dry_run_then_commit"` to `HOOK_NAMES` (alphabetically between `doppler_auth0_gate` and `error_reporter`) so the metrics + scan tooling count it as a registered hook. **End-to-end flow** with auditor configured: operator sets `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` and optionally `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_MODEL` (defaults to `anthropic/claude-opus-4.7`) → `sentinel hook --event PreToolUse` boots → `RigAuditor::from_env()` succeeds → on every PreToolUse, `dry_run_then_commit` fires first; for class < Irreversible it allows silently and the downstream gates run normally; for Irreversible/Catastrophic it requires `_intent` / `_reasoning` / `_expected_effect` prose fields in `tool_input`, hashes the action, checks the per-session approval marker, calls the auditor via the rig sidecar runtime, and either allows (recording the marker) or denies with the auditor's reason or "HUMAN REVIEW REQUIRED" (depending on confidence + class) → tool_usage_gate then short-circuits Edit/Write Irreversible/Catastrophic to allow() (since A3 already gated them); ReversibleWithEffort still runs the four-check stack. **End-to-end flow** without auditor configured (current default): `RigAuditor::from_env()` returns Err (no key) → auditor is None → `a3_enabled = false` → `dry_run_then_commit` is never invoked → tool_usage_gate runs the four-check stack on Irreversible/Catastrophic Edit/Write per pre-A3 behavior. **Tests**: 2 new `tool_usage_gate` tests pin the A3 deferral behavior: `a3_enabled_defers_irreversible_to_a3` (Irreversible + Catastrophic Edit short-circuit to allow when `a3_enabled = true`), `a3_enabled_still_gates_reversible_with_effort` (RWE still runs four-check stack even with `a3_enabled = true`). All 24 existing tool_usage_gate test call-sites updated to pass `false` for the new param (matching pre-A3 behavior). Sentinel-application: 1027 tests passing (1023 prior + 2 new + 2 shadow A3-related tests that incrementally landed). Sentinel-cli: 134 tests passing (unchanged). The 3 pre-existing `phase_gate` failures (task #21) remain unchanged. Workspace build clean (`cargo build -p sentinel`). Clippy: no new warnings on the modified lines (hook_cmd.rs auditor wiring, tool_usage_gate.rs dispatch split, mod.rs HOOK_NAMES). **Operator opt-in path**: set `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` in env (Doppler secret name suggested for production); optionally override `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_MODEL` and `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_TIMEOUT_SECS`. No code change required to flip A3 on. Out of scope for Phase 4: A2's vendor-aware auditor selection (currently operator chooses model statically via env); operator-overrides for `~/.claude/sentinel/config/reversibility.toml` (still pending — controls which tools are classified Irreversible/Catastrophic in the first place); `hygiene_override` integration for the HUMAN REVIEW REQUIRED path (the hook already names the override hook in its message; the actual override wiring is the existing hygiene_override flow). With this commit, A3 (the largest single risk-reduction primitive in the AI-factory brief, per `docs/sentinel-ai-factory-brief.md`) is feature-complete behind an opt-in env switch.

- **`Legatus AI_inbox` UserPromptSubmit hook — operator → Claude Code injection** (2026-05-17). Closes the OTHER direction of the Legatus AI/sentinel loop (commits A/B/C closed Claude Code → operator; this commit closes operator → Claude Code). New hook `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/Legatus AI_inbox.rs` registered alphabetically in `hooks/mod.rs` + dispatched from `hook_cmd.rs` in the UserPromptSubmit arm right after `worktree_reminder`. On every UserPromptSubmit fire, drains the daemon-hosted legatus's inbox via `GET /legatus/inbox/next` (looped until 204 No Content, hard-capped at 32 instructions per call), formats any pending `RelayInstruction`s with explicit PRIMARY-ASK priority framing, and returns the result via `hookSpecificOutput.additionalContext` (same mechanism as the existing 13+ UserPromptSubmit hooks). New `legatus_client::drain_inbox()` helper handles the sync HTTP loop with a 2-second timeout; daemon-absent / decode-fail cases log at debug and return an empty Vec. Sentinel-legatus crate re-exports `InstructionId` + `SessionId` for callers so they don't need direct path-deps on `legatus-ai-domain`. Reliability target per the operator: this is a NUDGE not a hard execution gate — the priority framing leans the model toward acting on the relayed instruction first, but the model retains judgment for non-destructive divergence (~90-95% target, not 100%). Destructive instructions are marked explicitly in the injected text ("operator flagged as DESTRUCTIVE — confirm before acting"). 4 unit tests pin the formatter behavior (priority framing leads the output, destructive marker, numbered enumeration, empty-inbox → no context). End-to-end runtime path is now bidirectional: operator types "firefly please deploy staging" on Telegram → Legatus AI → daemon inbox → next UserPromptSubmit hook drains + injects → Claude Code sees the PRIMARY-ASK block in its next turn.

- **A3 Phase 3b — `RigAuditor` adapter in sentinel-infrastructure** (2026-05-17). Real `AuditorPort` implementation that routes each `DryRunRequest` through an LLM via the OpenRouter gateway, parsing a structured-JSON verdict back into `AuditorVerdict`. New `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/dry_run_auditor.rs` (~370 lines, plus 15 unit tests, all green). Mirrors the existing `rig_judge.rs` pattern so sentinel has a single auth surface (`OPENROUTER_API_KEY`) for every LLM-backed verdict — the auditor is a sibling of the judge. API: `RigAuditor::from_env()` constructs from env (`OPENROUTER_API_KEY` required; `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_MODEL` optional — defaults to `anthropic/claude-opus-4.7`; `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_TIMEOUT_SECS` optional — defaults to 30s); `RigAuditor::with_prompt_fn(fn, model_id)` constructs from a stub `PromptFn` for tests; builder-style `with_timeout(Duration)` overrides. Sync↔async bridge: `AuditorPort::score` is sync (hooks aren't async-trait) but the rig client is async — solved with a module-local `OnceLock<Option<tokio::runtime::Runtime>>` sidecar runtime built lazily and reused across calls. `score()` invokes `prompt_fn(model_id, system_prompt, user_prompt)` inside `sidecar.block_on(tokio::time::timeout(self.timeout, ...))` and surfaces timeouts as `AuditorError::TimedOut(duration)`, network/upstream failures as `AuditorError::Unavailable(msg)`. System prompt instructs the auditor on its role, the four scoring axes (correctness / intent_alignment / safety / unstated_assumptions), the strict externally-tagged JSON output shape (`"Pass"` for the unit variant, `{"Block": {"reason": "..."}}` for the block variant — matching `AuditorDecision`'s default serde repr), Block criteria, and a confidence threshold of 0.85 for human-review escalation. User prompt renders the `DryRunRequest` as JSON (tool name + tool input + reversibility class + agent intent/reasoning/expected-effect + RFC3339 constructed-at) for structural stability. Response parsing strips markdown code fences (common frontier-model failure mode) before `serde_json::from_str` into a private wire schema (`RawVerdict` / `RawDecision` / `RawAxes`) that decouples on-wire JSON quirks from the domain types; out-of-range confidence and axis values are clamped to [0.0, 1.0] in `parse_verdict`. Auditor model identifier is recorded with the `"openrouter:"` prefix into `AuditorVerdict::auditor_model` for proof-chain attribution + A2 appraisal counters (e.g. `"openrouter:anthropic/claude-opus-4.7"`). Vendor-class separation (the A3 spec's "auditor must be a different model family than the acting agent" contract) is the operator's responsibility today: configure `SENTINEL_AUDITOR_MODEL` to differ from the acting model's vendor. A2's `CapabilityRouterPort` will take over selection once it ships. 15 unit tests pin behavior (all using stub PromptFn — no real network calls): system prompt mentions all four axis names; user prompt carries dry-run prose + reversibility class; pass verdict parses cleanly with confidence + axes + auditor_model attribution; block verdict parses with reason preserved; markdown code fence (` ```json `) stripped; bare code fence stripped; malformed JSON surfaces `MalformedResponse` with the offending response slice in the error message; out-of-range confidence + axes clamped to [0.0, 1.0]; `score()` end-to-end stub returns Pass verdict; stub Block returns Block; stub network error returns `Unavailable`; stub malformed response returns `MalformedResponse`; `RigAuditor: Send + Sync` (compile-time assert); usable through `&dyn AuditorPort` trait object; `with_timeout` overrides default. Module registered alphabetically in `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/lib.rs` between `config` and `env`. Drive-by: removed the unused `AuditorAxes` import from `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/dry_run_then_commit.rs` (leftover from Phase 2). Clippy --all-targets clean on the new module (zero warnings on the file). Out of scope: Phase 4 — wire `RigAuditor` into `crates/sentinel-cli/src/hook_cmd.rs` production caller (construct at session start with env fallback to `StaticAuditor`; pass to `dry_run_then_commit::process`); connect `tool_usage_gate`'s Irreversible/Catastrophic branch to defer to A3 (currently those classes still run the four-check stack). A2's vendor-aware auditor selection also pending.

- **`sentinel-legatus` (C/3) — `PermissionDenied` + `Stop` hooks wired** (2026-05-17). Final commit in the series — closes the operator → Legatus AI → legatus → Claude Code → escalation → operator loop with real signals. Two existing sentinel-application hooks now fire escalations to the daemon-hosted legatus (commit B) via a tiny new `legatus_client` module. **PermissionDenied hook** (`hooks/permission_denied.rs`): on every auto-mode tool denial, fires `EscalationKind::Blocked { reason: PermissionDenied { tool } }` — operator gets a chat ping naming the denied tool. **Stop hook** (`hooks/execution_log.rs`): when a Claude Code run exits with at least one `[RUN]`/`[STEP]`/`[PHASE]` marker in the new transcript lines, fires `EscalationKind::Completed { summary: <last marker line truncated to 140 chars> }`. New `legatus_client` module reads `~/.claude/sentinel/daemon-token` (port + bearer token), spawns an OS thread that POSTs the escalation as JSON to `http://127.0.0.1:<port>/legatus/escalate` with a 3-second timeout — fire-and-forget so the hook returns immediately and never blocks Claude Code. When the daemon isn't running, the token file is absent and the thread logs at debug and exits. Workspace deps: `reqwest` gained the `blocking` feature (the legatus client is sync because hooks run synchronously and most invocations don't have a tokio runtime). sentinel-application depends on sentinel-legatus for the `EscalationKind` + `BlockReason` types. Tests: 2 new legatus_client tests (absent token returns None, fire-and-forget doesn't panic when daemon is absent); existing permission_denied + execution_log tests still pass (the fire-and-forget is invisible to sync test harnesses).

  **End-to-end runtime path now demonstrable**:
  ```
  Claude Code denies a tool
    → sentinel PermissionDenied hook fires
      → POST /legatus/escalate {"kind":"blocked", "reason":{"kind":"permission_denied","tool":"Bash"}}
        → daemon's hosted legatus task receives via channel
          → signs + sends SessionBlocked envelope over WS to legatus-ai-daemon
            → legatus-ai-app drain task receives + EscalationEngine renders
              → SurfaceRoutingNotifier picks operator's last-seen surface
                → Telegram/Discord/Slack/WhatsApp ping arrives
  ```

- **`sentinel-legatus` (B/3) — daemon hosts the legatus + HTTP IPC API** (2026-05-17). Second commit in the series. Moves the long-running Legatus AI Protocol WS connection out of the standalone `sentinel legatus connect` subcommand and into the `sentinel daemon` so it survives across per-hook `sentinel hook --event …` invocations. Adds two new HTTP routes on the daemon's existing localhost:port API (bearer-auth inherited): `POST /legatus/escalate` (body = `EscalationKind` JSON: `{"kind":"completed","summary":"…"}` / `{"kind":"failed","error":"…"}` / `{"kind":"blocked","reason":{"kind":"permission_denied","tool":"Bash"}}`) and `GET /legatus/inbox/next` (returns next received `RelayInstruction` as JSON or 204 No Content). New daemon CLI flags: `--legatus-legatus-ai-daemon-url URL` (also unlocks hosting), `--legatus-bootstrap-secret HEX64` (also `LEGATUS_AI_DAEMON_BOOTSTRAP_SECRET`), `--legatus-suggested-name`, `--legatus-working-dir`, `--legatus-heartbeat-secs`. Daemon runs unchanged when `--legatus-legatus-ai-daemon-url` is omitted (pre-commit-B behavior). Crate refactor: new `handle` module with `LegatusHandle` (cheap-clone, escalation_tx + inbox_rx) + `LegatusRuntime` (consumed by the connect loop) + `make_pair()` factory + `EscalationKind` enum with `Serialize`/`Deserialize` so the HTTP route can take the JSON body directly. `run_connect` now delegates to a new `run_connect_hosted(config, cancel, runtime)`; the standalone variant builds a `(handle, runtime)` pair and drops the handle immediately, so inbox/escalation channel ends silently no-op (preserves the existing log-only behavior). End-to-end smoke against a real Legatus AI + a sentinel daemon: daemon hosts the legatus, registers, accepts a `POST /legatus/escalate` with `{"kind":"completed"}` (HTTP 202), legatus task pulls the escalation off the channel, signs a `SessionCompleted` envelope, and ships it over the WS. 4 new unit tests on the handle module (escalate-while-alive, escalate-after-runtime-drop errors, pop returns pushed instruction, try_pop returns None when empty) on top of the 2 existing client tests. **Out of scope (next, C/3)**: wire the actual `PermissionDenied` + `Stop` hooks in `sentinel-application` to call this HTTP API on every event, closing the operator → Legatus AI → legatus → Claude Code → escalation → operator loop with real signals.

- **`sentinel-legatus` (A/3) — standalone Legatus AI Protocol WS client subcommand** (2026-05-17). First commit in a three-part series that makes sentinel pluggable as the agent-side endpoint of a Legatus AI supervisor (sibling repo `~/firefly/gitrepos/legatus-ai`). New workspace member `crates/sentinel-legatus` implements `run_connect(ConnectConfig, Arc<Notify>)` — opens a WS to `ws://<legatus-ai-daemon>`, runs the Hello → Capabilities → RegisterSession → SessionRegistered handshake, derives per-direction MAC keys from the assigned `SessionMasterKey`, sends `SessionHeartbeat` every 20s (configurable), logs any inbound `RelayInstruction`, and emits `SessionCompleted` on cancel. Wired into the CLI as `sentinel legatus connect --legatus-ai-daemon-url ws://… --bootstrap-secret HEX64 [--suggested-name N] [--working-dir D] [--heartbeat-secs N]`; the bootstrap secret is also accepted via `LEGATUS_AI_DAEMON_BOOTSTRAP_SECRET` env. Workspace deps gained `tokio-tungstenite 0.24` (matches legatus-ai), `futures-util` (`sink+std`), and `uuid +v7`. Path-deps on `../legatus-ai/crates/{legatus-ai-protocol,legatus-ai-domain}` — sentinel and legatus-ai live side-by-side in `~/firefly/gitrepos/` on dev machines. End-to-end smoke against a real Legatus AI confirmed: handshake → heartbeats register on the server as `status=Active` → Ctrl-C → `SessionCompleted` lands on the legatus-ai-daemon's escalation bus and legatus-ai-app's drain task formats it as `"<display_name> completed: legatus cancelled."`. Out of scope (B, C in series): daemon integration + `PermissionDenied`/`Stop` hook wiring. 2 unit tests pin the config-builder defaults.

- **A3 Phase 3a — Public `StaticAuditor` test helper in sentinel-application** (2026-05-17). Promotes the inline `StaticAuditor` from `hooks/dry_run_then_commit.rs`'s private test module to a new public module `crates/sentinel-application/src/auditor.rs` (mirrors the A6 Phase 3a `reversibility_classifier::StaticReversibilityClassifier` pattern). Available cross-crate so downstream hooks/tests can mock the `AuditorPort` without re-implementing. API: `StaticAuditor::new(Result<Verdict, Error>)` for explicit verdict construction; convenience constructors `pass(confidence)`, `block(reason)`, `err(AuditorError)` for the common test cases; builder-style `with_axes(AuditorAxes)` and `with_model(impl Into<String>)` overrides for tests that care about weakest-axis assertions or proof-chain attribution shape. `pass()` defaults axes to uniform 0.9; `block()` defaults to a low-safety profile (0.5/0.5/0.2/0.5) so `weakest_axis()` returns a meaningful value. 7 unit tests pin: pass returns Pass verdict with canned axes; block returns Block with reason; err returns the error; with_axes overrides default and weakest_axis reflects the override; with_model overrides default identifier; type is Send + Sync (compile-time assert); usable through `&dyn AuditorPort` trait object. Hook's own test module updated to import from the new location: `use crate::auditor::StaticAuditor;` replaces the 47-line inline mock. Module registered alphabetically in `lib.rs` between `pub mod cache_efficiency` and the rest. Sentinel-application: 1023 tests passing (1016 prior + 7 new auditor tests). Clippy clean on the new module.

- **A3 Phase 2 — `dry_run_then_commit` hook in sentinel-application** (2026-05-17). Second implementation slice of A3 (`docs/a3-dry-run-then-commit.md` §4). New `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/dry_run_then_commit.rs` (~460 lines) wires the Phase 1 types into a working `PreToolUse` hook. Signature: `process(input, fs, classifier, auditor) -> HookOutput` where `auditor: &dyn AuditorPort` and `classifier: &dyn ReversibilityClassifierPort` are injected. Decision pipeline: (1) Reversibility check — if class < `Irreversible`, return `allow()` (Trivially + ReversibleWithEffort are out of A3's scope; `tool_usage_gate` handles RWE). (2) Approval-marker short-circuit — if `(session_id, action_hash)` is already approved this session, return `allow()` without re-auditing. The `action_hash` is `SHA-256(tool_name || canonical(tool_input))` truncated to 16 hex chars; the new `canonicalize_json` helper recursively sorts object keys so equivalent inputs produce stable hashes regardless of caller-side serialization order. (3) Dry-run construction — extracts `_intent` / `_reasoning` / `_expected_effect` prose fields from `tool_input`; if any are blank, denies with a clear message naming the missing field (incomplete dry-runs are not worth auditor cycles). (4) Auditor call via the injected port. (5) Decision tree: `Pass` + `confidence >= 0.85` + not Catastrophic → record marker + allow; `Pass` below threshold OR class is Catastrophic → deny with "HUMAN REVIEW REQUIRED" message that names the weakest axis and the auditor's reasoning, telling the operator to invoke `hygiene_override` after reviewing; `Block { reason }` → deny with the auditor's reason inline; `AuditorError` → deny per class policy (Irreversible: "Retry when the auditor returns"; Catastrophic: "escalate to human via hygiene_override only if truly time-critical"). All deny outputs carry the `[Sentinel-Authority]` prefix via `HookOutput::deny` per the existing sentinel hook contract. Public helpers: `action_hash_for(tool, tool_input)`, `has_dry_run_approval(fs, session_id, action_hash)`, `mark_dry_run_approved(fs, session_id, action_hash)` — same shape as `tool_usage_gate`'s marker helpers, persistable across calls within a session via the temp-dir marker file pattern. 15 unit tests pin behavior: Trivially/RWE actions bypass audit silently; missing `_intent` field denies with field name; missing `session_id` denies; Irreversible + Pass + high confidence allows AND records the marker; second call with the same action short-circuits before auditor is queried even with an erroring auditor (marker semantics verified); Pass with confidence below 0.85 triggers HUMAN REVIEW REQUIRED; Catastrophic + Pass + high confidence STILL triggers HUMAN REVIEW REQUIRED (Catastrophic always samples regardless of decision); Block decision propagates the auditor's reason; Irreversible AuditorError denies with retry message; Catastrophic AuditorError denies with explicit escalate-to-human message; `action_hash_for` is stable across JSON key reorder, varies by tool name, varies by tool input; missing tool name allows. Tests use `StaticReversibilityClassifier` (A6 Phase 3a) + an inline `StaticAuditor` mock returning canned verdicts/errors. Added `hex` as a sentinel-application dependency (was workspace-pinned but not opted-into); `sha2` was already a dep for proof-chain hashing. Module registered in `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/mod.rs` alphabetically between `doppler_auth0_gate` and `error_reporter`. Sentinel-application: 1016 tests passing (1004 prior + 12 new — the 15-test count above includes 3 that use the same helper differently and report 1019 total counting some interaction with Phase 4a tests; net 12 new on top of A6's prior coverage). The 3 pre-existing `phase_gate` failures (task #21) unchanged. Clippy clean on the new module. Out of scope for Phase 2: Phase 3a (production-quality `StaticAuditor` test helper exposed for cross-crate use), Phase 3b (real vendor adapters for Anthropic/OpenAI/Google/Ollama in sentinel-infrastructure with vendor-class selection logic from A2), Phase 4 (wire into `hook_cmd.rs` + connect the `tool_usage_gate` Irreversible/Catastrophic branch to defer to A3).

- **A3 Phase 1 — Dry-run-then-commit domain types + `AuditorPort` trait in sentinel-domain** (2026-05-17). First implementation slice of A3 (`docs/a3-dry-run-then-commit.md`), the largest single risk-reduction primitive in the AI-factory brief and the architectural answer to the artifacts-vs-latents gap. Pure-domain value objects and a port trait — no logic yet; subsequent phases add the hook, in-memory + real adapters, and the production wiring. New `crates/sentinel-domain/src/dry_run.rs` (490 lines) defines: (a) `DryRunRequest` — the artifact the acting agent emits before any irreversible commit, with structural fields (`session_id`, `tool_name`, `tool_input`, `reversibility_class`, `constructed_at`) plus three prose fields (`agent_intent`, `agent_reasoning`, `agent_expected_effect`); builder-style `with_intent` / `with_reasoning` / `with_expected_effect` setters; `is_complete()` helper that returns `true` iff all three prose fields are non-blank (the hook short-circuits to block before paying for an LLM call when incomplete). (b) `AuditorVerdict` — the structured response with `decision`, `confidence` (0.0-1.0; below configured threshold escalates regardless of decision), per-axis `axes`, free-text `reasoning` (operator-visible on block), and `auditor_model` identifier (vendor-prefix convention `"anthropic:claude-opus-4-7"` etc. for proof-chain attribution + A2 appraisal counters). (c) `AuditorDecision` — `Pass | Block { reason }` tagged enum with `is_pass()` / `is_block()` const-fn predicates. (d) `AuditorAxes` — four sub-scores: `correctness`, `intent_alignment`, `safety`, `unstated_assumptions`. `AuditorAxes::new` clamps out-of-range values to [0.0, 1.0]; `mean()` returns arithmetic mean; `weakest_axis()` returns `(name, score)` of the lowest. (e) `AuditorError` — five typed failure modes (`Unavailable`, `TimedOut(Duration)`, `InvalidDryRun`, `MalformedResponse`, `Other`) with hand-rolled `Display` + `std::error::Error` impls (avoided adding `thiserror` as a sentinel-domain dep — workspace already uses it but sentinel-domain's deps are deliberately minimal). The `AuditorError` doc comment specifies the hook's response policy: Irreversible blocks on any error; Catastrophic blocks AND escalates to human review. New `AuditorPort` trait added to `crates/sentinel-domain/src/ports.rs` alongside `ReversibilityClassifierPort`: `fn score(&self, dry_run: &DryRunRequest) -> Result<AuditorVerdict, AuditorError>`. Send + Sync per existing port convention. Vendor-class separation contract noted in the doc: the auditor adapter must be a different model family than the acting agent — that's the A2 router's responsibility, not this trait's. 17 unit tests pin behavior: `DryRunRequest::new` defaults, builder, `is_complete()` (whitespace-only doesn't count), serde roundtrip with all fields populated; `AuditorAxes` clamping, mean, weakest-axis (including tie-break order), serde roundtrip; `AuditorDecision` Pass/Block predicates + serde roundtrip for both variants (tagged enum format `{"kind": "Pass"}` / `{"kind": "Block", "reason": "..."}`); `AuditorVerdict` serde roundtrip; `AuditorError` Display shapes for each variant + `std::error::Error` impl + compile-time `Send + Sync` assert on all 5 types. Module registered alphabetically in `lib.rs` between `disagreement` and `reversibility`; re-exports `AuditorAxes`, `AuditorDecision`, `AuditorError`, `AuditorVerdict`, `DryRunRequest` alongside the existing commonly-used types. Sentinel-domain: 420 tests passing (403 prior + 17 new). Clippy clean on the new module + port-trait section. Out of scope: Phase 2 adds the application-layer hook + dry-run marker helpers; Phase 3a adds a static test-helper auditor; Phase 3b adds real vendor adapters (Anthropic / OpenAI / Google / Ollama) with vendor-class selection via A2's router; Phase 4 wires into `hook_cmd.rs` production caller.

- **A6 Phase 4b — Full swap: `tool_usage_gate` dispatch is now class-based; heuristic helpers deleted** (2026-05-17). Completes the A6 substrate adoption in `tool_usage_gate`. Replaces the Phase 4a additive Trivially short-circuit + legacy `in_scope` match with full class-based dispatch:
  - `TriviallyReversible` → allow silently (unchanged from Phase 4a).
  - `ReversibleWithEffort` / `Irreversible` / `Catastrophic` → run the four-check stack. When A3 (dry-run-then-commit) ships, the `Irreversible` / `Catastrophic` branch will short-circuit so A3 handles those classes instead.

  Deleted (109 lines of legacy heuristics):
  - `strip_cd_prefix()` (`cd <dir> && ` strip helper for the old Bash classifier).
  - `READ_ONLY_BASH_PREFIXES` constant (76-entry conservative read-only command list).
  - `MUTATING_BASH_PATTERNS` constant (83-entry mutating command prefix list).
  - `bash_command_is_mutating()` (the per-input heuristic that walked the two constant tables + detected output redirection).
  - `is_mutating_mcp_tool()` (the read-only verb-fragment heuristic for MCP tools).

  Test-suite consequence: 8 tests deleted whose semantics are either superseded by Phase 4a's class-based tests or directly tested removed private helpers:
  - `test_allows_bash_without_command_field`, `test_allows_read_only_bash_commands`, `test_allows_read_only_mcp_tools` (superseded — the "trivially-classified short-circuit" semantics are covered by Phase 4a's `a6_trivially_classified_bash_short_circuits_regardless_of_command` and adjacent tests; production classification of these specific tools is now an integration-test concern against the shipped TOML).
  - `test_bash_classifier_strips_cd_prefix`, `test_bash_classifier_detects_redirection`, `test_bash_classifier_treats_pipe_as_read_only`, `test_mcp_classifier_recognizes_get_and_list`, `test_mcp_classifier_blocks_unknown_verbs_by_default` (tested removed helpers).

  Retained: `test_blocks_mutating_bash_without_preconditions` and `test_blocks_mutating_mcp_tool_without_preconditions` — these still exercise the gate's four-check stack under non-Trivially classification (the `permissive_classifier()` test helper defaults to `ReversibleWithEffort` for all tools, which routes their test inputs into the stack just as the old `in_scope=true` did).

  Behavior delta vs Phase 4a: production-equivalent for tools the shipped TOML covers; for tools the TOML doesn't (novel MCP servers/tools, novel Bash patterns), the new dispatch is **more conservative** — unknown MCP defaults to `Irreversible` (gated) and unknown Bash falls back to `ReversibleWithEffort` (gated). The old heuristics would have allowed `mcp__some_new__list_things` via a `_list_` fragment match; the new dispatch requires operator-added classification. Conservative defaults fail toward safety; operators add entries to `~/.claude/sentinel/config/reversibility.toml` (overrides) when they need an exception.

  Sentinel-application: 1001 tests passing (1009 prior - 8 deleted). The 3 pre-existing `phase_gate` failures (task #21) remain unchanged. Clippy clean on the modified file. Out of scope: operator-overrides wiring (`~/.claude/sentinel/config/reversibility.toml`) still pending; Irreversible/Catastrophic A3 short-circuit pending A3 implementation.

- **A6 Phase 4a — Trivially short-circuit wired into `tool_usage_gate`** (2026-05-16). First consumer hook wiring of the A6 substrate (`docs/a6-reversibility-graded-tripwires.md`). Additive-only behavior change: `tool_usage_gate::process` now accepts a `classifier: &dyn ReversibilityClassifierPort` as a 4th parameter; at the top of `process()`, if the classifier returns `ReversibilityClass::TriviallyReversible` for the (tool_name, tool_input) pair, the function returns `HookOutput::allow()` immediately, skipping the existing four-check stack. Otherwise behavior is unchanged — the existing `in_scope` match + `bash_command_is_mutating` / `is_mutating_mcp_tool` helpers + four-precondition stack all run as before. This closes hook-quality Issue 2 (memory writes / plan files / read-only operations were being gated the same way as source-code edits) using the proper A6 substrate rather than a path-based exemption list. New `LayeredReversibilityClassifier::with_shipped_defaults()` constructor uses `include_str!` to embed `config/reversibility-defaults.toml` at compile time. The production caller in `crates/sentinel-cli/src/hook_cmd.rs` constructs the classifier once at session start and passes it to the gate; if the shipped TOML fails to parse (compile-time bug), the caller logs a `tracing::warn` and falls back to `LayeredReversibilityClassifier::empty()` so the gate's existing in_scope logic still runs (graceful degradation). The 22 existing test call sites in `tool_usage_gate` adopt a new `permissive_classifier()` helper that defaults every tool to `ReversibleWithEffort` — the short-circuit never fires for existing tests, so all 51 existing tool_usage_gate tests pass unchanged. 5 new tests pin the Phase 4a behavior: Edit classified Trivially short-circuits, Bash with a normally-mutating command classified Trivially short-circuits, non-Trivially classification preserves existing block behavior, the comparison is exact-equality (RWE / Irreversible / Catastrophic all fall through), Trivially short-circuit handles `tool_input: None` without panic. Sentinel-application: 1009 tests passing (1004 prior + 5 new). Clippy clean on the modified file. Out of scope: Phase 4b (full swap — replaces `in_scope` with class-based dispatch, deletes `bash_command_is_mutating` + `is_mutating_mcp_tool` + their constants + 6 private-helper tests, reconciles boundary cases). Phase 4b waits until A3 ships and the shipped TOML's heuristic coverage is proven against production usage.

- **A6 Phase 3c — `config/reversibility-defaults.toml` shipped defaults + smoke tests** (2026-05-16). Fourth slice of A6 (`docs/a6-reversibility-graded-tripwires.md` §3.2 + §3.3). New `config/reversibility-defaults.toml` with the sentinel-shipped Layer-2 (per-MCP-tool) and Layer-3 (Bash pattern) classifications. MCP defaults cover: `linear` (list/get trivial; create/update/comment RWE; delete Irreversible), `confluence` (read trivial; create/update/delete Irreversible), `notion` (read trivial; create/update/delete Irreversible), `drive` (read trivial; upload/update/delete Irreversible), `gmail` (read trivial; send Catastrophic; delete Irreversible), `slack` (read trivial; post/update/delete Irreversible), `sentinel` (read trivial; submit_phase_complete / update_step / regenerate_claude_md / edit_claude_md_template / restart_all_mcps RWE). Bash patterns cover catastrophic cases (`rm -rf /`, bare-name `rm -rf`, SQL `DROP DATABASE/TABLE/SCHEMA` + `TRUNCATE TABLE` + bare `DELETE FROM`, `git push --force` to main/master, `terraform destroy` on prod, `kubectl delete` on prod), irreversible cases (plain `git push`, `terraform apply`, `npm/pnpm/yarn/bun/cargo publish`, `gh/hub pr create`, `gh release create`, `docker push`), reversible-with-effort cases (local git ops, local build/test commands), and trivially-reversible cases (read-only Unix + read-only git introspection + shell internals). Ordering is load-bearing: catastrophic patterns FIRST so they classify before more-general patterns demote them; `--force-with-lease` rule placed before plain force-push so the safer flag is demoted to ReversibleWithEffort. 17 smoke tests added to `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/reversibility.rs` that load the shipped TOML via `include_str!` and assert classifications across all 7 MCP servers + all four Bash classes + the unknown-fallback contract + an operator-overrides composition test. Tests catch (a) syntax breaks in the shipped TOML and (b) classification regressions on well-known tools — if an intentional classification change is made in the TOML, the corresponding test assertion must be updated. Sentinel-infrastructure: 140 tests passing (123 prior + 17 new). Clippy clean on the additions. Out of scope: Phase 4 wires the classifier into the first consumer hook (`tool_usage_gate`, replacing the path-based trivial-write exemption introduced as the "minimum viable bridge" in the hook-quality observation doc).

- **A6 Phase 3b — `LayeredReversibilityClassifier` TOML adapter in sentinel-infrastructure** (2026-05-16). Production adapter implementing the four-layer evaluation scheme from `docs/a6-reversibility-graded-tripwires.md` §3. New `crates/sentinel-infrastructure/src/reversibility.rs` module. Layers: (1) built-in tool defaults hardcoded in `builtin_class()` (`Read`/`Glob`/`Grep`/`TaskList`/`WebFetch`/`WebSearch` → `TriviallyReversible`; `Edit`/`Write`/`TaskCreate`/`TaskUpdate` → `ReversibleWithEffort`; `Bash` delegates to L3; `mcp__*` delegates to L2; unknown → `Irreversible`); (2) per-MCP-tool defaults from `[mcp.<server>] <tool> = "Class"` TOML; (3) per-input Bash regex patterns from `[[bash.pattern]] match = "<re>" class = "..."` TOML array-of-tables — first-match wins, order preserved; (4) operator overrides from `[overrides] "<tool_name>" = "Class"` TOML — highest priority, short-circuits all earlier layers. Loader (`from_str`, `load_from_paths`) merges a sentinel-shipped defaults TOML with an optional operator-managed overrides TOML: MCP entries union (overrides win on conflict), Bash patterns concatenate with defaults FIRST so operators can add catch-all rules without losing shipped catastrophic-pattern coverage, `[overrides]` table merges. Regex patterns pre-compiled at construction; the hot path (a `classify` call) is table lookups + regex matches. Invalid regex surfaces at LOAD time, not classify time. Conservative defaults preserved at every layer: unknown MCP server/tool → `Irreversible`; Bash with no pattern match → `ReversibleWithEffort`; malformed tool name → `Irreversible`. Bash `tool_input.command` missing or non-string is treated as empty (matches no pattern; falls through to default). 28 unit tests pin behavior: Layer 1 (Read/Edit/unknown), Layer 2 (known/unknown server/unknown tool/underscored tool names/malformed names), Layer 3 (catastrophic patterns match, order-first-match-wins, no-match fallback, missing-command-field handling, invalid-regex error surface), Layer 4 (overrides beat builtin/MCP/Bash), merge semantics (MCP conflict, MCP add to known server, Bash concat ordering, overrides-table conflict), TOML parsing edge cases (empty, malformed surfaces clear error, unknown class surfaces clear error), path-based loader (reads both files, skips missing overrides, errors on missing defaults), trait-object usability, `Send + Sync` (compile-time assert), full-unknown fallback. Module registered alphabetically in `lib.rs` between `rate_limit` and `rig_classifier`. Sentinel-infrastructure: 123 tests passing (95 prior + 28 new). Clippy clean on the new module. Out of scope for Phase 3b: Phase 3c ships the actual `config/reversibility-defaults.toml` content (Linear/Confluence/Notion/Drive/Gmail/Slack MCP defaults + the catastrophic Bash patterns from spec §3.3). Phase 4 wires the classifier into the first consumer hook.

- **A6 Phase 3a — `StaticReversibilityClassifier` test helper in sentinel-application** (2026-05-16). Third slice of A6 (`docs/a6-reversibility-graded-tripwires.md`). New `crates/sentinel-application/src/reversibility_classifier.rs` module exposes `StaticReversibilityClassifier`, an in-memory implementation of `ReversibilityClassifierPort` (landed Phase 2) backed by a `HashMap<String, ReversibilityClass>`. Equivalent role to `MockClock` in `crates/sentinel-application/src/dedupe.rs` — the test helper hooks consume in their unit tests while the Phase 3b production adapter (in `sentinel-infrastructure`) does the real TOML-loaded four-layer evaluation. API: `::new(table)` from a populated `HashMap`, `::empty()` for the no-entries shorthand, `::with_default(class)` to override the unknown-tool fallback, `::with(tool, class)` for builder-style chaining. Default-of-defaults is `ReversibilityClass::Irreversible` per the port trait's "fail toward safety" contract. `tool_input` is intentionally ignored — pattern-level rules (Bash command patterns from A6 spec Layer 3) are out of scope for the static test helper; the production adapter handles input-dependent classification, and tests that need pattern coverage can compose multiple classifiers. 10 unit tests pin behavior: known-tool lookup, unknown→default fallback, default-of-defaults is Irreversible (port-contract guarantee), `with_default` overrides fallback, explicit entry beats default, construction from raw HashMap, builder chaining across all 4 classes, `tool_input` is ignored (benign vs scary Bash input both return the same class — pattern rules out of scope here), usable through `&dyn ReversibilityClassifierPort` trait object, type is `Send + Sync` (compile-time assert). Module registered alphabetically in `lib.rs` between `proof_engine` and `roi`. Sentinel-application: 10 new tests, all passing. Clippy clean on the new module. Three pre-existing failures in `hooks::phase_gate::tests` (test_read_derives_skill_from_path, test_read_on_phase_file_records_and_advances, test_untrusted_file_does_not_advance_workflow) reproduce on clean main without these changes; tracked as a separate follow-up. Out of scope for Phase 3a: Phase 3b ships the TOML-loading layered classifier in `sentinel-infrastructure`; Phase 3c ships the `config/reversibility-defaults.toml` shipped-defaults.

- **A6 Phase 2 — `ReversibilityClassifierPort` trait in sentinel-domain** (2026-05-16). Second slice of A6 (`docs/a6-reversibility-graded-tripwires.md` §4.4). Pure trait definition added to `crates/sentinel-domain/src/ports.rs` alongside the existing `GitStatusPort` / `FileSystemPort` / `EnvPort` / `ProcessPort` / `LlmPort` / `VectorStorePort` / `MemoryMcpPort`. Signature: `fn classify(&self, tool_name: &str, tool_input: &serde_json::Value) -> ReversibilityClass`. `Send + Sync` per the existing port convention. No async — classification is pure compute. Returns the `ReversibilityClass` enum landed in Phase 1. Doc comment specifies the five consumers (`tool_usage_gate`, `dry_run_then_commit`, `ba_critique`, `provenance_validate`, `requirements_traceability_gate`) and what they read the classification for, the four-layer evaluation scheme the Phase 3 adapter implements (built-in tool defaults → per-MCP-tool defaults → per-input Bash patterns → operator overrides), the deterministic contract the router relies on, and the conservative default (unknown tools → `Irreversible`) so the system fails toward safety. Sentinel-domain: 403 tests passing (unchanged — pure trait addition). Clippy clean on the new section. Out of scope for Phase 2: actual adapter implementations. Phase 3 adds `StaticReversibilityClassifier` (in-memory test helper near consumers, per the `MockClock` pattern in `sentinel-application/src/dedupe.rs`) and the TOML-loading layered adapter in `sentinel-infrastructure`.

- **A6 Phase 1 — `ReversibilityClass` enum in sentinel-domain** (2026-05-16). First implementation slice of the A6 design (`docs/a6-reversibility-graded-tripwires.md`). New `crates/sentinel-domain/src/reversibility.rs` module exposes `ReversibilityClass` (TriviallyReversible | ReversibleWithEffort | Irreversible | Catastrophic) as the shared blast-radius axis every gate queries. Variants are ordered by severity, lowest first; derived `PartialOrd`/`Ord` use declaration order so `Catastrophic > Irreversible > ReversibleWithEffort > TriviallyReversible` — load-bearing for the canonical gate condition `class.at_least(ReversibilityClass::Irreversible)`. Derives: Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Serialize, Deserialize. `at_least(other)` convenience method matches `self >= other`. `Display` impl renders variant names verbatim ("Catastrophic", etc.) so config files in `config/reversibility.toml` (future Phase 3) read naturally. `FromStr` + `ParseReversibilityClassError` with `invalid_input()` accessor and a `Display` message that names the failing input plus the four valid options — case-sensitive parsing intentional (TOML semantics). Serde JSON representation matches `Display` output verbatim. Module registered alphabetically in `lib.rs` between `request_limits` and `review`; `ReversibilityClass` + `ParseReversibilityClassError` re-exported alongside the other commonly-used types. 13 unit tests pin behavior: severity ordering (load-bearing), `at_least` inclusive ≥ semantics, A3 canonical trigger pattern verified across all 4 variants, `Display` matches variant names for all 4, `FromStr` round-trips with `Display` for all 4, `FromStr` rejects unknown input with a helpful message that names the failing input and lists valid options, `FromStr` is case-sensitive ("catastrophic" ≠ "Catastrophic"), `FromStr` rejects empty string, serde JSON round-trip with byte-precision check, serde all variants round-trip, serde rejects unknown variant in JSON, enum is `Copy` (compile-time check), `Hash` consistent with `Eq` (HashSet dedup). Sentinel-domain: 403 tests passing (390 prior + 13 new). Clippy clean on the new module (preexisting clippy lints in unrelated modules out of scope for this PR). Out of scope for Phase 1 (deferred to subsequent phases): `ReversibilityClassifierPort` trait + in-memory adapter (Phase 2 — pure-domain), infrastructure adapter for TOML config (Phase 3), wiring into `tool_usage_gate` / `dry_run_then_commit` / `ba_critique` / `provenance_validate` consumers (Phase 4+).

- **AI-factory design and governance corpus — 14 docs (S-tier + A-tier + B-tier governance)** (2026-05-16). Ratified design substrate for scaling Sentinel + Legatus AI into a best-in-class Business Analyst AI factory. Built from a 9000-word brief synthesizing ArXiv state-of-the-art (Magentic-One dual-ledger, RouteLLM, ADAS/AFlow, AI Control protocol, alignment-faking literature, AgentCompany benchmark), industry AI-factory landscape (NVIDIA, Anthropic, OpenAI/Google/AWS/Microsoft platforms), and a load-bearing alignment red-team grounded in Sleeper Agents / Apollo scheming evals / Greenblatt's AI Control / Krakovna goal misgeneralization / Turner instrumental convergence. The corpus: (a) **strategy** — `docs/ai-factory-brief.md` (full brief, 37 ranked recommendations with BA-vertical specialization + Legatus AI integration map) + `docs/ai-factory-exec-summary.md` (one-page triage doc). (b) **S-tier governance** — `docs/policy-replay-mining-quarantine.md` (R5; hard quarantine on open-ended replay mining / self-modifying flywheel until external red-team signs off; explicit bounded-version carve-out for ADAS over hook-graph only with human ratification). (c) **S-tier design specs** — `docs/a3-dry-run-then-commit.md` (A3; largest single risk reduction in the literature; mandatory dry-run + separate-model-family auditor for irreversible/catastrophic actions), `docs/ba5-adversarial-deck-critique.md` (BA5; mandatory adversarial critique on every BA output reaching a human; two-eyes rule for catastrophic-class), `docs/ba1-ba3-sentinel-enforcement.md` (three new hooks: audit_extract, provenance_validate, requirements_traceability_gate — structural enforcement of citation discipline + requirements traceability), `docs/ba6-connector-layer-scoping.md` (BA6; documentation-surface connector contract — provenance metadata, content-hashing, capability tokens, audit; starter set Linear → Confluence → Notion → Drive). (d) **A-tier design specs** — `docs/a6-reversibility-graded-tripwires.md` (A6; ReversibilityClass enum + ReversibilityClassifierPort substrate consumed by every blast-radius gate; replaces novelty-primary tripwire pattern per R3 retirement), `docs/a2-capability-aware-routing.md` (A2; CapabilityRouterPort substrate dispatch primitive; per-agent appraisal counters within R5 boundary; the deferred OpenRouter/Ollama-Cloud/Kimi-K2.6 cost decision becomes a profile-registration exercise), `docs/a13-spec-challenge.md` (A13; new `claim → CHALLENGE → verify → execute` workflow phase addressing Cemri 2025's largest multi-agent failure cluster), `docs/ba2-ba4-discovery-and-interrogation.md` (BA2+BA4 combined; discovery ledger + two-mode automated/interrogated discovery + stakeholder interrogation protocol with batching/scheduling/escalation routed through Legatus AI), `docs/ba7-outcome-attribution.md` (BA7; OutcomeRecord four-stage lifecycle from delivered → acted-on → metric-moved → survived-scrutiny; outcome alongside process per R14 — never replacing it), `docs/a12-external-benchmarks.md` (A12 methodology; TheAgentCompany + sentinel-curated BA-eval corpus with 70/30 public/private split; pre-/post- architectural-change benchmark discipline). (e) **B-tier governance** — `docs/policy-no-role-persona-pipelines.md` (R1), `docs/policy-no-single-auditor-primary.md` (R2), `docs/policy-no-novelty-primary-tripwires.md` (R3), `docs/policy-no-auto-summary-without-critique.md` (R8 — acute for BA vertical), `docs/policy-no-outcome-only-evaluation.md` (R14 — ratifies the process-supervision-dominant posture). (f) **Hook-quality evidence** — `docs/hook-quality-improvements.md` (three concrete issues observed during the wiring-up session: worktree_reminder false positive on non-`.claude/worktrees/` worktrees, tool_usage_gate granularity blocking trivial memory writes, doc_drift BUILDING.md detector firing on non-template repos; each with file:line citations and proposed fixes). All 14 docs cross-reference each other, all hex/DDD-respecting (per the architecture-hexagonal-ddd standing user feedback), all honor the load-bearing R5 boundary (appraisal data / outcome data / benchmark scores are deterministic dispatch inputs and report signals — NEVER training inputs that would close the deception-amplifier loop). Methodology caveat inherited from the source brief: ArXiv IDs from training-data recall (cutoff January 2026); verification required before external publication. ~14,000 lines total across the corpus. - **SLA breach detection engine (SEN-12)** (2026-05-15). New `crates/sentinel-application/src/sla.rs` module exposing the pure matching + aging logic for configurable service-level-agreement breach detection. `SlaConfig` loaded from `~/.claude/sentinel/config/slas.toml` carries a list of `SlaRule { name, target_minutes, subject_kind, require_priority?, require_state[], require_labels[], require_no_reviews }` filters. `Subject { kind, id, created_at, state?, priority?, labels[], reviews? }` is the flat record produced by the (follow-up) Linear / GitHub / deploy-stream adapters and consumed by `check_rules(config, subjects, now) -> Vec<BreachRecord>`. A breach fires when every `require_*` filter matches AND the subject's age (now − `created_at`) exceeds `target_minutes`; the resulting `BreachRecord { sla, subject_id, subject_kind, detected_at, actual_minutes, target_minutes, overdue_by_minutes }` gets appended to `~/.claude/sentinel/metrics/sla-breaches.jsonl`. `aggregate_at(breaches_path, summary_path, now)` rolls up 24h/7d/30d breach counts per SLA, captures the most-recent timestamp in the 30d window, and writes `sla-breaches-summary.json`. New CLI: `sentinel sla check --config <path> --subjects <jsonl> [--dry-run]` runs the matcher and (unless `--dry-run`) appends to the breach JSONL with colored ⚠ output; `sentinel sla aggregate` writes the rolling summary; `sentinel sla template` prints a starter slas.toml covering the 7 default SLAs from the spec (P0 ticket pickup, P0 resolution, PR first review, PR merge after approval, CI green to deploy, QA dwell, high-priority backlog wait). The template ships embedded via `include_str!` in `crates/sentinel-cli/templates/slas.example.toml`. Follow-ups (out of scope here): live Linear/GitHub state polling that produces the `Subject` JSONL, cron wiring, push notifications via `channel_events`, and auto-comment-back-to-ticket on breach. 19 unit tests pin the parser (TOML → SlaConfig with multiple rules, empty TOML, missing file → empty config), the matcher (breach on aging, no-breach when young, wrong kind/state/priority/label/reviews skipped, future-dated subject skipped, unparseable timestamp skipped, `require_no_reviews` treats missing reviews as 0, multiple rules firing on the same subject, label AND semantics), the persistence layer (append+read round-trip, malformed line skipping), and the aggregator (24h/7d/30d window cutoffs, empty input, most-recent picked from the 30d window). Sentinel-application: 988 tests passing (969 prior + 19 new). Clippy --all-targets clean on the new code.

- **Deploy frequency tracker (SEN-9, DORA core metric #2)** (2026-05-15). New `crates/sentinel-application/src/deploy_freq.rs` module with the data model + aggregation seam for tracking deploys per repo/env. `DeployRecord { timestamp, repo, env, commit, duration_s }` is appended to `~/.claude/sentinel/metrics/deploys.jsonl` via `append_deploy()` — append-only, atomic per line, parent dir created on demand. `aggregate_at(deploys_path, summary_path, now)` (production wrapper `aggregate()` uses `Utc::now()`) reads the JSONL, buckets into rolling 7d/30d windows per (repo, env), and writes `deploys-summary.json` with `RepoEnvAggregate { deploys_7d, deploys_30d, rate_per_day_7d, rate_per_day_30d, tier, first_in_window, last_in_window }` plus a 60-day `DailyPoint` sparkline series. `DoraTier::from_rate_per_day(rate)` classifies on the 30-day rate (avoids bursty-week flips): Elite (≥1/day), High (≥1/week), Medium (≥1/month), Low (<1/month). Malformed JSONL lines are logged via `tracing::warn` and skipped — a single corrupt entry can't poison the whole aggregation. New CLI: `sentinel deploy-freq aggregate` (read + summarize + print, sorted by 30d rate desc with colored tier badges) and `sentinel deploy-freq record --repo X --env Y --commit Z [--duration-s N] [--timestamp ...]` (manual entry for testing + the backfill path before Hookdeck `deployment.success` ingest lands). 16 unit tests cover the 4 DORA tier boundaries (Elite/High/Medium/Low and the exact-boundary case), append+read round-trip with multiple lines, append creates parent dir, read skips malformed lines, read returns empty on nonexistent file, aggregation groups by (repo, env), excludes records outside 30d, writes summary JSON, classifies tier on the 30d rate, handles empty JSONL, emits daily points within the 60d window, and skips unparseable timestamps. Webhook ingest from Hookdeck (Vercel + Railway `deployment.success`) and Vercel/Railway API backfill remain follow-ups; this PR ships the data model + aggregation + CLI seam so those follow-ups can plug in via the existing `append_deploy()` interface. Sentinel-application: 969 tests passing (953 prior + 16 new). Clippy --all-targets clean on the new code.

- **Context propagation through StepProofs (sentinel #58 / M7.9)** (2026-05-14). `submit_step_complete` now inherits `account_context` forward through a skill's chain when the field is omitted from the call. Three explicit cases: (1) **key absent** → inherit from the most recent `StepProof` in this skill's chain (phase-only entries skipped — they don't carry the account dimension); (2) **key present, null** → explicit clear, no inheritance; (3) **key present, string** → use that value verbatim. Same semantics as HTTP request headers: missing header inherits from upstream, explicitly empty header clears it. Production benefit: callers driving a multi-step pipeline (linear's claim → fetch → intelligence → worktree → review → qa-handoff sequence) only need to set `account_context` once, on the claim step — every downstream step inherits the same tenant scope without each call re-specifying it. Override is always available by passing the field explicitly. Audit-trail benefit: when a chain crosses tenant boundaries (rare but possible during admin operations), the override shows up in the sealed proof as the explicit attribution. 4 new tests covering inherited-after-explicit, explicit-override-beats-inheritance, explicit-null-clears, and no-prior-chain-stays-none cases. Sentinel-application: 953 tests passing.

- **`sentinel policy suggest` — plain-English → TOML (sentinel #59 / M7.10 — AEGIS pattern)** (2026-05-14). New CLI subcommand: `sentinel policy suggest "<policy>"` parses a one-line policy statement and emits a ready-to-paste `[[step_verifiers]]` TOML fragment. Grammar (deliberately small, rule-based, no LLM in this slice): `<skill>/<phase>/<step> requires <adapter> [verified|provenance]`. Mode defaults to `verified` (strict production mode where smoke-test FAILED receipts must NOT satisfy the gate); `provenance` is the audit-only mode where the act of producing the receipt is what's witnessed. Output includes header comments citing the source policy AND a `# Mode: ...` line explaining the trust model, so future readers can trace any active verifier back to the policy that introduced it. Emitted TOML round-trips through `toml::from_str` as a `Vec<StepVerifierRequirement>` — pasting it directly into a sentinel config works. The CLI is the deterministic floor; a future LLM-assisted skill can interpret fuzzier prompts (e.g. "make sure all QA-handoff steps need Browserbase") and pipe through this same parser, so the safety-net validation lives in one place. 14 tests covering parser happy paths (verified default, explicit verified, provenance, case-insensitive keywords), error paths (empty input, missing parts, missing 'requires', unknown mode, trailing garbage, illegal chars), and TOML-fragment round-trip via the toml crate. Sentinel-cli: 134 tests passing.

- **Sandboxed judge wrapper (sentinel #60 / M7.11 — EQTY Lab principle)** (2026-05-14). New `sentinel_application::sandboxed_judge::SandboxedJudge` wraps any `JudgeService` impl with two protections against misbehaving inner judges: (1) **wall-clock timeout** (default 60s, configurable per-instance via `with_timeout`) — a wedged provider or hanging round-trip produces a synthetic `SANDBOX:`-prefixed verdict instead of hanging sentinel; (2) **panic isolation** — the inner call is dispatched via `tokio::spawn` so a panic in the judge becomes a `JoinError` at the wrapper layer, converted into a `PANIC:`-prefixed verdict so callers see something happened. Anyhow errors (configuration failures like "no API key") still propagate as `Err` — the sandbox catches HANGS and PANICS, not legitimate config errors. Three trait methods are individually wrapped: `evaluate`, `evaluate_step`, and `evaluate_multi`. For `evaluate_multi`, a sandbox timeout or panic synthesizes a single-run `MultiJudgeVerdict` tagged with `provider: Some("sandbox")` so consumers preserve the typed shape downstream. Documents what the sandbox does NOT enforce (memory caps, network egress, CPU caps — those need real subprocess isolation, deferred to future work). 6 unit tests covering happy-path pass-through, timeout on slow inner judge, panic isolation, timeout on `evaluate_step`, timeout on `evaluate_multi`, and config-error propagation. Sentinel-application: 949 tests passing.

- **Pluggable judge backends — `evaluate_multi` on JudgeService (sentinel #69)** (2026-05-14). New default method on the `JudgeService` trait: `evaluate_multi(skill, phase_id, phase_objectives, evidence, tier) -> Result<MultiJudgeVerdict>`. Dispatches the same evidence to every judge model in the configured `JudgeTrustTier`, collects per-judge `JudgeRun`s with model + verdict + cost + provider attribution, then synthesizes the cross-vendor result via the existing `MultiJudgeVerdict::synthesize`. The synthesized verdict surfaces (a) sufficient (conservative AND across all judges — any FAIL flips the multi-verdict to false), (b) confidence (min across runs), and (c) **disagreement flag** (true when judges disagree). Per-judge errors do NOT propagate as `Err` — they become a `sufficient=false` JudgeRun with `ERROR:`-prefixed reasoning, so one flaky vendor can't mask the others' verdicts (the whole point of cross-vendor verification). Default tier (`Review` = Kimi K2.6 alone, OSS-first) costs no more than the existing single-judge path; `Critical` (Kimi + Sonnet) and `CriticalStrict` (Kimi + Sonnet + Opus) layer additional judges for production-blocking decisions where missed defects cost more than the extra inference. Default impl is sequential — `MultiModelJudge` and other implementers can override to parallelize when the cost/latency tradeoff favors it. 5 new unit tests covering Review-tier single-model dispatch, Critical-tier multi-model dispatch with order preservation, disagreement synthesis on split votes, per-judge error tolerance (the failure surfaces as an ERROR run but doesn't abort the call), and FallbackJudge back-compat. Sentinel-application: 943 tests passing.

- **Browserbase as federated skill subgraph (sentinel #72)** (2026-05-14). New `config/steps/browserbase.toml` makes Browserbase a first-class member of sentinel's skill federation. Five phases × 12 steps wrap the full Steel session lifecycle: `session` (create + configure), `interact` (navigate, inject Doppler-personal-branch credentials, run interactions), `observe` (screenshots, console-error inspection, recording URL capture), `verify` (submit a Browserbase evidence claim through sentinel — adapter seals receipt with provenance binding per #70/#71), `cleanup` (release the session). Each step's `suggested_tools` references the actual MCP tools (`mcp__browserbase__create_session`, `mcp__browserbase__navigate`, `mcp__browserbase__screenshot`, `mcp__sentinel__submit_step_complete`, etc.), so any other skill that needs UI verification can reference these steps via federation directives. The `verify/4.1` step closes the loop with the BIBLE adapter (#70) + step_verifier gate (#71) — downstream skills like linear's qa-handoff that demand a verified Browserbase receipt get a clean federation contract. Federation compose now reports 48 skills (was 47) × 203 phases × 949 steps, composes cleanly with zero validation errors. Browserbase is now a runtime-agnostic federation peer — any MCP client (Claude Code, Cursor, custom Python harness) can route UI steps through it via the standard skill-step dispatch.

- **Browserbase as third-party verifier — `step_verifier` gate (sentinel #71)** (2026-05-14). New `sentinel_domain::step_verifier` module + wireup in `McpHandler`. `StepVerifierRequirement { skill, phase_id, step_id, adapter_name, verified_only }` declares "step at these coordinates cannot seal unless its evidence carries a receipt from the named adapter." `McpHandler::with_step_verifiers(Vec<...>)` registers the set at bootstrap; `submit_step_complete` checks every matching requirement AFTER the BIBLE wireup folds any receipt in (so the verifier sees the fresh receipt). Failures block the seal with a clear error naming the adapter and the specific failure mode (missing receipt, wrong adapter, unverified result, malformed receipt). Two construction modes: `new` (default `verified_only=true` — production case where smoke-test FAILED receipts must NOT satisfy the gate) and `provenance_only` (audit-only — the act of producing the receipt is what's witnessed, verification verdict ignored). This realizes the "Browserbase as third-party verifier" pattern: register a `StepVerifierRequirement` at the `qa-handoff/3.5.5` step requiring a `browserbase` adapter receipt, and the proof chain will refuse to seal the implementation-comment step unless the Browserbase smoke test passed (or, in provenance-only mode, was at least run). Two layers of defense alongside `step_gate`: step_gate blocks the *attempt* to fire downstream tools at PreToolUse; step_verifier blocks the *seal* of the next step's proof at submit_step_complete time — a misconfigured client that bypasses step_gate still can't bypass step_verifier. 9 unit tests on the domain module (coordinate matching, verified/provenance-only paths, missing/wrong-adapter/unverified/malformed-receipt rejections, Display strings) + 4 new mcp_handler integration tests (no-match no-impact back-compat, matching verifier+BIBLE-folded receipt round-trip, blocking on missing receipt with the "absent" + adapter-name error message, blocking on `verified=false` receipt with the "verified=true" + adapter-name error message). Sentinel-domain: 390 tests passing. Sentinel-application: 938 tests passing.

- **Browserbase evidence adapter (sentinel #70)** (2026-05-14). Second concrete adapter for THE BIBLE framework (filesystem was first per #38). New `sentinel_infrastructure::evidence_browserbase::BrowserbaseAdapter` implements `EvidenceAdapter` for `browserbase.<verb>` claims. Two claim types supported: (1) **`browserbase.session_observed`** — caller swears they ran *a* Browserbase session; receipt seals `verified: true` iff `context.session_id` is a non-empty string; permissive on purpose since the act of running a session is the witnessed fact; payload preserves `screenshot_count`, `console_errors`, `recording_url`, `artifacts` array. (2) **`browserbase.smoke_test_passed`** — caller asserts the smoke test passed cleanly; receipt seals `verified: true` iff all three predicates hold (`session_id` present, `screenshot_count >= 1`, `console_errors == 0`); failures still seal but with `verified: false` and a `predicates` breakdown object showing exactly which check failed (corpus queries on `verified == false` surface these as follow-up). Design choice: **metadata-shape adapter, not HTTP-calling adapter** — the full "phone home to Browserbase API and re-fetch the session" path would require `BROWSERBASE_API_KEY` + reqwest in sentinel-infrastructure for one adapter, and would conflict with the [Doppler-personal-branch convention](#90–#102) pushing credentials OUT of sentinel onto each MCP server. Instead, the Browserbase MCP server collects the artifacts (it already has the credentials) and this adapter validates them + seals receipts with provenance binding. Future #69 work can layer a `browserbase_remote` adapter that DOES phone home, for cross-vendor verification. 10 unit tests covering claim-type matching, missing/empty session_id rejection, full happy-path round-trip, predicate-breakdown for partial failures, and provenance-verification round-trip on the sealed receipt. Sentinel-infrastructure: 95 tests passing.

- **THE BIBLE: evidence-adapter wireup in `submit_step_complete` (sentinel #68)** (2026-05-14). The pure-domain evidence-adapter framework (`sentinel_domain::evidence_adapter`) + application-layer registry (`sentinel_application::evidence_adapters`) + first filesystem adapter shipped earlier; this commit wires the registry into the actual proof-sealing path. `McpHandler` gains an optional `evidence_adapters` field configured via new builder method `with_evidence_adapters(Arc<EvidenceAdapterRegistry>)`. `sentinel__submit_step_complete` gains an optional `evidence_claim` arg with shape `{skill, phase_id, step_id, claim_type, context}`. When supplied alongside a wired registry, the registry fetches an `EvidenceReceipt`, the provenance hash is verified against the claim, and the receipt is folded into the sealed proof's `Evidence.custom.evidence_receipt` (single canonical key, lookup is O(1) for verifiers). When supplied without a registry wired, the call FAILS LOUDLY rather than silently dropping the claim — the whole point of THE BIBLE is "we know we don't know" being a first-class chain entry, not a missing-data ambiguity. When no claim is supplied, behavior is unchanged from M4.2 (every existing caller stays back-compat). Three new tests cover (1) no-claim-no-registry back-compat, (2) claim-with-self-attested-fallback-registry round-trip producing a receipt with `verified=false` in the chain, and (3) claim-without-registry fail-loudly path. Sentinel-application: 934 tests passing. With this wireup, "every step claim requires external evidence" is now opt-in via per-call arg AND an opt-out fallback receipt is also a first-class chain entry — the framework can extend to GitHub / Browserbase / Doppler adapters one at a time without further wiring changes.

- **M2.13 signed step-config manifests with Ed25519 (sentinel #26)** (2026-05-14). New `sentinel-domain::step_manifest` module + `sentinel manifest` CLI subcommand. Each step-config TOML under `<config_dir>/steps/` can be paired with a `manifest.toml` recording the canonical SHA-256 of every step file plus an optional Ed25519 signature over that hash. Producers (`sentinel manifest write [--key-env VAR]`) canonicalize each source (strip BOM, normalize CRLF→LF, trim trailing whitespace per line, strip trailing blank lines, ensure one trailing newline) and write the manifest. Consumers (`sentinel manifest verify [--pubkey HEX] [--strict|--hash-only]`) re-canonicalize, re-hash, and check entries; strict mode also verifies signatures against the manifest's recorded `public_key` header (or an explicit `--pubkey` override). Three trust levels: (1) **hash-only mode** — bit-rot protection without authenticated trust, manifest reviewable in PRs; (2) **signed with key in manifest header** — the typical published case where the public key is delivered with the manifest (still trusts the channel that carried it); (3) **signed with pinned key** — production case where consumers pin the verifying key out-of-band (binary constant, TUF root). `sentinel manifest show` prints a summary (entry count, signed-vs-unsigned, public key fingerprint, per-entry hash prefix). 16 new unit tests on the domain module (canonicalization round-trips, hash stability across whitespace variants, signed/unsigned upsert, wrong-key rejection, hash-only fallback for signed entries, serde TOML round-trip, missing/drifted entry detection) + 7 new CLI integration tests (write/verify round-trip, drift detection, signing-key env-var validation, full sign-then-verify-strict round-trip). Sentinel-domain: 381 tests passing. Sentinel-cli: 120 tests passing.

- **M5.3 race-condition + batch-ops stress tests for the proof chain (sentinel #44)** (2026-05-14). Closes out the M5 epic. Three new `#[tokio::test]`s in `crates/sentinel-application/src/mcp_handler.rs` stress the proof-chain engine under concurrent and deep-sequential load: `m5_3_concurrent_different_skills_seals_all_chains` fires 50 concurrent `submit_step_complete` calls through one shared handler, each for a distinct skill (`stress_skill_000`..`stress_skill_049`), and asserts every submission succeeds, every skill ends up with exactly one chain entry, and no chain is silently lost — guards against the engine's `RwLock` lock-ordering bugs (lock-before-validate or release-between-read-and-write that drops writes). `m5_3_concurrent_same_skill_does_not_fork_chain` fires 30 concurrent submissions to the SAME skill (`linear`); the engine must serialize so the final chain has exactly 30 entries with unique `combined_hash`es and a strictly linear prev_hash chain (`previous_hash` of step N must equal `combined_hash` of step N-1). If two siblings shared a `previous_hash`, the chain forked — the test catches that. `m5_3_deep_sequential_batch_stays_linear` runs 100 sequential submissions to one skill and re-verifies the prev_hash chain integrity at depth, also asserts the final entry's `artifact.index` is `depth - 1` so we'd catch silent reordering or dropped entries. All three pass on first run. Sentinel-application: 931 tests passing, 0 failures. **M5 epic (#41) is now complete — Backlog → Completed lifecycle covered end-to-end + concurrency-stressed.**

- **M5.2 in-process E2E test for Code Review → QA Testing → Completed (sentinel #43)** (2026-05-14). Two new `#[tokio::test]`s in `crates/sentinel-application/src/mcp_handler.rs` cover the back half of the linear-skill pipeline (M2.3.G qa-handoff + M2.3.H cleanup + the QA-tester pass). `m5_2_code_review_to_completed_seals_qa_handoff_and_cleanup` pre-seeds the chain with a `review/3.L3` "Code Review" entry (where M5.1 ends), then drives 9 back-half steps (review CI+merge, deploy, Steel smoke, Loom upload, Linear QA-Testing transition, QA reassign, implementation comment, worktree cleanup) followed by a final QA-pass step transitioning Linear to "Completed". Asserts: 11 total sealed entries; consecutive step hashes always differ (catches the engine forgetting to fold prev_hash); the final entry lands at `qa-handoff/3.5.6` with `new_state: "Completed"`; every step's artifact carries the same `issue_id` forward so the chain alone reconstructs the full life of FPCRM-200. `m5_2_qa_fail_keeps_ticket_at_qa_testing` covers the honest-recording counterpart: drives to QA Testing, then a QA-fail step lands with `new_state: "QA Failed"` (not Completed) and a `rejection_reason` field — the proof chain can't lie about what happened. Composed with M5.1, the full Backlog → Completed lifecycle is now smoke-tested end-to-end in-process. Sentinel-application: 928 tests passing, 0 failures.

- **M5.1 in-process E2E pipeline test for Linear skill (sentinel #42)** (2026-05-14). Two new `#[tokio::test]`s in `crates/sentinel-application/src/mcp_handler.rs` exercise the `submit_step_complete` path Claude takes in real linear-skill execution: `m5_1_backlog_to_code_review_pipeline_seals_chain_in_order` drives a full Backlog → Code Review journey through 7 sequential steps spanning all 5 lead-up phases (claim → fetch → intelligence → worktree → review), asserting each step seals into the chain, the phase-and-step sequence matches submission order, every sealed step has a distinct `combined_hash` (guards against the engine forgetting to fold the previous entry's hash into the next), and the final entry lands at `review/3.L3` with `linear_state: "Code Review"` in its artifact. `m5_1_insufficient_verdict_halts_pipeline_midflight` proves the gate holds: two good steps land in the chain, an `insufficient` verdict on the third does NOT extend the chain, and the same step resubmitted with sufficient evidence does. Uses the existing `StubJudge` + `ProofEngine` + `McpHandler` triple from M4.2's test bed — no new infrastructure. Deliberately in-process per the M5 runbook decision: the proof chain logic and the MCP API surface are what's covered here; a real-Linear E2E harness would require credentials and someone to babysit it, and the manual recipe at `docs/m5-linear-e2e-runbook.md` already exists for that case. Full sentinel-application suite: 926 tests passing, 0 failures.

### Changed
- **`hooks::stop_failure::rotate_accounts` calls canonical `claude-accounts` binary** (2026-05-14). The CLI was renamed from `accounts` to `claude-accounts` (per `claude-accounts-cli-rust` Cargo.toml `[[bin]] name`). A shadow legacy `accounts.exe` lingered in `~/.cargo/bin` for a while but drifts — any `cargo install` of the renamed CLI only refreshes the canonical name, so the shadow gets stale and `stop_failure`'s rotate path was potentially hitting an out-of-date binary. Now calls `claude-accounts` directly.

- **CLAUDE.md generator includes time-of-day + timezone abbreviation** (2026-05-13, sentinel 0.4.1). The auto-generated `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md` Date Context section now reads `Today is Wednesday, May 13, 2026 at 08:58 AM CDT.` (previously only the date). The assistant was greeting Gary with "Good evening" at 8:55 AM because nothing in the LLM's context disambiguated AM/PM. Switched `chrono::Utc::now()` → `chrono::Local::now()` (also fixes a latent near-midnight off-by-one), formats time as zero-padded 12-hour with AM/PM (`%I:%M %p`), and resolves a DST-aware IANA abbreviation via `iana-time-zone` → `chrono-tz` (chrono's `%Z` on Windows returns "Central Standard Time", not "CDT"). Helper `local_tz_abbreviation()` falls back to `%Z` then `"UTC"` if the IANA lookup fails. Footer `*Auto-generated on session start: …*` also gets the same time + tz. Two new workspace deps: `chrono-tz = "0.10"` and `iana-time-zone = "0.1"`.

### Removed
- **All ntfy push code** (2026-05-09, sentinel 0.4.1). Deleted `sentinel-application::ntfy_push` module and all 11 callsites across `hooks/stop_failure.rs` (rate-limit recovery, auth recovery, generic turn-aborted), `hooks/build_notify.rs` (build/deploy notifications), and `sentinel-cli/src/hook_cmd.rs` (hook-level block notifications). Sentinel emits zero ntfy pushes after this. Account-failure notifications moved into `claude-code-handler-rust` so they have direct access to slot/trace/session forensics that sentinel's hook-level vantage point doesn't have. The previous "every event sends a push" volume was unhelpful — too noisy to act on, too generic to debug. Cleaned up now-orphaned helpers `project_name`, `first_error_line`, `truncate_for_push` and the 3 tests that referenced them. 917 tests still pass.

### Added
- **`sentinel project handover` and `sentinel project lesson` CLI subcommands (M9.3, #67)** (2026-05-14). Two new explicit-trigger subcommands under `sentinel project`, completing the M9 family. `handover --title "..." [--summary "..."] [--dir <path>]` writes a Markdown stub to `<repo>/.sentinel/handovers/YYYY-MM-DD-<slug>.md` with the README's suggested sections (Context, What got done, What's still open, Gotchas for next session, Pointers); `--summary` pre-fills the Context section. `lesson --title "..." [--summary "..."] [--tag X --tag Y]` writes a structured JSON to `<repo>/.sentinel/lessons/L-<NNN>.json` with the next monotonic ID — scans existing `L-<NNN>.json` files for the max, increments by 1, respecting the "mark resolved, don't delete" convention so retired IDs stay occupied. Both walk up from cwd looking for a `.git` entry (file OR directory — worktrees work) and error clearly on missing `.git`, missing `.sentinel/{handovers,lessons}/`, or empty `--title`. Handover filenames append `-2`/`-3`/... when two handovers share a slug on the same day.
