Lesson JSON is rendered via `serde_json::to_string_pretty` against an ordered Map so field order matches the README and special characters are safely escaped. 14 new unit tests bring `project_cmd`'s count to 20 (slugify edge cases, non-colliding handover paths, full handover write with date verification, summary-fills-context, error paths, next_lesson_id semantics, JSON shape verification, monotonic-after-existing). cargo check --tests clean (30s); cargo test execution blocked by a transient local MSVC link.exe lookup issue but the test code itself compiles. Closes M9.3 (#67) and the full M9 family (epic #64 / scaffold #65 / plans #66 / handovers + lessons #67).

- **`plan_organizer` hook also writes to `<repo>/.sentinel/plans/` (M9.2, #66)** (2026-05-14). Extends the existing ExitPlanMode → archive flow with a second write destination: when the repo has been initialized via `sentinel project init` (`<repo>/.sentinel/plans/` exists), plans land there too with their own independent version sequence. Failures in the repo-local step are silent — the global `~/.claude/plans/<project>/<slug>-v<N>.md` archive remains the authoritative copy. Two new helpers: `find_repo_root` walks up from cwd looking for a `.git` entry (file OR directory, so worktrees work), `try_write_repo_local_archive` returns `Some(path)` when the write succeeds, `None` when the repo isn't initialized or anything fails. The repo-local copy is OPT-IN — sentinel doesn't auto-create `.sentinel/plans/`; that's `sentinel project init`'s job. The injected context now mentions the repo-local path when it landed, and the channel event metadata includes `repo_local_archived_path` for downstream consumers. 7 new tests bring `plan_organizer`'s count to 15/15 passing (find_repo_root walks-up + accepts-git-file + outside-repo, try_write_repo_local writes-when-dir-exists + skips-when-dir-missing + skips-when-not-in-repo + versions-independently).

- **`sentinel project init` CLI subcommand — `.sentinel/` repo-local scaffold (M9.1, #65)** (2026-05-14). New `Project { Init { ... } }` subcommand wired through `project_cmd.rs` (~470 lines). Creates `.sentinel/` inside the target repo (default: current directory) with five subdirectories (`tickets/`, `plans/`, `handovers/`, `lessons/`, `proof-chains/`), a root `README.md` documenting the convention + the global-vs-repo-local split, a `config.json` per-repo config stub, and one `README.md` per subdirectory documenting its schema and naming conventions. Idempotent: existing files are preserved unless `--force` is passed; missing files are filled in. `--dry-run` previews without touching the filesystem. Use cases: `tickets/` holds local-first JSON tickets (`T-001.json`) that can be Linear-mirrored or stand alone for repos without Linear; `plans/` holds `/plan` outputs that should live with the code (different from the per-machine archive at `~/.claude/plans/`); `handovers/` holds per-session summaries; `lessons/` holds project-specific lessons learned (`L-NNN.json` with resolved/still-valid markers); `proof-chains/` holds chains worth committing alongside the code (audit-grade trust tier, high-risk changes, explicit author opt-in). 6 unit tests cover scaffold creation, idempotency, `--force` semantics, `--dry-run` semantics, `config.json` parsing as valid JSON, and partial-state re-runs. M9.2 (plans-with-code automation, #66) and M9.3 (handovers automation, #67) build on this scaffold.

- **`config/steps/linear/templates/` — pre-baked virtual skill pack templates (M2.14, #27)** (2026-05-14). New convention parallel to `references/`: each TOML in `templates/` is a multi-step recipe the router (M7.3, pending) can offer as a quick-start instead of replanning from scratch. Schema: `[template]` header with `id` (matches filename), `name`, `description`, `triggers` (prompts the router matches against), `estimate_minutes`, `catalog`, then ordered `[[template.steps]]` entries with `ref = "<skill>.<phase>.<step>"`. Two worked examples on the linear skill: `claim-and-pr.toml` (44 steps — claim → fetch → intelligence → worktree → review L0-L3, stops at draft PR open; the most common multi-step recipe), `quick-comment.toml` (4 steps — read issue + ack prior comments + post status comment, no state change; smallest viable template proving the schema handles short packs as cleanly as long ones). README documents when to add a template (frequent reuse, clean stop point, stable step list) vs. when not to (cross-skill, branching). No router consumption yet — templates are documentation-only until M7.3 lands; until then they're useful as "canonical recipe for X" references for humans.

- **`config/steps/linear/references/` — progressive-disclosure docs pattern (M2.10, #23)** (2026-05-14). Apollo Skills' progressive-disclosure split: the TOML (`config/steps/linear.toml`) keeps the schema-bearing data (step IDs, descriptions, `suggested_tools`, `artifact_schema`, federation directives, judge config). Long-form prose — rationale, edge cases, AI-judge rubrics, walkthroughs — moves into `config/steps/<skill>/references/<phase>.md`. The TOML stays small enough for `build.rs` codegen and tool-schema rendering; the references load on demand for humans and (later) for judges that need rubric context. Worked example for linear: `references/README.md` documents the convention + when-to-use-which split, `claim-phase.md` covers the 8 steps from -0.1 through 0.4 with sub-phase guard rails / claim execution / edge cases / judge rubric, `review-phase.md` covers the 22-step 6-layer review pipeline (L0 tests, L1 lens agent, L2 Codex, L3 PR, L4 CI+CodeRabbit, L5 final gate) including circuit-breaker semantics, CodeRabbit triage, and cross-vendor disagreement handling. No schema integration yet — references are discoverable by path convention (`<phase-id>-phase.md`). Adding an optional `references = [...]` field to `WorkflowStep` is the natural follow-up; until then the convention is enforced by review, not by validator. Other skills can adopt the same layout incrementally.

- **Competitive-intel framework + first-pass snapshot — `docs/competitive-intelligence.md` (#80)** (2026-05-14). Active doc tracking the five named players in sentinel's category (Apollo MCP Server, IBM ContextForge, Microsoft Agent Governance Toolkit, EQTY Lab, AEGIS policy library) plus an "other/new entrants" bucket. Each row carries seven fields: latest release, architecture posture, cryptographic story, policy/governance story, multi-vendor story, threat to sentinel (none/wide-moat/direct-overlap/leapfrog), and action (none/file Linear ticket/file design note). First-pass snapshot is filled today, ahead of the formal Q3 review (target 2026-09-30); each quarterly review replaces *Current state* in place with prior versions pushed to *History*. Includes a sentinel-positioning table — every primitive sentinel ships vs the closest competitor that ships it — making the novel-to-sentinel column (per-developer Doppler personal-branch identity) legible to buyers. Includes the review process template so future quarters don't have to rebuild the framework.

- **M5 linear-skill E2E manual verification runbook — `docs/m5-linear-e2e-runbook.md` (#104)** (2026-05-14). Active manual recipe that walks a developer (or future session) through verifying the linear-skill pipeline end-to-end against real firefly-pro Linear and real GitHub, ahead of automated M5.1/M5.2/M5.3 (#42/#43/#44) shipping. Three stages: Backlog → Code Review (claim phase + worktree + PR creation with `Ref FPCRM-XXX`, deliberately NOT `Fixes` to avoid Linear's auto-Done bypass), Code Review → QA Testing → Completed (PR merge triggers `linear-on-merge.yml`, auto-transitions issue + reassigns to QA tester), race-condition stress test (concurrent batch_create_issues + concurrent claims). Plus identity-chain sanity check (verify `mcp__linear__viewer` returns gary@fireflypro.com from Doppler personal branch), schema pre-flight (run #103's validator), and StepProof chain assembly steps. Covers prerequisites (DOPPLER_TOKEN_FIREFLY_PRO + DOPPLER_PERSONAL_BRANCH env vars, personal-branch Linear key population in Doppler UI), per-stage verification checklists, and a 5-minute "is the foundation working" quick check. Explicitly NOT a substitute for the automated tests — those need cross-crate test scaffolding tracked under #42/#43/#44.

- **Step-config schema validator — `schema_validator.rs` (M5.0, #103)** (2026-05-14). New module under `sentinel-cli/src/` that catches typo-class bugs in `config/steps/*.toml` enrichment data before any E2E run hits real Linear/GitHub. Two checks: (1) **Forward-reference dangling** — every `(from <phase>/<step>)` substring in a step's `artifact_schema` must resolve to a real `(phase_id, step_id)` pair in the same file; catches typos like `(from fetch/1.10)` instead of `1.1`. Walks `artifact_schema` recursively so the check works on arbitrary inline-table shapes. (2) **Suggested-tool name shape** — `suggested_tools` entries must match `mcp__<server>__<tool>` (lowercase server/tool with `_` separator, hyphens allowed in server names like `claude-accounts`), `Bash:<cmd>`, or an internal Claude tool name (`EnterPlanMode`, `EnterWorktree`, etc); flags camelCase typos (`mcp__linear__GetIssue`) and old single-underscore conventions. 14 unit tests cover forward-ref parsing (including negative step IDs like `-0.1`, multi-ref strings, annotated refs), MCP-name validation accept/reject, well-formed/suspicious classification, and end-to-end synthetic-TOML cases. A 15th test (`production_step_configs_are_clean`, `#[ignore]`d) runs the validator against the real `config/steps/` directory — currently passes for all 47 shipped configs, including the 91 enriched linear.toml steps. The validator is **report-only** today; promoting failures into `federation compose`'s blocking gate is a follow-up — let the test bake first. Re-parses the TOML with its own struct (rather than extending `sentinel-domain::WorkflowStep`) because `artifact_schema` and `suggested_tools` are skills-mcp build.rs codegen fields that the canonical sentinel loader silently drops; keeping the validator self-contained avoids rippling through `federation_cmd`'s 1200+ lines.

- **`sentinel cleanup tasks` — orphan session task dirs pruner (#78)** (2026-05-14). New subcommand under `sentinel cleanup` that prunes orphan directories under `~/.claude/tasks/`. A session task directory is orphan when (a) its name is a UUID matching no `<id>.jsonl` transcript anywhere under `~/.claude/projects/*/`, AND (b) its mtime is older than the cutoff (default 30 days, configurable via `--older-than N`). The age gate defends against active sessions whose transcript hasn't been written to disk yet — younger orphans are kept as "younger-than-cutoff" and reported but not removed. Non-UUID directory names (e.g. `.lock`, junk dirs) are reported as "not-a-session" and never auto-removed. Default mode is dry-run with a structured audit report (live / younger / not-a-session / orphan counts plus total orphan bytes); `--apply` performs the removal. Helper `format_size` renders B/KB/MB without pulling in a dep. 9 new unit tests cover the classifier (live, orphan, young, not-a-session), the live-session scanner, the apply path's selective removal, and the UUID heuristic — all 15 `cleanup_cmd` tests pass.

- **Linear skill — fully step-gated (M2.3, #17 closed)** (2026-05-14). All 91 steps in `config/steps/linear.toml` now carry `suggested_tools` (the specific peer-MCP tool names the caller should invoke, e.g. `mcp__linear__update_issue`, `mcp__browserbase__create_session`) and `artifact_schema` (typed handoff shape with forward refs naming the upstream step that produced each field, e.g. `issue_id = "string (from fetch/1.1)"`). 91/91 steps have `artifact_schema`; 78/91 have `suggested_tools` — the 13 without are intentional gate/synthesis steps where the work is reasoning, not tool invocation. Tool names cross-checked against the registered MCP servers (linear, github, browserbase, loom, agents, codex, sentinel, vercel, railway, doppler, sequential-thinking) — no phantom references. Verified end-to-end via `SKILLS_MCP_STEPS_DIR` override pointing skills-mcp-rust at this dir: `cargo build --release` succeeds, codegen reports "939 step tools across 47 skill(s)", generated body for `linear__claim__neg_0_1` contains the enriched suggested_tools array and artifact_schema JSON. Closes the M2.3 epic and the M2 epic gate from the M2.3 angle (remaining M2.10–M2.14 are follow-on Apollo-pattern enhancements, not core M2 functionality).

- **Multi-judge verdict types in `sentinel-domain` (#82 Stage B Part 1, follow-up to commit 2089896)**: new `crates/sentinel-domain/src/multi_judge.rs` module ships the wire-format types for parallel multi-judge verification — `JudgeTrustTier` (Routine / Review / Critical / CriticalStrict / AuditGrade), `JudgeRun` (one model + verdict + optional cost + optional resolved provider), and `MultiJudgeVerdict` synthesised across N runs with worst-case-wins logic. Mirrors the M3.3 review-types staging strategy: ship the types first so the wire format is locked, then the infrastructure-side producer (`rig_judge::evaluate_multi`) and the chain-entry consumer (`ProofEntry::Disagreement`) wire in next.
  - **Trust tier → judge models mapping**: `Routine → [Haiku]`, `Review (default) → [Kimi]`, `Critical → [Kimi, Sonnet]`, `CriticalStrict → [Kimi, Sonnet, Opus]`, `AuditGrade → [Kimi]` plus resolved-provider recording. Cross-distribution diversity is the load-bearing property — Eastern OSS Kimi + Western closed GPT/Opus produces real disagreement signal because the model families share fewer failure modes than 3-of-Western-closed.
  - **Synthesis rules (worst-case-wins)**: `sufficient` = `false` if ANY judge said `false`; `confidence` = floor (min) across all individuals (averaging would mask uncertainty); `disagreement` = `true` iff judges differ on `sufficient`. Drives the `ProofEntry::Disagreement` chain entry that lands in a follow-up commit.
  - **Cost aggregation**: `total_cost_usd` sums `JudgeRun.cost_usd` values. `None` when no individual reported a cost; `Some(0.0)` when reported but zero; partial-report case sums what exists (a single priced judge still produces a meaningful aggregate). Drives per-skill cost rollup on the report once OpenRouter cost-header capture lands in `rig_judge`.
  - **Audit-grade replay**: `JudgeTrustTier::AuditGrade.records_provider() == true` flags the producer to capture OpenRouter's resolved `model_id@provider` (e.g. `moonshotai/kimi-k2.6@parasail-fp8`) into `JudgeRun.provider`. EU AI Act Article 12 compliance: "prove which model judged this" over a 10-year retention window.
  - **Empty-runs degenerate case**: synthesizing zero runs returns `sufficient: true` (vacuous all() on empty iterator), `disagreement: false`, `confidence: 0.0` (we have no judges, we can't claim any confidence — the safe answer for what's a producer bug).
  - **Kebab-case wire format pinned**: `serde(rename_all = "kebab-case")` plus an explicit `tier_serde_kebab_case` test asserting `"routine"` / `"review"` / `"critical"` / `"critical-strict"` / `"audit-grade"`. Step config TOMLs declare `trust_tier = "critical-strict"`; pinning prevents a future serde rename from silently demoting configs.
  - 14 unit tests pin: tier default = Review, judge_models per tier, audit-grade-only provider recording, logs_disagreement only for multi-judge tiers, all-pass synthesis (sufficient + no disagreement + min confidence), one-fail flips overall (any Fail → Fail + disagreement), unanimous fail (no disagreement when everyone agrees), empty runs (safe default), tier preserved through synthesis (replay needs it), cost aggregation (full / none / partial-report), kebab-case wire format, full JSON round-trip.
  - **Out of scope (subsequent Stage B commits)**: `rig_judge::evaluate_multi` running judges in parallel via tokio::join_all + capturing OpenRouter cost headers; `ProofEntry::Disagreement` chain entry variant; step config `trust_tier` field threading through the engine. Today's commit ships the **types** so the wire format is locked. 1348 workspace tests green (923 application + 353 domain + 72 infra). Release build clean.

- **M4.8 fail-fast config validation (#26, ContextForge pattern)**: new `crates/sentinel-domain/src/config.rs` module ships `SentinelConfig` — the canonical top-level config struct that aggregates every existing sub-config (`RequestLimits`, `SsrfPolicy`, plus new `JudgeConfig` / `ProofArchiveConfig` / `SigningConfig`) and a `validate()` method that runs every sub-validator on startup, **collecting every error before returning** (Pydantic-style multi-error). The load-bearing property: misconfig that surfaces three days later when a hook fires for the first time is the failure mode this layer exists to prevent. Surface a complete punch list at startup, fix all of it in one round-trip with the operator, never bail on the first error.
  - `SentinelConfig::validate()` returns `Result<(), Vec<ConfigError>>`. Each error variant carries the offending value + the rule that was broken so a deny-banner can render an actionable line per error without parsing the enum. Display impls include the actual numbers (test pins `EvidenceLimitTooLarge { actual: 200, ceiling: 100 }` Display string contains both "200" and "100" — operators search the log for the value).
  - Validation rules shipped today: `EvidenceLimitTooLarge` (max_evidence_bytes ≤ 100 MiB), `ArtifactLimitTooLarge` (max_artifact_bytes ≤ 10 MiB), `RateLimitWindowZero` (window_seconds == 0 with non-zero max_calls_per_window is divide-by-zero in any sliding-window math; window_seconds == 0 AND max_calls_per_window == 0 is valid — rate limiting just disabled), `SsrfAllowlistInvalidHost` / `SsrfDenylistInvalidHost` (no whitespace or control characters; doesn't try to be a full DNS validator, just catches the obvious typos that produce silent drift), `ProofArchiveAgingTooLarge` (sanity ceiling 365 days; > 1 year is almost certainly a typo and the router-as-planner moat doesn't get measurably better with chains older than a quarter), `HardwareSigningRequiredButNoKeyEnv` (true + None is unreachable — there's no path to produce a signature).
  - New sub-configs: `JudgeConfig { default_tier: JudgeModel }` (defaults to `JudgeModel::default_review_tier()` — Kimi K2.6); `ProofArchiveConfig { aging_days: Option<u32> }` (None ⇒ keep everything); `SigningConfig { signing_key_env: Option<String>, hardware_required: bool }` (defaults to `Some("SENTINEL_SIGNING_KEY")` + software). All composable via `#[serde(default)]` so dropping a new sub-config in is a one-line change at the parent.
  - 15 new unit tests pin: default validates clean; each rule fires independently; `multiple_errors_collected_pydantic_style` (the core invariant — 4 distinct broken fields produce 4 errors, not 1); `rate_limit_disabled_with_zero_calls_validates` (window_seconds=0 AND max_calls=0 is valid); `proof_archive_aging_none_validates` (None is valid); `hardware_required_with_env_validates`; `config_error_display_includes_actual_values`; `serde_round_trip_preserves_all_fields`; `toml_round_trip_preserves_all_fields` (TOML is the production format — pin explicitly).
  - **What's NOT in this commit (follow-up surface):** env-var loading (e.g. `SENTINEL_ALLOW_PRIVATE=1`) is a fragile surface that touches each adapter and deserves its own commit so the env-var registry can be reviewed end-to-end. Per-component plumbing (migrating every component from "reads its own RequestLimits/SsrfPolicy" to "reads from a shared SentinelConfig") is a refactor that lands skill-by-skill. Today's deliverable is the **shape + the rules**; future commits plug existing components into this struct without changing the validation surface.
  - 1322 workspace tests green (923 application + 327 domain + 72 infra). Release build clean.

- **M4.7 SSRF guard — default-block private network ranges (#25, ContextForge pattern)**: pure-domain classification module at `crates/sentinel-domain/src/ssrf.rs`. Takes a hostname (or literal IP) + an `SsrfPolicy` and returns `Ok` or `SsrfError::{EmptyHost, DeniedHost, PrivateIp, Reserved}`. No I/O, no DNS resolution — callers extract the host from their URL (via `reqwest::Url::host_str` etc.) and pass it in. This keeps `sentinel-domain` free of HTTP/URL crate deps and lets every infrastructure adapter (skills-mcp, sentinel-mcp, evidence adapters from #38) gate their outbound calls through the same policy without duplicating the classification table.
  - **What's blocked by default** (IPv4): 10/8, 172.16/12, 192.168/16 (RFC1918), 127/8 (loopback), 169.254/16 (link-local — covers AWS/GCP/Azure metadata at 169.254.169.254), 0.0.0.0/8 (current-network/DNS-rebinding pivot), 100.64/10 (CGN/Tailscale ULA), 224.0/4 (multicast), 240.0/4 (reserved). (IPv6): ::1/128 (loopback), fc00::/7 (ULA — checked manually since `Ipv6Addr::is_unique_local` is unstable in Rust 1.83), fe80::/10 (link-local), ::/128 (unspecified), `::ffff:V.W.X.Y` (IPv4-mapped — re-classified by the embedded v4 so `::ffff:127.0.0.1` resolves as loopback).
  - **Default denylist by hostname**: `localhost`, `metadata.google.internal`, `metadata.aws.internal`, `metadata.gke.internal`, `metadata.azure.com`, `169.254.169.254`. These hard-block by name even if DNS misconfig would have resolved them to a public IP. Comparison is case-insensitive (DNS is).
  - **Escape hatches**: `SsrfPolicy.allow_private = true` flips the global default-deny (useful when running against a local-network environment where private addressing is expected). `SsrfPolicy.allowlist` adds specific hosts that bypass the private-IP check (finer-grained than the global flag). The denylist runs FIRST and unconditionally — even an allowlisted host can't bypass the denylist (`localhost` cannot be allowlist-overridden).
  - **What's NOT covered (yet)**: DNS rebinding. A hostname can resolve to a public IP at lookup-time and a private IP at request-time. Closing this hole requires resolving the host once, pinning the connection to that IP, and validating the IP — that's an infrastructure concern (custom resolver in the HTTP client) and lands as a follow-up. Today's guard catches the obvious cases (literal IPs and "localhost"), which is most of the real-world SSRF surface.
  - 23 new unit tests pin every category: empty/whitespace host, localhost via denylist, all 5 cloud-metadata hostnames, IPv4 loopback, RFC1918 (10/172.16/192.168), link-local (169.254 IP literals beyond the denylisted .169.254), 0.0.0.0/8, 100.64/10 CGN, 224.0/4 multicast, 240.0/4 reserved, IPv6 ::1, IPv6 brackets stripping (`[::1]`), fe80::/10, fc00::/7 (fc00::/fd00::/fdff::), 2001:db8:: (global IPv6 stays allowed), `::ffff:127.0.0.1` mapped, public IPv4 8.8.8.8/1.1.1.1 allowed, public IPv6 2001:4860::8888 allowed, public hostnames allowed (no resolution), allowlist bypasses private-IP check, allowlist does NOT bypass denylist (localhost stays blocked), `allow_private=true` relaxes global check but denylist still wins, denylist case-insensitive, `SsrfPolicy::default()` has the metadata hosts, serde round-trip preserves all three fields.
  - **No new dependencies** — uses `std::net::IpAddr`, `serde` (already in domain), and a hand-written `Display` impl (no thiserror dep). The classification table fits in ~50 lines of `match` arms; the 7 helper functions are all const-friendly.
  - Hook integration (calling `check_host` from `step_judge::process` when an outbound HTTP claim is being evaluated, plus skills-mcp wiring for tool bodies that make HTTP calls) lands as a follow-up — this commit ships the policy layer; the integration touches a different surface and deserves its own commit. 1307 workspace tests green (923 application + 312 domain + 72 infra). Release build clean.

- **M6.3 trust score from proof corpus history (Microsoft AGT pattern)**: aggregates `ArchivedChainSummary` entries (from the cross-session corpus shipped in #39 / commit e969b61) into a 0–1000 trust score with five behavioral tiers — `Probationary` (0–200), `Developing` (201–500), `Established` (501–800), `Trusted` (801–950), `Verified` (951–1000). Scoped per-skill (via `score_for_skill`) and per-session_id (via `score_for_session`, where session_id is the agent identifier proxy). New module `crates/sentinel-application/src/trust.rs`; pure-application math (no I/O), public types `TrustTier` + `TrustScore`. Formula: base = round(pass_rate × 1000), then sample-size cap — 0 → 0, 1–4 → cap 200, 5–20 → cap 500, 21–100 → cap 800, 101–199 → cap 950, 200+ → uncapped. **Load-bearing invariant pinned by tests:** 100% pass on n=1 caps at Probationary 200 — the whole point of the trust score is to gate auto-approval, and "1 successful chain" is not evidence of reliability. The cap is intentionally aggressive at the low end. Surfaces ready to consume: pack contracts (#12 / orig M7.8) for "auto-merge agents need Trusted+ tier" policies, report #71/#72 for per-skill/per-agent trends. **Out of scope for this commit** (depends on later work): folding anomaly counts (task #17 ships the hook, corpus rollup is follow-on) and per-step cost (task #82 Stage B) into the score — both will compose in without changing the public API. 12 unit tests pin: empty corpus → Probationary 0; n=1 perfect → caps at Probationary 200; the 5/21/101/200 sample-size band edges; mixed pass/fail lowers score; all-failures → 0; skill filter excludes other skills; session filter groups by agent; `TrustTier::from_score` band edges; kebab-case serde wire format. 1284 workspace tests green (923 application + 289 domain + 72 infra). Release build clean.

- **`sentinel cleanup persistent-tasks` — orphan project_hash bucket pruner (#33)**: prunes stale buckets under `~/.claude/sentinel/persistent-tasks/` whose originating cwd no longer exists on disk. These accumulate every time sentinel saw a new cwd including every removed git worktree path; the worktree-collapse fix to `project_hash` only landed in commit 5ac549a (this session's first merge), so anything from before that lives under per-worktree-path hashes that no living cwd points to. On Gary's machine today: 299 of 390 buckets are orphans (77% bloat). New `crates/sentinel-cli/src/cleanup_cmd.rs` module: walks the dir, reads each bucket's `meta.json`, classifies by stat-ing the recorded `cwd` path, prints an audit report grouped by Live/Unreadable/Orphan, and removes orphan + unreadable buckets only when `--apply` is passed. Default mode is dry-run — no destructive surprises. New CLI surface: `sentinel cleanup persistent-tasks` (audit) / `sentinel cleanup persistent-tasks --apply` (act). New `Cleanup` command + `CleanupAction` subcommand enum on the existing clap structure to make room for follow-on cleanups (orphan session task dirs is filed as task #32 and slots in here next). 6 unit tests pin classification: live cwd, missing cwd, missing meta.json, malformed meta.json, empty cwd field, and the apply-removes-orphans-preserves-live invariant. Release build clean, no new warnings. Caller is unprivileged: `std::fs::remove_dir_all` only — does NOT touch `~/.claude/tasks/<session>/` (that's task #32's surface), does NOT touch `~/.claude/sentinel/proofs/` (those are the cross-session corpus and should outlive their originating cwd).

- **Cross-session proof chain archive (#39)**: turns the live-session-only `query_proof_corpus` (M4.3) into a cross-session corpus by archiving every chain to `~/.claude/sentinel/proofs/` on Stop and walking the index on read. This is the load-bearing input M7.5 router-as-planner needs to answer "for prompts like X, which step sequences had which success rates across all past chains?" — without it, the moat tool sees one session's worth of evidence and the planner is replicating yesterday's classifier.
  - New module `sentinel-application/src/proof_archive.rs`: `ArchivedChainRecord` (versioned wrapper carrying `schema_version: 1` + `archived_at` + the full chain), `ArchivedChainSummary` (one-line index entry: skill, session_id, step_count, phase_count, head_hash, all_sufficient, step_sequence, archived_at). Both versioned at the top level — cheap to add now, painful to retrofit later when v2 readers need to dispatch on shape.
  - Storage layout: one file per `(session_id, skill)` pair at `~/.claude/sentinel/proofs/<session>__<skill>.json` (avoids read-modify-write across multiple Stop fires) plus an append-only `index.jsonl`. Atomic writes via `<dir>/.<name>.tmp` + rename — a crashed Stop can never leave half-written JSON in the bucket. Idempotency: re-running Stop for the same session does not duplicate index lines (existing entries are detected by `(session_id, skill)` key on read).
  - Stop hook integration in `crates/sentinel-cli/src/hook_cmd.rs`: best-effort `archive_chains(&state, ctx.fs, &home)` call right before state.save(), failures logged via `tracing::warn!` and not propagated — proof archiving is a corpus-feature, not a session-shutdown gate.
  - `query_proof_corpus` extension in `crates/sentinel-application/src/mcp_handler.rs`: optional `ProofArchiveBacking { home, fs }` injected via new `with_archive(...)` builder. When wired (production path via `mcp_cmd.rs`), the response merges archived summaries with live state. Live wins ties on `(session_id, skill)` — the in-flight chain is current truth, the archived snapshot is by definition stale for that pair. Response gains a `scope: "live-session" | "cross-session"` field and an `archived_at` field on archived entries so callers can see what they got.
  - 9 new tests in `proof_archive.rs` pin: schema_version=1 in JSON, one-index-line-per-chain, idempotency across 3 Stop fires (still 1 line), one-file-per-(session,skill), malformed-line skip in `read_index`, empty-archive read returns Vec::new, future schema versions silently skipped, separator chars in session_id sanitized to safe filenames, empty-state archive is a no-op (no JSONs, no index file).
  - **Out of scope (later commits):** aging / cold-archive subdir for chains older than N days (deliverable d in the task description), gzip compression on the wire, cross-machine federation. The index keeps everything for now; aging gets added when there's actual volume to drive heuristics. 1272 workspace tests green (911 application + 289 domain + 72 infra). Release build clean.

### Changed

- **Pluggable judge backends: Kimi K2.6 added as new review-tier default; OpenRouter dispatches every JudgeModel tier (Stage A of task #34)**: the `JudgeModel` enum had 3 tiers (Haiku/Sonnet/Opus) with Display strings shaped like OpenRouter model paths, but `rig_judge.rs` ignored the model parameter and hardcoded `JUDGE_MODEL = "openai/gpt-5.4"` for every call — the tier abstraction was decorative. This commit makes the dispatch real and adds Kimi as the review-tier default per task #34's research (Moonshot K2.6 ships 58.6 SWE-Bench Pro / 89.6 LiveCodeBench / 256K context at $1.15-2.15/M tokens — 4-10x cheaper than the closed frontier with stronger agentic-coding accuracy, plus Eastern training-distribution diversity to break the shared-blind-spot failure mode of all-Western-closed multi-judging).
  - `JudgeModel` enum is now 4 tiers: `Haiku` (fast, Cerebras GLM-4.7), `Kimi` (review **default**, Moonshot K2.6), `Sonnet` (cross-vendor verification, OpenAI GPT-5.4), `Opus` (critical-strict, Anthropic Claude Opus 4.7). Variant order is cost-ascending so reading the source matches the routing-cost ladder. Bumps from old `gpt-5.3 / opus-4.6` to `gpt-5.4 / claude-opus-4.7` to match current latest available on OpenRouter (the Display strings *were* OpenRouter ids, just stale).
  - New methods on `JudgeModel`: `default_review_tier()` (returns `Kimi` — the canonical answer to "what tier does a step that didn't declare one get?"), `openrouter_model_id()` (returns the same string as `Display` but at a const fn call site for type-safe dispatch).
  - `rig_judge::JudgeProvider` now carries a runtime model_id parameter through its `PromptFn` type alias and the `judge()` method. Single OpenRouter client serves every tier. The `MultiModelJudge::evaluate` impl reads `model.openrouter_model_id()` and passes it through, so step configs that declare `judge = "kimi"` actually get Kimi instead of silently using GPT-5.4.
  - `anthropic.rs` legacy direct-Anthropic LlmPort handles the new `Kimi` variant by mapping it to `claude-sonnet-4-6` (closest review-tier substitute); doc-comment on `model_id` records the rationale and points readers to OpenRouter for actual Kimi routing.
  - 5 new tests in `judge.rs` pin the wire format: Display strings for all 4 tiers, Display ↔ openrouter_model_id() invariant, `default_review_tier() == Kimi`, kebab-case serde round-trip across all variants, Kimi/Sonnet kebab-case serialization. 2 mcp_handler tests updated to the new Sonnet/Opus model strings (they pinned the exact wire output).
  - **What's NOT in this commit (deferred to Stage B):** multi-judge parallel verification at the `critical` trust tier (Kimi+Sonnet, escalating to Opus on disagreement), DisagreementMarker chain entries, per-step pricing accounting from OpenRouter response headers, audit-grade variant recording resolved provider in StepProof. All of those sit on top of the single-judge dispatch this commit ships and deserve their own commit. 1263/1263 workspace tests green.

### Added

- **M4.6 request shape limits — content size + sliding-window rate (ContextForge pattern)**: defends against the two failure modes production MCP servers consistently get bitten by — oversized payloads (50MB tool-result bodies that explode judge token costs / log lines / classifier memory) and rate flooding (retry storms hammering one step 200×/min). New `sentinel-domain::request_limits` module ships pure-domain `RequestLimits` config (`max_evidence_bytes` default 1 MB, `max_artifact_bytes` default 256 KB, `max_calls_per_window` default 60, `window_seconds` default 60), `CallWindow` (sliding-window deque with lazy eviction, no background thread), `LimitError` enum (`EvidenceTooLarge` / `ArtifactTooLarge` / `RateLimitExceeded` each carrying actuals + limits for actionable deny messages), and the `enforce_limits()` pure function callers invoke before dispatching to the judge. **Critical invariant pinned by tests:** rejected calls do NOT count toward the rate window — otherwise a flood would self-amplify (the more you get rejected, the longer until you can call again). Callers control the `record_on_accept` knob so two-phase enforce-then-record gates don't double-count. `limit == 0` disables rate limiting entirely (useful for trusted background coordinates exempt from the policy). Order is evidence-size → artifact-size → rate (cheapest checks first; "evidence too big" is more actionable than "you're rate-limited" when both apply). 17 new tests covering defaults, serde round-trip, eviction semantics (including window-shrink-at-query-time), would_exceed at/under/over limit, rate-limit-disabled-on-zero, all three rejection paths, the no-counting-rejected invariant, the record_on_accept knob, the check-order priority, and `Display` impl message content. Hook integration (calling enforce_limits from `step_judge::process` + threading `CallWindow` through `SessionState`) lands as a follow-up — this commit ships the policy layer; the hook wiring touches a different surface and deserves its own commit. 1283/1283 workspace tests green.

- **M4.5 OpenTelemetry tracing alongside the proof chain**: ports W3C Trace Context plus a `TracingPort` trait into the workspace as the audit-substrate / operational-substrate split — the proof chain answers "what happened, signed, immutable" and OTEL answers "how long, what called what, where the latency lives." They link via a new `Option<TraceContext>` field on `StepProof` so a corpus query can pivot directly to Grafana / Tempo / Honeycomb reports. New `sentinel-domain::tracing` module owns the W3C wire format (`traceparent` v00 parser/formatter, `tracestate` key-value list, all-zero / non-hex / uppercase / arity rejection per spec), the `TraceContext` data type, and a `TraceParseError` enum with display impls. New `sentinel-application::tracing_service` module owns the use-case interface: `TracingPort` trait with `start_span` / `set_attribute` / `record_event` / `end_span`, `SpanKind` / `SpanStatus` / `AttributeValue` enums (with `From` impls for `&str` / `i64` / `u64` / `f64` / `bool`), `SpanHandle` carrying the W3C context, plus `NoOpTracer` (the off-by-default impl) and a `cfg(test)` `RecordingTracer` that captures every call for hook-level assertions. **Critical invariant:** `trace_context` is operational metadata — it does NOT participate in `combined_hash` and signing covers the hash only, so OTEL-on and OTEL-off sentinel builds share identical chains and a post-hoc trace attachment does not invalidate signatures (both pinned by tests). 40 new tests (24 in tracing module covering W3C wire format / parse rejections / round-trips, 11 in tracing_service covering NoOp + RecordingTracer + AttributeValue conversions + idempotent end-then-attribute, 5 in step_proof covering default-None / skip-on-None serialization / round-trip / hash-independence / signature-independence). The OTLP exporter wiring (heavy `opentelemetry-otlp` dep) lands as a follow-up — the trait and types are stable so it can plug in without touching the proof-chain layer. 1266/1266 workspace tests green.

- **M2.9 step plugin extensibility — `extra: serde_json::Value` on `WorkflowStep`**: ports Apollo Federation's `@composeDirective` analog. Lets external plugins (lens registries, custom routers, telemetry adapters) attach typed metadata to a step without forcing the core schema to know about every plugin. The field is opaque at the core level — plugins enforce their own schemas at their boundaries (M4.8 will add Pydantic-style fail-fast validation). The TOML loader captures the field as `Option<toml::Value>` then converts via a new `toml_to_json` helper that maps each TOML primitive to its JSON equivalent (Datetime → ISO-8601 string; NaN/Infinity → null since JSON has no representation). Realistic plugin shape: `{ lens: { code_review: { rubric: "owasp", weight: 0.7 } }, telemetry: { skip: true } }` — multiple plugins coexist on one step keyed by their top-level name, no collisions. 5 new tests (default-null, nested-table round-trip, primitive type conversions, nested array+table conversion, NaN-to-null). 1226/1226 workspace tests green.

- **M2.6 federation deprecation/migration directives — `deprecated` + `override`**: ports Apollo Federation's `@deprecated` (with reason string) and `@override` (replacement declaration) to step configs. `WorkflowStep` gains `deprecated: Option<String>` and `r#override: Option<String>`, both `#[serde(default)]` so M2.5 configs load unchanged. Override grammar accepts `"phase.step_id"` (same skill — the common case) and `"skill.phase.step_id"` (cross-skill, when one skill takes over capability previously owned by another). `sentinel federation compose` (and its `check` companion) gain a deprecation pass: deprecated steps surface as warnings (not errors — they still work), dangling override targets surface as hard errors (you can't replace a step that isn't there), and override targets that aren't themselves marked `deprecated` surface as warnings (encourages disciplined migration paths). New helper `parse_override_target()` handles both grammars. 12 new tests (3 in `config.rs` for round-trip, 6 cross-skill compose tests covering deprecated warning / dangling override / target-not-deprecated / clean migration / malformed grammar / cross-skill resolution, 3 helper-fn unit tests). 1221/1221 workspace tests green.

- **M2.5 federation directives — `provides`, `requires`, `external`, `inaccessible` on step configs**: ports Apollo Federation's `@provides` / `@requires` / `@external` / `@inaccessible` directives to the federated step namespace. `WorkflowStep` in `sentinel-domain` gains four optional fields with `#[serde(default)]` so every existing TOML loads unchanged. `StepToml` in `sentinel-infrastructure` threads them through the loader. `sentinel federation compose` (and its `check` companion) gain a second pass after the per-skill internal checks: it builds two indexes from the union of all loaded skills (artifact providers + step coordinates) and walks every step's `requires` / `external` declarations, raising hard errors when a `requires` has no producer in the supergraph or an `external` reference is dangling/malformed. `inaccessible` steps still participate in the provides graph — they're internal-only from the router's perspective (M7 will filter on the flag), not from the federation contract's. 8 new tests (3 in `config.rs` for round-trip + defaults, 5 in `federation_cmd.rs` for cross-skill resolution: clean cross-skill chain, missing producer, dangling external, malformed external, inaccessible-still-counts). 1209/1209 workspace tests green.

### Fixed

- **`project_hash` now canonicalizes worktree paths to their parent repo — task durability survives worktree-switches**: the bug task #70 (orig_id) and bloat task #72 (orig_id) had the same root cause. Six hook files (`task_persist`, `task_rehydrate`, `memory_extract`, `session_index`, `session_init`, `todo_interceptor`) each carried a copy-paste of `fn project_hash(cwd) -> sha256(cwd.as_bytes())[..4]`. Hashing the cwd verbatim meant `/repo` and `/repo/.claude/worktrees/feat-x` produced different hashes, so `task_persist` wrote one bucket while `task_rehydrate` looked up another every time the user crossed a worktree boundary — tasks silently disappeared. New shared helpers in `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/mod.rs`: `canonical_project_cwd(cwd)` strips the literal segment `/.claude/worktrees/` (and the `\.claude\worktrees\` Windows variant) plus everything after it, collapsing any worktree to its repo root; `project_hash(cwd)` uses the canonical form. All 6 callers now delegate to `super::project_hash`. Dead `sha2::{Digest, Sha256}` imports + the local `hex_encode` helper removed from `task_rehydrate.rs` and `todo_interceptor.rs`. 6 new unit tests pin the worktree-collapse invariant: forward-slash collapse, backslash collapse, deep subpath collapse, non-worktree paths unchanged, sentinel main + sentinel worktree produce identical hashes, different repos still produce different hashes. The 390 orphan project-hash directories accumulated under the broken behavior remain on disk — cleanup is filed as a separate task. 798 sentinel-application library tests pass; release build clean; engine staged via `sentinel stage` for hot-swap on next session.

- **`memory_verify` re-wired to PreCompact — completes the relocation tracked as a follow-up in the previous hooks.toml fix**: the module had been orphaned on disk since the SessionStart removal (Qdrant scroll + per-claim Cerebras verification was blocking startup 5–20s on a cold cache). Three coordinated changes: (1) `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/memory_verify.rs` — module + function doc-comments updated to describe the PreCompact home and explain why (24h cooldown means a long session typically verifies once on its first compaction event of the day; `run_async()`'s 3s wall-clock timeout is retained as defence in depth); the one hardcoded `HookEvent::SessionStart` in the context-injection path at line 323 corrected to `HookEvent::PreCompact`. (2) `crates/sentinel-cli/src/hook_cmd.rs` — `memory_verify::process` now invoked from the PreCompact dispatcher branch alongside `pre_compact::process` and `session_index::process`, with an inline comment recording the relocation rationale. (3) `config/hooks.toml` — replaced the "orphaned, kept on disk" comment with a registration entry under PreCompact (`depends_on = ["pre-compact"]`, `has_api_call = true`); the inline comment now points readers to the new home. 792 sentinel-application library tests pass; release build clean.

- **`config/hooks.toml` reconciled with the dispatcher's actual behavior**: the registration file had drifted in both directions — `memory-verify` was registered for SessionStart but the dispatcher had already removed it (Qdrant HTTP calls were blocking startup 5–20s; comment in `hook_cmd.rs:677` documents the removal); meanwhile three real, dispatched memory hooks (`memory_inject` on UserPromptSubmit + Stop, `memory_extract` on Stop, `session_index` on PreCompact) had no registration entries at all. The `memory-feedback` entry's `depends_on = ["memory-extract"]` was a dangling reference because of this. Fix: removed the stale `memory-verify` SessionStart entry (replaced with a comment explaining the situation), added registrations for `memory-inject` (UserPromptSubmit), `memory-extract` (Stop), `memory-inject-precompute` (Stop), and `session-index` (PreCompact, depends on `pre-compact`). The `depends_on = ["memory-extract"]` on `memory-feedback` is now a real reference. The orphaned `memory_verify` Rust module is left in place for a planned PreCompact relocation, tracked as a follow-up. 1075 workspace tests pass.

- **Flaky `api::memory::tests::daemon_url_falls_back_to_default_when_unset` race**: three tests in `crates/sentinel-cli/src/api/memory.rs` (`daemon_url_uses_env_override_when_set`, `daemon_url_falls_back_to_default_when_unset`, `daemon_unreachable_returns_503`) all read+mutate `SENTINEL_MEMORY_DAEMON_URL`. Cargo runs unit tests in parallel by default, so without coordination the fall-back test intermittently observed the override test's value before its own `remove_var` ran. The previous comment claimed the override test was "the only env-touching test" — wrong, the unreachable test was added later without the same treatment. Fix: module-scoped `static ENV_LOCK: Mutex<()>` plus a `lock_env()` helper that tolerates poisoning; each affected test takes the lock at function entry and holds it across the full env-mutation + `daemon_url()` read window. 5 consecutive `cargo test --release -p sentinel api::memory::tests` runs all green (4/4 each).

### Changed

- **`task_rehydrate` is mode-aware: auto-rehydrates in Autopilot, asks first in Planned**: prior behavior was "always ASK FIRST regardless of mode" which made every Autopilot session pay an interruption tax to recover its task queue from the previous session. The hook context already exposes `autopilot_enabled()` (reads `SENTINEL_AUTOPILOT`); `task_rehydrate.rs` now queries it and emits one of four instruction variants (autopilot+blocking, autopilot+flat, planned+blocking, planned+flat). Autopilot variants direct immediate `TaskCreate` (and `TaskUpdate(addBlockedBy)` for blocking chains) followed by a one-sentence brief; Planned variants preserve the y/n ask-gate. Logic extracted to a pure helper `format_rehydrate_instruction(count, has_blocking, autopilot)` so the four-way branching is unit-tested without FS plumbing — 4 new tests pin each variant's invariants (mode tag, action verb, count formatting, mutual-exclusion of mode strings).

- **`tool_usage_gate` now strictly requires `TaskCreate` — `TodoWrite` no longer satisfies the gate**: per the operator's `CLAUDE.md` "Required Tool Usage" §3, the agent-harness `TaskCreate` / `TaskUpdate` (TaskList) tool is mandatory for tracking work, and the dual-acceptance of `TodoWrite` was the slippage point that let agents drift into the lesser fallback. Two changes in `crates/sentinel-cli/src/hook_cmd.rs`: (1) the PostToolUse marker writer no longer fires `mark_task_created` / `mark_task_active` on `TodoWrite` — only `TaskCreate` does; (2) the entire `TodoWrite`-with-`in_progress`-payload branch that opportunistically wrote `TASK_ACTIVE_PREFIX` is removed. Deny messages in `tool_usage_gate.rs` updated in two places (Check 2 and Check 4) to specifically name `TaskCreate` and explicitly reject `TodoWrite` with a "NOT accepted — the operator's CLAUDE.md mandates the agent-harness TaskList tool" callout, so agents that hit the block know exactly what to use. The signed `verification` override (60s escape hatch) still works as before. New regression test `test_check2_deny_message_rejects_todowrite_and_names_taskcreate` pins both invariants — if a future edit drops either the `TaskCreate` mention or the `TodoWrite` rejection, the test fails.

- **`tool_usage_gate` Check 4 reads the persistent task store, not just the sticky marker**: the `TASK_ACTIVE_PREFIX` marker only flips ON — it never reflects task completion — so once any task was marked active, the marker satisfied the gate forever even after every task completed. New `persistent_store_has_active_task(fs)` reads `~/.claude/sentinel/persistent-tasks/*/tasks.json` (and the legacy `~/.claude/persistent-tasks/*/tasks.json` location during the migration window) and returns `true` only when at least one task currently has `status=in_progress`. Check 4 queries this authoritative source first; the marker is retained as a fast-path/fallback for the rare case the store can't be read (no home dir, malformed JSON). Catches the "all tasks are completed but agent is still editing" drift that motivated the recurring complaint.

### Added

- **`scripts/bootstrap.sh` — one-command installer for sentinel + linear MCP/CLI + marketplace.** Clones the four code repos (vulcan-mcp-sdk-rust, sentinel, linear-mcp-rust, linear-cli-rust) under `$SENTINEL_GH_DIR` (default `~/Documents/GitHub`), clones claude-code-marketplace into `$SENTINEL_CLAUDE_DIR` (default `~/.claude`) — only if the target dir doesn't already exist as a git repo or isn't non-empty — runs `cargo build --release` in each, copies the launcher + engine binaries (`sentinel`, `sentinel-engine`, `linear-mcp`, `linear`, plus `mcp-router` if vulcan built it) into `~/.cargo/bin/` so the launcher/engine split lands correctly without relying on `cargo install`'s crate-path guesswork, copies `hooks.toml` + `workflows.toml` from the sentinel repo into `~/.claude/sentinel/config/`, writes a starter `settings.json` with the seven event handlers (SessionStart, SessionEnd, UserPromptSubmit, PreToolUse, PostToolUse, Stop, PreCompact) all wired to `sentinel hook --event <Event>` plus an env block with `REPLACE_ME` placeholders for `LINEAR_API_KEY` / `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` / `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` / `QDRANT_URL` / `QDRANT_API_KEY`, and writes `~/.claude.json` with `sentinel` + `linear` MCP server entries — but only if the file doesn't already exist; if it does, prints the JSON snippet to paste manually. Every step is idempotent: re-running skips anything already present. `gh` is preferred for cloning private repos when authenticated, falls back to `https` otherwise. README links it under a new Quick Install section. Verified with `bash -n scripts/bootstrap.sh` syntax check + `cargo check --workspace` clean.
- **`task_persist` writes a `source: auto` marker in the YAML frontmatter of project_tasks.md**: lets memory audits filter auto-generated TaskList snapshots from human-curated entries. Approach (a) — adding a `source` field to the `qdrant-mcp-rust` `store_memory` tool — wasn't viable without modifying that crate's domain `Memory` struct, so the marker lives on the flat file (`~/.claude/projects/<key>/memory/project_tasks.md`), which IS the memory file. Survives round-trips through `sync_from_files`; greppable. Two-line change in `crates/sentinel-application/src/hooks/task_persist.rs::write_memory_summary` plus a regression assertion on `test_write_memory_summary_creates_files`. Plan recorded at `plans/task-persist-source-marker.md`.

- **`good_citizen_observer` hook — soft-enforces "fix pre-existing issues you spot"**: two-phase observational hook that operationalizes the global `CLAUDE.md` "good citizens" rule. PostToolUse(Bash) scans tool stdout/stderr for compile warnings, dead-code diagnostics, lint findings, test failures, panics, and inline `TODO`/`FIXME`/`HACK` markers (12 patterns spanning Rust/clippy, TypeScript, ESLint, generic test failures), and appends a one-line `Observation` to `~/.claude/sentinel/state/good-citizen/{session_id}.jsonl`. Stop reads the per-session log and, if any observations exist, injects a soft reminder via `additionalContext` listing up to three findings grouped by category — naming `TaskCreate` as the action ("File a `TaskCreate` for any pre-existing issue worth fixing — scale the fix to the change"). Soft (advisory) rather than hard-blocking by design: "is that warning worth a task?" is fuzzy, and a hard block would false-fire on outputs the agent already understands and intends to ignore. Per-call write cap of 10 observations, total reminder shows top 3 — bounds JSONL growth and reminder length. 5 unit tests (records dead code, records test failure, ignores clean output, ignores non-Bash tools, Stop emits/skips correctly).

### Fixed

- **`pre_commit_verification` no longer parses Claude Code's transcript — Sentinel records its own evidence**: the hook input `session_id` is the harness wrapper ID, which does **not** match the on-disk `{sessionId}.jsonl` filename Claude Code writes (an internal `G8.sessionId`). Searching the transcript directory by the hook's session_id never finds the right file, so transcript-based verification falsely blocked every commit/push (the symptom: "BLOCKED: Run Tests Before Committing" even right after `cargo test` passed). Replaced with a self-recorded evidence file: new PostToolUse hook `test_evidence_recorder` (Bash matcher) appends a JSONL entry to `~/.claude/sentinel/state/test-evidence/{session_id}.jsonl` whenever a Bash command matches a test/build pattern; `pre_commit_verification` reads from that file instead. Both hooks see the same `session_id` from `HookInput`, so the lookup is exact — the transcript-ID mismatch is now irrelevant. Pure types live in new `sentinel-domain::test_evidence` (`TestEvidenceEntry`, `TEST_COMMAND_PATTERNS`, `evidence_path`, `compile_command_patterns`) so recorder + reader share the same source of truth. Deleted the dead `find_transcript_by_session` and `transcript_has_test_evidence` functions and their three transcript-search tests. Added 4 recorder tests + 2 evidence-file reader tests; 1067 workspace tests pass.

### Added

- **WIP-by-stage snapshot module + MCP read tool (SEN-8, data half)**: new `wip_snapshot` module owns the on-disk format for `~/.claude/sentinel/state/wip-snapshot.json` (atomic tmp+rename, `BTreeMap` for deterministic ordering) plus the bottleneck rule engine. The `review_clog` rule is implemented and tested: fires when `Code Review WIP / 7d throughput > 14 days`, silent at exactly 14d, silent when no review WIP, silent when throughput is zero/missing, and per-team independent. The `qa_ceiling` rule is shaped in the public API but deferred to the live poller (needs per-ticket dwell time). New MCP tool `mcp__sentinel__get_wip_snapshot` reads the file and returns a friendly "no snapshot captured yet" payload before the poller has run. The 5-minute Linear API poller is tracked as a follow-up task. 10 new unit tests, 781/781 workspace pass.

- **Cycle-time event capture (SEN-1, persistence half)**: new `cycle_time` module in `sentinel-application` extracts Linear `Issue.update` state transitions from incoming Hookdeck webhook bodies and appends them to `~/.claude/sentinel/metrics/cycle-time.jsonl`. Fires as a side effect inside `channel_event_from_webhook` so the existing channel-emission contract is unchanged — JSONL persistence is opportunistic and never blocks the channel event. Schema matches the SEN-1 spec verbatim (`issue_id`, optional `team`, `from_state`, `to_state`, `timestamp`, `estimate`, `priority`, `labels`). Pure parser (`extract_from_linear_webhook`) is fully fixture-driven; 9 unit tests cover the transition-vs-not-a-transition matrix, prior-state-name fallback, label array shape variants (objects vs strings), missing-optional serialization, and append round-trip. The Hookdeck route admin and 60-day Linear backfill are tracked as follow-up tasks. 771/771 sentinel-application tests still green.

### Changed

- **Doc updates for `accounts-mcp` → `claude-accounts-mcp` rename**: the `accounts` MCP and its CLI sibling were renamed to `claude-accounts` (across GitHub repos, local dirs, Cargo packages, internal crates, and binaries) on 2026-05-02 to disambiguate from "Linear accounts" / "Doppler accounts" / "project configs" — the word "accounts" was massively overloaded. Sentinel itself only had two stale comments referencing the old name in `account_cascade.rs::process` and `is_error_result`; both updated to point at `claude-accounts-mcp` with a parenthetical noting the rename date.

### Fixed

- **`git_hygiene` threshold raised + `pre_commit_verification` recognizes more verifiers**: `MAX_UNCOMMITTED_FILES` was 10, which constantly false-fired on routine work in repos with legacy index noise (stale build dirs, in-progress refactors, .gitignore drift) and forced cleanup detours before the actual task could resume. Raised to 150 — still catches genuinely out-of-control sessions but no longer blocks normal work. Separately, `pre_commit_verification`'s `TEST_COMMAND_PATTERNS` was missing `cargo check`, `cargo clippy`, `go build`, and `go vet` — meaning Rust changes verified via `cargo check` (the most common Rust verifier) would still be blocked at commit because the gate didn't recognize the evidence. Patterns added. Tests updated to compute file counts off `MAX_UNCOMMITTED_FILES` instead of hardcoded 12/15 so they remain correct under any future threshold changes. 964 tests pass.

- **Interceptor false-positives on flag-like text inside commit messages**: `evaluate_git_command` substring-matched the joined args string, so a commit body containing literal `--force` (or `reset --hard`, `filter-branch`, etc.) would block the commit. Real-world reproduction this session: `git commit -m "fix(interceptor): rm -rf orphaned worktree shells on Windows + better cleanup reminder ... worktree remove [--force] path ..."` was rejected as if `--force` were a real flag. Fix: new `evaluate_git_args(&[String])` entrypoint that strips the values of `-m` / `--message` / `-F` / `--file` (both space-separated and `=` forms) before applying substring-match policy. The application layer (`crates/sentinel-application/src/interceptor.rs`) now uses the args-aware entrypoint. The legacy `evaluate_git_command(&str)` stays for backward compat. 11 new unit tests pin the false-positive cases (commit with `--force` / `reset --hard` / `filter-branch` / `--force-with-lease` / `rebase -i` in the message body, long-form `--message`, `=` form, `-F path`) AND verify real `--force`, `push --force`, `reset --hard` are still blocked/confirmed correctly. 762/762 app + 26/26 domain tests still green.

- **Orphaned worktree shells on Windows**: `git worktree remove` on Windows routinely fails to delete the on-disk directory because some process (file watcher, mcp-router, IDE) holds a handle inside the tree. Git itself unregisters the worktree and exits 0, leaving an empty (or near-empty) directory shell behind that `hygiene_reminders` then correctly flags as stale on every prompt. Two-layer fix:
  - `sentinel-git-interceptor` now runs a `post_exec_cleanup` pass after every wrapped git invocation (allow path, confirm path, and `--bypass` path). When the args parse as `worktree remove [--force] <path>` and git returned 0 *and* the on-disk directory still exists, retries `std::fs::remove_dir_all` up to 3 times with 150ms backoff. Failures are logged to stderr and never bubble up — git already considered the command successful. NotFound errors are treated as a benign race.
  - `hygiene_reminders` cleanup message now includes a copy-paste `rm -rf <path1> <path2> ...` one-liner spanning every detected stale shell, so users can wipe leftovers from prior sessions in one shot. The reminder also now explains the typical cause (Windows file locks) so future-Gary doesn't have to re-derive it.
  - 6 unit tests pin the `worktree remove` arg parser (relative + absolute path, `--force` before/after path, non-`worktree-remove` commands, empty args). Existing 7 hygiene_reminders tests still green. Full sentinel-application lib suite: 762/762.

### Changed

- **Persistent-tasks dir relocated under `sentinel/`**: snapshots written by `task_persist` and read by `task_rehydrate` (and the CLAUDE.md "Active Tasks" section in `session_init`) now live at `~/.claude/sentinel/persistent-tasks/{project_hash}/` instead of `~/.claude/persistent-tasks/`. Centralizes sentinel-owned state alongside `metrics/`, `state/`, `proofs/`, etc. so `~/.claude/` stays clean. New `persistent_tasks_root(home)` and `legacy_persistent_tasks_root(home)` helpers in `hooks::mod.rs`; both `task_persist` and `task_rehydrate` resolve their dir through them. One-time migration via `migrate_persistent_tasks_dir(fs, home)` triggers on first read after upgrade — atomic rename when possible, per-entry copy fallback for cross-mount or Windows-locked cases. Idempotent: no-op when the new dir already exists or the legacy dir doesn't. `session_init::render_tasks_section` reads new location first, falls back to legacy during the migration window so CLAUDE.md generation stays correct mid-upgrade. 5 new unit tests in `migrate_tests` (move, no-op when new exists, no-op when legacy missing, path shape under sentinel, legacy path unchanged).

### Added

- **Project-scoped `tasks.md` sync (single source of truth)**: `task_persist` hook now writes `<repo_root>/tasks.md` on every `TaskCreated` / `TaskCompleted` / `Stop` event in addition to the existing `~/.claude/persistent-tasks/{hash}/tasks.json` rehydration snapshot. The on-repo file is wrapped in `<!-- SENTINEL:TASKS:START -->` / `<!-- SENTINEL:TASKS:END -->` markers so any hand-written content (e.g. a curated roadmap that already lives at `tasks.md`) is preserved — first run prepends the auto block above existing content; subsequent runs splice in place. Skip-if-unchanged compares a SHA-256 of the rendered block against `meta.json` so unchanged turns are no-ops. Repo-root resolution goes through `GitStatusPort::repo_root(cwd)` so non-repo directories silently skip the markdown write while still updating the global JSON.
  - **Linear merge**: when `~/.claude/sentinel/linear-assigned-{project}.json` exists (populated by the existing Linear cron), open issues for the project are merged into a `## Linear Assigned` section inside the auto block — sorted started → unstarted → backlog → triage, capped at 50 rows, completed/canceled filtered out, priority emoji per row. No network call from the hook itself; the Linear cron owns the cache.
  - **Native Claude memory writeback**: a project-scoped `~/.claude/projects/<encoded-key>/memory/project_tasks.md` is updated alongside `tasks.md` on every fire (frontmatter `type: project`, top-10 open tasks with blocked-by chains). One line in `MEMORY.md` is added/replaced (`- [Tasks for <project>](project_tasks.md) — N open, M in progress`) so it lands in the auto-loaded memory at session start. Repo-root key encoding (`C:\Users\…` → `C--Users-…`) means worktree sessions update the canonical project entry instead of fragmenting per branch.
  - **Auto-block enforcement (`tasks_md_guard`)**: new PreToolUse hook blocks `Edit` / `Write` on `<repo_root>/tasks.md` when the change would mutate content **inside** the marker block (Edit `old_string` overlapping the marker range, or Write whose between-marker bytes differ from disk). Edits OUTSIDE the markers, or Writes that re-emit the same block, are still allowed — the block-message tells agents to use `TaskCreate` / Linear instead. Anchored on `GitStatusPort::repo_root(parent(file_path))` so only the actual project tasks.md is guarded; sibling tasks.md files in subdirectories are left alone.
  - 26 unit tests across `task_persist` (marker insertion, replace-in-place, idempotent re-merge, skip-if-unchanged, Linear filter/order/empty, memory writeback skip-when-no-projects-dir, memory writeback creates files + indexes correctly, MEMORY.md duplicate-line collapse, project-key encoding for Windows + Unix paths) plus 12 in `tasks_md_guard` (marker range parsing, edit-overlap detection above/below/inside, write delta detection, fresh-file allow, no-marker allow). Builds clean across the workspace.

- **ROI vs human-team baseline (SEN-15)**: new `sentinel roi scan` CLI subcommand joins SEN-7 `tokens-per-ticket.jsonl` with the SEN-13 `cost-per-point-summary.json` and computes the headline factory metric — $ Claude spent vs $ a human team would spend shipping the same work. Human baseline constants land in `sentinel-domain::constants` (`HUMAN_FULLY_LOADED_USD_PER_YEAR = 170_000`, `HUMAN_FULLY_LOADED_USD_PER_DAY = 654`, `HUMAN_DAYS_PER_POINT = 0.5`, `HUMAN_USD_PER_POINT = 327`, `HUMAN_WORKING_DAYS_PER_YEAR = 260`) so the ratio is reproducible and reviewable. For each rolling window (7d / 30d / 90d / all-time) the analyzer reports tickets shipped, points shipped, Claude cost, equivalent human cost, ROI ratio, and projected annual savings. Window membership is derived from the most-recent session-file mtime per ticket under `~/.claude/projects/*` (best-effort — collapses to all-time only when the projects root is missing). When SEN-13 has zero tickets-with-estimate the analyzer engages a transparent fallback path: assume `FALLBACK_AVG_POINTS_PER_TICKET = 3.0`, mark every row `fallback_used: true`, and surface a fallback note explaining the synthesis. Outputs land at `~/.claude/sentinel/metrics/roi.jsonl` (one row per window) and `~/.claude/sentinel/metrics/roi-summary.json` (top-line headline + nested windows). Stdout report prints the headline ROI as a big-number, per-window breakdown table, and a tip when fallback is in play. 6 unit tests pin ROI ratio against a known-input case (10x), annual savings projection scaling against a 30d window, missing-input clean degradation, fallback engagement when SEN-13 reports zero estimates, ticket-id slug extraction (with prefix allow-list), and weighted-median collapse over SEN-13 buckets. Live first-scan against 24 tickets / $12,073 spend produces 2.0x all-time ROI and ~$103k projected annual savings via the fallback path.

- **PR review thoroughness metrics (SEN-18)**: new `sentinel pr-review scan` CLI subcommand walks merged PRs across the firefly-pro-gh org (firefly-pro-crm, firefly-pro-web-app, firefly-pro-api-rust, firefly-pro-routing, firefly-pro-routing-engine, firefly-pro-routing-api, firefly-pro-marketing) plus legatus-ai/sentinel via `gh` CLI shell-out, computes review-depth metrics (avg comments per PR, time-to-first-review p50/p90 in hours), counts Codex severity blocks (CRITICAL/HIGH/MEDIUM/LOW) and CodeRabbit findings (critical / potential issue / refactor suggestion / nitpick) by parsing comment + review bodies, distinguishes bot reviewers (coderabbitai, github-actions, linear, greptile-apps, codex, renovate, dependabot, vercel) from human reviewers to compute the human-in-the-loop %, and heuristically scores CodeRabbit remediation rate via post-review commit timing. Writes `~/.claude/sentinel/metrics/pr-review.jsonl` (one row per PR with full per-PR breakdown) and `~/.claude/sentinel/metrics/pr-review-summary.json` (aggregate roll-up + per-repo). Stdout report prints global summary + per-repo breakdown. Window default 30d (configurable via `--days`). 12 unit tests pin the Codex severity parser (text + emoji forms), CodeRabbit category detection, bot vs. human classification, time-to-first-review computation, percentile aggregation (linear interpolation), `gh` JSON parsers (list + view), and end-to-end report aggregation. Live first-scan against the 8 default repos: 282 merged PRs over 30 days, 2.83 avg comments per PR, 505 CodeRabbit findings, 9.57% human-in-the-loop coverage.

- **Cost-per-story-point analyzer (SEN-13)**: new `sentinel cost-per-point scan` CLI subcommand joins the SEN-7 `tokens-per-ticket.jsonl` rows with Linear estimates to compute `tokens_per_point = total_tokens / estimate` and `cost_per_point = cost_usd / estimate` per ticket. Tickets are bucketed to the nearest canonical Linear estimate (1, 2, 3, 5, 8, 16) — ties round up so 6 → 8 not 5, 12 → 16 not 8. Per-bucket p25/p50/p75/p90 are computed via numpy-default linear interpolation. The "estimating drift" ratio = `bucket-8 cost_p50 / bucket-2 cost_p50` flags non-linear sizing curves with a default alarm threshold of 5.0x. Outputs land at `~/.claude/sentinel/metrics/cost-per-point.jsonl` (one row per ticket-with-estimate, sorted descending by `cost_per_point`) and `~/.claude/sentinel/metrics/cost-per-point-summary.json` (totals, per-bucket stats, drift ratio + alarm flag). The Linear cache loader is permissive — accepts both top-level `[...]` arrays and `{"issues": [...]}` objects, reads the estimate from any of `estimate`/`estimateValue`/`estimate_value`/`points`/`story_points`/`storyPoints`, and silently skips issues with missing or null estimates. When zero tickets carry estimates the report says so honestly (`tickets_with_estimate: 0` + a yellow stdout warning) rather than fabricating point values — the correct answer until SEN-1's webhook capture lands an estimate-aware Linear snapshot. 9 unit tests cover bucket assignment (exact + ties + clamps), percentile computation against numpy reference values, drift alarm trigger at 6x synthetic data, empty-estimate clean report, both Linear cache shapes, and missing-input graceful degradation.

- **Cache hit rate + token efficiency tracker (SEN-14)**: new `sentinel cache scan` CLI subcommand walks `~/.claude/projects/*/` for session JSONL files, parses every `assistant` message's `usage` block, and computes the prompt-cache hit rate per session as `cache_read_input_tokens / (cache_read + input_tokens + cache_creation_input_tokens)`. Aggregates p50/p90 globally and per-project, surfaces the top-N "worst" sessions ranked by waste estimate `(1 - hit_rate) * total_tokens` (filtered to sessions with ≥50K total tokens so trivially-tiny zero-cache sessions don't dominate the list), rolls a per-day mean, and converts waste tokens to USD at the conservative Opus input rate ($15/Mtok). Writes a per-session JSONL at `~/.claude/sentinel/metrics/cache-efficiency.jsonl` (one row per session with hit rate, waste estimate, and raw token counts) plus a structured summary at `~/.claude/sentinel/metrics/cache-efficiency-summary.json` (global percentiles, per-project breakdown, daily trend, top-10 worst). Stdout report colours hit-rate %, prints the worst-N list with token volume + dollar waste, and renders a 7-day bar-chart trend. Edge cases pinned: zero-usage sessions return `None` for hit rate (no 0/0 NaN), empty percentile input returns 0.0, missing project root writes empty outputs without panicking. Walker pattern duplicated from SEN-7's `tokens.rs`; consolidation into a shared session-walker helper deferred to a follow-up. 8 unit tests.

- **Tokens-per-ticket aggregator (SEN-7)**: new `sentinel tokens scan` CLI subcommand walks `~/.claude/projects/*/` for session JSONL files, extracts the Linear ticket id from the worktree path slug first (high-confidence) and grep of the first 50 user prompts second (medium-confidence), aggregates `usage` blocks across every `assistant` message in the session, applies per-model Anthropic pricing via the new `sentinel_domain::pricing` module, and writes one `{ticket, sessions, total_input, cache_read, cache_creation, output, cost_usd, models, confidence}` row per ticket to `~/.claude/sentinel/metrics/tokens-per-ticket.jsonl`. Output is full-overwrite each scan — input session JSONLs are the source of truth so re-scanning is idempotent. Pricing tiers (Opus / Sonnet / Haiku) are hardcoded constants for now; TODO move to a TOML lookup in a follow-up. Stdout report prints total sessions, mapping coverage %, and top-N most expensive tickets. Known prefix allow-list (FPCRM, FPFIELD, FPROUTE, FPMD, FPTRIBU, LEG, COR, EXA, SYN, TES, TRI, SEN) keeps `HTTP-200`-style false positives out. 15 unit tests cover path-slug extraction, prompt grep with cap, cost computation against published rates, and an end-to-end fixture scan.

### Fixed

- **Drop malformed `task_completed` / `teammate_idle` channel events (SEN-1)**: both hooks previously fell back to placeholder strings (`"?"`, `"unknown task"`, `"unknown"`) when `input.extra` was missing required fields, then emitted those placeholders as channel notifications. The result: lead sessions saw a constant trickle of `"Task #? completed: 'unknown task' (by unknown)"` and `"Teammate 'unknown' (team: unknown) is going idle"` notifications for every malformed dispatch. Both hooks now `return HookOutput::allow()` without emitting when any of `task_id` / `task_subject` / `teammate_name` is missing or contains the literal placeholder. 4 new unit tests pin both the missing-fields and unknown-literals branches.

- **Skill router: strip injected hook context before classification (SEN-2)**: the AI classifier was routing on words appearing in hook-injected reminders rather than the actual user message. Concrete trigger from a recent session: a turn that included the hook reminder `[Worktree Cleanup] 4 stale worktree(s) found` caused the `cleanup` skill to fire even though the user said nothing about cleanup. New `strip_hook_context()` helper removes `<system-reminder>...</system-reminder>` blocks (multi-line), `<channel ...>...</channel>` blocks, and bare `[Bracketed Tag] message` reminder lines before classification. If the cleaned prompt is empty (input was 100% hook context), short-circuit to `allow()`. 5 new unit tests cover all four strip cases plus pure-user-text passthrough.

- **PR auto-monitor: suppress `git push` recommendation when no remote (SEN-3)**: the merge-to-main branch unconditionally injected `1. Push to remote: \`git push\`` even when the repo had no remote configured (e.g., a fresh repo not yet pushed to GitHub). Detect remote presence by reading `<cwd>/.git/config` directly — no subprocess, no latency — and looking for any `[remote "..."]` section. Worktrees have a `.git` *file* pointing at the main repo's `.git/config`; follow that pointer. When no remote is configured, swap step 1 with `1. Configure a remote (\`git remote add origin <url>\`) before the first push`. 2 new tests pin both branches.

### Added

- **Hook invocation telemetry (`hook_metrics` module + `sentinel stats hooks`)**: every wrapped hook call now appends a single JSON line to `~/.claude/sentinel/metrics/hook-invocations.jsonl` with `ts`, `event`, `hook`, `tool`, `session_id`, `repo_root`, `duration_us`, `outcome` (allow/block/deny/inject), and a 120-char `reason` snippet for blocks. Privacy: `tool_input` and `tool_result` are never logged. Telemetry errors are swallowed so they can't break a hook. New `sentinel stats hooks [--limit N] [--hours H]` subcommand reads the file back and prints top-N by call count, top-N by total time, an outcome breakdown, and a recent-blocks list. Local API endpoints land in a follow-up PR. Phase A wiring covers the `PreToolUse` and `UserPromptSubmit` event branches (~25 hook call sites); the remaining branches migrate incrementally.

- **Bug task gate (new hook `bug_task_gate`)**: when a tool result reveals a bug — `cargo test` `test result: FAILED`, a Rust compile error with a code (`error[E0277]: …`), or a runtime `panicked at` — the hook records pending-bug state at `~/.claude/sentinel/state/pending-bug-{repo_hash}.json` and blocks subsequent mutating tools (matching the `tool_usage_gate` scope) until a `TaskCreate` or `TaskUpdate` references the bug. Subject/description must contain at least one of: `bug`, `fix`, `error`, `regression`, `broken`, `failure`, `failing`, `panic`, `crash`. State auto-clears after a 10-minute TTL so a transient signal doesn't deadlock the session. Detection is conservative on purpose: only the three high-confidence patterns above trigger, so the gate doesn't fire on routine log output that happens to contain the word "error". 16 unit tests cover signal detection, false-positive suppression, TaskCreate keyword matching, and TTL behaviour.

- **Tool usage gate broadened to mutating Bash + write MCP tools**: previously the gate enforced "sequential-thinking + TaskCreate + plan-mode + active task" only on `Edit`/`Write`. Bash and MCP tools bypassed it entirely, which let large mutations (commits, pushes, Linear writes, Doppler updates) ship without a tracked task. The gate now also covers Bash commands matching mutating prefixes (`git commit/push/merge/rebase/reset`, `gh pr create/merge`, `cargo build/run/install`, `npm/yarn/pnpm install`, `rm/mv/cp/mkdir/chmod`, `docker run/build`, `kubectl apply/delete`, output redirections `>`/`>>`) and MCP tools whose verb part doesn't contain a read-only fragment (`get`, `list`, `view`, `search`, `check`, `status`, `show`, `describe`, `health`, …). Read-only Bash (`git status/log/diff`, `ls`, `cargo check`, `gh pr view`, …) and read-only MCP tools (`mcp__linear__list_issues`, `mcp__doppler__get_secret`, …) still bypass. `cd <dir> &&` prefixes are stripped before classification so compound commands aren't mis-classified. New test coverage: 7 classifier-specific cases + 4 end-to-end gate cases.

- **Skill banner enforcement**: `skill_router` always renders an activation banner now — when a SKILL.md doesn't define a `## Activation Banner` section, the router synthesizes a fallback banner from the skill's frontmatter `description` field (with a 160-char hard cap) so the visual cue is consistent across all 76+ skills regardless of authoring discipline. `sentinel scan --validate` adds a new "Skill Banner" category that flags any SKILL.md missing an explicit `## Activation Banner` as a `warn` (not `fail`, so unmigrated skills don't break CI). Audit at write-time: only 1 of 77 skills (qdrant) currently lacks a banner.

- **Skill invocation gate (new hook `skill_invocation_gate`)**: enforces that skills detected by `skill_router` are actually invoked. When a skill is detected, `skill_router` writes a pending-skill state file (`~/.claude/sentinel/state/skill-pending-{session_hash}.json`). The new `PreToolUse` gate blocks tool calls outside an allowlist of read-only / progress-toward-load tools (Read, Glob, Grep, LSP, WebSearch/Fetch, ToolSearch, Skill, Task*, sequential-thinking) until the pending skill is invoked or its SKILL.md is read. The matching `PostToolUse` handler clears the state on `Skill(skill: "<name>")` matching the pending skill or on a `Read(...)` of its SKILL.md. State auto-clears after a 5-minute TTL so a skill the user explicitly skipped doesn't deadlock the session. 12 new unit tests cover stale TTL handling, allowlist sanity, and Windows/Unix/tilde path matching.

- **Sentinel engine version + hook count in SessionStart banner**: the `[SessionStart]` line now reads `session_id: X | engine: sentinel v0.4.0 | hooks: 54` so the running build is always visible at the top of every session. Version comes from `CARGO_PKG_VERSION` (compile-time); hook count is `HOOK_NAMES.len()` so it can't drift from the registered handlers.

- **Canonical hook output envelope (`HookEnvelope` + `HookTier`)**: new types in `sentinel-domain::events` plus `HookOutput::inject_envelope(event, envelope)` constructor. Renders as `[<HookName>] <emoji> <message>` with 🟢 Info / 🟡 Warn / 🔴 Block tier emojis so the user sees a consistent prefix across all 54 hooks instead of the ad-hoc mix of brackets, emoji, and box-drawing currently in use. Phase A only — existing `inject_context` call sites are unchanged. Migration of the 50+ legacy callers will land in follow-up tasks (one batch per hook group).

### Changed

- **Worktree/branch cleanup discipline (hygiene_reminders + worktree_reminder + pr_auto_monitor)**: surface merged `worktree-*` branches as actionable cleanup commands, both local (`git branch -d`) and remote (`git push origin --delete`).
